# THE BOOK OF DANIEL{.heading_16}

Introduction {.heading_67-1}

We take up, here, the study of one of the most important books in the Old Testament: the book of Daniel. Although chapters 1--7 are written in the third person as history, chapter 8 opens up with Daniel giving his prophecies directly in the first person. It is nothing unusual for a Bible author to write of himself in the third person (e.g., Moses, Jonah, and John). So there is no doubt, for the Bible believer, that Daniel is the author of the book, especially when it is verified by Jesus Christ Himself (Matt. 24:15; Mark 13:14).

Daniel is what is known as an "Exilic" writing; that is, it was written during the time of Judah's Exile in Babylon, and on into the beginning of the Persian Empire. The date of authorship runs from 607 B.C., when Daniel was taken to Babylon, to 534 B.C., during the reign of ["Cyrus king of Persia"]{.class_1939} in Babylon (10:1).

The book is opposed by Jewish, Catholic, and Protestant scholars alike because of its overt, detailed prophecies of world history. Daniel records four accurate accounts of world history, each one ending in the takeover of the United Nations by the Son of Perdition. Those four accounts are in chapters 2, 7, 8, and 11.

Furthermore, history is narrowed down with each consecutive account. In chapter 2, there are [four]{.class_1925} kingdoms, a break, and then the Antichrist's kingdom. In chapter 7, there are [three]{.class_1925} kingdoms, a break, and then the Antichrist's kingdom. In chapter 8, there are [two]{.class_1925} kingdoms, a break, and then the Antichrist's kingdom. And finally, chapter 11 gives only [one]{.class_1925} kingdom---the Antichrist's kingdom.

Because the prophecies of the rise and fall of Babylon, Persia, Greece, and Rome are so obvious, and since prophecy is the surest proof of Scripture (2 Pet. 1:20--21 cf. Isa. 41:22--23, 42:9, 44:7--8, 45:21, 46:9--10, 48:3), the higher critics have tried to "uninspire" Daniel as part of the word of God as quickly as they picked it up. They relegate the date of authorship to some time in the intertestamental period [after]{.class_1925} the events recorded in the book. Of course, that still doesn't explain the prophecies of the Roman Empire, which wasn't a power until 27 B.C. (Manuscripts of Daniel []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw61.xhtml_page_4}have been found in the Dead Sea Scrolls dating to 180 B.C.) Moreover, the testimony and wisdom of Daniel was already well known to the Jews who later were carried into captivity after Daniel 1--2 (see Ezek. 14:14, 28:3).

(The Bible-rejecting, Christ-rejecting Jewish Rabbis make the ["Daniel"]{.class_1939} of Ezek. 14:14 some unknown "pre-Mosaic saint," but this is ludicrous in light of the fact that Noah and Job were prominent, well-known figures in Scripture. Why dredge up a "nobody" whom no one knew simply because you don't like what Daniel wrote? We will get into that in a moment.)

Again, the testimony of Jesus Christ to the authorship of Daniel should be enough for anybody who receives the Bible as the words of God and not man (1 Thess. 2:13), but if you are a lost scholar, bound for Hell, trying to exalt your own authority over that of the Scriptures, then I recommend to you two excellent works on the historicity of Daniel. The first, and arguably the best book on the subject, is by Sir Robert Anderson; it is entitled [Daniel in the Critics' Den.]{.class_1925} The other is by Robert Dick Wilson. He was Professor of Semitic Languages and Old Testament Criticism at Princeton Theological Seminary. He knew 45 different languages. He was not only well-versed in Hebrew, Aramaic, and Greek; he also knew every language into which the Bible had been translated all the way up to A.D. 600. He knew more than any higher critic you can cite on the philology of the Old Testament writings; and he said, "I have come to the conviction that [no man]{.class_1925} knows enough to assail the truthfulness of the Old Testament" (from the Foreward by Philip Howard Sr. to Robert Dick Wilson's work [Is the Higher Criticism Scholarly?]{.class_1925}). His main work on Daniel was [Studies in the Book of Daniel,]{.class_1925} but he also has some good material against higher criticism in [Is the Higher Criticism Scholarly?]{.class_1925} (included in [Which Bible?,]{.class_1925} David Otis Fuller, ed.) and [A Scientific Investigation of the Old Testament.]{.class_1925}

In your [King James]{.class_1925} Bible, Daniel is the last of what are known as the Major Prophets (called "Major" due to their [length,]{.class_1925} not their [content]{.class_1925}). But in the Hebrew Bible, the book has been relegated to the third section, called the "Writings" ([Hagiographa]{.class_1925} in Gk.; [Kethubim]{.class_1925} in Heb.). The Rabbis consider the Writings to be the [least]{.class_1925} authoritative of the three sections of the Old Testament (the other []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw61.xhtml_page_5}two being, in order of importance, the Law and the Prophets), and Daniel has been put in the least of that section.

The reason for this is that the [Talmud]{.class_1925} denied Daniel was a prophet. [Jesus Christ denied the Talmud]{.class_1925} (Mark 13:14), so modern versions, like the [NIV, NASV, RSV,]{.class_1925} and [ESV]{.class_1925} (the so-called "Conservative" version of the [RSV]{.class_1925}), [denied the word of Jesus Christ.]{.class_1925} They drop ["Daniel the prophet"]{.class_1939} from Mark 13:14. The alibi for this, as it is in many other passages, is since you can find it [somewhere else]{.class_1925} in Scripture (in this case, Matt. 24:15), it is perfectly all right to remove it from Mark 13:14. Of course, that destroys the Holy Spirit's establishment of the statement, since, now, there is only [one ]{.class_1925}witness instead of [two]{.class_1925} (2 Cor. 13:1).

The reason the [Talmud]{.class_1925} denies Daniel as a prophet is, supposedly, because he is not called a prophet anywhere in the book. Of course, neither are Hosea, Joel, Amos, Obadiah, Micah, Nahum, Zephaniah, and Malachi; yet every Hebrew Bible includes them in the "Twelve Prophets." In fact, Amos outright says in his book, ["I was no prophet, neither was I a prophet's son"]{.class_1939} (Amos 7:14).

You say, "Yeah, but the Lord told him to prophesy in the next verse" (Amos 7:15). Exactly, and God called what He gave Daniel a ["prophecy"]{.class_1939} (Dan. 9:24). Never mind all the gas about a prophet "forthtelling"; Daniel [foretells]{.class_1925} the future to the "T" under the power of the Holy Spirit (Dan. 4:8--9, 18, 5:11).

Now what is the real reason Jewish [tradition]{.class_1925} (see Mark 7:7--13) denied the prophethood of Daniel? The [Talmud]{.class_1925} had to get rid of Daniel as a prophet and obscure the authority of the book as much as possible because [Daniel gave the exact time the Messiah would show up]{.class_1925}---Daniel 9:24--26. If the Jewish Rabbis acknowledged Daniel as a prophet, they would have to admit that they [missed]{.class_1925} the coming of their Messiah and were responsible for having Him ["cut off"]{.class_1939} (Dan. 9:26).

The book of Daniel has 12 chapters, 357 verses, and 11,602 words. From 1:1--2:3, it is written in Hebrew; from 2:4--7:28, it is written in Aramaic, with a little Chaldean; and from 8:1--12:13, it is written in Hebrew again.

The name [Daniel]{.class_1925} means "my judge is God" or "God is my judge" ([Dan]{.class_1925} meaning "judge" \[Gen. 30:6\], and [El]{.class_1925} being an abbreviation for [Elohim]{.class_1925}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw61.xhtml_page_6 .class-3}---"God"). This is evident throughout the book. God judges between Daniel and his three friends, and the rest of the captives, when it came to eating the King's meat (chap.1); God judges between Daniel and his three buddies, and the magicians, astrologers, sorcerers, etc., when it came to interpreting Nebuchadnezzar's dream (chap. 2); He judges the three Hebrew children faithful when they wouldn't bow the knee to Nebuchadnezzar's image (chap. 3); He judges Nebuchadnezzar and turns him into a beast for his pride (chap. 4); He judges Belshazzar for desecrating the vessels of the Temple in his drunken orgy (chap. 5); He judges between Daniel and the other Presidents and Princes who tried to have Daniel killed out of envy (chap. 6). The book is concluded with visions showing Daniel that the Lord will judge nations, Israel, the Antichrist, and mankind in general (chaps. 7--12).

The typology in the book is another reason, I am sure, that Christ-rejecting Jewish Rabbis have no use for Daniel. You see, in chapter 5, Daniel is a type of the Holy Ghost, the third Person of the Trinity (5:29 cf. Gen. 41:41--44). In chapter 6, Daniel is a type of the Lord Jesus, the second Person of the Trinity.

The matchmeet in the New Testament to Daniel is the book of Revelation. The two books complement each other. They overlap, sustain, and supplement each other time after time. Daniel fills in the gap between the close of the Old Testament canon and the First Coming of Christ. Revelation fills in the gap between the completion of the New Testament and the Second Coming of Christ. Time and again, we will be referring to the book of Revelation in our study of Daniel, especially in chapters 7--12.

One of the best works you can get on Daniel is Clarence Larkin's commentary [The Book of Daniel.]{.class_1925} There is nothing in the works of Salem Kirban, Hal Lindsey, M. R. DeHaan, Charlie Fuller, C. I. Scofield, G. H. Pember, John Walvoord, or the Southwest Radio Church that goes beyond Larkin in 1929. Authors like Kirban and Lindsey may have "best-selling" books, but they got their material from Larkin. For a modern illustration of this, see John Hagee "commissioning" a large wall-chart on dispensational truth to con a lot of TV viewers out of a buck without ever telling them [it was Clarence Larkin's chart,]{.class_1925} copied exactly as you find it in his [Greatest Book on Dispensational Truth.]{.class_1925}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw61.xhtml_page_7 .class-3} That is "the author of 34 major books"---afraid to tell people where he got his material.

So here we begin our study of ["Daniel the prophet."]{.class_1939} We are at ["the time of the end"]{.class_1939} (12:9), right before the ["time of trouble"]{.class_1939} (12:1)---the Tribulation. Daniel's words are no longer ["closed up"]{.class_1939} or ["sealed"]{.class_1939} (12:9) to those of us who have trusted Jesus Christ as our Saviour. We have the same Spirit who indwelt Daniel (4:8, 5:11) living in us to guide us ["into all truth"]{.class_1939} (John 16:13). He has "unsealed" the book for us (Rev. 22:10).

[We shall not rely on our knowledge of Hebrew or Greek to give us any "light" on Daniel's prophecy. As has been our practice throughout the Bible Believer's Commentary Series, we will accept the plain English of the ]{.class_1922}[Authorized Version]{.class_1935}[ of 1611 as the very words of God in our language (1 Thess. 2:13). We will believe them in their context, comparing Scripture with Scripture to get the Author's interpretation (1 Cor. 2:13). Where necessary, we will rightly divide the Book so we will not be ashamed before God in our work of expositing ]{.class_1922}"the scripture of truth"[ (2 Tim. 2:15 cf. Dan. 10:21). And above all, we will not rely on our ]{.class_1922}"own understanding"[ (Prov. 3:5) to tell you what Daniel wrote. We will look to the One who ]{.class_1922}"opened"[ the ]{.class_1922}"understanding"[ of the disciples ]{.class_1922}"that they might understand the scriptures"[ (Luke 24:45).]{.class_1922}

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml}

# Chapter 1 {.heading_67-0}

1:1 In the third year of the reign of Jehoiakim king of Judah came Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon unto Jerusalem, and besieged it.

2 And the Lord gave Jehoiakim king of Judah into his hand, with part of the vessels of the house of God: which he carried into the land of Shinar to the house of his god; and he brought the vessels into the treasure house of his god.

The book of Daniel starts out in the historical context of the last several years of the southern kingdom of Judah. The King of Judah at the time when Daniel was carried into captivity to Babylon was Jehoiakim (vs. 1). Jehoiakim was the second son of the last "good" King of Judah---Josiah (1 Chron. 3:15). His original name was ["Eliakim"]{.class_1922} (2 Kings 23:24; 2 Chron. 36:4).

There is an apparent discrepancy between Daniel 1:1 and Jeremiah 25:1 as to the year of Jehoiakim's reign when Nebuchadnezzar began his reign and began his siege of Jerusalem. Jeremiah 25:1 says ["the fourth year of Jehoiakim"]{.class_1922} was ["the first year of Nebuchadrezzar king of Babylon,"]{.class_1922} while Daniel 1:1 says ["Nebuchadnezzar"]{.class_1922} was ["king of Babylon"]{.class_1922} during ["the third year of the reign of Jehoiakim."]{.class_1922}

Two things are going on here. First, Nebuchadnezzar has a two-year coreign with his father, so it all depends when Jeremiah counts the beginning of Nebuchadnezzar's reign, whether it is [officially or actually]{.class_1921}. The second is that Jehoiakim came to the throne so late in the year that Daniel may not be counting it as part of Jehoikim's reign, while Jeremiah counts part of the year as a full year. Given the possibilities, one could not conclusively prove a contradiction between the two passages if he tried.

Now, trying to line up the events of Jehoiakim's reign as given in 2 Kings 24:1--2; 2 Chronicles 36:5--7; and Daniel 1:1--2 can be difficult, and I am not sure anybody has it completely right. What we know for sure is that Jehoiakim had an eleven-year reign (2 Kings 23:36; 2 Chron. 36:5), and we know that in the third full year of that []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_9}reign, Nebuchadnezzar besieged Jerusalem and took captives and some of the Temple vessels back to Babylon (Dan. 1:1--2).

After that, it becomes "shaky." Some of the commentators make Nebuchadnezzar's attack in 2 Chronicles 36:6--7 the siege of Daniel 1:1--2. If that be the case, then obviously Nebuchadnezzar either brought Jehoiakim back from Babylon and reinstated him as a subservient King until Jehoiakim rebelled three years later (2 Kings 24:1), or he never took him to Babylon as he intended. That is the position taken by both Easton and Smith in their Bible dictionaries. Other expositors have 2 Chronicles 36:6--7 as a second attack of Nebuchadnezzar at the end of the reign of Jehoiakim, in which the King of Judah was assassinated by his own people and his body thrown over the wall before Nebuchadnezzar could haul him off to Babylon (see Jer. 22:18--19, 36:30). We will reserve our judgment in these matters for what we know for sure and leave the speculation to others until the Lord gives us (or someone else) more light from the [Scriptures,]{.class_1921} not secular history or scholars' opinions.

["The land of Shinar"]{.class_1922} (vs. 2) is where the city of Babylon was located; it was founded by Nimrod (Gen. 10:8--10), a type of the Antichrist. It is where the Tower of Babel was built (Gen. 11:2--4). The first time ["war"]{.class_1922} shows up in your Bible, it is connected with ["the king of Shinar"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 14:1--2). And as here in verse 2, it is associated with [idolatry:]{.class_1921} it is connected with the image of the Antichrist during the Tribulation (see our comments on Zech. 5:11 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Minor Prophets,]{.class_1921} Vol. II).

3 And the king spake unto Ashpenaz the master of his eunuchs, that he should bring certain of the children of Israel, and of the king's seed, and of the princes;

4 Children in whom was no blemish, but well favoured, and skilful in all wisdom, and cunning in knowledge, and understanding science, and such as had ability in them to stand in the king's palace, and whom they might teach the learning and the tongue of the Chaldeans.

5 And the king appointed them a daily provision of the king's meat, and of the wine which he drank: so nourishing them three years, that at the end thereof they might stand []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_10}before the king.

6 Now among these were of the children of Judah, Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah:

7 Unto whom the prince of the eunuchs gave names: for he gave unto Daniel the name of Belteshazzar; and to Hananiah, of Shadrach; and to Mishael, of Meshach; and to Azariah, of Abednego.

Verse 3 is a fulfillment of 2 Kings 20:17--18 and Isaiah 39:7. In those passages, Hezekiah had gotten his prayer answered for God to heal him and spare his life for fifteen more years (2 Kings 20:6), and Hezekiah was feeling pretty good about himself (2 Chron. 32:25). About that time, some ambassadors from the King of Babylon showed up with a "get well card" (2 Kings 20:12), and Hezekiah "showed off" in front of them. He gave them a tour of his house and made sure they saw all his gold, silver, jewels, etc., so they would know just how rich and powerful he was.

After the ambassadors left, the Lord came to Hezekiah and said, "What have you done? Didn't you see those guys taking notes? One of these days when the King of Babylon needs an 'additional source of revenue' \[I believe that's what the President and Congress call it when they want to take more of your money to spend themselves\], he's going to come in here and take everything you've got, including your sons. He's going to take them and make them eunuchs in his palace."

And that's exactly what happens here in verse 3. Look at the end of the verse: ["of the king's seed, and of the princes."]{.class_1922} That's two separate groups there. The first is the sons of the Kings of Judah, the heirs to the throne. The second is the children of the chief rulers. That word [Prince]{.class_1921} in the Bible doesn't mean "the son of a monarch," as it does today. There were Princes in Israel long before there was any King (see Num. 7): they were the heads of the twelve tribes. So that word [Prince]{.class_1921} is a reference to a [ruler]{.class_1921} (Exod. 2:14 cf. Acts 7:27). So what you have here is Daniel being in the [royal]{.class_1921} line of Judah, and his three buddies being in the line of "nobility."

They are turned over to ["the master of the eunuchs,"]{.class_1922} which means they were made eunuchs themselves, just as the Lord told []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_11}Hezekiah. A eunuch is a man that cannot have children. Jesus said some eunuchs are born that way---they have a physical defect that prevents them from having children; some eunuchs refrain from getting married and having children ["for the kingdom of heaven's sake"]{.class_1922}; and some eunuchs are ["made eunuchs of men"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 19:12). That is what happens here. These boys are castrated as a sign of their subjection and servitude to their conquerors, and to prevent them from violating the King's harem.

Notice, in verse 4, the qualifications for these eunuchs Ashpenaz was to pick for training: ["no blemish"]{.class_1922}---no acne, no scars, no physical flaws or deformities (cf. Lev. 21:18--21). ["Well favoured"]{.class_1922}---good looking, healthy, likeable. ["Skilful in all wisdom"]{.class_1922}---they knew how to put their knowledge to good use. ["Cunning in knowledge"]{.class_1922}---they knew a lot in many fields of study; we would call them today "Renaissance men."

["Understanding science."]{.class_1922} There is nothing new about science. The Babylonians were skilled in mathematics long before Pythagoras came up with his "theorem." They developed astronomy and could accurately measure a solar year to within four minutes, thirty seconds. In medicine, they introduced diagnosis and prognosis, as well as prescription medications.

Of course, Babylonian science was mixed with a lot of superstitious nonsense, just as modern science is today (modern science believes life arose through[ spontaneous generation;]{.class_1921} you can't get more superstitious or ridiculous than that), but the ancients weren't ignorant Neanderthals and savages. Modern science and technology can't reproduce the Egyptians' methods of preserving a body or building a pyramid with such precision as the Great Pyramid in Giza. The idea that the ancients were stupid but we are smart comes from the concept of evolution---things are progressing upwards and forwards.

To the contrary, things are getting worse. Just because you have advances in transportation and communication doesn't mean you have the sense of a bunch of heathen in Mesopotamia. When Adam and Eve walked out of the garden of Eden, they had nothing but the clothes God put on them. From that, they and their descendants, within six generations, were able to develop agriculture, husbandry, architecture, music, and metallurgy---FROM SCRATCH. Are []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_12}[you]{.class_1921} smart enough to do that? They were.

And they lived long enough to learn and become proficient at all kinds of things. Adam lived 930 years. Think of everything men accomplish now with only seventy years; now multiply it by twelve or thirteen. That's how long those people before the Flood had, individually, to learn and build a civilization. And that doesn't even take into account the knowledge they gained from ["the sons of God"]{.class_1922} in Genesis 6.

It is important to note that verse 4 is one of only two places in the [Authorized Version]{.class_1921} where the word ["science"]{.class_1922} is found. The new "Bibles" get rid of ["science"]{.class_1922} in both places: first, so you won't beware of it as you are commanded in 1 Timothy 6:20, and second, so you won't associate ["science"]{.class_1922} with the idolatrous Babylonian system.

Back to Daniel 1:4---["Such as had ability in them to stand in the king's palace."]{.class_1922} Proverbs 22:29 says, ["Seest thou a man diligent in his business? he shall stand before kings; he shall not stand before mean men ]{.class_1922}\[as in "lowlifes"\][."]{.class_1922} So Daniel and his companions were hard workers; they weren't slackards.

["And whom they might teach the learning and tongue of the Chaldeans."]{.class_1922} And now we come to the real purpose of the training. Nebuchadnezzar wants to take these Jewish young men and erase all their roots so they would be completely displaced and transplanted. He is going to try to turn them into Chaldeans.

He intends to change what they [learn.]{.class_1921} Those Jews were to be taught the Scriptures from the time they were children (Deut. 6:7; 2 Tim. 3:15) so they would learn to fear the Lord and obey Him (Deut. 4:10, 31:12). Nebuchadnezzar intends to send them off to public school to learn evolution, philosophy, hedonism, and Marxism.

He intends to change their [language.]{.class_1921} They won't be speaking Hebrew anymore; they'll be speaking Chaldean. You don't teach the kiddies how to read so they can read the Bible, like your forefathers intended. You teach them to read just enough to program them with magazines, newspapers, and a bunch of pornographic stuff. You remove the language of the Bible from their speech as much as possible with 323 (plus!) different versions so they don't know what []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_13}it says. You pump their eyes and ears full of stuff about sex, liquor, drugs, cussing, perversion, and generally living like hell, through radio and television, until they talk and act like the stuff they see and hear.

He changes their [diet.]{.class_1921} Here in verse 5, they are to eat what the King eats and drink what he drinks. In modern application, you take the kids off Bible reading and prayer, and put them on a steady diet of radio, television, computers, magazines, trashy books, rock music, movies, etc., to change their appetite away from spiritual things.

And finally, he changes their [names.]{.class_1921} That breaks the ties of family. Those boys, up to this point, had been born and raised as ["Daniel"]{.class_1922} ("God is my judge"), ["Hananiah"]{.class_1922} ("Jehovah has given"), ["Mishael"]{.class_1922} ("Who is like God!"), and ["Azariah"]{.class_1922} ("Whom Jehovah helps") (vs. 6). Their parents had given them those names to remind them [the Lord was their God.]{.class_1921}

Now Nebuchadnezzar changed their names to ["Belteshazzar"]{.class_1922} ("Beltis protect the King"), ["Shadrach"]{.class_1922} ("Aku's command"), ["Meshach"]{.class_1922} ("Who is like Aku!"), and ["Abednego"]{.class_1922} ("Servant of Nebo"). Beltis, Aku, and Nebo were different gods of the Babylonians. So in changing their names, Nebuchadnezzar was also changing their [religion.]{.class_1921} You get rid of Jesus Christ and the Bible, and substitute for them Elvis Presley, Barack Obama, Hillary Clinton, Madonna, Michael Jackson, Miley Cyrus, LeBron James, "J Lo," Robin Williams, Chris Rock, et al. The heroes and "role models" for teenagers these days aren't Statesmen, inventors, doctors, or preachers; they are actors, rock musicians, athletes, and dirty comedians who live like the devil and have the morals of an alley cat. The kids learn to please and serve [self]{.class_1921} instead of the God who made them.

8 But Daniel purposed in his heart that he would not defile himself with the portion of the king's meat, nor with the wine which he drank: therefore he requested of the prince of the eunuchs that he might not defile himself.

The verse is a great text for preaching to teenagers. It shows []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_14}nonconformity to the world.

["And be not conformed to this world: but be ye transformed by the renewing of your mind, that ye may prove what is that good, and acceptable, and perfect, will of God"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 12:2).

There may have been some things Daniel was forced to do on the outside to ["be subject unto the higher powers"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 13:1), but in his heart, he never submitted. The learning of the Chaldeans may have been forced on him, but when he could, he got a copy of the Scriptures and read and studied it (see 9:2). He may have had to learn and speak Chaldean before the King, but he never lost the ability to read and write his native tongue (see remarks on the languages in which Daniel was written in the Introduction). When operating in an official capacity (as in chaps. 3 and 4), they may have gone by their Babylonian names, but when by themselves, they still went by their Hebrew names (see 2:17).

Here, Daniel has to take a public stand because of his public testimony. You see, there is something wrong with the meat. Of course, there is always the chance that Nebuchadnezzar was enjoying some country ham, hickory-smoked bacon, rabbit stew, bratwurst, pork chops, lobster thermidor, fried shrimp and scallops, and raw oysters. Those were forbidden under the Mosaic Law (see Lev. 11). As a Jew, Daniel would have been defiled had he eaten them.

But far more likely is that the meat had been [offered to idols.]{.class_1921} Like most heathen, Nebuchadnezzar was a very religious man. His false gods have already shown up in Daniel twice within the first seven verses. It was the practice of pagan idolaters, before they ate their food, to offer it to the gods.

Paul deals with this for the New Testament believer in 1 Corinthians 8 and 10. The fact is, an idol, in and of itself, is [nothing]{.class_1921} (1 Cor. 8:4). It can't see what you've prepared, it can't smell the food, it can't taste it, and it can't walk over to the plate and lift it up to its mouth (Psa. 115:4--8).

But the idol represents a devil (1 Cor. 10:19--20). While a thing sacrificed to an idol may not mean anything to you as a Christian, it does to the lost person making the offering. Moreover, it might []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_15}offend a Christian who has not grown enough in the Lord to realize his liberty in Christ. So the rule of thumb is, don't be a stumblingblock to a young Christian or an unbeliever.

The Christian was allowed to buy and eat any meat he wanted, but if he didn't want to violate his conscience or someone else's, he wasn't to inquire as from where it came (1 Cor. 10:25--26). If he were invited over to someone's house for dinner, he could eat what was set before him without asking questions about its source (1 Cor. 10:27). But the minute his host said, "You like that cut of meat there? Well, I got it for a good price because it was marked down after it had been offered to Diana (or Jupiter or whatever)," then he was to push it away and say, "No thank you." Why? For testimony's sake. That way no one could associate him with the idolatry behind the meat.

Now just in case you think that principle is antiquated, do you realize that the Moslems have talked one meat company that sells turkeys for Thanksgiving to raise and slaughter their turkeys in accordance with Koranic law (known as "halal meat"). When the turkeys are killed, the blessing of "Allah" is invoked on the meat. You are right back in the setting of 1 Corinthians 8, 10. Instead of the idol being one of wood, stone, or metal, it is one of the heart. There is nothing wrong with eating such meat at all, [unless it ruins your testimony before unsaved Moslems]{.class_1921} or some weak Christian looking to see what you will do.

Daniel knows the guy in charge of the eunuchs knows him and is looking at him and judging the worshipers of the true God by what Daniel does. It's the old excuse: "Well, So-and-so does it, and he's a Christian, so it must be all right." Christian, it might not be "fair," but it certainly is so: you are the best Christian someone knows, and that person is judging Christianity and the Bible by [you.]{.class_1921}

Daniel makes up his mind to do right, and when he does, his buddies follow suit. If he hadn't done right, there is a good chance they wouldn't have done right either. They looked up to Daniel and followed him.

And that brings up another issue. Someone is following you, Christian. If you do what is right, so will that person, because he is looking up to you. You say, "Oh no, Dr. Ruckman, not me." Yes, [you.]{.class_1921} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_16}It may be a son or daughter; it may be a husband or wife; it may be a friend or co-worker. It may only be one person, but I guarantee, you are someone's "idol." If you follow God, that person will too, and if you don't, he won't.

I have seen that in my own life as an unsaved young man and later on in my ministry. Before I was saved and before I went into ROTC and OCS to get my commission in the Army, I had me a gang of "hoodlums" (that's what my dad called them, and he was right). We were going to catch a banana boat out of New Orleans and run away to South America. My dad got wind of it and had me "front and center" to talk to me about it the night we were getting ready to leave. He had worked in the oil fields down in South America and knew the disaster into which we were headed. Since he was third-generation military, he laid out my situation like this:

"Pete, if you knew that you were about to lead your troops into a certain massacre, and you knew that it was unnecessary, and you didn't have to take them in, would you give the order? Would you take them in anyway to attack an objective where you knew you would lose every one of them?"

"No sir," I said.

He went on and said, "Son, those boys are going to follow you anywhere. To them, you are a General. They would obey you before they would obey their own parents. And you are going to take them to certain ruin. They are going to follow you to their ruin and probably an early death."

With that, I was dismissed. I went down to the drugstore where the others were waiting on me and called the whole thing off.

Later on, after I was saved and had entered the ministry, I was preaching in a jail where two teenage girls were being held on a morals charge. I had my drawing board set up and was drawing a picture of the Crucifixion. The older of the two girls paid attention intently, and the tears just streamed down her face as I drew the blood running down Christ for our sins. I don't believe the younger of the two girls looked at me one time during the whole sermon. The whole time she was looking at that other girl to see what she would do.

When I gave the invitation and asked those girls if they would, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_17}the best way they knew how, trust Jesus Christ as their Saviour, that older girl, still crying, shook her head yes. When that younger girl saw that, she turned to me for the first time, and with a big smile on her face, she shook her head yes too. Do you know what would have happened if that older girl had rejected Christ? She would have dropkicked that younger girl into Hell just as sure as you are reading this page. That younger girl was going to do whatever that older girl did.

Let that be a lesson to you, Christian. Someone is looking to you as an example. Don't be the wrong kind.

9 Now God had brought Daniel into favour and tender love with the prince of the eunuchs.

10 And the prince of the eunuchs said unto Daniel, I fear my lord the king, who hath appointed your meat and your drink: for why should he see your faces worse liking than the children which are of your sort? then shall ye make me endanger my head to the king.

11 Then said Daniel to Melzar, whom the prince of the eunuchs had set over Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah,

12 Prove thy servants, I beseech thee, ten days; and let them give us pulse to eat, and water to drink.

13 Then let our countenances be looked upon before thee, and the countenance of the children that eat of the portion of the king's meat: and as thou seest, deal with thy servants.

14 So he consented to them in this matter, and proved them ten days.

15 And at the end of ten days their countenances appeared fairer and fatter in flesh than all the children which did eat the portion of the king's meat.

16 Thus Melzar took away the portion of their meat, and the wine that they should drink; and gave them pulse.

Now, Daniel has been taken captive, and he's far away from his home. He has been mutilated and enslaved. But the Lord was still Daniel's God, and []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_18}["God had brought Daniel into favor and tender love with the prince of the eunuchs."]{.class_1922} It is just like when Joseph was thrown into prison in Egypt: ["the LORD was with Joseph, and shewed him mercy, and gave him favour in the sight of the keeper of the prison"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 39:21).

Verse 9 is one of the places in Scripture the sodomites use to try to justify their filthy perversion. They see ["tender love,"]{.class_1922} and because their minds are fixated on one thing, they figure Ashpenaz fornicated with Daniel. Of course, they twist the Hebrew to prove their point, but as we have pointed out many times in this series of commentaries, if a man has to resort to Greek or Hebrew to prove a point, he is trying to foist something that [isn't so]{.class_1921} on you. Anything that is so in that Book can be proven by Scripture with Scripture without having to go to the Hebrew or Greek.

The Hebrew word in question here is [racham]{.class_1921} (translated ["tender love"]{.class_1922} in the [AV]{.class_1921}). It is translated ["tender mercies"]{.class_1922} in the Psalms (e.g., Psa. 25:6, 40:11, 69:16, 77:9). One of its meanings is "compassion." This is not some older sex pervert seducing and molesting a teenager under his charge, like some Catholic Priest. This is God answering Solomon's prayer in 1 Kings 8:50.

["And forgive thy people that have sinned against thee, and all their transgressions wherein they have transgressed against thee, and give them COMPASSION]{.class_1922} \[[racham]{.class_1921}\][ before them who have carried them captive, that they may have COMPASSION]{.class_1922} \[[racham]{.class_1921}\] [on them."]{.class_1922}

The ["tender love"]{.class_1922} Ashpenaz showed Daniel was not two sex perverts fornicating. It was a captor showing mercy and compassion on his captive; in this case, because God moved the heart of the captor to look favorably on his captive.

Now Daniel has gone to his benefactor and asked to be excused from the diet on which the King had put all the trainees (vs. 8). The problem is, Ashpenaz is scared to death of Nebuchadnezzar, and for good reason. Nebuchadnezzar was one of those Oriental monarchs with absolute power of life and death: ["whom he would he slew; and whom he would he kept alive"]{.class_1922} (5:19). And he had the temper to make heads roll "at the drop of a hat" (2:12--13, 3:13--19). Ashpenaz figures that if Daniel doesn't eat what everyone else is []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_19}eating that he will turn out scrawny, sickly, and puny at the end of the testing period, and then the one in charge (Ashpenaz!) was going to lose his head---literally.

While Ashpenaz himself does not agree to Daniel's request, Daniel makes a deal with his "handler" (the man Ashpenaz had set over Daniel and his three friends to train them), ["Melzar"]{.class_1922} (vs. 11). The deal was to give the boys a "test" for ten days. For ten days, the four Hebrews would eat and drink nothing but ["pulse"]{.class_1922} and water (vs. 12), and at the end of ten days, if they didn't look as healthy or better than all the other trainees, they would take whatever Melzar decided to put on them. (They actually never did agree to defile themselves with the King's meat and wine; all they agreed to was to leave it up to Melzar on how to deal with them.)

Now the word ["pulse"]{.class_1922} is one of those archaic words in the [King James Version]{.class_1921} the translators, editors, revisers, and publishers of the modern translations use as an excuse for mutilating your Bible. There are only about 100 archaic words in a [King James]{.class_1921} Bible, and of that hundred all but about 20--25 can be understood by the context or guessed at correctly. You mean to tell me you have to make 36,000 ([NASV]{.class_1921}) to 64,000 ([NIV]{.class_1921}) changes in the Bible based on 25 words that have to be looked up in a dictionary? You mean defining those words in the margin wouldn't help you understand the text just as well as retranslating the whole thing?

The excuse these incredible hypocrites use to justify changing your Bible is that no major doctrine is affected. Well, is any major doctrine affected if you [don't]{.class_1921} change it? Then why not leave it alone?

["Pulse"]{.class_1922} is a word used of vegetables in general, but more specifically, it is "the edible seeds of leguminous plants." Those are any kind of beans or peas. They're also called "lentiles" in Genesis 25:34 and 2 Samuel 23:11. You can see the connection between all three words (["beans," "lentiles,"]{.class_1922} and ["pulse"]{.class_1922}) in 2 Samuel 17:28.

Verse 12 is the first indication in the book of Daniel that it is connected to the book of Revelation. In verse 12, Daniel and his buddies are going on a ten-day trial. Over in Revelation 2:10, somebody is going to be cast into prison and tried ["ten days."]{.class_1922}

Ten, of course, is the number of the Gentiles. Noah, the father of the Gentiles, was the tenth from Adam. The Gentile nations are first []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_20}recorded in Genesis 10. The first Gentile convert in the New Testament who wasn't a Jewish proselyte is in Acts 10. Romans 10 deals with taking the Gospel to the Gentiles. So what you have here in verses 12--15 is a Jew being put on trial by the Gentiles as a testimony to them. That is something else the Rabbis don't like about Daniel. He wasn't a prophet to Israel; he was a prophet to the [Gentiles]{.class_1921}. That's what sent the Jews into spasms in Luke 4:24--29 and Acts 22:21--23 (see our comments on those passages in their respective Commentaries). The Jews can't stand the thought of God dumping them for their sins and dealing with the Gentiles. That is the state in which they are right now, but it is changing (read Rom. 11). Right now, just before the Rapture of the Church, the Lord is in the process of dumping the Gentiles in order to deal once more with His people, the Jews.

Now Daniel and his three friends go on a trial diet of pulse and water for ten days, and at the end of that period, they look healthier and have more "meat" on their cheeks than all the other trainees who had been eating the food assigned them by Nebuchadnezzar (vs. 15). So Melzar let them eat pulse and drink water for the full three-year training period (see vs. 5).

Because of that, there is a new fad going around Christian circles called the "Daniel diet" (sometimes called the "Daniel fast"). The idea is if you eat what Daniel ate here in verses 12--16, you will get the results Daniel got in health and weight loss.

While I agree that we all need to eat healthier and have more vegetables in our diets, that has nothing to do with the text. Daniel wasn't trying to eat healthier or lose weight or "detox" his system. He wasn't "taking on a challenge to show the value of a natural diet." And he wasn't on it for only ten days (as the Daniel diet does); he was on his diet for [three years.]{.class_1921} The reason Daniel and his companions did that was not to defile themselves under the Mosaic Law with either "unclean meats" or food sacrificed to idols. If they had been back home in Israel, their diet would have included beef, lamb, goat, and fish; not just vegetables. The reason the "diet" worked was because God blessed those Jewish boys for doing right. Somebody is just trying to make a quick buck off some overweight Christians.

Before moving on, notice the phrase ["the end"]{.class_1922} in verse 15. It []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_21}was in verse 5, and it shows up again in verse 18. That is not coincidence or accidental. That phrase shows up six times in the last chapter of the book (12:4, 6, 8, 9, 13 \[twice\]). It is a reference to the end times before the Lord comes back. So right in the first chapter, God gives you a warning that Daniel deals with more than just the period of the Maccabees before Matthew. The book deals with events clear up to the end of the Tribulation.

17  As for these four children, God gave them knowledge and skill in all learning and wisdom: and Daniel had understanding in all visions and dreams.

18 Now at the end of the days that the king had said he should bring them in, then the prince of the eunuchs brought them in before Nebuchadnezzar.

19 And the king communed with them; and among them all was found none like Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah: therefore stood they before the king.

20 And in all matters of wisdom and understanding, that the king enquired of them, he found them ten times better than all the magicians and astrologers that were in all his realm.

21 And Daniel continued even unto the first year of king Cyrus.

Notice in verse 17, it is God who gives ["knowledge and skill in all learning and wisdom."]{.class_1922} I talked with an Ensign in the Navy one time who fancied himself an intellectual. He was too smart for his own good and was sure I was an "Elmer Gantry." He didn't believe in God or the Bible, so I was getting nowhere with him. Finally, I asked him three questions with the promise he would answer them honestly and then ask me the same three questions.

I asked him, "Do you consider yourself to have a good mind?" "Yes," he said emphatically with no false humility. "Where did you get it from?" I asked. "It came with the equipment," he said sarcastically. Finally, I asked him, "And how long will you have it?" "For the rest of my life," he replied.

Then I made him ask me the same questions. "Do you have a []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_22}good mind?" "Yes, as a matter of fact, I do," I replied. "Where did you get it from?" "God gave it to me," I said; and then before he could ask the last question, I said, "And He could take it away tonight and leave me a raving lunatic."

That Ensign got as white as a sheet, excused himself, and got out of there as quickly as he could. I found out later he had been seeing a psychiatrist for mental problems; he was about to lose his mind. God gives a man whatever intellect, wisdom, and understanding he has, and God can take it away as quickly as He gives it (see chap. 4 here in Daniel).

God gave Daniel such wisdom and understanding that twenty years later, under the inspiration of the Holy Ghost, Ezekiel compared him second only to the Devil (Ezek. 28:3). The first time I ever opened a Bible was to that verse. I had stolen a Bible from a flophouse and brought it back to my room. I came in drunk and opened that Bible, not even knowing where to turn. I was 27 years old, with a College education, and had never read the Bible. I wouldn't have been able to turn to the Gospel of John without looking it up in the index.

I opened up that Bible and put my finger down on Ezekiel 28:3. I figured if that Book were more than any other kind of book, it would speak to me personally. Boy, was I in for a surprise! I read, ["Behold, thou art wiser than Daniel; there is no secret that they can hide from thee."]{.class_1922}

That hit me like a jackhammer. I claimed to be intellectual and searching for the truth; at one point, I even had plans to go to Tibet and the Himalayas to find the hidden wisdom of the Lamas (["Lost Horizon,"]{.class_1921} "Shangri-La"; that sort of thing, you know). I read down to verse 10 there in Ezekiel 28 where it said, ["Thou shall die the deaths of the uncircumcised by the hand of strangers: for I have spoken it, saith the Lord GOD."]{.class_1922}

I got so scared that I threw that Bible across the room. Wisdom does not guarantee morality or obedience to God; Solomon is a good example of that. Satan has more knowledge and wisdom than the smartest person you know, and he's headed for the Lake of Fire.

That is why no Christian should put his faith in science, even [true science.]{.class_1921} All science is, is a collation of facts based on observation and experimentation; it is [not truth.]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_23} The Devil knows more facts about the universe than the National Academy of Sciences will ever know, and he is still ["a liar, and the father of it"]{.class_1922} (John 8:44). Truth is to be found in [God's Son]{.class_1921} (John 14:6), [God's Book]{.class_1921} (John 17:17), and [God's Spirit]{.class_1921} (1 John 5:6).

Back to verse 17: ["Daniel had understanding in all visions and dreams."]{.class_1922} Here is another way in which Daniel is like Joseph (cf. Gen. 41:14--15). The verse should be a "red flag" to the Jewish Rabbis who disclaim the prophethood of Daniel. God said back in the Old Testament that He made Himself known to His prophets through visions and spoke to them in dreams (Num. 12:6).

Now, when the three-year training period is over, all the captives who were put through the program are brought before Nebuchadnezzar and "grilled." Not only did ["Daniel, Haniah, Mishael, and Azariah"]{.class_1922} stand out among the other captives (vs. 19), they stood out among ["ALL the magicians and astrologers that were in ALL his realm"]{.class_1922} (vs. 20). The implication of verse 19 is that after Nebuchadnezzar got through quizzing all the captives who had been trained, he sent the rest out and kept the four Hebrew boys and continued to talk to them.

Again, in verse 20, the Gentile number ["ten"]{.class_1922} shows up. Among these Gentile ["magicians and astrologers,"]{.class_1922} the Lord elevates four Jews, with Daniel as the best of the four.

["Magicians"]{.class_1922} use incantations and charms to gain "supernatural power"; the "power" coming from Satan and devils, not God. These ["magicians"]{.class_1922} aren't the illusionists you see on stage, like Houdini, Blackstone, Copperfield, et al. Those are performers using illusion and misdirection to pull off their tricks.

["Astrologers"]{.class_1922} predict the future from the planets and stars. It is not the science of astronomy. Astronomy means "the law of the stars"; i.e., the celestial bodies operate by physical laws set up by God. Astrology means "the knowledge of the stars"; it is knowledge gained through [occult]{.class_1921} means. Real magic and astrology were forbidden by God in the Law (Deut. 18:10--11); they were moral abominations (Deut. 18:12), just like sex perversion (Lev. 18:22).

["And Daniel continued even unto the first year of king Cyrus"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21). Daniel serves as a right-hand man to the ruler of []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw91.xhtml_page_24}Babylon from Nebuchadnezzar all the way through to the reign of Cyrus in the Persian Empire. So one decision Daniel made as a teenager put him on top for the rest of his life. You might not obtain the political position God gave Daniel, but if you want God's blessings in your life, you will get right young and stay right.

Before closing the chapter, I want to give you the spiritual lessons from it.

1\) [An ordinary meal can afford an opportunity to witness]{.class_1921} (vss. 8--14). A meal isn't a sermon or an evangelistic crusade, but it gave Daniel the chance to be a testimony. The most common occurrences of life---a flat tire, a wrong number, picking up the dry cleaning---can be opportunities to witness for Jesus Christ.

2\) [As a man]{.class_1921} ["thinketh in his heart, so is he"]{.class_1922} (vs. 8 cf. Prov. 23:7). The decisions a man makes in his heart, the seat of his affections, are eventually carried out.

["A good man out of the good treasure of his heart bringeth forth that which is good; and an evil man out of the evil treasure of his heart bringeth forth that which is evil; for of the abundance of the heart his mouth speaketh"]{.class_1922} (Luke 6:45).

That is why the Christian is commanded:[ "Set your AFFECTION]{.class_1922} \[the things you [love;]{.class_1921} not ["your minds"]{.class_1921} as perversions of Scripture like the [ESV]{.class_1921} read\] [on things above, not on things on the earth"]{.class_1922} (Col. 3:2).

The measure of a man is not his intellect. Some of the smartest men have been some of the most wicked. The measure of a man is what he [loves]{.class_1921} and what he [fears.]{.class_1921} If the Lord controls those two things in you, He controls [you.]{.class_1921} Those are matters of the [heart,]{.class_1921} not the mind.

3\) ["Let no man despise thy youth; but be thou an example of the believers"]{.class_1922} (vs. 10 cf. 1 Tim. 4:12). Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah were in their late teens here in chapter 1; but they still were determined to stay clean and serve God.

4\) [Human opposition can be overcome, and it is often overcome by humility and kind solicitation. ]{.class_1921}The Christian is going to face opposition in this world. It's all through the New Testament.

["Woe unto the world because of offences! for it must needs be that offences come"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 18:7).

["In the world ye shall have tribulation: but be of good cheer; I have overcome the world"]{.class_1922} (John 16:23).

["Confirming the souls of the disciples, and exhorting them to continue in the faith, and that we must through much tribulation enter into the kingdom of God"]{.class_1922} (Acts 14:22).

["For verily, when we were with you, we told you before that we should suffer tribulation; even as it came to pass, and ye know"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 3:4).

["Yea, and all that will live godly in Christ Jesus shall suffer persecution"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 3:12).

So there is no doubt about it: you [will]{.class_1921} face opposition. When you do, don't be too quick to give up and throw in the towel. The first thing you should do is pray about it. If you have to take a stand, do so in kindness and humility. Daniel wasn't obnoxious about not eating the King's meat. He asked politely; he was humble; he was reasonable. There are times to get rough, but don't go around with a chip on your shoulder daring anybody to knock it off.

5\) [God will take care of those who take care of Him. ]{.class_1921}Daniel took care of the Lord's business, and the Lord took care of Daniel. The Lord Jesus put it this way:

["For whosoever will save his life shall lose it; but whosoever shall lose his life for my sake and the gospel's, the same shall save it"]{.class_1922} (Mark 8:35).

Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "God will put the angels on half rations to feed a soulwinner." If you spend your life doing what God wants you to do and trying to win souls, the Lord will make sure you are fed and clothed and the bills are paid. That doesn't mean you will necessarily be healthy and wealthy like the "prosperity gospel" boys preach. It does mean ["my God shall supply all your need ]{.class_1922}\[not all your [greed]{.class_1921}\][ according to his riches in glory by Christ Jesus"]{.class_1922} (Phil. 4:19).

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml}

# Chapter 2 {.heading_67-0}

Now we come to one of the greatest chapters in the Bible. While all the Bible is the word of God, some chapters are more "loaded" than others. Daniel chapter 2 is salient for understanding God's plan in history. As a matter of fact, what one does with Daniel 2 will determine whether he is Premillennial, Postmillennial, or Amillennial. Although we have thoroughly covered this in our prefatory remarks to Revelation 1 in that Commentary, here we give you some basic definitions for understanding about what we are to cover in Daniel 2.

1\. [Millennium]{.class_1921}---The 1,000-year reign of Jesus Christ on this earth. Although the word [Millennium]{.class_1921} never appears in the Scripture, the thousand-year reign of Jesus Christ does---six times in Revelation 20 (Rev. 20:2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7). [Millennium]{.class_1921} is from two Latin words: [mil]{.class_1921}---thousand; [anum---]{.class_1921}year.

2\. [Premillennial---]{.class_1921}Jesus Christ returns [before]{.class_1921} His thousand-year reign here on earth.

3\. [Postmillennial---]{.class_1921}Jesus Christ returns to reign on earth [after]{.class_1921} mankind (or the Church) has ushered in a thousand years of peace and prosperity.

4\. [Amillennial---]{.class_1921}There is no literal thousand-year reign of Jesus Christ on earth. He [spiritually]{.class_1921} reigns in the hearts of Christians. Usually, [theological Amillennialists]{.class_1921} are [practical Postmillennialists:]{.class_1921} they are still trying to "spread the kingdom."

Every person on this earth, saved or lost, takes one of these three positions on Christ's kingdom: Christ will bring in His kingdom; man will bring in the kingdom; there will be no kingdom. Practically speaking, though, it really comes down to Premillennialism and Postmillennialism. Every politician, evolutionist, and philosopher (and most religious leaders) on this earth are, and have been, trying to bring in the kingdom without the King. Of course, it goes by many different names: progress, the New Deal, the War on Poverty, utopia, "the war to end all wars," Marxism, Socialism, redistribution of wealth, civil rights, women's lib, "gay" liberation, integration, Obamacare, "making the world a better place to live in," the Third []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_27}Reich, "peace in our time," etc. In the end, though, they are all merely attempts of the prodigal to renovate the hog pen. As we are about to see, mankind's destiny, without the King, is not "upward and onward"; it's [downward and backward.]{.class_1921}

2:1 And in the second year of the reign of Nebuchadnezzar Nebuchadnezzar dreamed dreams, wherewith his spirit was troubled, and his sleep brake from him.

2 Then the king commanded to call the magicians, and the astrologers, and the sorcerers, and the Chaldeans, for to shew the king his dreams. So they came and stood before the king.

Once again we run into the differences in the reigns of Kings which we discussed back under 1:1. Jeremiah 25:1 is obviously calculating from the beginning of Nebuchadnezzar's two-year coreign with his father, while Daniel 2:1 is calculating from the beginning of Nebuchadnezzar's solo reign. This is the fourth year of Daniel's captivity, after the three-year probationary period of chapter 1.

["Nebuchadnezzar dreamed dreams"]{.class_1922} (vs. 1). Here is God revealing something to a lost heathen ruler just as He did in Genesis 20:3 and 41:1--7. The question often arises: "What about the heathen who've never heard?" This is one of those passages that shows you the heathen know more than you think they know. Back in the Old Testament, God would reveal things to men in dreams (Job 33:15--17). Even today, there are testimonies from the Moslem world where God uses dreams to point lost Moslems to the Bible and Jesus Christ for salvation.

Here, God sends Nebuchadnezzar a nightmare that wakes him out of sleep, like He did with Pharaoh back in Genesis 41:4, 7. It happens to him again over in 4:5. The Lord does this for three reasons: 1) to warn the ruler of what God is going to do, 2) to repudiate the false diviners, and 3) to validate the prophet in whom God put His spirit. That was the case with Pharaoh and Joseph in Genesis 41, and that is the case with Nebuchadnezzar and Daniel here.

Now, Nebuchadnezzar called in those magicians and astrologers whom Daniel and his buddies "upstaged" back in 1:20 (see our comments on the verse). But he also called in two other groups: ["the sorcerers, and the Chaldeans"]{.class_1922} (vs. 2). Sorcery, in the New Testament, involves the use of drugs and potions to practice magic (the Greek word being [pharmakeia]{.class_1921} from where we get our word [pharmacy]{.class_1921}). ["The Chaldeans"]{.class_1922} were the highly educated class (see 1:4); they were the "wise men" of the Chaldean people, the "cream of the crop" intellectually.

These are the ones who were supposed to be able to interpret dreams for the King. But notice, Nebuchadnezzar wants more than just the interpretation; he wants the dream itself---["for to shew the king HIS DREAMS"]{.class_1922} (vs. 2). That is what is coming up in verses 5--6.

3 And the king said unto them, I have dreamed a dream, and my spirit was troubled to know the dream.

4 Then spake the Chaldeans to the king in Syriack, O king, live for ever: tell thy servants the dream, and we will shew the interpretation.

5 The king answered and said to the Chaldeans, The thing is gone from me: if ye will not make known unto me the dream, with the interpretation thereof, ye shall be cut in pieces, and your houses shall be made a dunghill.

6 But if ye shew the dream, and the interpretation thereof, ye shall receive of me gifts and rewards and great honour: therefore shew me the dream, and the interpretation thereof.

7 They answered again and said, Let the king tell his servants the dream, and we will shew the interpretation of it.

8 The king answered and said, I know of certainty that ye would gain the time, because ye see the thing is gone from me.

9 But if ye will not make known unto me the dream, there is but one decree for you: for ye have prepared lying and corrupt words to speak before me, till the time be []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_29}changed: therefore tell me the dream, and I shall know that ye can shew me the interpretation thereof.

10 The Chaldeans answered before the king, and said, There is not a man upon the earth that can shew the king's matter: therefore there is no king, lord, nor ruler, that asked such things at any magician, or astrologer, or Chaldean.

11 And it is a rare thing that the king requireth, and there is none other that can shew it before the king, except the gods, whose dwelling is not with flesh.

Notice, Nebuchadnezzar says, ["my spirit was troubled to KNOW THE DREAM" ]{.class_1922}(vs. 3), not just the interpretation of the dream as he requests in 4:6.

["Then spake the Chaldeans to the king in Syriack"]{.class_1922} (vs. 4), and from here to 7:28, the book is written in Aramaic, which is just another name for the [Syrian]{.class_1921} language (["Syriack"]{.class_1922}). Aramaic was the ["lingua franca"]{.class_1921} for that part of the world, much as Greek would become under Alexander the Great. Aramaic was a second language to the Hebrews because Isaac and Jacob got their wives from Syria (Deut. 26:5 cf. Gen. 25:20, 28:5, 31:20--43).

Now, the magicians, astrologers, sorcerers, and Chaldeans want the King to do as he had always done before: give them the dream so they could give him the interpretation (vss. 4, 7). But Nebuchadnezzar won't budge; he wants the dream and the interpretation both from them.

Now it may indeed have been that Nebuchadnezzar honestly couldn't remember the dream. It is nothing unusual to forget the details of a dream moments after you awake, but if someone were to recount the details, you could remember it again. Of course, that won't happen [naturally.]{.class_1921}

That brings us to Nebuchadnezzar's real motive behind the request. After conversing with Daniel and his three companions, and finding ["them ten times better than all the magicians and astrologers that were in all his realm"]{.class_1922} (1:20), the King has a sneaking suspicion that those ["magicians and astrologers"]{.class_1922} have been "buffaloing" him all along. He is giving them a test to prove []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_30}their supernatural abilities, and to provide the proper "motivation" for them, he says this: ["if ye will not make known unto me the dream, with the interpretation thereof, ye shall be cut in pieces, and your houses shall be made a dunghill. But if ye shew the dream, and the interpretation thereof, ye shall receive of me gifts and rewards and great honour"]{.class_1922} (vss. 5--6).

They'll either cash in, or they'll [cash out.]{.class_1921} They'll either be made rich and famous, or they'll be chopped into little bits and their houses turned into manure piles. Those Oriental monarchs had absolute power, boy; there was no getting around it.

Nebuchadnezzar figures that if they have the power to find out the interpretation, the same power should be able to give them the dream. But it is obvious to him that they are just stalling for time because they are [fakes]{.class_1921} and [liars]{.class_1921} (vss. 8--9).

Verse 10: ["There is not a man upon the earth that can shew the king's matter."]{.class_1922} Well, there was. It was Daniel (vs. 19), but he had to get it from God (vs. 18). Now look at that verse again. We understand the King, in this case, is a lost heathen despot, but if you applied it spiritually to the ultimate King---God Himself (Psa. 47:7, 98:6; Isa. 6:5; Jer. 51:57; Zech. 14:16--17; Mal. 1:14)---the statement is just as true.

Paul wrote, ["For who hath known the mind of the Lord? or who hath been his counsellor?"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 11:34). The obvious answer is [no one.]{.class_1921} There is no man in his natural state that understands the things of God (1 Cor. 2:14); they have to be [revealed]{.class_1921} to him by the Holy Spirit (1 Cor. 2:10--13). That is why ["no prophecy of the scripture is of any private interpretation"]{.class_1922} (2 Pet. 1:20). When Joseph interpreted the dreams of Pharaoh, he said, ["Do not interpretations belong to God?"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 40:8). They sure do; they sure don't belong to any church praying to a female demon (["the queen of heaven"]{.class_1922}---Jer. 44:17--19, 25) and practicing ritualistic cannibalism and vampirism (transubstantiation in the Mass).

[Folks, a Bible teacher can take you through th]{.class_1934}e Scriptures and show you the verses that explain a passage (1 Cor. 2:14). He can explain a passage to the best of his ability (Neh. 8:8). But there is only one Person who can take the truth, put it in your "craw," and make it stick; and it is nobody who walks on two legs. []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_31}[It is the Holy Spirit of God]{.class_1921} (John 14:26, 16:13). If the Spirit of God and of Christ doesn't do a work in you, you can sit under a Bible teacher for a lifetime and come out knowing nothing.

Just in case you think I was stretching the application a bit there, look at the next verse: ["there is none other that can shew it before the king, except the gods, whose dwelling is not with flesh"]{.class_1922} (vs. 11). Of course, those diviners are all polytheists, but even they recognize that only a god could do what the King asked. The problem was, out of all the gods out there (1 Cor. 8:5), they didn't know the One who could, and would, reveal secrets (vs. 47; Amos 3:7). (That last reference is a perfect verse for refuting the Rabbis' claim that Daniel wasn't a prophet, for God revealed ["his secret"]{.class_1922} to him.)

12 For this cause the king was angry and very furious, and commanded to destroy all the wise men of Babylon.

13 And the decree went forth that the wise men should be slain; and they sought Daniel and his fellows to be slain.

14 Then Daniel answered with counsel and wisdom to Arioch the captain of the king's guard, which was gone forth to slay the wise men of Babylon:

15 He answered and said to Arioch the king's captain, Why is the decree so hasty from the king? Then Arioch made the thing known to Daniel.

16 Then Daniel went in, and desired of the king that he would give him time, and that he would shew the king the interpretation.

17 Then Daniel went to his house, and made the thing known to Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah, his companions:

18 That they would desire mercies of the God of heaven concerning this secret; that Daniel and his fellows should not perish with the rest of the wise men of Babylon.

The passage is a perfect illustration of Proverbs 16:14.

"The wrath of a king is as messengers of death: but a []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_32}wise man will pacify it."

That being the case, there was only one truly ["wise man"]{.class_1922} among ["all the wise men of Babylon"]{.class_1922}: Daniel. He was the one who stopped Nebuchadnezzar from killing every last magician, astrologer, sorcerer, and Chaldean in the realm (vs. 24).

Of course, Daniel and his friends had been trained as wise men back in chapter 1, so they were on the "hit list" to be executed. But they had no idea why they were to be killed because they had not been among the wise men called in before the King. So when they found out from the Captain sent around to carry out the sentence what was going on, Daniel went straight to the King to "buy time." Buy time for what? [A prayer meeting.]{.class_1921}

Daniel and his buddies had no more idea of what the King dreamed than any other wise man in Babylon, but they knew Someone who did. They went straight to the One who gave Nebuchadnezzar the dream: they desired ["mercies of the God of heaven concerning this secret"]{.class_1922} (vs. 18).

Brethren, the way to understand that Book is [not]{.class_1921} by going to "the original text." If a knowledge of Hebrew and Greek gave a person understanding of the Scriptures, the Jewish Rabbis and the Greek Orthodox Priests should know the Bible better than anyone. [They are just as lost as a golf ball in high weeds.]{.class_1921} A. T. Robertson, who wrote the monumental Greek grammar, couldn't find the Judgment Seat of Christ or the Millennial reign of Christ in the Bible. Robert Dick Wilson knew every language in which the Bible had been written and translated up to A. D. 600, and he believed in baby sprinkling. A knowledge of the Biblical languages means nothing when it comes to knowing and understanding the Book.

When the disciples wanted to know the interpretation of the things Christ taught, do you know what they did? [They asked Him]{.class_1921} (Mark 4:10). I guarantee you, a conversation with the Author of Scripture will do more for you when it comes to understanding what He wrote than consulting anybody's lexicon, grammar, or "word study."

In my work on [The Alexandrian Cult Series,]{.class_1921} I have quotes from popular and well-known Bible teachers who will tell you that the way to find out what God says is to find out what the "originals" say. That []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_33}sure leaves some of you who can't read Hebrew or Greek in a fix, doesn't it? But don't worry; if you can't read Hebrew or Greek, just read the [American Standard Version,]{.class_1921} and you will get as close to what God said as you can get. I would hate to think that the closest I can get to what God said is a version that gets rid of Christ's Deity from 1 Timothy 3:16 and the Trinity from 1 John 5:7 and the Lord's virgin birth from Luke 2:33 and the blood atonement from Colossians 1:14 and the infallible proofs of His resurrection from Acts 1:3 . . . , but why go on? The [American Standard Version]{.class_1921} gets rid of 36,000 of God's words; the [New International Version]{.class_1921} gets rid of 64,000 of them. If that is as close as I can get, ["I pray thee have me excused"]{.class_1922} (cf. Luke 14:18--19).

19 Then was the secret revealed unto Daniel in a night vision. Then Daniel blessed the God of heaven.

20 Daniel answered and said, Blessed be the name of God for ever and ever: for wisdom and might are his:

21 And he changeth the times and the seasons: he removeth kings, and setteth up kings: he giveth wisdom unto the wise, and knowledge to them that know understanding:

22 He revealeth the deep and secret things: he knoweth what is in the darkness, and the light dwelleth with him.

23 I thank thee, and praise thee, O thou God of my fathers, who hast given me wisdom and might, and hast made known unto me now what we desired of thee: for thou hast now made known unto us the king's matter.

God answers Daniel's prayer by allowing him to see in a dream (see Job 33:15) exactly what Nebuchadnezzar dreamed. Daniel's response to answered prayer was to bless God (vs. 19). When God answers your prayer, be grateful; give thanks (Phil. 4:6; Col. 2:7).

["Bless the LORD, O my soul, and forget not all his benefits"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 103:2).

Verse 20: ["Blessed be the name of God for ever and ever." ]{.class_1922}The cross-reference is Psalm 113:2. Both verses should alert the reader that much more is going on here, though, than personal []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_34}thanks and praise for God's mercy in answered prayer. God's name is being blasphemed on a daily basis (Rom. 3:14); blasphemy will be the hallmark of the whole world in the next several years (Rev. 13:5--6, 16:9). The time when God's name will be blessed everywhere, 24 hours a day, will be in the Millennium and on into Eternity (Mal. 1:11 cf. Rev. 11:15). The reason Daniel brings it up here is because Nebuchadnezzar's dream ends with the establishment of God's kingdom (vs. 44).

["For wisdom and might are his."]{.class_1922} Attested to throughout the Scripture (e.g., Job 12:13, 16; Psa. 147:5; Prov. 8:14; Jer. 32:19). In Christ ["are hid all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge"]{.class_1922} (Col. 2:3). Jesus said, ["All power is given unto me in heaven and in earth"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 28:18), so when we fight the Devil, we are commanded to ["be strong in the Lord, and in the power of his might"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:10). The saints in Glory, whether they be from the Church Age or the Tribulation, praise God and the Lamb with ["blessing,"]{.class_1922} ["wisdom,"]{.class_1922} and ["might"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 5:12, 7:12), as Daniel does here.

["He changeth the times and the seasons"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21). Again, a reference to the establishment of the Millennial kingdom at the return of Jesus Christ (Acts 1:7, 3:19, 21; 1 Thess. 5:1). The idea of the statement is that [only God]{.class_1921} can "bring in the kingdom." The Antichrist will try, but will fail (7:25). God literally changed ["the times and the seasons"]{.class_1922} in the book of Acts in regards to the kingdom. In Acts 1, when the disciples asked Christ, ["Lord, wilt thou at this time restore the kingdom to Israel?"]{.class_1922} (Acts 1:6), Jesus replied, ["It is not for you to know the times or the seasons, which the Father hath put in his own power"]{.class_1922} (Acts 1:7). But when you get over to 1 Thessalonians 5:1--2, Paul says:

"But of the times and the seasons, brethren, ye have no need that I write unto you. For yourselves know perfectly that the day of the Lord so cometh as a thief in the night."

What happened between Acts 1 and 1 Thessalonians 5? The Lord changed the times and seasons! Jesus was ready to come back in Acts 7, and the Father postponed the Second Coming for 2,000 years (see our comments on Acts 7:56 in that Commentary).

["He removeth kings, and setteth up kings"]{.class_1922}---a lesson []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_35}Nebuchadnezzar will learn in a dramatic way in a couple of chapters (4:17, 32). Ditto Belshazzar (5:28). Prophetically, this is a reference to those who rule and reign with Christ in His Millennial kingdom (Rev. 20:4 cf. 1 Sam. 2:8; Psa. 113:7--8; Luke 1:52).

["He giveth wisdom unto the wise, and knowledge to them that know understanding."]{.class_1922} We have already discussed the fact that it is God who gives wisdom, knowledge, and understanding under our remarks on 1:17, which see. Notice, though, that this statement goes beyond that. God gives [more]{.class_1921} wisdom, knowledge, and understanding to those who already have it. The principle is found reiterated by Christ in Matthew 13:12, 25:29 (see also Mark 4:25; Luke 8:18, 19:26); it is, God gives [more]{.class_1921} to someone who [believes and uses ]{.class_1921}what he's been given by God before. God gave Daniel and his companions wisdom, knowledge, and understanding back in 1:17; and now He gives them more because they use what God gives them for His glory.

["He revealeth the deep and secret things"]{.class_1922} (vs. 22). Deuteronomy 29:29 says, ["The secret things belong unto the LORD our God . . . ."]{.class_1922} Whatever men don't know about a thing, God does. [". . . but ]{.class_1922}[those things which are revealed belong unto us . . . ."]{.class_1937-1}[ ]{.class_1934}God gave them to you, and if He didn't, you would never have gotten them. [". . . and to our children for ever . . . ."]{.class_1922} Those Jews were commanded to teach their children ["diligently"]{.class_1922} what God had revealed to them (Deut. 6:7).[ ". . . that we may do all the words of this law."]{.class_1922} In other words, what God reveals to a man is not for the purpose of puffing him up with knowledge (1 Cor. 8:1), but [to get him to do right.]{.class_1921}

Paul says the Holy Spirit has revealed ["the deep things of God"]{.class_1922} to those of us who love the Lord (1 Cor. 2:9--10). The things God has revealed to us about the Rapture and Christ's Advent are not so a man can hang a dispensational chart on the wall and show off to other Christians how much he knows about prophecy. They were revealed so a Christian would get right and stay right in preparation for his Lord's return (1 John 3:3). In the New Testament, God revealed ["the mystery of Christ"]{.class_1922} to Paul and the other apostles (Eph. 3:4--5) so that ["all nations"]{.class_1922} would come to Christ in ["the obedience of faith"]{.class_1922} for salvation (Rom. 16:26).

["He knoweth what is in the darkness, and the light dwelleth with him."]{.class_1922} John wrote, ["God is light, and in him is no darkness at all"]{.class_1922} (1 John 1:5). Jesus said, ["men loved darkness rather than light, because their deeds were evil"]{.class_1922} (John 3:19). Men prefer doing their devilment at night because they think no one will see them commit their wickedness (Psa. 139:11 cf. Isa. 29:15). But when it comes to ["our secret sins"]{.class_1922} being exposed ["in the light of ]{.class_1922}\[God's\][ countenance"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 90:8), there is no difference to God between light and darkness, or between day and night (Psa. 137:12). God sees and knows what goes on in both (Job 32:22). That Bible says, ["all things are naked and opened unto the eyes of him with whom we have to do"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 4:13).

One day, everything done in the dark and in secret will come out (Luke 12:2--3; 1 Cor. 4:5). God will take the top of the car you were in last Saturday night, young man, young lady, and peel it back to let everyone know what you did. He will take what you did in that bedroom or hotel room and play it in "high definition," "surround sound" for the whole universe to see and hear.

["In the day when God shall judge the SECRETS OF MEN by Jesus Christ according to my gospel"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 2:16).

Verse 23: ["I thank thee, and praise thee, O thou God, who hast given me wisdom and might, and hast made known unto me now what we desire of thee."]{.class_1922} He's thanking God for answered prayer. The answer to his prayer was first and foremost ["wisdom."]{.class_1922}

James wrote, ["If any of you lack wisdom, let him ask of God, that giveth to all men liberally, and upbraideth not; and it shall be given him"]{.class_1922} (James 1:5). If you don't receive wisdom from God, it is either because you didn't ask for it (James 4:2) or you asked for it with the wrong motive (James 4:3) or you didn't believe God when you asked (James 1:6--7).

Jesus thanked His Father that He heard Him when He prayed (John 11:41), but when it came to God revealing things, do you know for what Jesus thanked God? He thanked God for hiding some things from smart folks and revealing them to intellectual babies.

["In that hour Jesus rejoiced in spirit, and said, I thank thee, O Father, Lord of heaven and earth, that thou hast hid []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_37}these things from the wise and prudent, and hast revealed them unto babes: even so, Father; for so it seemed good in thy sight"]{.class_1922} (Luke 10:21).

Of course, Daniel, Hananiah, Azariah, and Mishael were wise; but it wasn't from earning their Bachelor's, Master's, and Doctor's degrees. It was from [obeying God.]{.class_1921} These teenage slaves "outshined" all the brilliant intellectuals of their day because God revealed to them what He hid from those with more "seniority" and experience. Those Hebrew boys didn't ["mind . . . high things"]{.class_1922}; they weren't ["wise in ]{.class_1922}\[their\][ own conceits" ]{.class_1922}(Rom. 12:16).

24 Therefore Daniel went in unto Arioch, whom the king had ordained to destroy the wise men of Babylon: he went and said thus unto him; Destroy not the wise men of Babylon: bring me in before the king, and I will shew unto the king the interpretation.

25 Then Arioch brought in Daniel before the king in haste, and said thus unto him, I have found a man of the captives of Judah, that will make known unto the king the interpretation.

26 The king answered and said to Daniel, whose name was Belteshazzar, Art thou able to make known unto me the dream which I have seen, and the interpretation thereof?

27 Daniel answered in the presence of the king, and said, The secret which the king hath demanded cannot the wise men, the astrologers, the magicians, the soothsayers, shew unto the king;

28 But there is a God in heaven that revealeth secrets, and maketh known to the king Nebuchadnezzar what shall be in the latter days. Thy dream, and the visions of thy head upon thy bed, are these;

29 As for thee, O king, thy thoughts came into thy mind upon thy bed, what should come to pass hereafter: and he that revealeth secrets maketh known to thee what shall come to pass.
