30 But as for me, this secret is not revealed to me for []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_38}any wisdom that I have more than any living, but for their sakes that shall make known the interpretation to the king, and that thou mightest know the thoughts of thy heart.

Those demon-possessed magicians, astrologers, sorcerers, and Chaldeans owed their lives to four praying Jewish boys. The heathen will often "get in on the goodies" of a bunch of saints in their midst. Laban said to Jacob, ["I have learned by experience that the LORD hath blessed me for thy sake"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 30:27). The Lord blessed the house of Potiphar for the sake of Joseph (Gen. 39:5). Over in 2 Kings 3:14, the only reason the Lord answered Jehoram, the son of Ahab, was because of ["the presence of Jehoshaphat, the king of Judah."]{.class_1922} And all of the lives of the men on that ship in Acts 27 were spared because the Apostle Paul was on board (Acts 27:24). I am convinced that the only reason God hasn't blown the United States to a "fare thee well" is because there are still some Christians in this country who believe that Book, are praying, and are putting out the Gospel.

A Christian was witnessing to a lost fellow one time and urged him to trust Christ before the Lord came back and left him behind to face the Tribulation. That lost fellow scowled and said, "You Christians, always talking about the Rapture and the Lord coming back. You're nothing but a bunch of nuts." That Christian replied, "When we nuts are gone, you squirrels are going to be up a tree." That's right. When those angels pulled Lot and his family out of Sodom and Gomorrha, that's when the fire fell; Jesus said that was a picture of His return (Luke 17:29--30).

It is obvious from verse 25 that Arioch did not relish his job as executioner, at least not in the case of Daniel and his friends. He brought Daniel to Nebuchadnezzar ["in haste."]{.class_1922} Notice, again, that when Daniel stood in his official position before the King, his Babylonian name was used; you will see the same thing in 4:8, 19 and 5:12. In private, the four boys went by their Jewish names (see vs. 17).

Nebuchadnezzar puts the question to Daniel: ["Art thou able to make known unto me the dream which I have seen, and the interpretation thereof?"]{.class_1922} (vs. 26). Daniel's answer, in a []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_39}nutshell, is: "Nobody but God can tell you that King, and He didn't reveal it to me because I am any smarter than these other guys. He showed me so you wouldn't kill me and my buddies, and so you would ['know the thoughts of thy heart']{.class_1922}" (vs. 30). Nebuchadnezzar had been pondering that dream since he woke up; he had been thinking about it and mulling it over.

["But there is a God in heaven that revealeth secrets, and maketh known to the king"]{.class_1922} (vs. 28). The revelation doesn't come from scholarship or linguistics or archaeology or manuscript evidence. It comes from God opening the eyes of your understanding to what's in that Book (Luke 24:45; Psa. 119:18).

Did you know that nine times out of ten, when you read your Bible and believe what you read, you will get it right. If you read it through prayerfully, paying attention to the impressions the Holy Spirit makes on you as you read, you will get it right. There will be some places, of course, where you get confused and mess things up, but everywhere where it counts, you will get right. You can work on those other places later with deeper study (2 Tim. 2:15).

["There is a God in heaven that . . . maketh known to the king Nebuchadnezzar what shall be in THE LATTER DAYS"]{.class_1922} (vs. 28). ["As for thee, O king, thy thoughts came into thy mind . . . what should come to pass HEREAFTER"]{.class_1922} (vs. 29). This is to what I called your attention in my comments on 1:15 (which see). Daniel deals prophetically with what will happen in the end times. There will be references, both typically and prophetically, to the First Advent, but they will always be in relation to, and of secondary importance to, Christ's Second Advent. That is because the day in which God the Father is interested is not the day wicked men crucified His Son. That is the day that is important to us sinners because it accomplished our atonement. Of far more importance to the Father is the day His Son gets what is rightfully His---the throne of this world. The prophecies about Christ's Second Advent outnumber the prophecies about His First Advent about four to one.

31 Thou, O king, sawest, and behold a great image. This great image, whose brightness was excellent, stood before []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_40}thee; and the form thereof was terrible.

32 This image's head was of fine gold, his breast and his arms of silver, his belly and his thighs of brass,

33 His legs of iron, his feet part of iron and part of clay.

34 Thou sawest till that a stone was cut out without hands, which smote the image upon his feet that were of iron and clay, and brake them to pieces.

35 Then was the iron, the clay, the brass, the silver, and the gold, broken to pieces together, and became like the chaff of the summer threshingfloors; and the wind carried them away, that no place was found for them: and the stone that smote the image became a great mountain, and filled the whole earth.

36 This is the dream; and we will tell the interpretation thereof before the king.

37 Thou, O king, art a king of kings: for the God of heaven hath given thee a kingdom, power, and strength, and glory.

38 And wheresoever the children of men dwell, the beasts of the field and the fowls of the heaven hath he given into thine hand, and hath made thee ruler over them all. Thou art this head of gold.

39 And after thee shall arise another kingdom inferior to thee, and another third kingdom of brass, which shall bear rule over all the earth.

40 And the fourth kingdom shall be strong as iron: forasmuch as iron breaketh in pieces and subdueth all things: and as iron that breaketh all these, shall it break in pieces and bruise.

41 And whereas thou sawest the feet and toes, part of potters' clay, and part of iron, the kingdom shall be divided; but there shall be in it of the strength of the iron, forasmuch as thou sawest the iron mixed with miry clay.

42 And as the toes of the feet were part of iron, and part of clay, so the kingdom shall be partly strong, and partly broken.

43 And whereas thou sawest iron mixed with miry clay, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw216.xhtml_page_41}they shall mingle themselves with the seed of men: but they shall not cleave one to another, even as iron is not mixed with clay.

44 And in the days of these kings shall the God of heaven set up a kingdom, which shall never be destroyed: and the kingdom shall not be left to other people, but it shall break in pieces and consume all these kingdoms, and it shall stand for ever.

45 Forasmuch as thou sawest that the stone was cut out of the mountain without hands, and that it brake in pieces the iron, the brass, the clay, the silver, and the gold; the great God hath made known to the king what shall come to pass hereafter: and the dream is certain, and the interpretation thereof sure.

Now we come to the "meat" of the chapter: Nebuchadnezzar's dream and its interpretation. I have included all the verses dealing with both, though it makes for a large passage on which to comment, because we will be going back and forth between the dream and the interpretation in our remarks. I have also included a chart of the image, with a brief description of its meanings to illustrate the passage. With all that being said, let's get into the exposition of the passage.

This dream gives the basic outline of Gentile history for the next 900 years, and then beyond to the Tribulation. This time period is called ["the times of the Gentiles"]{.class_1922} (Luke 21:24). This is prophecy---the foretelling of the future---plain and simple. And as I said in the Introduction, the prophecy is so detailed and obvious that the higher critics have tried to relegate it to history, recorded after the fact in "apocalyptic imagery." Anything but accept the proof God gave you that the Scriptures are His Book (2 Pet. 1:20--21), written under the direction of ["the testimony of Jesus"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 19:10).

The first thing you need to notice about this image is the [devolution of human history.]{.class_1921} This is not the "fairytale for grown-ups": Darwin's "puddle to paradise." This is [Darwin in reverse.]{.class_1921} This is the [degeneration of man,]{.class_1921} not his "evolution." The metals decline in [value:]{.class_1921} gold to silver, silver to brass, brass to iron, iron to an iron-clay mixture. They decline in [function:]{.class_1921} they go from the intellectual function of the brain in the head, to the vital functions of the heart and lungs in the chest, to the digestive and reproductive functions in the belly and thighs area, to the means of locomotion in the legs, and wind up with man's contact with the dirt at the toes. And finally, they decline in [weight.]{.class_1921} The "specific gravities" of the metals---i.e., the weight of a substance in ratio to the weight of an equal volume of water---as given by Clarence Larkin are: gold, 19.5; silver, 10.47; brass, 8.0; iron, 5.0; and iron-clay, 1.93. If you look on the Internet, you will get different numbers, but the results will still be the same: the metals decline in weight, making the image top heavy and unstable.

This image is a typical illustration of all human history. All views of origins and the future can be summed up by three simple diagrams. The first is a line that starts out at the bottom and gradually goes up at about a fifteen degree angle. That is the view of Darwin, Haeckel, and Huxley: things start out simple and gradually progress. The second is a series of spirals that proceed along the same inclination. That is the view of Bateson, DeVries, and Goldschmidt: evolution is by random mutations of genes. The third is a maze of lines going helter skelter, crisscrossing themselves any number of times, with no progress or regress one way or another. That is the view of Einstein, Heisenberg, Frankl, and Sartre. It is complete anarchy and chaos, with no goal or purpose to existence other than one's own whims.

The fourth line is the Biblical view of history. The line starts out at the top and plummets down. Then it shoots back up, but not quite as high as before and then plummets down again. That cycle repeats itself over and over again until finally the line shoots back up to where it was originally and stays there. That is God starting man up at the top in the Garden of Eden and then man falling into sin. God reaches down and puts man back on his feet with a way to get his sins []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_44}forgiven and a promise of complete redemption, and man blows it again until God wipes out everyone but Noah and his family in the Flood. Noah steps out into a clean world only for his great grandson, Nimrod, to unite his followers in rebellion against God at the Tower of Babel. God busts up the whole thing by confusing the languages, and then He calls out Abraham to be a blessing to all the ["families of the earth"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 12:3). Abraham's descendants wind up as slaves down in Egypt, so God calls them out and gives them the Ten Commandments.

And you know how the story progresses: wanderings in the wilderness for forty years, apostasy throughout the book of Judges, Saul, Solomon, the divided kingdom, captivity to Assyria, captivity to Babylon. Finally, God sends them a Saviour, and what do they do? They crucify Him. God lifts those Jews up, and then they fall.

It's no different with you. You start out ["dead in trespasses and sins"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 2:1), and you have to be born again (John 3:3--5). You get born again, and without the intervention of God through prayer and the word, you go right back to the old nature.

In science, that's called the Law of Entropy. Unless something from outside injects fresh energy, everything runs down. You have to wind up a clock; you have to replace the batteries. The car turns into a rolling pile of junk; you get old and die. Things don't get better; they get worse. Mankind left to themselves would wipe out every living thing on the planet (Matt. 24:22; Mark 13:20).

All dispensations in the Bible end in degeneration and apostasy. The Church Age ends in Laodicea---the lukewarm church that makes God sick. ["The times of the Gentiles"]{.class_1922} end with the Devil incarnate in charge. Even the Millennium ends with Satan being released from the Bottomless Pit and deceiving a bunch of people to attack Jerusalem. It isn't until the final "lift up"---the New Heavens, the New Earth, and the New Jerusalem---where everything goes back to the top and stays there. And no evolution, random chance, survival of the fittest, natural selection, mutation of genes, or man as "the measure of all things" has anything to do with it. It is all entirely the divine intervention of God Almighty.

Note, also, this image lays out history from east to west. That is the direction God moves in history. The sun, a picture of the Lord []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_45}Jesus Christ (Mal. 4:2 cf. Psa. 19:4--5), moves east to west. The line of progression through the Tabernacle was from east to west. The Gospel started out in Jerusalem and moved east to west across Asia Minor, Greece, then Rome. In the modern era, the Reformation started out in Germany, then it moved over to England with the [King James]{.class_1921} Bible, then the Pilgrims came over to America, and from there and England, it went back around the world to India, China, the South Seas, and Africa. Here, it starts out over in Babylon, moves north and west with the Persians conquering Asia Minor. Then it goes to Greece with Alexander the Great, and then Rome. The toes represent a ten-nation confederated kingdom, west of Rome. The UN, headquartered in New York City, is a harbinger of that final kingdom.

Now, look at some things given in the interpretation of this image. The first is in verse 37: ["Thou, O king, art A king of kings."]{.class_1922} Note that indefinite article. That separates the Antichrist from the true Christ. Nebuchadnezzar was a King who had conquered other Kings and was now ruling over them. The Antichrist is a King who rules over ten Kings (Dan. 7:24; Rev. 17:12). But each King of the four kingdoms represented here is supplanted by the kingdom that follows it. The kingdom of Jesus Christ, though, isn't superseded by any other kingdom; it stands forever (vs. 44). So Jesus Christ isn't just ["a king of kings"]{.class_1922}; He is ["THE King of kings"]{.class_1922} (1 Tim. 6:15).

Verse 38, still speaking of Nebuchadnezzar: ["And wheresoever the children of men dwell, the beasts of the field and the fowls of the heaven hath he given into thine hand, and hath made thee ruler over them all."]{.class_1922} The imagery is repeated in Nebuchadnezzar's dream of the great tree over in 4:20--22. The Lord had told Jehoiakim through Jeremiah that God, as the Creator of land, men, and beasts, had given all the nations and lands (including Israel) to Nebuchadnezzar, along with ["the beasts of the field," "to serve him"]{.class_1922} until God was through using Nebuchadnezzar (Jer. 27:5--7).

["Thou art this head of gold."]{.class_1922} So each metal doesn't just represent a kingdom (vs. 39), but its King as well. That is what those beasts in Daniel's dream in chapter 7 represent: ["four KINGS"]{.class_1922} (7:17) as well as their ["KINGDOMS"]{.class_1922} (7:23). You need to get that, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_46}because the expositors, like Scofield and Clarke, will make them just the kingdoms or monarchies. It is more than just the political system; it is the head of that political system.

Notice in verse 39:[ "after thee shall arise another kingdom INFERIOR to thee."]{.class_1922} So the highest form of government is an [absolute dictatorship.]{.class_1921} That was what Nebuchadnezzar was: an absolute dictator. The problem with such a government is that absolute power in the hands of a [sinner.]{.class_1921} What you want is an absolute dictatorship in the hands of a [sinless man,]{.class_1921} and when God finally sets up His kingdom, that's what you get (see Zech. 14).

The Persian government that follows Babylon is a [military dictatorship.]{.class_1921} Darius and Cyrus were Generals who enforced their laws through their armies. When you get to Alexander and the Greek Empire, you have a [military monarchy.]{.class_1921} Alexander was a General and a King, but he really didn't run the territory he conquered. Somebody else ran it for him. He was too busy running all over the Middle East looking for new lands to conquer. When Rome finally takes over, you have a [republican monarchy:]{.class_1921} Caesar was answerable to the Roman Senate. And the Antichrist's kingdom is only a [socialistic democracy,]{.class_1921} a loose confederation of nation-States held together by the charisma and popularity of the Antichrist.

Now notice the peculiar description of the toes of iron and clay in verse 43. The iron represents more than merely strength (vs. 41), and the clay represents more than brokenness or weakness (vs. 42). There is no doubt what the clay pictures: it pictures [men.]{.class_1926}

["How much less in them ]{.class_1922}\[speaking of men back up in Job 4:17\][ that dwell in houses of clay, whose foundation is in the dust ]{.class_1922}\[Gen. 2:7\][" ]{.class_1922}(Job 4:19).

["Remember, I beseech thee, that thou hast made me as the clay; and wilt thou bring me into dust again?"]{.class_1922} (Job 10:9).

["Your remembrances are like unto ashes, your bodies to bodies of clay"]{.class_1922} (Job 13:12).

["Behold, I am according to thy wish in God's stead: I also am formed out of the clay"]{.class_1922} (Job 33:6).

So the ["miry clay"]{.class_1922} of verse 43 corresponds with ["the seed of men."]{.class_1922} That being the case, what about that ["iron"]{.class_1922} that is ["mixed with miry clay"]{.class_1922}? The verse says, ["they]{.class_1922} \[referring to the iron\][ shall mingle themselves with the seed of men."]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_47} So whatever iron had to do with the Roman Empire and the Caesars back up in verse 40, in verse 43, there is a deeper, more sinister connection.

Iron doesn't have a good connotation in the Scripture. There was nothing of iron in the construction of Noah's ark (Gen. 6:14), and no ["tool of iron"]{.class_1922} was allowed by Solomon in building the Temple (1 Kings 6:7). Both of those are types of the Lord Jesus Christ (cf. Rom. 8:1; John 2:19). The name [Cain]{.class_1921} means "iron spear" (see our comments on Gen. 4:1 in that Commentary), like Goliath's spear head (1 Sam. 17:7). Both Cain and Goliath were types of the Son of Perdition (2 Thess. 2:3). The Bible says, ["Cain . . . was of that wicked one"]{.class_1922} (1 John 3:12), just like those people of whom Christ said Satan was their father (Matt. 13:38; John 8:44). In the case of the Antichrist, that relationship is a [literal]{.class_1921} one (2 Thess. 2:7--9). Goliath was a giant; those giants were the product of fallen angels cohabitating with women (Gen. 6:4). So that iron typifies ten demoniac "humanoids" from outer space who come down to take human wives so they can beget giants like their predecessors did back in Genesis 6.

Now there was more to Nebuchadnezzar's dream than just that image which typified the Gentile kingdoms in charge of this world. In his dream, Nebuchadnezzar sees ["a stone . . . cut out without hands, which smote the image upon his feet . . . and brake them in pieces"]{.class_1922} (vs. 34). That stone not only breaks the feet to pieces, it busts up the whole image and grinds it into such fine powder that it blows away in the wind. Then that stone becomes ["a great mountain, and filled the whole earth."]{.class_1922} That mountain turns out to be God's kingdom here on earth that wipes out the UN. But remember, it's not just the kingdom; it's the King too (see our remarks under vs. 38). So the Smiting Stone is [Jesus Christ,]{.class_1921} God's King (Matt. 25:31).

["To whom coming, as unto a LIVING STONE, disallowed indeed of men, but chosen of God, and precious . . . Wherefore also it is contained in the scripture, Behold, I lay in Sion a chief corner stone, elect, precious: and he that believeth on him shall not be confounded"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 2:4, 6).

On the chart, I have the Smiting Stone falling from Heaven, like a []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_48}meteor. That's not in the text of Daniel 2, but it is in Matthew 21:44.

"And whosoever shall fall on this stone shall be broken: but on whomsoever IT SHALL FALL, it will grind him to powder."

There's the Smiting Stone of Daniel 2:35. He comes down from Heaven to ["smite the nations"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 19:11--15) and stomps the United Nations troops (Rev. 14:20) into ["powder"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 21:44).

As I said, in the chart, I drew that Smiting Stone like a meteor, but if I had drawn it as it should be, it would look like [a small pyramid.]{.class_1921} Look at Christ's words in Matthew 21:42---["The stone which the builders rejected, the same is become THE HEAD OF THE CORNER."]{.class_1922} The only structure where one of its corners is also its head is a pyramid. A pyramid looks like a [mountain.]{.class_1921} So all over the ancient world, starting at Babel, you have men building different forms of pyramids. That's man trying to bring in the kingdom from the bottom up (Gen. 11:4), instead of God bringing it in from the top down (Dan. 2:44).

Now I want to go back up to verse 34, which I glossed over before to identify the Stone. It shouldn't be ignored because it is the key to the dream. Remember in my prefatory remarks to this chapter, I told you that how one interprets this passage determines whether he is Premillennial, Postmillennial, or Amillennial. All of that hinges on verse 34.

Notice! Mark it down! The Stone strikes the FEET, not the [legs!]{.class_1921} The legs are the kingdom in charge at Christ's [First Advent:]{.class_1921} the Roman Empire. Christ was not a Smiting Stone at His First Advent. He didn't smite; He was [smitten.]{.class_1921}

["Surely he hath borne our griefs, and carried our sorrows: yet we did esteem him stricken, SMITTEN OF GOD, and afflicted"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 53:4).

He smites when He returns at the Battle of Armageddon (Rev. 19:15). So no kingdom came down at Calvary to slowly fill the whole world (Amillennialism) or be brought in over a period of time by Christ's followers (Postmillennialism). The kingdom doesn't come until the King comes during the reign of the Antichrist and his ten underlings, and pitches him and his False Prophet into the Lake of Fire (Rev. 19:20), and feeds those Kings under him to the buzzards []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_49}(Rev. 19:17--18, 21).

What messes up all the scholars is that the iron in the image goes down into the toes. That Roman Empire has two divisions, like the two legs of the image: the eastern part that was based in Constantinople (modern Istanbul) and the western part based in Rome. But then that iron goes into the feet and the ten toes, and mixes with ["miry clay,"]{.class_1922} so the Postmillennialists and Amillennialists relegate the whole image to the [past.]{.class_1921} This is best illustrated by the comment in the [Treasury of Scripture Knowledge]{.class_1921} on verse 43:

"The Roman Empire became weakened by a mixture of barbarous nations, by the incursions of whom it was torn asunder about the Fourth Century after Christ, and at length divided into ten kingdoms, answering to the ten toes of the image."

Do you know what you are to gather from that tidbit of historical trivia? Well, if you are an Amillennialist, you gather that Christ came back some time after the Fourth Century A.D., and that He is ruling [right now.]{.class_1921} If this is the best Jesus Christ can do as King, kick Him off the throne.

If you are a Postmillennialist, your conclusion is no better: you are working to make the ["great mountain"]{.class_1922} of verse 35 fill ["the whole earth,"]{.class_1922} because you think the Smiting Stone fell at Calvary (or Acts 2). If this is the best you can do at "bringing in the kingdom," just give it a rest and go do something useful, like selling used cars.

Listen, when Christ came the first time, the iron legs of Rome were in power. The Jews had every right to expect Jesus, if He were the Christ (i.e., the Messiah---John 1:41, 4:25), to liberate them from Rome (see Luke 1:69--71 and our comments on the passage in that Commentary), because that is what Daniel said He would do. What they couldn't seem to get were those prophecies on the Suffering Servant of Isaiah 53 (see what Jesus said in Luke 24:25--26).

For all intents and purposes, when Christ came the first time, everything was set up for both Advents to happen right then. If the Jews had accepted Him as their Messiah, He would have smashed Rome and set up the kingdom. Of course, He still would have had to die for sins and rise again. But in the book of Acts, a rapture could []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_50}have taken place in Acts 7, and Daniel's Seventieth Week could have started. Judas would have come up from the Bottomless Pit and gone and taken his place as the Antichrist at Rome. Then, ten of his demoniac buddies would have come down from outer space and helped him set up his kingdom. He would have made a covenant with the Jews and busted it in the middle of the "week," and at the end of the "week," Christ would have come back and wiped out Rome. If that had happened, there would not be, to your knowledge, any Body of Christ or any revealed mystery about it, so Paul would have never had to have written it.

But those Jews rejected Him in the Gospels, and they rejected Him in the book of Acts. So the whole thing was postponed 2,000-plus years (see our comments on Acts 7:56 in that Commentary). If you get that, you will know more than all the faculty members in all the Christian schools in America and Europe.

As it stands, the iron of Rome continues on in the form of an ecclesiastical organization: the Roman Catholic Church. Through religious subterfuge and duplicity, it manipulates the governments of this world to its own advantage. The Pope has always sought to be both a religious leader [and]{.class_1921} a political leader (see Boniface VIII's "bull" [Unam Sanctam]{.class_1921}). During the Tribulation, he finally gets his wish (2 Thess. 2:3--9). Those iron-clay rulers of Daniel 2 have no more to do with the Ostrogoths, Visigoths, Huns, Franks, or Lombards invading the Roman Empire than do Mickey Mouse, Daffy Duck, or Krazy Kat.

Now, the destruction of the UN is likened to chaff being blown away from the summer threshing floor. Psalm 1:4 says, ["The ungodly . . . are like the chaff which the wind driveth away."]{.class_1922}

If you are not familiar with the threshing process, it went like this. A threshing floor was a flat place on the top of a hill. The harvested grain was brought up there and spread across the hardened ground. A fellow would then bring a wooden sled pulled by an ox onto that floor. He would sit on a platform in the middle of the threshing floor and make that ox go around that platform pulling that sled. Underneath that sled were sharp stones and shards of broken glass and pottery. As that sled went over the grain, the good []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_51}grain was broken away from the husks and stems.

As the evening came on and the breezes from the Mediterranean picked up and blew across the top of that hill, some workers would come in with tools like pitchforks, called winnowing fans. They would throw that mess of broken husks, stems, and grain up into the air. The heavier grain would fall back to the ground, while the lighter husks and stems, the useless chaff, would be blown away.

That's to what the Lord likens the destruction of the UN, here in Daniel 2. What you see throughout the Prophets is some type of supernatural ["threshing instrument"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 28:27) that is described in Ezekiel 1:4--28, 10:8--17. It is associated with ["chariots of fire"]{.class_1922} (2 Kings 6:17) and ["horses of fire"]{.class_1922} (2 Kings 2:11). For further study, see Psalm 68:17; Joel 2:1--5; Habakkuk 3:8--15; and Revelation 14:14--19, 19:11--14, and comments on those passages in their respective Commentaries.

Now, when God's kingdom comes, ["it shall break in pieces and consume all these kingdoms"]{.class_1922} (vs. 44). "Well," someone says, "haven't Babylon, Persia, Greece, and Rome already been destroyed? How can Christ destroy those kingdoms when they've been dead and gone hundreds of years now?" But look at verse 44 again: ["the kingdom shall not be left to other people."]{.class_1922}

As each of those kingdoms gives way to the next one after it, the new one is built on the old. When the Persians conquered Babylon, Darius ruled from the city he conquered. After Alexander beat the Persian monarch Darius III, at the Battle of Gaugamela, the city of Babylon welcomed Alexander in, and Alexander used it as a base of operations for his conquests in Persia and India. He was planning his invasion of Arabia in Babylon when he died. And of course, Rome ended up adapting the religion of Babylon; and the Roman Church, under the leadership of the Antichrist, is called ["MYSTERY, BABYLON THE GREAT"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 17:5). Each kingdom assimilates the ones before it.

Not so the kingdom of Christ. When ["The kingdoms of this world are become the kingdoms of our Lord, and of his Christ"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 11:15), the Lord wipes out all traces of the Gentile kingdoms to the point where ["no place]{.class_1922} \[is\][ found for them"]{.class_1922} in His kingdom (vs. 35). No more Popes, Bishops, Secretary Generals, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_52}ambassadors, Presidents, Prime Ministers, despots with delusions of grandeur, virgin mothers, "Our Ladies," "Queens of Heaven," Masses, transubstantiations, encyclicals, "bulls," decrees, bills, Senators, Congressmen, Parliaments, Ayatollahs, Imams, Mullahs, NATOs, Security Councils, G-7s, Pentagons, Supreme Courts, World Courts, and the whole godless, depraved mess. Just Jesus Christ in charge with several million exact duplicates of Him carrying out the words of a holy God.

Christ's kingdom will fill ["the whole earth"]{.class_1922} (vs. 35). ["The earth shall be full of the knowledge of the LORD, as the waters cover the sea"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 11:9).

["For from the rising of the sun even unto the going down of the same my name shall be great among the Gentiles; and in every place incense shall be offered unto my name, and a pure offering: for my name shall be great among the heathen, saith the LORD of hosts"]{.class_1922} (Mal. 1:11).

I can hardly wait! ["Even so, come, Lord Jesus"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 22:20).

Verse 45: ["the great God hath made known to the king what shall come to pass hereafter: and the dream is CERTAIN, and the interpretation thereof SURE."]{.class_1922} Everything Daniel says comes to pass right on the money. Daniel tells Nebuchadnezzar what is going to happen anywhere from seventy to 2,500 years in the future. Don't look for anything like it in the [Koran.]{.class_1921} Mohammed as a prophet is a tragic joke.

The Bible not only gives you history in the past, it also records history before it ever takes place. It will give you 48 facts of one man's life anywhere from 4,000--400 years before He is born, and every single item comes to pass just as predicted. The chances of that happening, according to the laws of statistical probability, are one in ten to the 157th power; there aren't that many electrons in three universes the size of this one. Moreover, according to those same laws, if the chance of a thing is over one in ten to the fiftieth power, it will NEVER take place. You can get the calculations for all of that in Peter Stoner's work [Science Speaks.]{.class_1921} He proves conclusively by mathematics---not "religion" or anyone's "faith"---that the Bible is a supernatural Book that defies statistical probability. Jeane Dixon, Edgar Cayce, Nostradamus, Mohammed, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_53}and Zoroaster couldn't even come close to reproducing what the Bible did in its prophecies of Christ's First Coming.

But as important as those 48 prophecies of Christ's First Coming are, the Bible has nearly [ten times]{.class_1921} more on His Second Coming. That's what you are reading here in Daniel 2. The Lord recorded for you the vision of that image to let you know ["the stone . . . cut out of the mountain without hands"]{.class_1922} is headed this way to wipe out the United Nations just as ["certain"]{.class_1922} and ["sure"]{.class_1922} as the rise and fall of the Babylonian, Persian, Greek, and Roman Empires in history.

46 Then the king Nebuchadnezzar fell upon his face, and worshipped Daniel, and commanded that they should offer an oblation and sweet odours unto him.

47 The king answered unto Daniel, and said, Of a truth it is, that your God is a God of gods, and a Lord of kings, and a revealer of secrets, seeing thou couldest reveal this secret.

48 Then the king made Daniel a great man, and gave him many great gifts, and made him ruler over the whole province of Babylon, and chief of the governors over all the wise men of Babylon.

49 Then Daniel requested of the king, and he set Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, over the affairs of the province of Babylon: but Daniel sat in the gate of the king.

What Daniel did impresses Nebuchadnezzar. He falls down and worships Daniel (vs. 46). That worship goes beyond just praise and honor (see Luke 14:10). The King prostrates himself before Daniel, like the Samaritan did before Christ in Luke 17:16 and Cornelius did before Peter in Acts 10:25. He offers ["an oblation"]{.class_1922} to Daniel, which was only to be offered to the Lord, under the Law (Lev. 7:29, 22:18; Isa. 19:21). And Nebuchadnezzar is also offering ["sweet odours"]{.class_1922} to Daniel. He burns incense to Daniel, and that is indicative of [prayer]{.class_1921} (2 Chron. 32:12; Rev. 5:8).

Do you know what Daniel does? He stands there, with his mouth shut, and lets Nebuchadnezzar go through with it. He doesn't react like Peter did when Cornelius worshiped him (Acts 10:25--26), or Paul and Barnabas did when the people of Lystra proclaimed them []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_54}gods and tried to sacrifice to them (Acts 14:11--18), or the angel did when the Apostle John fell down to worship him (Rev. 22:8--9).

Daniel allows Nebuchadnezzar to commit sacrilege. That shows you that no matter how good a man is (Ezek. 14:14), he is still just a man and, therefore, a [sinner]{.class_1921} (Rom. 3:23). The best of men in that Book all have something wrong with them. Noah got drunk. Abraham lied about Sarah. Joseph lied about the silver cup. Moses struck the rock when he should have spoken to it. Joshua didn't pray over Ai or the Gibeonites. David committed adultery and murder. Even the best Christian in that Book, the Apostle Paul, went to Jerusalem against the explicit orders of the Holy Ghost. ["ALL flesh is as grass,"]{.class_1922} brethren (1 Pet. 1:24), and if you are looking for someone sinless to follow, the only One you are going to find is the Son of God (Heb. 4:15, 7:26). You sure won't find one in a pedophile, egotistical, murderous, sex-obsessed military dictator like Mohammed.

Verse 46 explains two things that follow here in the book of Daniel. The first is why Daniel doesn't show up in the next chapter when his buddies are thrown into the fiery furnace. Whether Daniel was there beside Nebuchadnezzar when everyone was to bow and was exempted because of his position (see vs. 49), or whether he found business elsewhere due to a guilty conscience, he really couldn't say anything after letting Nebuchadnezzar worship him. The second is, because Daniel didn't go into the fiery furnace with the other three Hebrew children, he had to go into the lions' den alone in chapter 6. The Bookkeeper has a long memory (Gal. 6:7).

Verse 47: ["The king answered unto Daniel, and said, Of a truth it is, that your God is A God of gods, and A Lord of kings." ]{.class_1922}Only partly right, Nebby, old boy. He is not just ["A God of gods"]{.class_1922}; He is ["THE God of gods"]{.class_1922} (11:36; Psa. 136:2). He's the only ["God of gods"]{.class_1922} there is (Deut. 10:17; Josh. 22:22). He is the God who judges every other god He created and kills them off when they get "uppity" (Psa. 82:1, 6--7). He is not just ["A Lord of kings"]{.class_1922} like you, Nebby; He is ["THE prince of the kings of the earth"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 1:5). He is the ["LORD OF LORDS"]{.class_1922} who stomps all over 200 million UN troops like grapes in a wine vat (Rev. 19:15--16; Isa. 63:1--4). He is the One from whom ["the kings of the earth"]{.class_1922} hide when He []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw336.xhtml_page_55}returns in wrath and judgment (Rev. 6:15--16). You had best tread lightly around Him. Better to bow in humility, repentance, and faith now than to bow in forced confession right before He pitches you into the Lake of Fire for your unbelief and rejection (Phil. 2:9--11 cf. Matt. 25:41).

["And a revealer of secrets."]{.class_1922} That's what Pharaoh called Joseph. One of the meanings of ["Zaphnath-paaneah"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 41:45) is "Revealer of secrets." According to Josephus, it also means ["Saviour of the world"]{.class_1921} (cf. John 4:42; 1 John 4:14).

True to his word, Nebuchadnezzar lavishes ["great gifts"]{.class_1922} and honor on Daniel for revealing the dream and its interpretation (vs. 48 cf. vs. 6). Daniel is ["made . . . ruler over the whole province of Babylon"]{.class_1922} (vs. 48). So in Scripture, Babylon is three things: it is a [city,]{.class_1921} it is a [kingdom,]{.class_1921} and it is a ["province"]{.class_1922} (what we would call a "State," today) in that kingdom.

That is something to remember when you get to 1 Peter 5:13. According to the scholars who seek to prop up the private interpretations of the Pope concerning Simon Peter being the first bishop of the church of Rome, the city of Babylon in the First Century A.D. wasn't big enough to support a church. Whether it was or whether it wasn't (and it is a safe bet that it [was]{.class_1921}), ["the church that is at Babylon"]{.class_1922} could have been the collective group of believers in the [region]{.class_1921} or [province]{.class_1921} of Babylon.

Not only is Daniel put in charge of the ["province of Babylon,"]{.class_1922} he is made ["chief of the governors over all the wise men of Babylon."]{.class_1922} There is a hierarchy of authority among all the different wise men in the kingdom of Babylon, and Daniel becomes the "top dog" in the chain of command.

Now even though God showed the dream and interpretation to Daniel, and he was the one who went before the King, he couldn't have done it without the prayer support of his buddies. So Daniel puts in a good word for them to the King and has them made his deputies and lieutenants in administering the day-to-day operations ["of the province of Babylon"]{.class_1922} (vs. 49). In the meanwhile, he sits ["in the gate of the king."]{.class_1922} That is a position like that of a Supreme Court judge.Matters of importance are brought to him to solve so the King won't be bothered with them.

Wrapping up the chapter from a devotional standpoint, the lessons we take away from Daniel 2 are:

1\) Give man time and he will [ruin everything.]{.class_1921} That's what I call the "Law of Human Collapse" (see the Introduction to the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Judges and Ruth]{.class_1921}).

2\) Do not forget to give God the glory, [always.]{.class_1921}

3\) [Prophecy]{.class_1921} is the true test of inspiration.

4\) The last "United Nations" will be controlled by [Rome.]{.class_1921}

5\) God is not through, [even if we are.]{.class_1921}

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml}

# Chapter 3 {.heading_67-0}

3:1 Nebuchadnezzar the king made an image of gold, whose height was threescore cubits, and the breadth thereof six cubits: he set it up in the plain of Dura, in the province of Babylon.

No sooner has Nebuchadnezzar received the interpretation that he is the head of gold in the image of which he dreamed than he goes out and builds an [entire statue of gold.]{.class_1921} We may infer that he builds an image of [himself.]{.class_1921} The idea is that Nebuchadnezzar can be the whole image of his dream and that his kingdom will never end. In other words, after paying lip service to the God who revealed his dream and its interpretation (2:47), Nebuchadnezzar turns right around and [defies what God showed him.]{.class_1921} A lot of people do that with the Bible (Ezek. 33:31; Mark 7:6--13; James 1:22).

Now, there are two things you should notice about this image in verse 1. The first is that only two dimensions are given: ["height"]{.class_1922} and ["breadth."]{.class_1922} The indication is that the idol was a [cylinder.]{.class_1921} It is a pillar, like the Egyptian obelisk in St. Peter's Square or the Washington Monument. Such structures are known as "phallic symbols," representing male reproduction. In ancient religions, these included totem poles and maypoles; modern equivalents would be Christmas trees, flagpoles, skyscrapers, and rockets. Like the Tower of Babel (Gen. 11:4), they all point to the place where Satan wanted to ascend (Isa. 14:12--14).

The second thing to notice is the measurements of the image: ["threescore cubits"]{.class_1922} for the ["height"]{.class_1922} and ["six cubits"]{.class_1922} for ["the breadth."]{.class_1922} A ["score"]{.class_1922} is twenty, so ["threescore"]{.class_1922} would be three times twenty; i.e., [sixty.]{.class_1921} So in ["cubits,"]{.class_1922} the measurement would be sixty by six. Since the width and the breadth are the same on a cylinder, what you have is sixty by six by six: three sixes in a row, 666. The number [six]{.class_1921} keeps popping up in the chapter. In the first paragraph (vss. 1--7), the fact that Nebuchadnezzar ["set up"]{.class_1922} the image is mentioned six times (vss. 1, 2, 3 \[twice\], 5, 7). There are six instruments mentioned in verse 5: 1. cornet, 2. flute, 3. harp, 4. []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_58}sackbut, 5. psaltery, 6. dulcimer. So what you are about to read is a type of the Antichrist and his image (Rev. 13:15--18).

The Antichrist and his kingdom are connected with gold just like Jesus Christ and His kingdom are (Rev. 3:18, 4:4, 21:18, 21). The number 666 is associated with Solomon multiplying gold in his kingdom (2 Chron. 9:13), contrary to the command of God (Deut. 17:17). Those demoniac locusts that come out of the Bottomless Pit in Revelation 9 have ["crowns like gold"]{.class_1922} ["on their heads"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 9:7). In the Tribulation, people ["worship devils"]{.class_1922} by, among other things, ["idols of gold"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 9:20). ["Babylon the great,"]{.class_1922} whether in its religious form (Rev. 17) or economic form (Rev. 18), is ["decked with gold"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 17:4, 18:16). And the first of Babylon's ["merchandise"]{.class_1922} listed in Revelation 18:12 is ["gold."]{.class_1922} Gold never loses its value, and although FDR got you off the "gold standard," it will come back. When it does, [one man will have control of all the gold]{.class_1921} (11:43).

2 Then Nebuchadnezzar the king sent to gather together the princes, the governors, and the captains, the judges, the treasurers, the counsellors, the sheriffs, and all the rulers of the provinces, to come to the dedication of the image which Nebuchadnezzar the king had set up.

3 Then the princes, the governors, and captains, the judges, the treasurers, the counsellors, the sheriffs, and all the rulers of the provinces, were gathered together unto the dedication of the image that Nebuchadnezzar the king had set up; and they stood before the image that Nebuchadnezzar had set up.

4 Then an herald cried aloud, To you it is commanded, O people, nations, and languages,

5 That at what time ye hear the sound of the cornet, flute, harp, sackbut, psaltery, dulcimer, and all kinds of musick, ye fall down and worship the golden image that Nebuchadnezzar the king hath set up:

6 And whoso falleth not down and worshippeth shall the same hour be cast into the midst of a burning fiery furnace.

One government under one religion---everything you just read points to the Antichrist and his image. Revelation 13 says, ["all that dwell upon the earth shall worship him]{.class_1922} \[the Beast\]["]{.class_1922} (Rev. 13:8 cf. Rev. 13:4). The False Prophet convinces people to make an image of the Beast and has anyone who won't worship it killed (Rev. 13:14--15). That's just what you are reading here.

Nebuchadnezzar is a perfect picture of the Antichrist. The Antichrist is called the Beast, and he gets his power from the Dragon (Rev. 13:2--4); that Dragon is Satan (Rev. 12:9). Do you know what Jeremiah 51:34 says of Nebuchadnezzar?

"Nebuchadrezzar the king of Babylon hath devoured me, he hath crushed me, he hath made me an empty vessel, he hath swallowed me up LIKE A DRAGON . . . ."

Now do you see those ["rulers of the provinces"]{.class_1922} there in verses 2 and 3? That included those three Hebrew young men from chapters 1 and 2, whom Nebuchadnezzar renamed ["Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego"]{.class_1922}; they had been put in charge ["over the affairs of the province of Babylon"]{.class_1922} (2:49). Daniel could have fallen under ["the governors"]{.class_1922} and ["the counsellors"]{.class_1922} of verses 2--3, for Nebuchadnezzar had made him ["chief of the governors over all the wise men of Babylon"]{.class_1922} (2:48). But remember, Daniel was Nebuchadnezzar's "Supreme Court judge" (2:49). He was what we would call a "prime minister" today. He was essentially second in command to the King. As such, he would have been exempted from the decree of verses 4--6. That is why Daniel is not mentioned in the chapter: he was probably right there beside Nebuchadnezzar. If that is not the case, then he is "out of town" on some business of the King. Either way, Daniel could not have legitimately spoken up for his buddies because he had let Nebuchadnezzar bow down and worship him back in 2:46 (see our comments on the verse).

Note in verses 5--7 that instrumental music figures prominently in worship. The Church of Christ won't use "mechanical instruments of music" in church because they are mentioned nowhere in the New Testament. The two Scriptures they use to prove this are Ephesians 5:19 and Colossians 3:16. Both verses say Christians are to use ["psalms"]{.class_1922} in their singing. Do you know what you are commanded to do in the ["psalms"]{.class_1922}? You are to praise God []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_60}["with the sound of the trumpet"]{.class_1922} and ["with the psaltery and harp"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 150:3), ["with the timbrel"]{.class_1922} and ["with stringed instruments and organs"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 150:4), and ["upon the loud cymbals"]{.class_1922} and ["upon the high sounding cymbals"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 150:5). ["Psalms"]{.class_1922} are to be [played,]{.class_1921} as well as [sung.]{.class_1921} You find the same thing in Psalm 33:2, 81:2, 92:3, 98:5--6, 108:2, and 149:3.

Music has been around since Genesis 1:1 (Job 38:4--7). The leader of that angelic choir was ["the anointed cherub that covereth"]{.class_1922} (Ezek. 28:13--14), Lucifer himself (Isa. 14:11--12). The modern idea that music itself is neutral and only lyrics make a song bad is a lie of the Devil. Satan desires worship (Luke 4:5--7), and music is part of worship. Bob Jones Sr. used to say, "Every bad thing on this earth is a good thing twisted." If ever a good thing were twisted into a bad thing, music would be it. ["Psalms and hymns and spiritual songs"]{.class_1922} have been replaced in many churches with rock music and "the bumps and the grinds."

Satan has corrupted music since Genesis 4:21, and he will continue to do so to Revelation 13:15. Music is a universal language understood by anyone who hears it. Music that appeals to the flesh and inflames carnal lusts does so for anyone, anywhere, no matter what the "lyrics" are. Such music is one of the principle instruments the Devil uses in these last days.

Although the reader is familiar with instruments like the ["flute"]{.class_1922} and ["harp,"]{.class_1922} he may not be with the other four instruments. The ["cornet"]{.class_1922} was a trumpet made out of metal, like gold, silver, or brass (Hos. 5:8 cf. 1 Chron. 15:28; Psa. 98:6).

The word ["sackbut"]{.class_1922} only appears in the [AV]{.class_1921} here in Daniel 3 (vss. 5, 7, 10, 15). Critics of the Holy Bible are quick to point out that the translation ["sackbut"]{.class_1922} is [wrong]{.class_1921} because the Chaldean word translated ["sackbut"]{.class_1922} here ([sabbeka]{.class_1921}) is similar to a [Greek]{.class_1921} word ([sabbeca]{.class_1921}), which is a [stringed ]{.class_1921}instrument instead of a[ wind]{.class_1921} instrument like the modern sackbut trombone. But the fact is, no scholar can definitely say what a sackbut is one way or another. If you look up the word in Bible dictionaries, you will read things like: ["IF]{.class_1921} this . . . be the same as the Greek or Latin," and the Hebrew word for ["sackbut"]{.class_1922} "has [no convincing etymology."]{.class_1921} Well, if you can't tell []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_61}exactly what it is, how can you definitely say what it "ain't"?

Are you any more "accurate" or "clearer" if you translate the word ["trigon"]{.class_1921} ([RSV, ESV, NASV)]{.class_1921} or ["lyre"]{.class_1921} ([NKJV, NIV]{.class_1921}) [when you don't really know what the instrument is?]{.class_1921} Isn't the truth that you are [guessing]{.class_1921} at the meaning as much as the [King James]{.class_1921} translators did? Of course, they had an advantage to their educated guess that this modern bunch of apostates don't: [they actually believed they were dealing with the words of the Holy Scripture.]{.class_1921} We will no more worry about the possibility of a ["sackbut"]{.class_1922} being some type of trombone than we do ["corn"]{.class_1922} being maize (see our comments on Luke 6:1 in that Commentary).

A ["psaltery"]{.class_1922} was a stringed instrument.

The new "Bibles" don't like the word ["dulcimer"]{.class_1922} any more than they did ["sackbut."]{.class_1922} The [RSV, ESV,]{.class_1921} and [NASV]{.class_1921} all translate the Chaldean word [sumponyah]{.class_1921} as ["bagpipe,"]{.class_1921} while some expositors will tell you, "it is quite unlikely that [sumponia]{.class_1921} is a bagpipe or a dulcimer." Nothing like the "consensus of scholars," is there?

We will stick with the [AV.]{.class_1921} It has never let us down yet, and we won't abandon it for some puffed-up stuffed-shirt who doesn't have a clue about what he is talking. A ["dulcimer"]{.class_1922} is a stringed instrument that can be played with small hammers or quills, or strummed like a mandolin.

The punishment for not bowing down and worshiping Nebuchadnezzar's idol was being ["cast into the midst of a burning fiery furnace"]{.class_1922} (vs. 6). Nebuchadnezzar was already well known for burning his enemies (Jer. 29:21--22, 21:10, 32:29, 34:2, etc.). Obviously this is a picture of [Hell]{.class_1921} (Matt. 13:42, 50).

7 Therefore at that time, when all the people heard the sound of the cornet, flute, harp, sackbut, psaltery, and all kinds of musick, all the people, the nations, and the languages, fell down and worshipped the golden image that Nebuchadnezzar the king had set up.

8 Wherefore at that time certain Chaldeans came near, and accused the Jews.

9 They spake and said to the king Nebuchadnezzar, O king, live for ever.

10 Thou, O king, hast made a decree, that every man that shall hear the sound of the cornet, flute, harp, sackbut, psaltery, and dulcimer, and all kinds of musick, shall fall down and worship the golden image:

11 And whoso falleth not down and worshippeth, that he should be cast into the midst of a burning fiery furnace.

12 There are certain Jews whom thou hast set over the affairs of the province of Babylon, Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego; these men, O king, have not regarded thee: they serve not thy gods, nor worship the golden image which thou hast set up.

The band starts the worship service, and the congregation bows. Notice how the word ["all"]{.class_1922} is used in verse 7. It doesn't mean "all without exception," because the three Hebrew children didn't bow and worship the image. It means "all without distinction"; i.e., all the people from the nations and languages represented there bowed. So just like back in chapter 1, there are undoubtedly some Jewish young men from the captivity who give in and do bow; but just as back in chapter 1, Hananiah, Azariah, and Mishael aren't going along with the crowd.

Anti-Semitism raises its ugly head in verse 7, and it involves [envy.]{.class_1921} Those Chaldeans already had their egos bruised by these Hebrew boys [twice:]{.class_1921} once in 1:19--20 and again in chapter 2 when the three, along with Daniel their leader, did what the Chaldeans couldn't---tell the King his dream. Like those Princes and Presidents in chapter 6, the only ["occasion against"]{.class_1922} these three young men could only be found ["concerning the law of ]{.class_1922}\[their\][ God"]{.class_1922} (cf. 6:5). As soon as these Chaldeans saw that Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego didn't bow, they went "tattling" to the King.

Anti-Semitism is a Satanic thing. The Devil hates that Jew because ["the oracles of God"]{.class_1922} were given to the Jews (Rom. 3:2), ["salvation is of the Jews"]{.class_1922} (John 4:22), the Messiah came from the Jews (Rom. 1:3), and when Satan and his King are cast into the Lake of Fire, it will be a [Judean Jew]{.class_1921} who does it (Rev. 19--20). There is no other reason for 191 nations turning against one nation with less than seven million Jews and blaming it for all the woes of this world.

Again, what you find commanded in verse 10 is [conformity.]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_63} The two things the lost world wants from you, Christian, are [conformity]{.class_1921} (Rom. 12:2) and [love]{.class_1921} (1 John 2:15). It can put up with whatever you believe or profess, as long as you live, talk, think, and act like it does, and love it over Jesus Christ, God, and the Book.

Nebuchadnezzar didn't care if those Hebrew captives continued to serve ["a God of gods, and a Lord of kings"]{.class_1922} (2:47) as long as they bowed to his image when he asked them. The test put to the Christians in the Roman Empire, especially those in the Roman legions, was to burn a pinch of incense to Caesar. That was acknowledging Caesar as a god, and those Christians wouldn't do it. Of course, that was considered "unpatriotic" if you were in the army. That's why those Christians were persecuted as badly as they were. The charge often leveled at them was ["odium humani generis"]{.class_1921}---hatred of the human race. The Christians wouldn't honor the gods in social activities, so the pagans figured they hated folks. If those Christians had worshiped Jesus Christ [and]{.class_1921} Caesar and the heathen gods, they could have gotten by just fine.

That is where you are in America right now. Now that the Supreme Court has made sex perversion "the law of the land," any Christian who sticks with the Book will be viewed as against the government (unpatriotic) and promoting "hate speech" (hatred of humanity). Fines and imprisonment for refusing to participate in the "marriage" of two queers or two dykes are just the beginning of what Christians will face in this country.

13 Then Nebuchadnezzar in his rage and fury commanded to bring Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego. Then they brought these men before the king.

14 Nebuchadnezzar spake and said unto them, Is it true, O Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, do not ye serve my gods, nor worship the golden image which I have set up?

15 Now if ye be ready that at what time ye hear the sound of the cornet, flute, harp, sackbut, psaltery, and dulcimer, and all kinds of musick, ye fall down and worship the image which I have made; well: but if ye worship not, ye shall be cast the same hour into the midst of a burning []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_64}fiery furnace; and who is that God that shall deliver you out of my hands?

This is the original "face the music." That phrase means "to be confronted with the consequences of one's actions." In this case, the "music" was literal. "When you hear the sound of the music, you must bow down and worship the idol, Shadrach, Meshach, Abednego." And if they didn't, it was the ["burning fiery furnace."]{.class_1922}

Verse 13 says Nebuchadnezzar had ["rage and fury."]{.class_1922} The one thing you didn't want to do to an Oriental monarch was make him angry at you. You had no recourse to any higher power on this earth. He had absolute power of life and death over you. You had no right to "trial by jury" or an "appeal." If he gave the order for your execution, you had better have had your will made out ahead of time.

Now although the King is furious with ["Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego,"]{.class_1922} he still tries to be fair with them: ["Is it true . . . ?"]{.class_1922} (vs. 14). He even gives them a second chance, which was probably unheard of for him: ["Now if ye be ready . . . well"]{.class_1922} (vs. 15). In the Middle Ages, during the Inquisition, this was called "recantation": retracting a belief. When Luther was asked by Archbishop Eck at the Diet of Worms whether he would recant what he had written, he ended his answer with this:

Unless I am convinced by the testimony of the Holy Scriptures or by evident reason---for I can believe neither Pope nor councils alone, as it is clear that they have erred repeatedly and contradicted themselves---I consider myself convicted by the testimony of Holy Scripture, which is my basis; my conscience is captive to the word of God. Thus I cannot and will not recant, because acting against one's conscience is neither safe nor sound. God help me. Amen.

Back to verse 14: ["do not ye serve my gods . . . ?"]{.class_1922} The gods of modern America are peace and prosperity (Deut. 23:6), security (Judg. 18:7), social image (1 Sam. 15:30; John 5:44), sex (Gal. 5:19; Eph. 4:19; 1 Pet. 4:13), money (Luke 16:13; 1 Tim. 6:9--10), and []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_65}education (Rom. 1:22; 1 Cor. 1:19--20). Those are the gods to which the world wants you to conform. Those things are just as idolatrous as statues of Baal, Ashtoreth, Jupiter, Mercury, Venus, Thor, Quetzalcoatl, Vishnu, Shiva, Ganesh, and Mary (cf. Col. 3:5).

Notice the archaic spelling of ["musick"]{.class_1922} in verse 15. Some [King James]{.class_1921} Bibles will update the spelling to ["music."]{.class_1921} There's a big difference between changing ["sope"]{.class_1922} to ["soap"]{.class_1922} or ["asswage"]{.class_1922} to ["assuage,"]{.class_1922} or even ["shew"]{.class_1922} to "[show" ]{.class_1921}than there is in changing ["Joseph"]{.class_1922} to ["father"]{.class_1921} in Luke 2:33 or getting rid of ["God"]{.class_1922} from 1 Timothy 3:16 or the Trinity from 1 John 5:7 or the blood from Colossians 1:14, etc. In the end, you haven't changed anything by changing ["ancle"]{.class_1922} to ["ankle"]{.class_1922} in Acts 3:7; [it is the same word.]{.class_1921} The new versions actually [change the text]{.class_1921} (e.g., ["child"]{.class_1922} to ["servant"]{.class_1921} in Acts 4:27, 30).

Verse 15:[ "and who is that God that shall deliver you out of my hands?"]{.class_1922} That's the same argument Sennacherib used when he sent Rabshakeh to issue his ultimatum to Hezekiah and Jerusalem (2 Kings 18:32--35). The idea was: "What makes you think your God can help you when the gods of all the other nations I conquered couldn't help them?" But like Hezekiah said in his prayer to the Lord, the reason those gods couldn't help those nations was because ["they were no gods"]{.class_1922} (2 Kings 19:18). Sennacherib ended up losing 185,000 of his troops and his own life when he tangled with Jehovah God (2 Kings 19:35--37).

It is interesting to note the word ["God"]{.class_1922} is capitalized in verse 15, even though it refers to [any]{.class_1921} god; you will see the same thing in 6:7. There are a couple of reasons for this. The first is that although Nebuchadnezzar makes allowance for other gods, he is aiming at the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego (ditto 6:7 where those Princes and Presidents are aiming at the God of Daniel). Since that God is the true God, the [King James]{.class_1921} translators capitalized the word. The second reason is that Nebuchadnezzar has already acknowledged the Hebrew God as the [supreme]{.class_1921} God (2:47).

And of course, the ultimatum of verse 15 is what the Jews will face again in the Tribulation. Then, it will be bow to the image of the Antichrist or [get your head cut off]{.class_1921} (Rev. 13:15 cf. Rev. 20:4). That is the choice Christians are given right now in places like Iraq, Syria, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_66}Indonesia, Nigeria, Sudan, Saudi Arabia, etc.: accept Islam, repeat the Shahada ("There is no God but Allah, and Mohammed is his prophet."), or get your head sawed off.

16 Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, answered and said to the king, O Nebuchadnezzar, we are not careful to answer thee in this matter.

17 If it be so, our God whom we serve is able to deliver us from the burning fiery furnace, and he will deliver us out of thine hand, O king.

18 But if not, be it known unto thee, O king, that we will not serve thy gods, nor worship the golden image which thou hast set up.

This is a great picture of a Christian testimony. If you want to show how much nerve you have, this is the way to do it. It is a polite, quiet, cool, calm, nice way to say, ["Go take a flying jump at the moon."]{.class_1921} Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego are respectful to Nebuchadnezzar, but they are emphatic:[ they will not bow.]{.class_1921}

["We are not careful to answer thee in this matter"]{.class_1922} (vs. 16). The word ["careful"]{.class_1922} is used in its original meaning: "full of care" (see the same usage in Phil. 4:6). Silly translations like the [ASV, NASV, RSV, ESV, NIV,]{.class_1921} and the [NEW KING JAMES VERSION]{.class_1921} (not a [King James Version]{.class_1921} in any sense) all read: ["We have no need to answer you in this matter."]{.class_1921} Then those three Hebrew boys proceed to give Nebuchadnezzar an answer in the matter. Someone will say, "Well, [chashach]{.class_1921} (the Chaldean word translated ["careful"]{.class_1922} here) means 'have need of.'" True, but it also can mean ["careful."]{.class_1922} When you have a choice between a translation that makes sense and one that doesn't, you always take the one that makes sense in the context---unless you are a modern Conservative, Liberal, Evangelical, or Fundamentalist; in which case you choose the reading that conflicts with the God-honored text of the Reformation.

Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego aren't being obstinate or sarcastic in their answer to the King and saying, "We don't need to give you an answer as to why we did what we did." They are saying, "We aren't worried or anxious about what we're about to say to you, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_67}Nebuchadnezzar."

The practical application for the Christian is that there are some things about which not only are you not to worry (Phil. 4:6), but about which you don't even need to pray. If the Bible is clear in a matter, you don't need to pray and say, "God, what should I do about this?" He already told you in the Book.

When it came to the matter of idolatry, those Hebrew boys didn't need to pray about it. God had already told them in the Scriptures not to bow down to or serve any graven image (Exod. 20:4--5). The consequences of obeying God over the King were irrelevant: [God came first]{.class_1921} (Acts 4:19--20). They weren't worried about what was expedient or convenient or "in their best interests"; they were concerned with [what was right.]{.class_1921}

Now, there has been many a Christian throughout history who has been hauled before the rulers and magistrates of his day to give account of his faith. With the way things are going in this nation right now, you can look forward to doing that yourself if you stick with the Book. The thing to remember is just do right day by day, and don't fret over what you are going to say when the time comes. Jesus told His apostles:

["But when they deliver you up, take no thought how or what ye shall speak: for it shall be given you in that same hour what ye shall speak. For it is not ye that speak, but the Spirit of your Father which speaketh in you"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 10:19--20).

Paul said that when he stood before Nero, ["the Lord stood with me, and strengthened me"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 4:17). You do right and stay prayed up and speak up for the Lord when you should, and if the time should ever come where you are put in the same situation as Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, the Holy Spirit will give you what to say.

Verse 17: ["IF IT BE SO, our God whom we serve is ABLE to deliver us."]{.class_1922} Now that's the problem when we get in trouble. We don't doubt God's [ability]{.class_1921} to get us out of a scrape; whether He [will]{.class_1921} is another matter. The Lord got Peter out of Herod's jail there in Acts 12, but He didn't get James out. The Lord let Herod kill James ["with the sword"]{.class_1922} (Acts 12:2). You can't dismiss that ["If the Lord WILL"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_68} about which James wrote (James 4:15).

Back during the Middle Ages, there was a Spanish Jew named Moses Botarel. Botarel claimed Elijah appeared to him in a dream and anointed him to be the Messiah. When he was hauled before the King of Spain to answer for what the Catholics considered to be blasphemy, Botarel, following the godly example of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, demanded to be thrown in ["a burning fiery furnace"]{.class_1922} (vs. 17) in order to prove his Messiahship. Those Spanish Catholics were only too happy to oblige him. You say, "What happened to him?" [Old "Mose" was burnt to a crisp.]{.class_1921}

What was the problem? [Moses Botarel was out of the will of God.]{.class_1921} The Messiah had already come, and Moses Botarel had rejected Him as Saviour. Even if he had accepted his Messiah, there was no guarantee he would have made it through the flame. The Catholics burned William Tyndale at the stake, and he was not only a born-again child of God, he gave England the Bible in its native tongue. That Bible says, ["others were tortured, not accepting deliverance"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 11:35).

Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego recognized the fact that it might not be the Lord's will to deliver them. Look at verse 18: ["BUT IF NOT, be it known unto thee, O king, that we will not serve thy gods, nor worship the golden image which thou hast set up."]{.class_1922} In other words, if God didn't deliver them, they still wouldn't bow.

People in Britain and America used to know the Bible so well that they could recognize a Bible verse when it was quoted. Back in 1940, before America entered World War II, the British Expeditionary Force had become trapped at Dunkirk on the English Channel when the Germans invaded France through Belgium and the Netherlands. Over 338,000 troops were about to be wiped out by Nazi forces, and if they had been, that would have been the beginning of the end for Britain. They wouldn't have been able to have defended themselves against a full-scale invasion. The General of the British forces, General Alan Brooke, said, "Nothing but a miracle can save the British Expeditionary Force now."

In desperation, a three-word message was sent back to England: ["But if not"]{.class_1922} (some accounts have ["And if not"]{.class_1921}). The British populace were so well-versed in the [King James]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_69} Bible that they recognized immediately the quote was from Daniel 3:18. In other words, unless God performed a miracle, those British troops knew they were going to die, but they were willing to make that sacrifice if they had to.

The British people responded and sent 800 vessels to evacuate those troops, everything from cruisers to canoes. When it looked like the German [Luftwaffe]{.class_1921} was going to prevent those ships from reaching the British troops, God sent in a weather system that grounded the German aircraft. But none of that would have happened if the British people hadn't responded to that three-word message from a [King James]{.class_1921} Bible.

19 Then was Nebuchadnezzar full of fury, and the form of his visage was changed against Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego: therefore he spake, and commanded that they should heat the furnace one seven times more than it was wont to be heated.

20 And he commanded the most mighty men that were in his army to bind Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, and to cast them into the burning fiery furnace.

21 Then these men were bound in their coats, their hosen, and their hats, and their other garments, and were cast into the midst of the burning fiery furnace.

22 Therefore because the king's commandment was urgent, and the furnace exceeding hot, the flame of the fire slew those men that took up Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego.

Nebuchadnezzar is "fit to be tied." Verse 19 says, ["the form of his visage was changed against Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego."]{.class_1922} That's the look on his face. Any self-control Nebuchadnezzar was exercising back in verses 13--15 was gone. That bird was so angry that his face probably turned red, purple, and black.

Nebuchadnezzar commands that furnace to be heated ["one seven times more than it was wont to be heated"]{.class_1922} (vs. 19). That word ["wont"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_70} there is an adjective that means "in the habit of" or "accustomed to." The translators of the modern versions will tell you that such a word is "archaic," and then they will change up to 64,000 words in your Bible to get rid of only about a hundred "archaic" words. Of course, not all of the "archaic words" are actually "archaic." In his work [Archaic Words and the Authorized Version,]{.class_1921} Dr. Laurence Vance shows you that a lot of the words the scholars claim are "archaic" are still used in modern books, magazines, newspapers, advertising, and parlance with their "archaic" meanings.

The truth is, any Christian can understand the so-called "archaic words" in the [AV]{.class_1921} if he is taught right or he [studies]{.class_1921} (2 Tim. 2:15---changed in all the new "Bibles" so you won't study God's word). The simple way of handling it is to put the meaning in the margin or center column. After all, editors put all kinds of notes in Bibles casting doubt on the text; why not, rather, put notes in there to [define]{.class_1921} the text without destroying the reader's faith in the word of God.

The text is clear without having to change anything: the furnace was heated seven times hotter than normal. Nebuchadnezzar was going to make an example of those Jewish captives just as He did to their hometown, Jerusalem, six years earlier (Ussher assigns a date of 580 B.C. to this passage, and Jerusalem was destroyed in 586 B.C.).

Nebuchadnezzar then gets his Green Berets, Rangers, Seals, and Delta Force elite troops (["the most mighty men that were in his army"]{.class_1931}---vs. 20) to tie up the three Hebrews, clothes and all (vs. 21), and pitch them into the furnace. The ["hosen"]{.class_1931} of verse 21 is easily understood. You women call them "panty hose" today. These ["hosen"]{.class_1931} would be called "leggings" or "leotards" today. They were originally a [man's]{.class_1932} article of clothing. (Where that leaves Fundamentalists who use Deut. 22:5 to stop the women in their congregations from wearing pants, I have no idea.)

Nebuchadnezzar is so angry that he takes no care for the safety of his own men. He orders the three Hebrews to be cast into the fire the moment the heat has been raised seven times hotter. To make sure those boys get into the furnace, the soldiers get so close to the fire []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_71}that they breathe in the flames and die themselves (vs. 22). Remember that if you have to face in Obama's and the Democrats' America what your brethren had to face in the Roman imperial persecutions and medieval Roman Catholic Europe. If you ever get burned alive at the stake, and you want to go quickly, bend your head down and breathe in the flames.

23 And these three men, Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, fell down bound into the midst of the burning fiery furnace.

24 Then Nebuchadnezzar the king was astonied, and rose up in haste, and spake, and said unto his counsellors, Did not we cast three men bound into the midst of the fire? They answered and said unto the king, True, O king.

25 He answered and said, Lo, I see four men loose, walking in the midst of the fire, and they have no hurt; and the form of the fourth is like the Son of God.

Now Nebuchadnezzar is playing "God" in this chapter. He has an image made of himself and demands everyone worship it. If they don't, they are pitched into a type of Hell. That's the state in which Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego find themselves. But if you trust God, you don't have to worry about Hell. If you did go, the Lord would be right there with you.

David wrote, ["If I ascend up into heaven, thou art there: if I make my bed in hell, behold, thou art there"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 139:8).

Brethren, all Hell is, is a manifestation of one of God's attributes: ["For our God is a consuming fire"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 12:29). If you are a believer, you are [in]{.class_1921} that God. The reason you are not burned by that fire is because your Saviour took it for you. The lost person has not availed himself of that imputation; he has to suffer the ["consuming fire"]{.class_1922} of God's wrath himself.

In the days when settlers were making their way across the continent to the West in Conestoga wagons, they would sometimes see a prairie fire being blown their way by the winds that swept across the open plains. There was no way to outrun it; the only thing to do was what was known as "backfiring." They would set a fire []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_72}behind them, and as soon as the burnt ground was cool enough, they would back the wagon train onto the blackened ground. When the prairie fire reached them, it couldn't go any further because all the grass had already been burned.

Now I trust you understand that illustration. If you are saved, the fires of God's wrath won't ever touch you. Why? [Because they already touched your Saviour on Calvary,]{.class_1921} and if you are in Him, you can't be burned. [He was already burned for you.]{.class_1921}

Those Hebrew boys wouldn't bend, they wouldn't bow, and [they wouldn't burn.]{.class_1921} Why not? Because ["the Son of God"]{.class_1922} was there in the fire with them (vs. 25).

Verse 25 is changed in all the new "Bibles" to ["a son of the gods."]{.class_1921} The egomaniacs who put out those apostate translations think they have more sense than God. They figure Nebuchadnezzar was a pagan polytheist who didn't believe in the one, true God and, therefore, couldn't possibly know anything about ["the Son of God."]{.class_1922}

But Nebuchadnezzar was not quite as ignorant as the translators and revisers of the modern versions would have you believe. He had obviously become acquainted with the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego back in 2:47. Moreover, he was familiar with Jeremiah and his prophecy (see Jer. 39:11--12, 40:1--2).

All the pagan Gentiles were familiar with ["the sons of God"]{.class_1922} who came down in Genesis 6:1--4, and that is the theme of all the "ancient astronaut" documentaries on the History Channel. They also knew those ["sons of God"]{.class_1922} were part of the angelic host from Heaven (Job 1:6, 2:1, 38:7).

Four hundred years before Nebuchadnezzar was born, Solomon wrote of the fact that God had a special "son," and asked concerning His name (Prov. 30:4). That's exactly what Jacob and Manoah did when they encountered the Angel of the Lord (Gen. 32:29--30; Judg. 13:16--18). That "son," who appeared as an ["angel"]{.class_1922} in the Old Testament, is identified in the New Testament as Jesus Christ, the Son of God (Acts 27:23; Gal. 4:14; also Josh. 5:13--15 cf. Heb. 2:10).

Nebuchadnezzar didn't need to know that ["the Son of God"]{.class_1922} was Jesus Christ or had anything to do with the man Jesus Christ. All he had to know was that God had ["sons,"]{.class_1922} that He had a special "son," and that that Son appeared from time to time to the Hebrews. He got []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_73}that, of course, from conversing with his "right hand man," Daniel (1:19--20 cf. 2:48--49).

Now have you noticed that when the new translations have a choice to honor and exalt Jesus Christ, or to dishonor and degrade Him, they will, many times, choose the latter. For example, in Acts 4:27, 30, when given the choice of translating [pais]{.class_1921} as ["child"]{.class_1922} (which it [can]{.class_1921} be) or ["servant"]{.class_1921} (which it also can be), they will choose the reading that de-emphasizes Christ's [incarnation.]{.class_1921}

That is the case here in Daniel 3:25. The phrase in question is ["bar elahin." "Bar" ]{.class_1921}is the Hebrew and Aramaic word for "son of" (as in ["Simon Barjona"]{.class_1922}---Matt. 16:17). ["Elahin"]{.class_1921} is a form of [Elohim,]{.class_1921} meaning "God" or "gods," depending on which is being referred to. Now in Hebrew, the word [bar]{.class_1921} is what is known as a "construct noun." The definiteness or indefiniteness of a construct depends on the "absolute noun" that follows it; in this case, ["elahin."]{.class_1921} If ["elahin"]{.class_1921} is translated [God,]{.class_1921} then the translation of ["bar"]{.class_1921} requires the definite article [the]{.class_1921}---["the Son of God."]{.class_1922}

But if ["elahin" ]{.class_1921}is translated ["gods,"]{.class_1921} then ["son"]{.class_1921} gets the indefinite article [a---"a son."]{.class_1921} The problem is ["elahin"]{.class_1921}[ ]{.class_1935}has no definite article. So ["a son of the gods"]{.class_1921} is not even a legitimate translation. It would have to be "a son of gods" or ["the Son of God,"]{.class_1922} but not ["a son of the gods."]{.class_1921} These incredible hypocrites won't even follow their own rules of Hebrew grammar---after complaining the [King James]{.class_1921} doesn't translate "the article" correctly.
