I understand all of this is highly technical, but you have to understand that all these translators who hold "the originals" in such high esteem don't care one whit about the Greek or Hebrew when it crosses [their opinions and preferences.]{.class_1921} The reason these apostates picked ["a son of the gods"]{.class_1921} over ["the Son of God"]{.class_1922} is because they will pick any translation that takes the glory away from Jesus Christ and gives it to the Devil. If you think that is an overstatement, look at what the [NIV]{.class_1921} and the [ESV]{.class_1921} do to identify Satan with Jesus Christ in Isaiah 14:12 (cf. Rev. 22:16).

Nebuchadnezzar knew Daniel and his buddies worshiped [one God,]{.class_1921} not "gods." He had acknowledged that this God was superior to all other gods. He knew that God could do what no other god could do, and when he doubted it (vs. 16), God proved it in a very dramatic []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_74}way by preserving Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego in a fire that slew the strongest men in Nebuchadnezzar's army. Why would he think the fourth man in the fire was a son of ["Nergal"]{.class_1922} or ["Succothbenoth"]{.class_1922} (2 Kings 17:30), or ["Bel"]{.class_1922} or ["Merodach"]{.class_1922} (Jer. 50:2), or ["Nebo"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 46:1)? These apostates are so crooked that if they fell in a barrel of fishhooks, they'd never get stuck.

What you have in verse 25 is a "theophany"---God appearing as the Angel of the Lord in the Old Testament. It is a "Christophany"---an appearance of Jesus Christ before His incarnation as a man.

Now, when Nebuchadnezzar looked in the fire, he was ["astonied."]{.class_1922} Our word is [astonished.]{.class_1921}[ ]{.class_1935}["Astonied" ]{.class_1922}is a good word: the King was [petrified ]{.class_1921}with fear. He saw ["four men loose, walking in the midst of the fire"]{.class_1922}---they were no longer bound; ["and they have no hurt"]{.class_1922}---no first, second, or third degree burns; ["and the form of the fourth is like the Son of God"]{.class_1922}---he saw the Angel of the Lord in there with Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego.

One of the first chances I got to preach after I was saved was on this story. Hugh Pyle, the preacher who led me to Christ, had me in to draw for some children. I had just gotten saved out of the Catholic Church, and I hadn't had all the "rough edges" knocked off my doctrine yet. I left the distinct impression with those kids that if they didn't live right, they might burn in Purgatory for a while. But Bro. Pyle had a lot of grace with me, and got up after I was through and straightened everything out.

Over the years, I have refined that message (I no longer put Purgatory in). I draw those three fellows there in the fire with mittens, ear muffs, scarves, and parkas. I don't think they even felt warm in that furnace. And the points of my sermon are things I see when I look in that furnace.

I. We see [grace]{.class_1921} in the furnace (cf. 2 Cor. 11:23--33, 12:7--10). The Son of God brings grace (John 1:17).

II\. We see [consecration]{.class_1921} in the furnace. Daniel wouldn't stop praying (Dan. 6:10), Peter wouldn't stop preaching (Acts 5:29), the Rechabites wouldn't disobey their daddy (Jer. 35:6--14), and those three boys wouldn't bow.

III\. We see [liberty]{.class_1921} in the furnace. The fire that wouldn't burn Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, was able to burn off the ropes []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_75}that bound them without even singeing their clothes. In your natural state, you are bound with the cords of sin (Prov. 5:22), but when you get saved, the Lord sets you free (Gal. 5:1) to ["walk in newness of life"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 6:4).

IV\. We see [protection]{.class_1921} in the furnace. Those young men were safer in the fire with Jesus Christ than Peter was by the fire without Him (Mark 14:54).

If you are a Christian, you will go through the fiery trials of life (1 Pet. 4:12). The thing to remember is that God allows you to go through them, not to destroy you, but to [refine]{.class_1921} you (Mal. 3:2--4). God's purpose is to bring out the gold that will survive the Judgment Seat of Christ (Job 23:10 cf. 1 Cor. 3:12--15). Down here, the Lord puts you through the purging process so you will bear fruit (John 15:2) and become ["a vessel . . . meet for the master's use, and prepared unto every good work"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 2:20--21). As you go through ["the fiery trial,"]{.class_1922} you can ["rejoice, inasmuch as ye are partakers of Christ's sufferings"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 4:13). We can ["endure"]{.class_1922} the trials with happiness because we know that, eventually, the Lord will bring us out of the furnace (James 5:11). It may be through the door of death, but we have the promise that ["to depart, and to be with Christ . . . is far better"]{.class_1922} (Phil. 1:23).

26 Then Nebuchadnezzar came near to the mouth of the burning fiery furnace, and spake, and said, Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, ye servants of the most high God, come forth, and come hither. Then Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, came forth of the midst of the fire.

27 And the princes, governors, and captains, and the king's counsellors, being gathered together, saw these men, upon whose bodies the fire had no power, nor was an hair of their head singed, neither were their coats changed, nor the smell of fire had passed on them.

28 Then Nebuchadnezzar spake, and said, Blessed be the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, who hath sent his angel, and delivered his servants that trusted in him, and have changed the king's word, and yielded their bodies, that they might not serve nor worship any god, except []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_76}their own God.

29 Therefore I make a decree, That every people, nation, and language, which speak any thing amiss against the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, shall be cut in pieces, and their houses shall be made a dunghill: because there is no other God that can deliver after this sort.

30 Then the king promoted Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, in the province of Babylon.

Nebuchadnezzar calls Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego out of the fire: ["come forth, and come hither"]{.class_1922} (vs. 26). It would have served Nebuchadnezzar right if they had retorted with: "Why don't you come in here and get us."

That's what Paul did at Philippi. He and Silas had been arrested, beaten, and thrown in jail without trial. That was a big "no no" when dealing with a Roman citizen. The next day when the magistrates of the city had calmed down, they sent word to the jailer to release Paul and Silas. But Paul wasn't going to let such a thing slide.

["But Paul said unto them, They have beaten us openly uncondemned, being Romans, and have cast us into prison; and now do they thrust us out privily? nay verily; but let them come themselves and fetch us out"]{.class_1922} (Acts 16:37).

That shook those "city fathers" up bad, boy. They came begging Paul and Silas to leave peacefully without causing any problem with them with the Roman authorities.

["Then Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, came forth of the midst of the fire"]{.class_1922} (vs. 26). Did you notice that the fourth man didn't come out? ["The Son of God"]{.class_1922} stayed in the fire.

One time when a Sunday school teacher was teaching this lesson, she asked the children, "Why do you think the Son of God stayed in the fire?" A little girl said, "So that He would be in there when we have to go through the fire." Amen! That's the best reason you'll ever hear. [Jesus is there in the fire to get you through it when it's your turn.]{.class_1921}

Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego acted respectfully to the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_77}King. They came out of the furnace before all the other government officials who had bowed down before the golden image. Not only were neither they nor their clothes burnt or even singed, they didn't even smell like fire or smoke. That's something else, did you know that? You can't even walk into a convenience store to pay for your gas without coming out smelling like Marlboros, Camels, Dorals, Chesterfields, etc.

Now what you just read is quite a "laser operation." The Lord manages to burn (or melt) the bonds off the boys with no harm or trace of the fire on their clothes or persons. That's a picture of an operation the Holy Ghost performs on every born-again child of God when he gets saved.

That ["word of God is quick, and powerful, and sharper than any twoedged sword, piercing even to the dividing asunder of soul and spirit, and of the joints and marrow"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 4:12). When you get saved, the Holy Ghost takes that ["sword of the Spirit"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:17) and cuts your ["new man"]{.class_1922} in Christ (Eph. 4:24; Col. 3:10) away from your body of sinful flesh so that it can never affect your spiritual destination ever again. That's what Paul called[ "the circumcision made without hands"]{.class_1922} (Col. 2:11) because it is ["the operation of God"]{.class_1922} (Col. 2:12). It is a [spiritual circumcision]{.class_1921} about which Fundamentalists like Curtis Hutson know nothing---[by their own admission.]{.class_1921}

Notice the Gentile designation for God in verse 26: ["the most high God."]{.class_1922} The first time that expression shows up is from the mouth of a Gentile priest---Melchizedek---whose priesthood transcends the Levitical priesthood (Gen. 14:18--22 cf. Heb. 6:20, 7:4--11). He is King of Jerusalem (Gen. 14:18; Heb. 7:2), and he is a type of Christ (Heb. 7:3). Melchizedek called ["the most high God"]{.class_1922} the ["possessor of heaven and earth"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 14:19, 22). As the Owner of the universe, ["the most high God"]{.class_1922} gives the earth to the descendants of Abraham through Isaac and Jacob (NOT Ishmael: [Mohammed doesn't get anything]{.class_1921}) (Rom. 4:13), and He divides the heavens to twelve Gentile nations (Deut. 32:8 cf. Deut. 4:19). The Church, the Body and Bride of Christ, gets the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:2).

Verse 28: ["Then Nebuchadnezzar spake, and said, Blessed []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_78}be the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, who hath sent HIS ANGEL."]{.class_1922} Then Nebuchadnezzar knew the fourth man in the fire wasn't ["a son of the gods."]{.class_1921} He calls that fourth man ["HIS ANGEL"]{.class_1922}---[the Angel of the Lord.]{.class_1921} That's not ["a son of the gods"]{.class_1921}; that's ["the Son of God"]{.class_1922} (Acts 27:23; Gal. 4:14).

There is a great sermon in verse 28. Those Hebrew boys ["trusted"]{.class_1922} God. Because they did, God ["delivered"]{.class_1922} them. That's [salvation.]{.class_1921} They ["yielded their bodies"]{.class_1922} so they could ["serve"]{.class_1922} God. And of course, that is what a Christian is supposed to do once he gets saved (Rom. 6:13--16, 12:1).

When those Hebrew boys trusted God and ["yielded their bodies"]{.class_1922} to Him, they ["changed the king's word."]{.class_1922} The King, in that case, is Satan's King---a type of the Antichrist. That's a picture of you getting victory over the Devil. That Bible says, ["Let not sin therefore reign in your mortal body"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 6:12), and ["sin shall not have dominion over you"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 6:14).

Notice the [personal relation]{.class_1921} the Hebrews had to God: ["their own God."]{.class_1922} That's why we ask folks, "Have you accepted Jesus Christ as your PERSONAL Saviour?" It's not enough just to "believe in God." The devils believe that, and they're headed for Hell (James 2:19). You must [personally]{.class_1921} trust the work Jesus Christ did for you (John 1:12).

Catholics have a real problem with that. They readily acknowledge that Jesus Christ came to save sinners and that He came to save the world. But if you ask a Catholic to name one sinner for whom Christ died, he will hem and haw and draw a blank. I know; I've asked them. I can tell you a sinner for whom Christ died---ME!

It doesn't do any good to stand up every Sunday morning and recite the Apostles' Creed, and profess to believe that Jesus "was crucified, died, and was buried. He descended into Hell; the third day He rose again from the dead." That's [not]{.class_1921} the Gospel. The Gospel is ["that Christ died FOR OUR SINS according to the scriptures; And that he was buried, and that he rose again the third day according to the scriptures"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 15:3--4). There's nothing in the Apostles' Creed about Christ dying for anybody's sins---READ IT! Believing in "the forgiveness of sins" is not the same as believing Christ died for YOUR sins. If all you believe for []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_79}salvation is what's in the Apostles' Creed, you'll go to Hell like a bullet. You have to trust Christ's sacrifice for YOUR SINS. Salvation is [personal.]{.class_1921}

Verse 29: ["Therefore I make a decree, that every people, nation, and language, which speak any thing amiss against the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, shall be cut in pieces, and their houses shall be made a dunghill: because there is no other God that can deliver after this sort."]{.class_1922} That's quite a decree, boy. That's better than what you have in America right now. The government will take taxpayer money and sponsor TV programs that will say outright, "The Bible is wrong," but if they were to sponsor a TV program saying, "The Bible is right," they would be sued by the ACLU for "separation of Church and State." You can get on TV and radio and use the names of [God]{.class_1921} and [Jesus Christ]{.class_1921} as curse words, and no one will say a word. But if you pay for television time on a secular television station or network and say that Jesus Christ is the only way to Heaven, a disclaimer will precede your program stating that "the views of this program aren't necessarily the views of this station or its sponsors." You can drive down the street with enough decibels coming out the radio speakers in your car to fry an egg, and that is your "freedom of expression," but get on a street corner and yell loud enough to be heard (because you aren't allowed to use a bullhorn), "No hope in the Pope! Turn or burn! Repent or perish! Rome enslaves, but Jesus saves!" and the city council will try to pass a "noise ordinance" with the specific purpose of [shutting you up.]{.class_1921} You can stand on the street corner with a sign advertising a "close-out" sale (going on for five years!), and no one will flip you off or yell obscenities at you or complain. But stand on that same street corner holding up a Scripture sign, and you are "distracting traffic."

Nebuchadnezzar said, "Believe and worship any god you want, but the moment you say anything bad about the God of the Hebrews, I'll 'slice and dice' you and make your house a manure pile." Why? ["Because there is no other God that can deliver after this sort."]{.class_1922}

That's what impressed Darius over in 6:27---["He delivereth and rescueth, and he worketh signs and wonders in heaven []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_80}and in earth, who hath delivered Daniel from the power of the lions."]{.class_1922}

Over in Psalm 50:15, the Lord says, ["And call upon me in the day of trouble: I will deliver thee, and thou shalt glorify me."]{.class_1922} Years ago I was going through, what I thought back then, some pretty rough times. Of course, looking back on it, things weren't as tough as I made them out to be, but as the old saying goes, "Hindsight is better than foresight." I had in the inside cover of my Bible Psalm 50:15 pasted to give me some encouragement. Well, I was in a first-rate mess, so I called on God ["in the day of trouble."]{.class_1922} I prayed, I confessed every sin I could think of, I searched the Scriptures, I claimed the promises, and [I got nothing.]{.class_1921}

Well, I got discouraged, and I stopped reading my Bible. You know that when Pete Ruckman stops reading his Bible, things are tough. I wasn't interested in any doctrine, and I couldn't even get anything out of the Psalms. Things got so bad that I couldn't find anything to read. To me, reading was just like liquor to a drunkard; I had read a book a day since I was ten years old.

But after you have read the Bible, all other books can seem pretty bland. Who has a taste for fiction after you have read the Bible? At one point, I went down to a newsstand to find something to read. I found a book there called [Stalingrad.]{.class_1921} It was by a reporter who had been on the Russian front during the Battle of Stalingrad. The front of that book had a picture on it of a couple of tanks in the snow with men shooting at each other.

I had been saved about fifteen years by then and had pretty well forgotten the old life. But as I looked at that cover, the Lord spoke to me and said, "You see that? That is what you were raised to do. You weren't raised to go around in a shirt, tie, and nice clothes. You weren't raised to shake folks' hands and smile at them. You weren't raised to teach Christians the Bible or play the harmonica for kids in vacation Bible school. You were raised to get out in the dirt, the mud, and the snow, and shoot and die out there."

To make a long story short, I bought that book, took it home, and read it. After reading what those German boys went through for a demon-possessed madman like Hitler, my troubles didn't seem so bad. My bed seemed to feel so good at night. I would get under those []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw413.xhtml_page_81}clean, white sheets at night, and they would feel so good. I would sit down to eat a bowl of smoky green pea soup with a piece of black bread, and it was just like a sirloin steak to me, man.

After a while, I said to myself, "Well, things could be worse." I picked up my Bible and started reading it again. Of course, I was still put out with the Lord, so when I came across a promise, I would explain it away with: "Well, that's for Israel; not me." But eventually, the Lord got me through my problem.

I went out and got that Scripture sticker I had torn out of my Bible and taped it back in. That's when I noticed the last part of that verse: ["and thou shalt glorify me."]{.class_1922} I had forgotten that part. The Lord put me through those troubles to [glorify Him.]{.class_1921} God gave Paul ["a thorn in the flesh"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 12:7) so that the Lord's ["strength"]{.class_1922} would be ["made perfect"]{.class_1922} in Paul's ["weakness]{.class_1922}" (2 Cor. 12:9).

Nebuchadnezzar himself still doesn't believe in God. That's what's coming up in chapter 4. Right now, Nebuchadnezzar has a high respect for a God who can reveal what Daniel's God revealed and deliver like Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego's God delivered. The New Testament spiritual application is that anything short of belief in the atoning work of Jesus Christ and receiving Him as your personal Saviour is NOT salvation. You can believe in one God like a Moslem, be baptized like a Campbellite, join the "one, true church" like a Catholic, "receive the initial evidence of the baptism of the Holy Ghost and speak in other tongues" like a Charismatic, keep the Ten Commandments and the Golden Rule like a Protestant, AND DIE LOST AND GO TO HELL. The touchstone of the Gospel is John 1:12.

"But as many as received him, to them gave he power to become the sons of God, even to them that believe on his name."

In closing, the lessons we learn from Daniel 3 are as follows:

1\) Most rulers are [religious.]{.class_1921}

2\) All rulers have the same ambition.

3\) You must have [convictions]{.class_1921} about the word of God in order to stand.

4\) God's people are always under attack.

5\) Compromise will solve nothing.

6\) God will honor an uncompromising stand.

7\) Christ is the only sure protection.

8\) "Every tub must stand on its own bottom."

That last one simply means that you can't ride the coattails of someone else's spirituality forever. You are going to have to  "prove" yourself, sooner or later, apart from your parents, your spouse, your friends, your pastor, your Bible teacher, etc. It will be just you and God.

Verse 30: ["Then the king promoted Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, in the province of Babylon."]{.class_1922} This promotion has nothing to do with Daniel going "to bats" for them, and getting them put ["over the affairs of the province of Babylon"]{.class_1922} (2:49). This promotion comes directly from the King based on what God did for Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego when they stood for what was right [apart from Daniel.]{.class_1921} You aren't told what extra responsibilities, authority, or privileges they were given above and beyond what they had at the end of chapter 2; but whatever they were, they were [better]{.class_1921} than what they had before. Why? They stood (literally) for God and what was right on their own, [no matter what Daniel did.]{.class_1921}

Brethren, sometimes you will have to stand for what is right even when the "good, godly" brethren don't. During my Christian life, I had to stand for that Book when my professors, teachers, and buddies in the ministry [didn't.]{.class_1921} After 65 years of butting heads with the Fundamental, Conservative, and Evangelical scholars over the Book, I am here to tell you that God can take care of you, even when the combined forces of "Christian scholarship" are all against you.

["Wherefore take unto you the whole armour of God, that ye may be able to withstand in the evil day, and having done all, TO STAND"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:13).

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml}

# Chapter 4 {.heading_67-0}

4:1 Nebuchadnezzar the king, unto all people, nations, and languages, that dwell in all the earth; Peace be multiplied unto you.

2 I thought it good to shew the signs and wonders that the high God hath wrought toward me.

3 How great are his signs! and how mighty are his wonders! his kingdom is an everlasting kingdom, and his dominion is from generation to generation.

The chapter is an unusual one in the Bible in that the whole thing is dictated to Daniel by a Gentile King---Nebuchadnezzar. The whole chapter is Nebuchadnezzar speaking in the first person. He is "giving his testimony."

Now this "testimony" is in the form of an official decree: ["unto all people, nations, and languages, that dwell in all the earth"]{.class_1922} (vs. 1). This is the third time such a decree has gone out; but my, my, my, how different it is from the previous two. Look at how the sentence ends: ["Peace be multiplied unto you."]{.class_1922} You talk about a "change of pace" for Nebuchadnezzar, that was it! When he made decrees to ["all people, nations, and languages"]{.class_1922} back in chapter 3, someone was going to [die]{.class_1921} (Dan. 3:5--6, 29). He wasn't interested in or worried about anybody's ["peace."]{.class_1922} Something has [changed ]{.class_1921}in the heart and life of this despot, and that is what Nebuchadnezzar is about to tell you.

Notice the ["signs and wonders"]{.class_1922} in verses 2--3. The ["signs and wonders"]{.class_1922} were given to the [Jews]{.class_1921} (1 Cor. 1:22; Exod. 4:28--31), but they are shown here to Nebuchadnezzar because he is dealing with a Jew---Daniel. That is exactly the case with the Apostle Paul in his work among the Gentiles (2 Cor. 12:12; Mark 16:15--18 cf. Acts 14:8--11, 19:10--12, 28:1--9; Rom. 15:16--20).

[Now what you are looking at, prophetically, is the ministry of the two witnesses and the 144,000 Jews in the Tribulation to the Antichrist and his crowd (Rev. 7 cf. Rev. 11:3--6). ]{.class_1920}Those 144,000 Jewish evangelists go out preaching ["the gospel of the kingdom"]{.class_1931} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_84}to the whole world (Matt. 24:14) with the apostolic signs and wonders (Mark 16:17--18), and ["a great multitude . . . of all nations"]{.class_1931} get saved (Rev. 7:9, 14).

["His kingdom is an everlasting kingdom, and his dominion is from generation to generation"]{.class_1922} (vs. 3). You can tell Nebuchadnezzar has been in a "Bible study" with Daniel, because what you just read is a quote from Psalm 145:13. Now Nebuchadnezzar may be thinking back to his vision and its interpretation back in 2:44, where ["the God of heaven set up a kingdom, which shall never be destroyed . . . and it shall stand for ever"]{.class_1922}; but as we are about to see in this chapter, the Lord is about to give Nebuchadnezzar a lesson so he will ["know that the most High ruleth in the kingdom of men, and giveth it to whomsoever he will"]{.class_1922} (vs. 25). So this ["everlasting kingdom"]{.class_1922} of verse 3 is God overseeing the political dominions of this world [now.]{.class_1921}

Now how do you reconcile that with the fact that Satan is ["the god of this world"]{.class_1922} [now]{.class_1921} (2 Cor. 4:4)? The Devil told Jesus ["all the kingdoms of the world"]{.class_1922} were ["delivered"]{.class_1922} to [him]{.class_1921} to dispense as he would (Luke 4:5--6), and Jesus didn't contradict him. Well, what you have is God delegating the power over the political nations of the world to the Devil, just like ["the power of death"]{.class_1922} is delegated to him (Heb. 2:14). That is due to the [sinfulness of man]{.class_1921} (Rom. 5:12, 7:14). The Lord turned His own nation of people, the Jews, over to Nebuchadnezzar (Ezra 5:12). Just like the Devil can't do anything to the child of God without the Lord's permission (Job 1--2), the rulers of this present world system, under Satan's control, can't take office without the allowance of God Almighty. ["The powers that be are ordained of God"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 13:1), even when the "power" is someone like Nebuchadnezzar, Nero, Napoleon, Hitler, or Obama; and quite often, they are ["ordained"]{.class_1922} for the [judgment]{.class_1921} of a nation in rebellion against the "Ordainer."

4 I Nebuchadnezzar was at rest in mine house, and flourishing in my palace:

5 I saw a dream which made me afraid, and the thoughts upon my bed and the visions of my head troubled me.

6 Therefore made I a decree to bring in all the wise men of Babylon before me, that they might make known unto me the interpretation of the dream.

7 Then came in the magicians, the astrologers, the Chaldeans, and the soothsayers: and I told the dream before them; but they did not make known unto me the interpretation thereof.

The word ["rest"]{.class_1922} in verse 4 is used in the same way it is in 2 Samuel 7:1, 11. Nebuchadnezzar has ceased his warfare and has built up his capital city (cf. vs. 30). It is this time of rest and prosperity that gets Nebuchadnezzar into trouble. Ditto the generation that enters into the Tribulation (1 Thess. 5:3).

Now Nebuchadnezzar has a second dream that ["troubled"]{.class_1922} him (vs. 5 cf. 2:1). The previous dream dealt with the devolution of human government to the kingdom of the Devil under the Antichrist; this one deals with Nebuchadnezzar [personally.]{.class_1921}

As before, Nebuchadnezzar calls in ["the magicians, the astrologers, the Chaldeans, and the soothsayers"]{.class_1922} (vs. 7). We have defined all these terms except one in our comments on 1:4, 20 and 2:2. The one with which we didn't deal was ["soothsayers."]{.class_1922} The word [sooth]{.class_1921} is the Middle English word for "truth," as in [forsooth]{.class_1921}---"of a truth." A soothsayer was someone who was supposed to tell the truth about something (usually the future) through [occult]{.class_1921} means. You have an example of this in Acts 16:16--17. There you have a girl ["possessed with a spirit of divination . . . which brought her masters much gain by soothsaying."]{.class_1922} When she saw Paul and his companions, that unclean spirit in her caused her to follow them, crying out, ["These men are the servants of the most high God, which shew unto us the way of salvation."]{.class_1922} That was the [truth,]{.class_1921} but it was used to be a [distraction]{.class_1921} to the apostles' ministry and take the glory for the revelation from God and give it to a devil.

Unlike before in chapter 2, this time, Nebuchadnezzar tells the dream to his wise men, but they fare no better than they did back in chapter 2: ["they did not make known unto me the interpretation thereof"]{.class_1922} (vs. 7). Perhaps they were afraid of what the King would do to them if they tried to "buffalo" him (cf. 2:8--9), but that just goes to show you that if God wants []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_86}["to conceal a thing"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 25:2), there is no way you will find it, not even by "faking it."

8 But at the last Daniel came in before me, whose name was Belteshazzar, according to the name of my god, and in whom is the spirit of the holy gods: and before him I told the dream, saying,

9 O Belteshazzar, master of the magicians, because I know that the spirit of the holy gods is in thee, and no secret troubleth thee, tell me the visions of my dream that I have seen, and the interpretation thereof.

Remember, Nebuchadnezzar is dictating these events after the fact. For the first time, Nebuchadnezzar refers to Daniel by his [Hebrew]{.class_1921} name and adds, ["whose name WAS Belteshazzar, according to the name of my god"]{.class_1922} (vs. 8). Something has changed in Nebuchadnezzar. He lets you know that he [used]{.class_1921} to call Daniel "Belteshazzar," but that has changed. After what takes place here in chapter 4, Nebuchadnezzar is now calling Daniel by the name of the Hebrews' God (see our comments on 1:6--7).

Notice that Nebuchadnezzar recognizes the difference between [his god]{.class_1921} (vs. 8---["my god"]{.class_1922}; i.e., the idol to which he personally prayed, like a "patron saint" in the Catholic Church) and ["the holy gods."]{.class_1922} Those ["holy gods"]{.class_1922} aren't some polytheistic "gods" of Babylonian mythology; they are ["the holy angels"]{.class_1922} of Matthew 25:31; Mark 8:38; Luke 9:26; and Revelation 14:10. They are called ["holy gods"]{.class_1922} to distinguish them from the gods whom God slew ["like men"]{.class_1922} in the Flood for leaving ["their first estate"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 82:6--7 cf. Job 38:6--7; Gen. 6:1--4; Jude 6).

The Bible believer should take note that ["the spirit of the holy gods"]{.class_1922} (i.e., the Holy Spirit) was ["IN"]{.class_1922} Daniel. This stands in stark contrast to the Fundamentalist view, taken from the [Scofield Reference Bible]{.class_1921} (see Scofield's note on "Summary of the Old Testament doctrine of the Holy Spirit" under Mal. 2:15), that in the Old Testament, the Holy Spirit would come [on]{.class_1921} a believer, but [not in ]{.class_1921}a believer. That view can only be taken by ignoring the word of the Holy Spirit in the [Authorized Version]{.class_1921} of 1611. []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_87}["The Spirit of God"]{.class_1922} was ["in"]{.class_1922} Joseph (Gen. 41:38). He was ["in"]{.class_1922} Joshua (Num. 27:18), as He was in Moses (Isa. 63:11). ["Bezaleel the son of Uri"]{.class_1922} was ["filled . . . with the spirit of God"]{.class_1922} (Exod. 31:3, 35:31). The Holy Spirit ["entered into"]{.class_1922} Ezekiel (Ezek. 2:2, 3:24). In fact, 1 Peter 1:10--11 says ["the Spirit of Christ"]{.class_1922} was ["in"]{.class_1922} all the Old Testament prophets.

The difference between the Holy Spirit coming into some believers in the Old Testament and the Holy Spirit indwelling all believers in the New Testament is that in the Old Testament, He would enter a believer for a [specific purpose]{.class_1921} (e.g., Exod. 31:3--4) and could [leave]{.class_1921} if the believer didn't live right (1 Sam. 16:14; Psa. 51:11). In the New Testament, the Holy Spirit comes into the believer to place him in Christ's spiritual Body (1 Cor. 12:13). Not only is ["Christ in you"]{.class_1922} (Col. 1:27), you are [in Him]{.class_1921} (2 Cor. 5:17). The Holy Spirit seals the believer in Christ ["unto the day of redemption"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 1:13, 4:30). Unlike the Old Testament believer who could lose his salvation through sin (see Ezek. 18:24--26), the New Testament believer is ["kept by the power of God through faith unto salvation ready to be revealed in the last time"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 1:5). The Holy Spirit has cut the "new man in Christ" away from the body of sinful flesh so it can never be affected by it again (Col. 2:11--12).

["No secret troubleth thee"]{.class_1922} (vs. 9). That's not in the sense of Daniel being upset when he found out what the dream meant, because he was ["troubled"]{.class_1922} when the interpretation was revealed to him (vs. 19). No secret troubled Daniel in the sense that he didn't have a hard time figuring out what the secret was and what it meant.

10 Thus were the visions of mine head in my bed; I saw, and behold a tree in the midst of the earth, and the height thereof was great.

11 The tree grew, and was strong, and the height thereof reached unto heaven, and the sight thereof to the end of all the earth:

12 The leaves thereof were fair, and the fruit thereof much, and in it was meat for all: the beasts of the field had shadow under it, and the fowls of the heaven dwelt in the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_88}boughs thereof, and all flesh was fed of it.

13 I saw in the visions of my head upon my bed, and, behold, a watcher and an holy one came down from heaven;

14 He cried aloud, and said thus, Hew down the tree, and cut off his branches, shake off his leaves, and scatter his fruit: let the beasts get away from under it, and the fowls from his branches:

15 Nevertheless leave the stump of his roots in the earth, even with a band of iron and brass, in the tender grass of the field; and let it be wet with the dew of heaven, and let his portion be with the beasts in the grass of the earth:

16 Let his heart be changed from man's, and let a beast's heart be given unto him; and let seven times pass over him.

17 This matter is by the decree of the watchers, and the demand by the word of the holy ones: to the intent that the living may know that the most High ruleth in the kingdom of men, and giveth it to whomsoever he will, and setteth up over it the basest of men.

18 This dream I king Nebuchadnezzar have seen. Now thou, O Belteshazzar, declare the interpretation thereof, forasmuch as all the wise men of my kingdom are not able to make known unto me the interpretation: but thou art able; for the spirit of the holy gods is in thee.

This vision of the great tree is repeated in Ezekiel 31:3--6, concerning ["the Assyrian."]{.class_1922} That's a reference to the [Antichrist]{.class_1921} in Isaiah 10. Jesus Christ uses the tree to picture a false, worldly faith that attracts demons (see Matt. 13:31--32 and comments on that passage in that Commentary). So Nebuchadnezzar is once more revealed as a type of the Antichrist, and Babylon as the source of a false religion (cf. Rev. 17).

The expression ["a watcher and an holy one"]{.class_1922} in verse 13 is what is known as a hendiadys: two words connected by the conjunction [and]{.class_1921} which refer to the same thing or person. The most well-known hendiadys in the Bible is in Titus 2:13, where []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_89}["the great God"]{.class_1922} is the same person as ["our Saviour Jesus Christ."]{.class_1922} Here, the ["watcher"]{.class_1922} and the ["holy one"]{.class_1922} are the same being. The word ["holy one"]{.class_1922} is another word for ["saint"]{.class_1922} in the Old Testament (see 8:13). While it can refer to an Old Testament saint individually (Psa. 106:16) or to the nation of Israel corporately (Psa. 50:5, 89:5, 7), it can also refer to angels of God (8:13).

Now we take it for granted, due to the reference to ["an holy one"]{.class_1922} that ["came down from heaven,"]{.class_1922} that this ["watcher"]{.class_1922} is an angel, but the Bible distinguishes between different spiritual beings from Heaven: angels, the archangel, cherubim, and seraphim. The Bible is not specific as to which of these the watchers of Daniel 4 are. We shall call them "angels," but realize that is just an opinion about which I am not absolutely sure.

Evidently, the Lord has specific angels whose job it is to keep an eye on things down here. Also, it appears, from verse 17, that they have some degree of authority and power from God to enact decisions against people down here on earth, and those decisions are based on the fact that they are very jealous for the Lord. They resent it when they see someone taking God's glory for himself. They testify against a sinful man or nation (Jer. 4:16).

["The decree . . . and demand"]{.class_1922} of these watchers and holy ones (vs. 17) is that the tree be cut down, the branches lopped off, the leaves shaken off, the fruit scattered, and the beasts and birds that found shade and lodging in it be chased away. But in the midst of this judgment, the stump and roots are left, ["with a band of iron and brass"]{.class_1922} around it. Those are symbols of strength and judgment. The gold head of 2:38 has been downgraded to ["a band of iron and brass."]{.class_1922} The stump and roots speak to the fact that the "tree" can make a "comeback" and sprout again (Job 14:7--9); the iron-brass band indicates that the tree will still have strength to execute judgment.

Verse 16 tells us that the tree represents a [man:]{.class_1921} ["Let his heart be changed from man's."]{.class_1922} But notice that ["a beast's heart"]{.class_1922} is given to this man. That's a mental condition the psychiatrists call "lycanthropy." It is a form of madness where the person takes on the characteristics of a beast, usually a wolf. That's from where the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_90}legend of the werewolf comes. It is classified as a form of "acute mania," a major mood disorder involving enduring periods of persistent "irritable moods." The "enduring period of persistent irritable moods," here, turns out to be [seven years]{.class_1921} (["let seven times pass over him"]{.class_1922}---vs. 16 cf. 7:25, 12:7; Rev. 12:14). As we shall see in the interpretation (vs. 25), this man who becomes an animal lives out in the field with other beasts, in "[the dew of heaven"]{.class_1922} (vs. 15).

We have already mentioned under our remarks on verse 3 how ["the most High ruleth in the kingdom of men, and giveth it to whomsoever he will"]{.class_1922} (vs. 17). But notice the "rule of thumb" for God's choice for Gentile rulers: ["and setteth up over it the BASEST of men."]{.class_1922} Of course, there are exceptions to the rule, but the rule is God gives a nation the kind of ruler it [deserves.]{.class_1921} Evidently, what the United States has deserved, for the most part, in the last sixty or so years is ["lewd fellows of the baser sort"]{.class_1922} (Eisenhower, JFK, Johnson, Nixon, Carter, both Bushes, Clinton, Obama). They weren't the good men or the big shots in God's sight; they were the "low lifes," the rotten men.

You aren't going to get a strong Christian man into office, because the majority of people in this country who do read the Bible don't believe it. "Christians," these days, fashion "Jesuses" and "Bibles" to fit their own "politically correct" philosophy to get along with a lost world. Don't expect God to give any country that does that the right kind of a ruler.

We have already commented on the material in verse 18 under our remarks on verses 7--9.

19 Then Daniel, whose name was Belteshazzar, was astonied for one hour, and his thoughts troubled him. The king spake, and said, Belteshazzar, let not the dream, or the interpretation thereof, trouble thee. Belteshazzar answered and said, My lord, the dream be to them that hate thee, and the interpretation thereof to thine enemies.

20 The tree that thou sawest, which grew, and was strong, whose height reached unto the heaven, and the sight thereof to all the earth;

21 Whose leaves were fair, and the fruit thereof much, and in it was meat for all; under which the beasts of the field dwelt, and upon whose branches the fowls of the heaven had their habitation:

22 It is thou, O king, that art grown and become strong: for thy greatness is grown, and reacheth unto heaven, and thy dominion to the end of the earth.

23 And whereas the king saw a watcher and an holy one coming down from heaven, and saying, Hew the tree down, and destroy it; yet leave the stump of the roots thereof in the earth, even with a band of iron and brass, in the tender grass of the field; and let it be wet with the dew of heaven, and let his portion be with the beasts of the field, till seven times pass over him;

24 This is the interpretation, O king, and this is the decree of the most High, which is come upon my lord the king:

25 That they shall drive thee from men, and thy dwelling shall be with the beasts of the field, and they shall make thee to eat grass as oxen, and they shall wet thee with the dew of heaven, and seven times shall pass over thee, till thou know that the most High ruleth in the kingdom of men, and giveth it to whomsoever he will.

26 And whereas they commanded to leave the stump of the tree roots; thy kingdom shall be sure unto thee, after that thou shalt have known that the heavens do rule.

27 Wherefore, O king, let my counsel be acceptable unto thee, and break off thy sins by righteousness, and thine iniquities by shewing mercy to the poor; if it may be a lengthening of thy tranquillity.

["Astonied"]{.class_1922} (vs. 19) is an archaic form of [astonished.]{.class_1921} It carries the idea that a person is like a stone in that he is petrified with fear. Daniel is so ["astonied"]{.class_1922} that he sits dazed for a whole hour, unable to tell Nebuchadnezzar what God has shown him. When he finally is able to speak, he says, ["My lord, the dream be to them that hate thee, and the interpretation thereof to thine enemies"]{.class_1922} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_92}(vs. 19). Even after all Nebuchadnezzar had done to Daniel, his family, his buddies, his people, and his city (Jerusalem), Daniel is still loyal to the King. The Christian is commanded to ["be subject unto the higher powers"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 13:1) and ["Honour the king"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 2:17). That was said of a demon-possessed egomaniac---Nero. I reckon if Peter and Paul can be loyal to a devil like that, you shouldn't have any problems submitting yourself to your government. I know things are getting bad and will get worse, but ["Ye have not yet resisted unto blood, striving against sin"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 12:4). You haven't gone through in this country what your brethren have in times past (the Roman Empire and Europe in the Middle Ages), or even what some of your brethren have in this day and age (Iran, Iraq, Syria, Saudi Arabia, Nigeria, Sudan, India, Pakistan, Russia, Bulgaria, Romania, Indonesia, China, Vietnam, etc.).

Daniel is upset for the King because [the tree is Nebuchadnezzar]{.class_1921} (vs. 22). David wrote, ["I have seen the wicked in great power, and spreading himself like a green bay tree"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 37:35). That was Nebuchadnezzar; that is the Catholic Church (Matt. 13:31--32); that will be the Antichrist (Ezek. 31:3--18).

Now the tree is a similitude (Hos. 12:10) the Holy Spirit uses to teach us about men. Not only is the wicked man likened to ["a green bay tree,"]{.class_1922} the righteous man is likened to a palm tree and a cedar tree (Psa. 92:12). The psalmist said he is ["like a tree planted by the rivers of water, that bringeth forth his fruit in his season; his leaf also shall not wither"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 1:3).

Like a tree, a man can produce good fruit or bad fruit (Matt. 7:17--18), and if he doesn't produce good fruit, he is cut down ["and cast into the fire"]{.class_1922} like a worthless tree (Matt. 7:19; Luke 3:9). Like a tree in the Winter and Spring, a man experiences a death and resurrection. Every Winter, a tree\
"dies," and every Spring, it "comes back to life." And a man's lineage is called his "family tree."

Some men are flexible, like a palm tree. When the winds of adversity blow, they are able to bend in the breeze and survive. Other men are inflexible like an oak tree. When the hurricane hits, they break. If you want a good lesson or sermon on men, study []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_93}different trees.

["Thy greatness is grown, and reacheth unto heaven"]{.class_1922} (vs. 22). Nebuchadnezzar imitated his "father" (John 8:44 cf. Isa. 14:13--14). That's why he set up that phallic symbol there ["in the plain of Dura"]{.class_1922} (see 3:1 and comments).

The expression ["the end of the earth"]{.class_1922} in verse 22 means "the furthest reaches of the land" (Isa. 42:10; Zech. 9:10). It is basically where the land ends and the sea begins; in Nebuchadnezzar's case, that would be the Mediterranean Sea, the Red Sea, and the Persian Gulf. It has come to mean the furthest reaches of man's dominion, what we would call the "known world," today.

Note that ["the decree of the watchers"]{.class_1922} from verse 17 turns out to be ["the decree of the most High"]{.class_1922} in verse 24. So just as the Devil has to get permission to do anything to a child of God, angels have to get permission to do anything to a lost man. God does not bring this trouble on Nebuchadnezzar just for "general purposes"; it is to [teach]{.class_1921} him something: ["till thou know that the most High ruleth in the kingdom of men, and giveth it to whomsoever he will"]{.class_1922} (vs. 25). And when Nebuchadnezzar learned that lesson, he was promised his kingdom back (vs. 26).

The judgment against Nebuchadnezzar was that he was to be turned, for all practical purposes, into an animal. He was to be put out to pasture and feed with the oxen for seven years. The ["they"]{.class_1922} of verse 25 is, undoubtedly, men and not the watchers; probably either his guards or ministers (vs. 33).

Notice all the references to the Antichrist here. Here is a man who is a [beast.]{.class_1921} He eats grass with the oxen. Satan was a cherub (Ezek. 28:14), and the face of a cherub was the face of an [ox]{.class_1921} (Ezek. 1:10 cf. Ezek. 10:14). Down in verse 33, Nebuchadnezzar's hair grew ["like eagles' feathers,"]{.class_1922} and one of the faces of the cherubim was that of an eagle (Ezek. 1:10, 10:14).

Note also, in verse 26, ["that the heavens ]{.class_1922}\[plural\][ do rule."]{.class_1922} It's not just God in Heaven; there is a hierarchy in the first, second, and third heavens that controls the affairs of nations. The Devil is ["the prince of the power of the air"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 2:2), and he has a chain of command under him by which he rules ["all the kingdoms of the world"]{.class_1922} (Luke 4:5). They are given in Ephesians 6:12---[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_94}["principalities," "powers," "the rulers of the darkness of this world," "spiritual wickedness in high places."]{.class_1922} Those ["high places"]{.class_1922} aren't [political]{.class_1926} high places; they are [literal]{.class_1926} ["high places."]{.class_1922}

["And it shall come to pass in that day, that the LORD shall punish the host of the HIGH PLACES that are ON HIGH, and the KINGS OF THE EARTH upon the EARTH"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 24:21).

Those ["principalities"]{.class_1922} of Ephesians 6:12 aren't real men like Presidents, Premiers, Prime Ministers, or "Chairmen." They are [angels.]{.class_1921} ["The prince of Persia"]{.class_1922} in Daniel 10:13, 20 wasn't a real man; ["the prince of Grecia"]{.class_1922} in Daniel 10:20 wasn't a real man. The Prince of Israel in Daniel 10:13, 12:1 wasn't a real man. We will reserve further comment on this until we get to chapter 10.

Back to Daniel 4. ["Wherefore, O king . . . break off thy sins by righteousness, and thine iniquities by shewing mercy to the poor"]{.class_1922} (vs. 27). Salvation by [works;]{.class_1921} no faith to it. Daniel didn't tell Nebuchadnezzar to "look forward" to any "cross." Of course, Nebuchadnezzar is about to exercise faith in ["the King of heaven"]{.class_1922} (vs. 37), but works were a part of it in a way they are [not]{.class_1921} for you this side of Calvary (Eph. 2:8--9). Salvation in the Old Testament, whether it was for Jews or Gentiles, was [not]{.class_1921} the same as salvation in the New Testament.

Note that Nebuchadnezzar could have avoided ["the decree of the watchers"]{.class_1922}; all he had to do was [repent. ]{.class_1921}How is that for changing Calvin's "eternal decrees of God" (cf. vs. 24). If you are under Calvin's "decree of reprobation," I'll tell you how to get out of it. Get to Jesus Christ just as quickly as you can, repent of your own self-righteousness, and trust Him and His blood atonement for salvation. You say, "What if I'm not one of the elect?" Come to Christ anyway and [hold Him to His word:]{.class_1921}[ "him that cometh to me I will in no wise cast out"]{.class_1922} (John 6:37). If you come to Jesus Christ for salvation, He won't turn you away, no matter how "reprobate" you are.

You want ["tranquillity"]{.class_1922} (vs. 27---the state of being at peace)? Come to Jesus Christ.

["Therefore being justified by faith, we have peace with God through our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_95} (Rom. 5:1).

["For he is our peace, who hath made both one, and hath broken down the middle wall of partition between us; Having abolished in his flesh the enmity, even the law of commandments contained in ordinances; for to make in himself of twain one new man, so making peace; And that he might reconcile both unto God in one body by the cross, having slain the enmity thereby: And came and preached peace to you which were afar off, and to them that were nigh"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 2:14--17).

The old saying is: "Know Jesus, know peace; no Jesus, no peace."

28 All this came upon the king Nebuchadnezzar.

29 At the end of twelve months he walked in the palace of the kingdom of Babylon.

30 The king spake, and said, Is not this great Babylon, that I have built for the house of the kingdom by the might of my power, and for the honour of my majesty?

31 While the word was in the king's mouth, there fell a voice from heaven, saying, O king Nebuchadnezzar, to thee it is spoken; The kingdom is departed from thee.

32 And they shall drive thee from men, and thy dwelling shall be with the beasts of the field: they shall make thee to eat grass as oxen, and seven times shall pass over thee, until thou know that the most High ruleth in the kingdom of men, and giveth it to whomsoever he will.

33 The same hour was the thing fulfilled upon Nebuchadnezzar: and he was driven from men, and did eat grass as oxen, and his body was wet with the dew of heaven, till his hairs were grown like eagles' feathers, and his nails like birds' claws.

["All this came upon the king Nebuchadnezzar"]{.class_1922} (vs. 28): he didn't repent, so everything Daniel told him came to pass. If you go to Hell after being told how to escape, you have no one to blame but yourself.

A whole year goes by, and Nebuchadnezzar is out strutting around the palace, gazing out over the city, bragging to himself, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_96}["Is not this great Babylon, that I have built for the house of the kingdom by the might of MY power, and for the honour of MY majesty?"]{.class_1922} (vs. 30). Wrong thing to say; wrong thing to think. It was God Almighty who had turned all the nations over to Nebuchadnezzar for him to conquer (Jer. 27:1--8). Without the Lord, Nebuchadnezzar would have had [nothing]{.class_1921} (cf. Deut. 8:18).

God [hates]{.class_1921}[ "a proud look"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 6:17); He [resists]{.class_1921}[ "the proud"]{.class_1922} (James 4:6; 1 Pet. 5:5). ["Pride goeth before destruction, and an haughty spirit before a fall"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 16:18). Nebuchadnezzar is about to fall, and he is about to fall hard.

["While the word was in the king's mouth . . ."]{.class_1947}[ ]{.class_1948}(vs. 31): he hasn't even gotten through with his boasting. [". . . there fell a voice from heaven, saying, O king Nebuchadnezzar, to thee it is spoken; The kingdom is departed from thee."]{.class_1922} And down on his hands and knees he goes, grunting and growling like an animal. One of his personal bodyguards looks into his eyes, and it is obvious that "the light's on, but nobody's home." The mind of the man is gone, and only a beast is left.

He becomes so wild that he is driven out of the palace. There's the King of the Babylonian Empire, on the front lawn of his palace, chewing up grass. For seven years he sleeps outdoors in the elements. No one can get near him to bathe him, change his clothes, cut his hair, give him a shave, or trim his nails. His hair grows so thick and is so matted that it looks ["like eagles' feathers"]{.class_1922}; his nails grow so long they look ["like birds' claws"]{.class_1922} (vs. 33). He was the "Howard Hughes" of his day: long hair, long nails, alone and naked, and [just as nutty as a fruitcake.]{.class_1921}

Now that brings up the question of mental illness: is it a [spiritual]{.class_1921} problem? The answer is, many times it is, but sometimes it isn't. Sometimes mental disorders are caused by chemical imbalances in the body or a traumatic event like what soldiers go through in battle. Those kinds of things require medicines and counseling. But a lot of people are in the "looney bin" because of [sin:]{.class_1921} they violated their conscience so badly it drove them crazy, or they yielded themselves to the Devil and became ensnared by him (1 Tim. 3:7; 2 Tim. 2:26). Nebuchadnezzar became so puffed up with pride that God took his []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_97}mind from him.

34 And at the end of the days I Nebuchadnezzar lifted up mine eyes unto heaven, and mine understanding returned unto me, and I blessed the most High, and I praised and honoured him that liveth for ever, whose dominion is an everlasting dominion, and his kingdom is from generation to generation:

35 And all the inhabitants of the earth are reputed as nothing: and he doeth according to his will in the army of heaven, and among the inhabitants of the earth: and none can stay his hand, or say unto him, What doest thou?

36 At the same time my reason returned unto me; and for the glory of my kingdom, mine honour and brightness returned unto me; and my counsellors and my lords sought unto me; and I was established in my kingdom, and excellent majesty was added unto me.

37 Now I Nebuchadnezzar praise and extol and honour the King of heaven, all whose works are truth, and his ways judgment: and those that walk in pride he is able to abase.

At the end of the seven years, Nebuchadnezzar lifts his eyes up to Heaven. That is a sign he is becoming a man again. Animals don't naturally look up; they look down or around. Man is able to look up to the One who made him.

When Nebuchadnezzar's understanding returned to him, the first thing he did was bless, praise, and honor the Lord. The word ["extol"]{.class_1922} (vs. 37) means "to praise highly." One is reminded of the words of the angels at Christ's birth: ["Glory to God IN THE HIGHEST, and on earth peace, good will toward men"]{.class_1922} (Luke 2:14). There can be no ["tranquillity,"]{.class_1922} personally or nationally, without ["Glory to God in the highest."]{.class_1922}

We have already commented on the latter part of verse 34 under our remarks on verse 3 (which see). But look at the connection to God's everlasting kingdom and dominion in what follows in verse 35: ["all the inhabitants of the earth are reputed as nothing: and he doeth according to his will . . . among the inhabitants of the earth: and none can stay his hand."]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_98} That's God dealing with the Gentile peoples with an ["army."]{.class_1922}

Jeremiah said, ["But the LORD is the true God, he is the living God, and an everlasting king: AT HIS WRATH THE EARTH SHALL TREMBLE, AND THE NATIONS SHALL NOT BE ABLE TO ABIDE HIS INDIGNATION"]{.class_1922} (Jer. 10:10).

God has ["a controversy with the nations"]{.class_1922} (Jer. 25:31), and when He settles accounts with them, He does it with [armed conflict]{.class_1921} (Rev. 19:11--15). The Lord intends to stomp all over the Antichrist and his armies, and when He does, no one is going to ["disannul it"]{.class_1922} or ["turn it back"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 14:25--27).

["All the inhabitants of the earth are reputed as nothing."]{.class_1922} They aren't just ["as nothing," "they are counted to him LESS THAN NOTHING"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 40:17). That's a cipher with the rim knocked out. That means the United States of America doesn't rate as high as a zero on God's scale of importance; we're in the [minus]{.class_1921} numbers.

Now look at what happened in verse 36. Here is a guy who has been living as a beast out in the field for seven years. He probably looked like a cross between a wolf, an ox, and a bird of prey. He's an absolute mess. But during all that time, the King's ministers never chose anyone else to take the throne. One day, this "beast-man" looks up to Heaven, starts praising God, and stands back upright on his feet. His ["counsellors"]{.class_1937-0} and ["lords"]{.class_1937-0} didn't hesitate a minute: they came out to him, cleaned him up, put the crown and his royal robes back on him, and set him back on the throne (vs. 36). In fact, he had ["excellent majesty . . . added"]{.class_1937-0} to him that he didn't have before he went mad. [That was a miracle of God.]{.class_1938} That was God taking care of that old boy.

["Now I Nebuchadnezzar praise and extol and honour the King of heaven"]{.class_1922} (vs. 37). Finally, Nebuchadnezzar becomes converted (in an Old Testament Gentile sense). Daniel's wisdom back in chapter 1 didn't convert him. Learning of God's prophetic plan back in chapter 2 didn't convert him. Not even the miracle of God delivering Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego from the fiery furnace converted him. It took God knocking him out for seven years to get him right. That is why the admonition is to ["Humble YOURSELVES"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_99} (James 4:10; 1 Pet. 5:6). You would do better to humble yourself than to force God to humble you. It is always easier to take God speaking to you to get you right than it is for Him to take the "belt" to you.

["All whose works are truth, and his ways judgment."]{.class_1922} The cross-references are Deuteronomy 32:4; Psalm 33:4--5; and Revelation 15:3, 16:7, 19:2. Notice that last reference. That's a reference to God's judgments being ["true and righteous"]{.class_1922} in burning ["MYSTERY, BABYLON THE GREAT, THE MOTHER OF HARLOTS AND ABOMINATIONS OF THE EARTH" ]{.class_1922}(Rev. 17:5, 16, 18:8). That's the system with which Nebuchadnezzar was connected.

Nebuchadnezzar said "Amen" to what God did to him. The practical lesson from that and Revelation 19:2 is that one day, the lost will have to agree with God [as to their own damnation.]{.class_1921} Bob Jones Sr. used to say that the most terrible sound in the world is a lost sinner being cast into Hell, and as he goes, he yells, "AAAAAMEEEN!"

I agreed with God on my own damnation, but I did it March 14, 1949. I told the Lord I was headed for Hell unless He did something for me pretty quickly. I then accepted the way out He provided for me: [the sacrifice of His Son.]{.class_1921} Because of that, I will never have to go to Hell. [Now]{.class_1921} is the time, sinner friend, to admit you are headed for Hell and need a Saviour (2 Cor. 6:2), not at the White Throne Judgment.

["Those that walk in pride he is able to abase."]{.class_1922} He sure can. He will take the Antichrist and abase him all the way ["down to hell, to the sides of the pit"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 14:15 cf. Ezek. 21:25--26; Job 40:11--12). That's true of any sinner who exalts himself and his righteousness over the righteousness of Jesus Christ (Luke 18:14 cf. Rom. 10:3).

In closing, here are the lessons we learn from Daniel 4.

1\. [The greater the man, the greater the humbling process.]{.class_1921} The saying out in the world is: "The bigger they are, the harder they fall."

Take a man like Hitler. He became dictator of Germany and managed to conquer nearly all of continental Europe. He was a great man, a famous man; so the humbling process had to be great. One by []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_100}one, the Allied forces took back everything he had conquered until Hitler was holed up in a bunker in Berlin as the Russians were coming in. He ended up committing suicide, and his body was burned. "Today Germany; tomorrow the world!" He got a bullet to the brain by his own hand. My, my, my, what a humbling.

You take Napoleon. He rose up from Second Lieutenant in the French army to crowning himself Emperor of France. He fought sixty battles across Europe, leaving the bloody deaths of Europe's finest young men in his wake. He wound up on an island in the Mediterranean by himself; no wife, no children, no family, and only a small cadre of followers. He would go down to the rocks, with the wind blowing in his face, grumbling about his living conditions. He didn't have a dime in his pocket. He finally died in his bed, alone. Quite a humbling process, wouldn't you say?

2\. [Brute passions take over when higher authority is rejected.]{.class_1921} When God is left out and ignored, something else besides God will control the conscience of man. That's when the brute nature of a man takes over and controls him. The Bible calls such men ["brute beasts"]{.class_1922} (2 Pet. 2:12; Jude 10). Those are things like [foxes]{.class_1921} (Luke 13:32), [snakes]{.class_1921} (Matt. 3:7, 12:34, 23:33), [bulls]{.class_1921} (Psa. 22:12), [dogs]{.class_1921} (Psa. 22:16; 2 Pet. 2:22), [hogs]{.class_1921} (2 Pet. 2:22; Prov. 11:22; Matt. 7:6), and [jackasses]{.class_1921} (Job 11:12). That's not me "dehumanizing" anybody; that's [God's]{.class_1921} opinion of the Adamic nature.

Don't tell me; I will tell you. I have seen the results of teaching children they came from animals (evolution). Animals kill without conscience. I have preached in juvenile facilities where the kids had to commit [three felonies before they were thirteen]{.class_1921} to get in. I preached to one sixteen year old who had killed [three people.]{.class_1921} I preached to a fifteen-year-old boy who had shot his daddy four times with a shotgun. He had tried to kill his mother too, but she locked herself in the bathroom. He fired through the door to get her; she managed to survive by lying flat on the floor. That kid was acting like a wild animal out of control.

Thank God He can tame a brute like that. I preached to that boy, and he got saved a week later. He won the drawing I had done while I was there, and he hung it up on the wall of his cell. Whenever new delinquents came into the facility, he would take them to that []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_101}picture and preach to them from it. What happened? That kid got born again and became ["a new creature" "in Christ"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 5:17). He came under a higher authority and was changed from the brute beast he was.

3\. [A test doesn't end until it has accomplished its purpose.]{.class_1921} If God is testing you in a matter, the testing will end when God's purpose with you is accomplished and not before. The test ends when you find out what God wants you to know. That means there is [hope]{.class_1921} in the midst of the trial. The quicker you can fulfill the Lord's purpose for the test, the sooner the end is in sight.

4\. [The greatest prosperity is no security against adversity. ]{.class_1921}I don't care how rich you are, how smart you are, how handsome or beautiful you are, or how talented you are; you are not exempt from trouble.

Trouble can reach into the lives of the greatest, most powerful people in the world. A good example is the Kennedy family. From grandmother Rose down to the last grandson, that family was filled with drunk, fornicating, crippled, killed, assassinated, sick, helpless people. God has taken that family and just about beaten it to death, but none of them seem to "get it." The beating goes right on until God's purpose comes about.

The terrible thing is, some people never learn from the beating. When it comes to the lost, the purpose of the whipping is clear: God lets the unsaved suffer to wake them up and show them their need of a Saviour. I can't imagine a more horrible thing than to go through life with God whipping you every time you turn around and never get the message, and then to wake up in Hell on top of that.

5\. [Although the punishment is severe, it is not hopeless.]{.class_1921} Of course, that is only applicable to a child of God or an unsaved person who responds correctly to the trial. For the lost who persist in their own way, there is ["no hope"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 2:12). All they have in their future is a lake of fire where they never will get out (Mark 9:44, 46, 48; Rev. 14:11).

For the child of God, no matter how bad things get down here, he has Heaven and his Saviour to which to look forward for all eternity. The psalmist wrote, ["The LORD hath chastened me sore: but he hath not given me over unto death"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 118:18). As a []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw570.xhtml_page_102}Christian, you aren't going to Hell, and that is something.

Now Christian, as you go through trials and testings, [don't give up.]{.class_1921} There is hope. If you get knocked down, get up and go on again for God. Unsaved people are watching you; other Christians are watching you. They are watching you to see if you'll quit. You have to get up and go on, even if all you can do is shuffle forward.

6\. [When deliverance comes, it is time for praise and thanksgiving.]{.class_1938} When the Lord finally gets you out of your mess, don't forget to thank Him. Nebuchadnezzar did what even a lot of Christians in America fail to do: [he gave public thanks.]{.class_1938} When the Lord delivered David from his enemies, the King said, ["There I will give thanks unto thee, O LORD, among the heathen, and I will sing praises unto thy name"]{.class_1937-0} (2 Sam. 22:50). Thanksgiving and praise can be a sacrifice for the believer in the midst of his trials.

["By him therefore let us offer the sacrifice of praise to God continually, that is, the fruit of our lips giving thanks to his name"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 13:15).

["In every thing give thanks: for this is the will of God in Christ Jesus concerning you"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 5:18).

For the Christian, trials can be a source of joy and happiness (1 Pet. 4:12--14), and that is something for which to be thankful and praise God.

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml}

# Chapter 5 {.heading_67-0}

5:1 Belshazzar the king made a great feast to a thousand of his lords, and drank wine before the thousand.

2 Belshazzar, whiles he tasted the wine, commanded to bring the golden and silver vessels which his father Nebuchadnezzar had taken out of the temple which was in Jerusalem; that the king, and his princes, his wives, and his concubines, might drink therein.

3 Then they brought the golden vessels that were taken out of the temple of the house of God which was at Jerusalem; and the king, and his princes, his wives, and his concubines, drank in them.

4 They drank wine, and praised the gods of gold, and of silver, of brass, of iron, of wood, and of stone.

The chapter deals with the last night of the last King of Babylon, Belshazzar. It deals with a night of [profanity]{.class_1921} (vss. 3--4). It was a night of [sinful pleasure]{.class_1921} (vs. 1). It was a night of [recklessness]{.class_1921} (vs. 2). It was a night of [warning]{.class_1921} (vss. 5, 22--28). And finally, it was a night of [judgment]{.class_1921} (vss. 30--31). That's an outline I have had in my Bible for years, but never had the chance to develop it into a full sermon. Perhaps some of you young preachers just starting out in the ministry can take it and do something with it.

Now for years and years, Daniel 5 was a favorite passage for infidels. As far as anybody knew from [secular history]{.class_1921} (taken from a Babylonian historian named Berosus from the Third Century B.C.), the last King of Babylon was Nabonidus. The infidels and agnostics took this as evidence that the book of Daniel was historically [wrong,]{.class_1921} so it could not be the word of God. The assumption by all the scholars is that the Bible is guilty until proven innocent; murderers get more of a break in the United States' judicial system than the Bible gets in State Universities.

An old riddle is: "What was the largest island before Australia was discovered?" The answer is [Australia;]{.class_1921} the fact that it hadn't been discovered yet didn't change what it was: the largest island. In 1853--[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_104}54, archaeologists digging around in Ur of the Chaldees found a collection of clay cylinders verifying the existence of Belshazzar as Nabonidus' son and coregent with his father. Riddle: Who was the last King of Babylon before the reference to Belshazzar was discovered? Belshazzar, stupid. The fact that a bunch of Ph.D.s and professors didn't have the sense to come in out of the rain didn't change that historic fact, as recorded in the Holy Bible, one way or another.

Verse 2 here in Daniel 5 says Nebuchadnezzar was the father of Belshazzar. In the Bible, a "son" can be one of several things. It can be an actual son; it can be an adopted or foster son (Luke 3:23); it can be a descendant in a family line (Matt. 1:1); it can be a son-in-law (1 Sam. 24:16, 26:17); it can even be a successor in a lineage who is not blood related (see our remarks on 1 Kings 22:51 in our work [The "Errors" in the King James Bible]{.class_1921}). What you have here is Belshazzar being the grandson of Nebuchadnezzar (see Jer. 27:7). The lineage runs:

1\. Nebuchadnezzar.

2\. Evilmerodach, the son of Nebuchadnezzar (2 Kings 25:27; Jer. 52:31).

3\. Neriglissar, married to Evilmerodach's sister.

4\. Laborosoarchod (also called Labashimarduk), the son of Neriglissar.

5\. Nabonidus, who had Laborosoarchod killed and then married his mother, Nebuchadnezzar's daughter.

6\. Belshazzar, grandson of Nebuchadnezzar through his mother.

All the political intrigue involved (used as "filler" in some commentaries) is irrelevant to belief in the Scriptures. At best, it is trivia for which you'll pay a bundle at an "institution of higher learning." You can get whatever you need to know about such things in Clarence Larkin's commentary on [The Book of Daniel. ]{.class_1921}In the Bible, the only three Kings who are mentioned are Nebuchadnezzar, Evilmerodach, and Belshazzar, which could be a picture of the satanic trinity (the Dragon, the Beast, and the False Prophet).

At this time, Nabonidus was "on vacation" (on leave, taking a "breather," on sabbatical) in the south of the kingdom while Belshazzar ruled in Babylon in the north. This would explain why Daniel was made ["the third ruler in the kingdom"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_105} (Dan. 5:7, 16, 29). Nabonidus would have been the first, Belshazzar the second, leaving the third spot open for Daniel.

Now with daddy away leaving him in charge of all the wealth and power which Nebuchadnezzar had secured, Belshazzar decides to throw a party for "[a thousand of his lords."]{.class_1922} When those Oriental monarchs threw a party, they went all out. You see that sort of thing with the Arab oil magnates today. I have in my notes where one of those Saudi Arabian sheiks held a feast where all the guests were served roasted pheasant eggs stuffed with caviar and three-quarters of an elephant trunk stuffed with kumquats and wrapped in papaya leaves. The cost of each individual plate was \$2,000.00 at the time I wrote the information down. One hundred-fifty-thousand dollars were spent on balloons; \$400,000 on electric lighting; and there were fountains there putting out 150,000 gallons a minute. The Hollywood tycoons couldn't come anywhere near it.

Belshazzar does this with the armies of the Medes and Persians preparing to enter and take the city. Why he decided to "party" rather than mount a proper defense to protect his people is anybody's guess. Perhaps it was to show he wasn't afraid of Cyrus and his armies. That is how Bush and Obama put it: the best response to ISIS and the terrorists is to let the party go on; go about your business as if the Moslems weren't trying to blow you up and saw your head off. I believe the term for that is a "fool's paradise."

Perhaps it was like the Israelites around the golden calf:

["And when Aaron saw it, he built an altar before it; and Aaron made proclamation, and said, To morrow is a feast to the LORD. And they rose up early on the morrow, and offered burnt offerings, and brought peace offerings; and the people sat down to eat and to drink, and rose up to play"]{.class_1922} (Exod. 32:5--6).

Here, everyone ends up praising ["the gods of gold, and of silver, of brass, of iron, of wood, and of stone"]{.class_1922} (vs. 4). Maybe Belshazzar thought this would somehow gain him the favor of those gods to defeat the Median and Persian forces.

Or it could have been simple hedonism. This is the "eat, drink, and be merry for tomorrow we die" philosophy (Isa. 22:13; Luke []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_106}12:19), when God is about to "lower the boom." Here, Belshazzar's feast degenerates quickly into a [drunken orgy.]{.class_1921}

Proverbs 20:1 says, ["Wine is a mocker, strong drink is raging: and whosoever is deceived thereby is not wise."]{.class_1922} That is what happens to Belshazzar here. He tasted the wine (vs. 2) and drank it (vs. 1) and [lost all his inhibitions.]{.class_1921} Belshazzar was not ignorant of what had happened to his grandfather back in chapter 4 (vs. 22); I dare say he even knew about God delivering Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego. But knowing what God did to Nebuchadnezzar, the drunken fool commits sacrilege ["against the Lord of heaven"]{.class_1922} (vs. 23).

Belshazzar decides if he and his lords are going to get drunk, they are going to get drunk "in style." He has all ["the golden and silver vessels"]{.class_1922} Nebuchadnez-zar had hauled away from the Temple in Jerusalem (see 1:2; he took away the rest in 2 Chron. 36:10, 18; Jer. 52:19) and brings them in to drink out of them. Those vessels had been dedicated and consecrated to the service of the Lord, and Belshazzar is using them not only to get drunk, but to praise a bunch of idols.

Human nature hasn't changed a bit since 563 B.C. (Ussher's date for the chapter). Men still praise ["the gods of gold"]{.class_1922} (vs. 4). The "Golden Rule" out in the world is: "He who has the gold makes the rules." That's what Nebuchadnezzar was trying to do back in chapter 3. The gods ["of silver"]{.class_1922} run a close second. At the time of this writing (2015), silver is actually a better investment than gold. The U.S. government has no gold to back up its money, so a lot of the big banks are buying up the silver. The gods ["of brass"]{.class_1922} and ["of iron"]{.class_1922} would be technology today: cars, boats, planes, computers, etc. That's how Bill Gates and Steve Jobs made their billions. The gods ["of wood, and of stone"]{.class_1922} would be buildings and property. Those are usually the gods of the big Christian works. Give more money to buy more property so you can build more and bigger buildings so you have to have more people give to pay for it. "Buy a brick on Liberty Mountain!" That sort of thing.

Just in case you think I'm just "preaching," look up Revelation 9:20 and read it. I'm not going to quote it for you this time; I want you to look up the verse and READ IT! That's the Tribulation, and []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_107}every single "god" found at Belshazzar's feast is found there in the exact same order. Moreover, they're associated with devil worship (cf. 1 Cor. 10:20). And they're connected with a certain church and city that succeeded Babylon (Rev. 17:4, 18:2, 12). Like I said, human nature hasn't changed one iota in 2,500 years. The drunkenness, fornication, idolatry, and sacrilege don't stop until the Owner of the hand that wrote on Belshazzar's wall comes to break up the party.

The practical lessons for the Christian are:

1\. ["And be not drunk with wine, wherein is excess; but be filled with the Spirit"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 5:18). The excuse used by Catholics, Lutherans, and Episcopalians (as well as any Baptist, Methodist, Presbyterian, or Charismatic who wants to "imbibe") is that the sin is only in drunkenness, not in drinking the liquor. But notice that the ["excess"]{.class_1922} is in the wine itself, not in drunkenness.

The command is: ["Look not thou upon the wine when it is red, when it giveth his colour in the cup, when it moveth itself aright"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 23:31). If you look at it, you'll taste it; if you taste it, you'll drink it; if you drink it, you will (sooner or later) drink it to excess and get drunk; if you get drunk, [you will do anything.]{.class_1921} When I was growing up, we had a saying: "If a girl will smoke, she'll drink; and if she'll drink, [she'll do anything."]{.class_1921} We were just a bunch of lost, hell-raising, drunken, fornicating heathen; but we knew the "lay of the land" when we saw it. You can get a girl who drinks to do [anything]{.class_1921} with you. Noah and Lot got in trouble when they "hit the bottle."

2\. ["If any man defile the temple of God, him shall God destroy; for the temple of God is holy, which temple ye are"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 3:17). The Lord had Nebuchadnezzar come into Jerusalem and burn His house to the ground because those Jews defiled it with their idolatry. He took the kingdom away from Belshazzar because he defiled the vessels of the Temple. In the New Testament, ["ye are the temple of God"]{.class_1922} because ["the Spirit of God dwelleth in you"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 3:16), so the warning of 1 Corinthians 3:17 is to [you]{.class_1921} if you are a born-again child of God. Don't defile ["the temple of the Holy Ghost"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 6:19--20).

5 In the same hour came forth fingers of a man's hand, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_108}and wrote over against the candlestick upon the plaister of the wall of the king's palace: and the king saw the part of the hand that wrote.

6 Then the king's countenance was changed, and his thoughts troubled him, so that the joints of his loins were loosed, and his knees smote one against another.

7 The king cried aloud to bring in the astrologers, the Chaldeans, and the soothsayers. And the king spake, and said to the wise men of Babylon, Whosoever shall read this writing, and shew me the interpretation thereof, shall be clothed with scarlet, and have a chain of gold about his neck, and shall be the third ruler in the kingdom.

8 Then came in all the king's wise men: but they could not read the writing, nor make known to the king the interpretation thereof.

9 Then was king Belshazzar greatly troubled, and his countenance was changed in him, and his lords were astonied.

Right in the middle of "happy hour," something happens that sets that drunken King's knees knocking in terror (vs. 6).
