The ["fingers of a man's hand"]{.class_1922} appear and write on ["the plaister]{.class_1922} \[we say [plaster]{.class_1921} today\][ of the wall"]{.class_1922} (vs. 5). Belshazzar is seeing this giant forefinger, with the other fingers curled in toward the palm, writing words on the wall. Obviously, this is ["the finger of God"]{.class_1922} (cf. Exod. 8:19; Luke 11:20).

This is one of four places in the Bible where God wrote something with His finger. Sinful man responded to those writings by [unthankfulness and pride]{.class_1921} (Psa. 8:3 cf. Rom. 1:20--22), [breaking them]{.class_1921} (Exod. 31:18 cf. Exod. 32:15--19), [ignoring them]{.class_1921} (here), and [stepping on them]{.class_1921} (John 8:6). The ["scripture . . . given by inspiration of God"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 3:16) is no different; it suffers corruption at the hands of apostate scholars (2 Cor. 2:17).

Now notice [where]{.class_1921} the writing takes place: ["over against the candlestick."]{.class_1922} Without a doubt, that is the Golden Candlestick taken out of the Temple. That candlestick is a type of the Holy Spirit (Rev. 4:5). In the Tabernacle, that candlestick shed light on the Table of []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_109}Showbread, a type of the word of God. That's the picture here. What you are about to read is a picture of the Holy Spirit interpreting something God wrote, that a man can't understand on his own.

Of course, Belshazzar calls in his ["astrologers," "Chaldeans," "soothsayers,"]{.class_1922} and ["wise men"]{.class_1922} just as Nebuchadnezzar did back in 2:2 and 4:7; but they fare no better here than they did before. They can't ["read the handwriting on the wall"]{.class_1922} (vs. 8). (It makes you wonder why those Babylonian Kings kept them around when their batting average was 0 for 3.)

The reason those pagan wise men "bomb out" (again!) is because ["the natural man receiveth not the things of the Spirit of God: for they are foolishness unto him: neither can he know them, because they are spiritually discerned"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 2:14). ["No prophecy of the scripture is of any private interpretation"]{.class_1922} (2 Pet. 1:20) because ["interpretations belong to God"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 40:8).

Now look at the reward Belshazzar promises anyone who can read the handwriting: ["clothed with scarlet," "a chain of gold about his neck,"]{.class_1922} and[ ]{.class_1921}["the THIRD ruler in the kingdom"]{.class_1922}[ ]{.class_1921}(vs. 7). Does that remind you of anyone else in Scripture? It should.

["And Pharaoh took off his ring from his hand, and put it upon Joseph's hand, and arrayed him in vestures of fine linen, and put a gold chain about his neck; And he made him to ride in the SECOND chariot which he had; and they cried before him, Bow the knee: and he made him ruler over all the land of Egypt"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 41:42--43).

Joseph is the greatest type of Christ in the entire Bible. He is given royal clothing, ["a gold chain,"]{.class_1922} and made the SECOND ruler in Egypt as a type of the Second Person of the Trinity. So here, Daniel is a type of the Holy Ghost, the Third Person of the Trinity (cf. vs. 29). It is the Holy Ghost who interprets the Scripture (2 Pet. 1:20--21; John 16:13; 1 Cor. 2:10--13); not any church, Pope, council, or school! Daniel is able to read and interpret the writing through the Holy Spirit in him (vs. 12); not through any knowledge of the "original languages," archaeology, church dogma, science, etc. Brethren, ["the wisdom of this world is foolishness with God"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 3:19). That is the great lesson of the book of Daniel. Those []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_110}wise men drew a "blank" because all they had was man's wisdom.

10 Now the queen, by reason of the words of the king and his lords, came into the banquet house: and the queen spake and said, O king, live for ever: let not thy thoughts trouble thee, nor let thy countenance be changed:

11 There is a man in thy kingdom, in whom is the spirit of the holy gods; and in the days of thy father light and understanding and wisdom, like the wisdom of the gods, was found in him; whom the king Nebuchadnezzar thy father, the king, I say, thy father, made master of the magicians, astrologers, Chaldeans, and soothsayers;

12 Forasmuch as an excellent spirit, and knowledge, and understanding, interpreting of dreams, and shewing of hard sentences, and dissolving of doubts, were found in the same Daniel, whom the king named Belteshazzar: now let Daniel be called, and he will shew the interpretation.

["The queen" ]{.class_1922}of verse 10 would be the Queen Mother, Belshazzar's mother who was married to Nabonidus. Belshazzar has been scared out of his wits by supernatural writing that none of his wise men can even read, much less interpret. His mother (who had not been at the party), upon hearing what had happened, comes to ["the banquet house"]{.class_1922} (vs. 10) to calm her son down and let him know there is someone who can give him some answers because he has the Spirit and wisdom of God. Of course, being a polytheistic pagan, she puts everything in her own terms based on her own beliefs just like Nebuchadnezzar did back in 4:8--9 (which see).

We have already commented on the fact that the Holy Spirit was ["in"]{.class_1922} Daniel, not just on him, under our remarks on 4:9, which see. The ["excellent spirit"]{.class_1922} of verse 12 is indeed the Holy Spirit of God and not just Daniel's human spirit, for it bears all the marks of the Holy Spirit. ["The spirit of the LORD"]{.class_1922} is ["the spirit of wisdom and understanding, the spirit of counsel and might,"]{.class_1922} and ["the spirit of knowledge"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 11:2). The Holy Spirit gives ["light"]{.class_1922} to the sinner (cf. 2 Cor. 4:4--6). It is the Holy Spirit of God who opens your understanding of the Scripture (Luke 24:25) to those things in it that are ["hard to be understood"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_111} (2 Pet. 3:16). And only the Spirit of God can dissolve your doubts and give you assurance of salvation (Rom. 8:15--17 cf. 1 John 5:13).

13 Then was Daniel brought in before the king. And the king spake and said unto Daniel, Art thou that Daniel, which art of the children of the captivity of Judah, whom the king my father brought out of Jewry?

14 I have even heard of thee, that the spirit of the gods is in thee, and that light and understanding and excellent wisdom is found in thee.

15 And now the wise men, the astrologers, have been brought in before me, that they should read this writing, and make known unto me the interpretation thereof: but they could not shew the interpretation of the thing:

16 And I have heard of thee, that thou canst make interpretations, and dissolve doubts: now if thou canst read the writing, and make known to me the interpretation thereof, thou shalt be clothed with scarlet, and have a chain of gold about thy neck, and shalt be the third ruler in the kingdom.

Much of the passage is simply a repetition of the material preceding it, on which we have commented already. There are a few things, though, of which we can take note.

The first is the word ["Jewry"]{.class_1922} in verse 13. It is found in only three places in Scripture: here in verse 13; Luke 23:5; and John 7:1. While the term can refer to the Jews collectively (as in Luke 23:5), here it refers to the land of Judah in particular (as in John 7:1).

Verse 14: ["I have even heard of thee."]{.class_1922} That's what Pharaoh said of Joseph when he wanted his dreams interpreted (Gen. 41:15). That's what the Queen of Sheba said when she wanted Solomon to answer her hard questions (1 King 10:1--6). That's what Job said of God after the Lord showed up at the end of his trials (Job 42:5). That is what was said of Herod concerning Christ when Herod wanted to see Jesus perform a miracle (Luke 23:8 cf. Mark 6:14).

Paul said about "the heathen who've never heard": ["But I say, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_112}Have they not heard? YES VERILY, their sound went into all the earth, and their words unto the ends of the world"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 10:18).

Every sinner on the face of this earth has heard from God in one way or another. The issue is not have they heard; they have. The issue is [what they've done with what they've heard.]{.class_1926} Pharaoh took heed to Joseph. The Queen of Sheba came to hear the wisdom of Solomon. Job repented. Herod had Jesus mocked. You have heard from God. Now what are you going to do with it? You will either accept it as God's word (1 Thess. 2:13) and act on it, or you will reject it and do whatever you want.

Belshazzar chooses to [ignore]{.class_1926} what Daniel says. Oh, he keeps his word to reward Daniel, just as Nebuchadnezzar did back in 2:48; but there is no repentance on Belshazzar's part, just as there was none with Nebuchadnezzar in chapters 2 or 3. I will say this, though, for the character of Nebuchadnezzar: at least he recognized God in a way his grandson did not (see 2:47, 3:29).

Note, once again, the rewards offered by Belshazzar (vs. 16), which he ended up giving to Daniel:

1\. ["Clothed with scarlet"]{.class_1922}---a type of blood. Hebrews 9:14 says, ["How much more shall the blood of Christ, who through the eternal Spirit offered himself without spot to God, purge your conscience from dead works to serve the living God?"]{.class_1922} You are justified through the blood (Rom. 5:1). You are redeemed and forgiven through the blood (Col. 1:14). You obtain peace with God through the blood (Col. 1:20). You are cleansed by the blood (1 John 1:7). And the only sacrifice that will satisfy the justice, holiness, and wrath of God against the sinner is the bloody sacrifice of His Son on Calvary (Rom. 3:25); and I don't mean a cup of hootch in a black-magic ceremony (transubstantiation in the Roman Catholic Mass).

2\. ["A chain of gold"]{.class_1922}---a picture of Deity. Notice the blood comes before the Deity. The only way you will come to God is through the blood of His Son. "Some through the waters, some through the flood, some through the fire, BUT ALL THROUGH THE BLOOD"---that's the business.

3\. ["The third ruler in the kingdom"]{.class_1922}---a type of the Holy []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_113}Spirit, the Third Person of the Trinity.

17 Then Daniel answered and said before the king, Let thy gifts be to thyself, and give thy rewards to another; yet I will read the writing unto the king, and make known to him the interpretation.

18 O thou king, the most high God gave Nebuchadnezzar thy father a kingdom, and majesty, and glory, and honour:

19 And for the majesty that he gave him, all people, nations, and languages, trembled and feared before him: whom he would he slew; and whom he would he kept alive; and whom he would he set up; and whom he would he put down.

20 But when his heart was lifted up, and his mind hardened in pride, he was deposed from his kingly throne, and they took his glory from him:

21 And he was driven from the sons of men; and his heart was made like the beasts, and his dwelling was with the wild asses: they fed him with grass like oxen, and his body was wet with the dew of heaven; till he knew that the most high God ruled in the kingdom of men, and that he appointeth over it whomsoever he will.

22 And thou his son, O Belshazzar, hast not humbled thine heart, though thou knewest all this;

23 But hast lifted up thyself against the Lord of heaven; and they have brought the vessels of his house before thee, and thou, and thy lords, thy wives, and thy concubines, have drunk wine in them; and thou hast praised the gods of silver, and gold, of brass, iron, wood, and stone, which see not, nor hear, nor know: and the God in whose hand thy breath is, and whose are all thy ways, hast thou not glorified:

Daniel turns down Belshazzar's rewards (vs. 17; although the King goes ahead and gives them to him anyway---vs. 29), and this is for a couple of reasons. The first is that it is a poor testimony to a lost world. Abram (Gen. 14:23), Elisha (2 Kings 5:16), and Peter (Acts []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_114}8:20) all turned down gifts, rewards, and money offered to them so that the lost people with whom they dealt wouldn't believe they were in the ministry for the money. Peter told the elders to whom he wrote: ["Feed the flock of God which is among you, taking the oversight thereof . . . NOT FOR FILTHY LUCRE, but of a ready mind"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 5:2).

But another reason, and the more obvious one, is that it was an [empty reward.]{.class_1921} There wasn't going to be a "kingdom" around in a few hours for Daniel to be third ruler of. It wasn't going to be long before the kingdom of Babylon would be replaced by the kingdom of Persia. The gold head of Daniel 2 was over and done with, and it was time for the silver chest. The change took place [that night]{.class_1921} (vss. 30--31).

Now before Daniel reads the writing for the King and interprets it, he does a little preaching. Remember that if you are ever put in a similar situation. I had a buddy in the ministry who was invited to his 25th high school class reunion. Being the only minister in the class, he was asked to pray to bless the food. Well, you know what he did. There is an awful lot of preaching you can do in a prayer if you word it right. I bet you that was the first time some of those people had ever heard a clear presentation of the Gospel.

One time, Peter Cartwright, the old-time, circuit-riding Methodist evangelist, was passing through a section of the Cumberland Mountains headed home from a meeting. It was Saturday evening, and he wanted to find a group of Christians with whom to stay. But that little hamlet was just a bunch of rednecks who enjoyed hunting, fishing, and carousing, with no thought for God, the Bible, or church. Cartwright got him a room in the only inn in town and found out a dance was being held there that night.

Well, Cartwright was sitting there at a table, having his supper, wondering what a Methodist preacher was going to do at a dance, when up came a pretty young girl asking him to dance. Cartwright sent up one of those quick Nehemiah prayers (Neh. 2:4), took the girl's hand, and said, "I believe I will." He went to the front of that room and, holding that girl tightly by the hand so she couldn't get away, he said to that crowd, "I don't undertake any matter of importance without first asking the blessing of God upon it." Then he kneeled down and started one of those old-time Methodist prayers []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_115}where he prayed at the top of his lungs, preaching through the whole prayer. He had fifteen saved that night, as well as that young lady. He organized a church from those converts and appointed the innkeeper as the lay leader.

Daniel reminds Belshazzar of what his granddaddy went through back in chapter 4. He starts out with the fact that [God]{.class_1921} gave the kingdom to Nebuchadnezzar along with all the majesty, glory, and honor that went with it. Nebuchadnezzar couldn't have won a single battle if God had not let him do it. Read Jeremiah 25:9--12 and note that it is [God]{.class_1921} who gave Nebuchadnezzar all the lands he conquered, and it was [God]{.class_1921} who took them away when He was done with Babylon.

Having recounted to Belshazzar the humiliation of Nebuchadnezzar (vss. 20--21), look at what Daniel said to the King in verse 22: ["And thou his son, O Belshazzar, hast not humbled thine heart, THOUGH THOU KNEWEST ALL THIS." ]{.class_1922}Belshazzar wasn't ignorant of his grandfather becoming an animal; he wasn't ignorant of God delivering Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego from the fiery furnace. He knew all about what the God of the Hebrews did in Daniel 3 and 4. Knowing all that, he still defied Him by defiling the vessels from His Temple. Don't you know there were many a pagan temple Nebuchadnezzar plundered in his conquests. Well, then, why did Belshazzar pick the vessels taken out of the Temple of the Jews to use in his drunken orgy? That was a personal, direct, purposeful act of rebellion on the part of Belshazzar against the God of Heaven.

That is the thing about sin. Men know what it is, they know its consequences, and they go through with it anyway. Do you know what Paul says about the sin of Adam and Eve? Look at 1 Timothy 2:14.

"And Adam was not deceived, but the woman being deceived was in the transgression."

The Devil didn't trick Adam into eating the forbidden fruit; that's what he did to Eve. Adam knew exactly what he was doing and what would happen if he did, and he went ahead and took his chances. That's how we are.

I told you above that Belshazzar was not ignorant of what took place in Daniel 3 and 4. The choice of idols back in verse 4 shows you []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_116}he wasn't ignorant of his grandfather's image back in chapter 2. The order is exactly the same as the image of Nebuchadnezzar's dream: gold, silver, brass, iron, and then wood and stone (representing the clay of the image). But notice the change of order in the first two here in verse 23: silver first, then gold. The silver chest is about to overthrow the gold head.

["Which see not, nor hear, nor know."]{.class_1922} They're not living. The cross-references are Psalm 115:4--8, 135:15--17; Isaiah 37:19, 46:6--7; and 1 Corinthians 8:4. Isaiah 49:14--18 talks about a fellow going out in the forest and cutting down a tree. He takes part of it and makes a fire to warm himself and cook his food, and he takes the rest and makes an idol out of it. He never considers the foolishness of praying to something he used to cook dinner. Men are the same way today. They serve a dollar bill made out of [rags;]{.class_1921} they serve gods that can be eaten, rusted, and stolen (Matt. 6:19).

The God I serve holds my breath in His hand (vs. 23 cf. Job 12:10). The God who ["created the heavens"]{.class_1922} and ["spread forth the earth"]{.class_1922} ["giveth breath unto the people upon it, and spirit to them that walk therein"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 42:5). He's the One who gives ["to all life, and breath, and all things"]{.class_1922} (Acts 17:25), so He's not like anything man makes from gold, silver, or stone (Acts 17:29). He doesn't have to exert Himself at all to get rid of you. All He has to do is touch you in the lungs or in the heart, and you're a dead man (Psa. 104:29).

That means if you are breathing, it's because God wants you to breath. If you are unsaved and still breathing, it's because God is giving you a chance to repent and trust Christ for salvation. If you are a Christian and still breathing, it's because God still has a purpose for you being on this earth.

I don't know why God lets some Christians just keep on breathing and suffering without taking them home right away, but He does. There was a lady named Mrs. Salter in a nursing home. Mrs. Salter was flat on her back in a bed for [25 years;]{.class_1921} she was bedridden longer than some of the students I sent by to visit her had been alive on this earth. I used to go see her and say, "Mrs. Salter, have you got the victory?" She'd say, "Amen, Bro. Pete!" I would say, "Let me hear you praise the Lord." At the top of her lungs that sister would yell, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_117}"PRAISE THE LORD!" She said it a lot louder than some Christians I know who walk around on two good feet, grumbling about the weather, their jobs, the pastor, the bills, etc. God let that sister keep on breathing to show everyone around her that a Christian could be victorious in intolerable circumstances.

Another fellow in our church, named Hunt, had a debilitating condition where he couldn't get around. His wife and kids had to take care of him. I'd go visit him, and he would cry and say, "Why doesn't God just take me and let me go home?" I must admit that I didn't know why, but I found out later. God let that fellow live long enough ([years]{.class_1921}) to qualify for some type of payments to his family? Bro. Hunt wanted to make sure his family was taken care of, and God kept him breathing long enough for that to happen.

So Christian, if you are still breathing, it is for the purpose and pleasure of your Saviour. When He is done with you down here, He will take you home, but until then, you are to find something to do for Him that will bring Him [glory.]{.class_1921} That's what Belshazzar [didn't do.]{.class_1921} God gave him his breath and his life, and he wasted it all on [himself]{.class_1921} (["hast thou not glorified"]{.class_1922}). That's why God sent that ["handwriting on the wall."]{.class_1922}

Do you know how apostasy begins in a society? Paul tells you in Romans 1:21.

["Because that, when they knew God. THEY GLORIFIED HIM NOT AS GOD, neither were thankful; but became vain in their imaginations, and their foolish heart was darkened"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 1:21).

From there it goes to evolution (Rom. 1:22), nature worship (Rom. 1:23), fornication (Rom. 1:24), and finally, dykes and faggots (Rom. 1:26--27). It all starts with failure to glorify God. Believing in one God does you no good at all if you don't glorify Him in the way you are instructed in the Holy Scriptures. Belshazzar knew all about the God of the Hebrews, and it didn't stop him from holding a drunken orgy to praise a bunch of devils (1 Cor. 10:20--21).

24 Then was the part of the hand sent from him; and this writing was written.

25 And this is the writing that was written, MENE, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_118}MENE, TEKEL, UPHARSIN.

26 This is the interpretation of the thing: MENE; God hath numbered thy kingdom, and finished it.

27 TEKEL; Thou art weighed in the balances, and art found wanting.

28 PERES; Thy kingdom is divided, and given to the Medes and Persians.

Having finished his sermon to Belshazzar, Daniel gets down to reading the writing for the King. There is all kind of speculation by the linguists discussing the four words of verse 25 in Chaldean, Aramaic, Syrian, "Old" Hebrew, "New" Hebrew, and Arabic. After all is said and done, you are no closer to understanding the words than if you had studied them in Pig Latin.

The words are all Chaldean words, but the reason the Chaldeans can't read them is because they are written in Hebrew letters. It would be like you trying to read English words in Chinese or Korean characters. But even if they had been able to read them, that doesn't mean those Chaldeans could have even guessed at the meaning (see 4:7).

Back in 1886, a Frenchman named Clermont-Ganneau proposed the idea that the writing was a play on words. As anyone knows who is familiar with Hebrew, the words are composed of only consonants. The Masoretes of the Seventh Century A.D. added the vowel markings. Hebrew words can have the same basic "radicals" (consonants), but the meaning changes when different vowel points are used (e.g., Adam and Edom). If you change the vowels in the four Hebrew words, you have something else in English.

The idea here is that these four words are actually four units of money: mina, mina, shekel, and peras. Having said that, the application is rather vague. A mina is the greatest value. The [Jewish Encyclopedia]{.class_1921} (1906) says it is "an allusion to Nebuchadnezzar." A shekel is one-sixtieth of a mina, and a peras is half a mina. So the shekel is the lowest value. That would make Belshazzar the shekel. He is killed off by two Kings who have united to overthrow the Chaldeans: the King of the Medes and the King of the Persians. So Media is one peras, and Persia would be the other peras to equal []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_119}Nebuchadnezzar's one mina.

That's interesting, and perhaps there is something to it, but it's obviously not what the text says.

In Chaldean, the word ["MENE"]{.class_1922} means "numbered." Not having the sense God gave a brass monkey, two of the authors of the [Septuagint]{.class_1921} (Origen and Theodotion---the fifth and sixth columns of Origen's [Hexapla]{.class_1921}) remove one of the ["Menes"]{.class_1921} from verse 25 to match verse 26. Why in the world would Daniel need to define the word twice? If there had been four ["Menes"]{.class_1921} in verse 25, Daniel would only have to give the meaning [once.]{.class_1921}

["TEKEL"]{.class_1922} means "weighed."

["UPHARSIN"]{.class_1922} (vs. 25) and ["PERES"]{.class_1922} (vs. 28) are the same word in the Hebrew lettering. The difference is in the prefix, suffix, and vowel markings in ["UPHARSIN."]{.class_1922} The ["U"]{.class_1921} is the conjunction [and.]{.class_1921} The ["P"]{.class_1921} of ["PERES,"]{.class_1922} therefore, becomes the ["PH"]{.class_1921} of ["UPHARSIN"]{.class_1922} because of the ["U." ]{.class_1921}The ["IN"]{.class_1921} of ["UPHARSIN"]{.class_1922} is a plural suffix which Daniel simplifies to its singular form ["PERES."]{.class_1922} There are a [few]{.class_1921} places in Scripture where a knowledge of the original languages helps you understand what you read in the Bible, but those places are nowhere near the number the scholars would lead you to believe.

["PERES"]{.class_1922} actually has a double meaning. In Chaldean, it means "divided." So what you have is "Numbered, Numbered, Weighed, Divided." But with different vowel markings, that last word (["PERES"]{.class_1922}) can also mean "Persia," and the ["Persians"]{.class_1922} show up in the interpretation. So the interpretation goes beyond the bare meaning of the word.

["MENE"]{.class_1922} is more than just ["God hath numbered thy kingdom"]{.class_1922}; it is a numbering for the purpose of [finishing it.]{.class_1921} That is why the word is doubled in the writing, because ["the thing is established by God, and God will shortly bring it to pass"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 41:32).

["TEKEL"]{.class_1922} is being ["found wanting"]{.class_1922} after being ["weighed in the balance."]{.class_1922} The standard idea of the final judgment is that God will have a giant balance scale like the one held up by Lady Justice out in front of the court house. On one side of the scale, God puts your good works; on the other side of that scale, God puts your bad works. If your good works outweigh your bad works, you go to []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_120}Heaven; if your bad works outweigh your good works, you go to Hell; and if you break even, you go to Purgatory, according to the Catholics.

The problem with that is, [it's found nowhere in the Bible.]{.class_1921} It comes from the Egyptian ["Book of the Dead"]{.class_1921} (a collection of scraps of paper found in Egyptian tombs, artificially put into one book by scholars). When God weighs you, friend, it won't be by your own works. God has a perfect standard, and it's not any sinner [like you.]{.class_1921} God will "weigh" you by the perfect standard of [His own Son]{.class_1921} (Acts 17:31).

That is what people don't like about that Book: it lays down an [absolute standard.]{.class_1921} Men are basically [anarchists:]{.class_1921} they judge everything by [their own opinions.]{.class_1921} If that were the standard, then everyone would make it, because all men are righteous in their own eyes (Prov. 20:6). If you are judged by the views of contemporary society, then you won't have any problem, because society is a hellhole these days. You would look pretty good alongside that mess.

If you are judged by education, you could make an argument for yourself either way. The professors, doctors, lawyers, etc., could argue they are better than the uneducated clods. The backwoods hillbilly (who may not have a formal education, but has a lot of "horse sense") looks at all the drunkenness, dope heads, fornicating, and Communism that go on at College campuses and figures he's better than that.

But if you judge yourself by that Book, you will fall short every time (see Mark 12:30). ["For ALL have sinned, and come short of the glory of God"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 3:23).

Now I'll tell you how to pass the judgment. When Jesus Christ is put on one side of the scale, you have to have something that's equal to Him on your side to pass. If you came to church and I placed armed men outside to shoot you if you couldn't give me a pocket knife [exactly]{.class_1921} like mine, do you know how you could get out? Have me give you the pocket knife so you could give it back to me, because the only pocket knife [exactly]{.class_1921} like mine, is [mine.]{.class_1921}

If you want to pass the judgment, then I'll tell you how to do it. [Be just as righteous as God's Son.]{.class_1921} You say, "I can't do that, Ruckman."[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_121}[ Then accept the righteousness of God freely offered you by faith in Christ]{.class_1921} (Rom. 3:21--22; 2 Cor. 5:21; 1 Pet. 3:18).

["PERES"]{.class_1922} is the division of Belshazzar's kingdom ["to the Medes and Persians"]{.class_1922} (vs. 28). ["UPHARSIN"]{.class_1922} is an active plural participle, meaning "those who divide" ("dividers"). ["PERES"]{.class_1922} is a singular passive participle taken from the three center radicals of ["UPHARSIN"]{.class_1922} (P, R, S), meaning "divided." It is a play on words: "the dividers have divided," except the "dividers" are given by name in the word: the Persians. It would be like saying, "The Russians rushed you."

29 Then commanded Belshazzar, and they clothed Daniel with scarlet, and put a chain of gold about his neck, and made a proclamation concerning him, that he should be the third ruler in the kingdom.

30 In that night was Belshazzar the king of the Chaldeans slain.

31 And Darius the Median took the kingdom, being about threescore and two years old.

True to his word, Belshazzar gives Daniel all the rewards he promised, but you will notice that he [did nothing]{.class_1921} about what Daniel had told him. That's because Belshazzar couldn't comprehend how a city fortified as Babylon was could be taken so quickly.

When Nebuchadnezzar bragged about ["this great Babylon, that I have built"]{.class_1922} (4:30), he wasn't just "whistling Dixie." What I am about to give you comes from Clarence Larkin, and it shows you exactly why Belshazzar thought the city couldn't be taken immediately.

The city was fifteen miles square, making it sixty miles all around. Can you imagine the size army you would have to have to besiege sixty miles of fortified wall? Along those sixty miles of wall were 250 towers, giving the defenders the "high ground" in combat. The wall itself was 350 feet high and 87 feet thick, allowing six chariots to travel side by side across the top of it. There were enough stores in the city to withstand years of siege, but on top of that, there were actually fields in the city for growing crops. The River []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_122}Euphrates flowed through the center of the city, providing both water for drinking, fishing, and irrigating crops. It had a sluice gate at either end that prevented invaders from entering the city by boat.

But while Belshazzar was hiding behind his walls and towers, Cyrus was planning a way to take the city, despite the impregnable fortifications. He had a trench dug to divert the Euphrates, and when he heard about Belshazzar's party, he had the waters of the river channeled away from the city. Then his army simply entered the city through the river bed from both ends while its defenders were "three sheets to the wind," and the massacre started. ["In that night was Belshazzar the king of the Chaldeans slain"]{.class_1922} (vs. 30).

Belshazzar didn't know it, but he wasn't fighting Cyrus or the Persians or the Medes. He was fighting against something that ["cannot be broken"]{.class_1922} (John 10:35). Back in 750 B.C., Isaiah the prophet, under the inspiration of the Holy Ghost, had given the conqueror of Babylon [by name]{.class_1921} (Isa. 44:28--45:1). Seventy years earlier, Jeremiah had written exactly what the "number" (vs. 26) of the kingdom of Babylon would be (Jer. 25:12).

Now although Cyrus is the head of the Medo-Persian armies, he leaves his chief General to rule the city while he goes on to other conquests. That is who ["Darius the Median"]{.class_1922} is (vs. 31). The historic records have no mention of ["Darius the Median"]{.class_1922} (yet! let's not forget what happened with the records of Belshazzar's reign). The best guess is either Gobryas, the General who is said in Babylonian tablets to have conquered Babylon, or Cyaxares the Median, uncle and father-in-law to Cyrus. It is nothing unusual in the Bible for a person to have more than one name. We have already seen here in Daniel where people had their native name and a Babylonian name. [Darius]{.class_1921} could also have been a title, like [Pharaoh]{.class_1921} or [Caesar]{.class_1921}. One thing is for certain, the only "literary fiction" (to quote the Liberal higher critics) of the account is the writings of apostates and infidels who won't accept the Bible as an historical document because they don't want to be accountable to its Author.

In closing, here are the lessons we learn from Daniel 5:

1\. ["Pride goeth before destruction, and an haughty spirit before a fall"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 16:18).

2\. [A joyous celebration can end in death and slaughter.]{.class_1921} Haman []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw692.xhtml_page_123}ended up hung at the end of a banquet (Esth. 7). Vlad the Impaler ("Dracula") invited all the poor and crippled in his kingdom to a banquet and then had them burned alive in the banquet hall after the feast. Al Capone held a dinner for three of his men and then beat them to death at the table with a baseball bat for plotting against him. Back in December 2015, the workers at the Public Health Department of San Bernardino, California were having a Christmas banquet when two Moslem gunmen came in and killed fourteen people. There have been many a young man and young woman who went to a party where the booze flowed freely and everyone was having a good time, only to end up in a car wreck on the highway on the way home, crippled, paralyzed, or dead.

3\. [If God writes something, you had better read it.]{.class_1921} Before I was saved, my mother-in-law sent me a Bible when I was in the Army. I opened the package in front of my unsaved buddies in the barracks, picked up that Bible, laughed at it, and said, "That thing won't stop bullets." Then I threw it in the trash can. Another time overseas in the Philippines, my company commander, Lt. Self, took out a Bible and said, "You're always reading something, Ruckman; let me read you something out of this." I told him, "Put that away; that's a bunch of baloney." By the time God got through with me, I wasn't throwing the Bible in the trash can or calling it pig's meat; I was so desperate to get that Book, I broke into a flophouse and stole one.

4\. [The wisest and most highly trained religious leaders can interpret nothing apart from the Holy Spirit.]{.class_1921}

5\. [Every man will eventually be weighed in God's balance against the perfect righteousness of Jesus Christ.]{.class_1921}

# [6. ]{.class_1942}[The destruction of the vicious is sudden]{.class_1943}[ (see Prov. 6:15, 29:1).]{.class_1942} {.heading_827}

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml}

# [Chapter 6]{.class_1936} {.heading_827}

Daniel 6 is the account of Daniel in the lions' den. It is one of the famous "children's stories" of the Bible (like "David and Goliath"). The Bible is a universal Book that appeals to all ages. You don't have to beat children to learn the Bible like Moslems do when forcing children to memorize the [Koran]{.class_1921}. There are many things in the Bible that are good for children because children can understand them. That is the case with Daniel 6.

But one should not dismiss such stories simply because they are simple enough for children to grasp. They contain some of the deepest truths you will find anywhere in the word of God. This interesting story isn't just myth, legend, or folklore; it is actual, factual [history,]{.class_1921} set down in Scripture by the Holy Spirit to point us to Jesus Christ.

In Daniel 5, we saw Daniel as a type of the Holy Ghost, the Third Person of the Trinity. Here in this chapter, Daniel is presented as a type of the Lord Jesus Christ, the Second Person of the Trinity. In fact, I call this chapter "The Gospel According to Daniel." With the exception of dying for someone's sins, Daniel experiences, in type, in this chapter, a death, burial, and resurrection (cf. 1 Cor. 15:1--4). As we go through this chapter, I will be calling these pictures and types to your attention.

6:1 It pleased Darius to set over the kingdom an hundred and twenty princes, which should be over the whole kingdom;

2 And over these three presidents; of whom Daniel was first: that the princes might give accounts unto them, and the king should have no damage.

3 Then this Daniel was preferred above the presidents and princes, because an excellent spirit was in him; and the king thought to set him over the whole realm.

Now Cyrus the Persian had conquered the city of Babylon and left Darius the Mede in charge while he went off on more conquests. []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_125}At this point, the Medes and Persians are sharing power. While Cyrus is off "spreading the kingdom," Darius organizes the territory taken up to that point. The kingdom is divided into 120 provinces (like our States), with a "Prince" appointed by the King over each one. Later on in Esther 1:1, there are 127 provinces in the Persian Empire, which means Cyrus and other Persian monarchs added to their territory and organized seven additional provinces.

["And over these three presidents"]{.class_1922} (vs. 2). These aren't Presidents as Americans understand the term. None of these guys "ran for office" or were "elected" by "voters." They were [presiding officials]{.class_1921} set up by the King to oversee the Princes of the provinces. The Princes answered to the Presidents (["that the princes might give accounts unto them"]{.class_1922}), and the Presidents answered to the King (["the king should have no damage"]{.class_1922}).

The number ["three"]{.class_1922} should alert the reader that the Trinity is pictured here. ["Of whom Daniel was first."]{.class_1922} Obviously a picture of Christ:[ "that in all things he might have the PREEMINENCE"]{.class_1922} (Col. 1:18).

["Then this Daniel was preferred above the presidents and princes, because an excellent spirit was in him"]{.class_1922} (vs. 3). The ["excellent spirit"]{.class_1922} was, of course, the Holy Spirit (see our comments on 5:12). The Bible says, ["therefore God, even thy God, hath anointed thee with the oil of gladness ABOVE THY FELLOWS"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 1:9); it says, ["God giveth not the Spirit by measure unto him"]{.class_1922} (John 3:34). Jesus Christ wasn't just filled with the Holy Spirit; He was the [Holy Spirit incarnate.]{.class_1921}

["For in him dwelleth all the fulness of the Godhead bodily"]{.class_1922} (Col. 2:9).

That's why the Holy Spirit is not just ["the Spirit of God"]{.class_1922}; He's ["the Spirit of Christ"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 8:9). The Bible says, ["the Lord is that Spirit"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 3:17), and the Holy Spirit who indwells the believer (1 Cor. 3:16) is ["Christ in you, the hope of glory"]{.class_1922} (Col. 1:27).

["And the king thought to set him over the whole realm."]{.class_1922} That's what Pharaoh said to Joseph, the greatest type of Christ in the word of God (Gen. 41:41). It is God's intent to put His Son on the throne of this earth (Zech. 14:9; Rev. 11:15) and make every knee in []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_126}Heaven, earth, and Hell bow to Him and confess that He's Lord (Phil. 2:9--11). That has been God's intent since before Jesus was born (Luke 1:31--33).

4 Then the presidents and princes sought to find occasion against Daniel concerning the kingdom; but they could find none occasion nor fault; forasmuch as he was faithful, neither was there any error or fault found in him.

5 Then said these men, We shall not find any occasion against this Daniel, except we find it against him concerning the law of his God.

Of course, with the exaltation of Daniel came the debasement of the other Presidents and the Princes of the provinces. When it was brought to the attention of John the Baptist that Jesus was surpassing him, John displayed the right attitude: ["He must increase, but I must decrease"]{.class_1922} (John 3:30). But that is not the attitude of those in charge in this world. They are like the wicked husbandmen in the Parable of the Vineyard:[ "This is the heir; come, let us kill him, and the inheritance shall be ours"]{.class_1922} (Mark 12:7). Like the Jewish leadership of Christ's day, those Presidents and Princes were envious of Daniel (cf. Mark 15:10).

["Then the presidents and princes sought to find occasion against Daniel concerning the kingdom"]{.class_1922} (vs. 4). There's the theme of the whole Bible (again!---see chap. 2): ["the kingdom."]{.class_1922} Those chief priests turned Jesus over to Pilate for claiming to be a King in opposition to Caesar (Luke 23:2; John 19:12). They didn't want Christ to reign over them (Luke 19:14).

["But they could find none occasion nor fault."]{.class_1922} Obviously a type of Christ. Pilate proclaimed three times that he found no fault in Jesus Christ (John 18:38, 19:4, 6). Herod found no fault in Him (Luke 23:14--15). The man who betrayed Him said He was innocent (Matt. 27:4). One of the men crucified with Him recognized He had ["done nothing amiss"]{.class_1922} (Luke 23:41). The centurion who carried out His execution said He ["was a righteous man"]{.class_1922} (Luke 23:47). One of the men closest to Him, who traveled with Him and conversed with Him for three years, could say He ["did no sin, neither was guile found in his mouth"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_127} (1 Pet. 2:22).

["Forasmuch as he was faithful."]{.class_1922} The writer of Hebrews says Jesus ["was faithful to him that appointed him"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 3:2). Jesus could honestly say, ["I do always those things that please him]{.class_1922} \[i.e., His Father\]["]{.class_1922} (John 8:29).

["Neither was there any error or fault in him."]{.class_1922} Do you know why I am convinced Jesus Christ will make a better ruler than Alexander the Great, Julius Caesar, Charlemagne, Genghis Khan, Peter the Great, the Pope (any of them), the Hapsburgs, the Bourbons, the Hohenzollerns, the Romanovs, the Plantagenets, the Tudors, the Stuarts, the Windsors, George Washington, Abraham Lincoln, FDR, JFK, Obama, Clinton (either of them), Bush (either of them), Mao Tse-Tung, Adolf Hitler, Lenin, Stalin, Putin, Arafat, et al.? It is that [He is sinless.]{.class_1921} The reason the Holy Spirit anointed Jesus Christ above His peers was because He ["loved righteousness, and hated iniquity"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 1:9). He is able to provide us access to God the Father because He is ["without sin"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 4:15--16).

Notice in verse 5 that the only way Daniel's enemies could find occasion against him was ["concerning the law of his God."]{.class_1922} That's exactly what Christ's enemies tried to do. They were always trying to catch Him violating the Mosaic Law, and they couldn't do it. "You're violating the Sabbath by healing." "Should we pay tribute to Caesar or not?" "The Law says we ought to stone this woman taken in adultery; what do you say?" That kind of stuff. Jesus answered every accusation against Him with Scripture and shut them up. When they finally did condemn Him, it was for blasphemy for claiming to be the Son of God (Mark 14:61--64; John 19:7). Of course, it was only blasphemy [if it weren't true;]{.class_1921} Jesus Christ provided plenty of evidence for His claims, the definitive proof being [His resurrection]{.class_1921} (Rom. 1:4).

6 Then these presidents and princes assembled together to the king, and said thus unto him, King Darius, live for ever.

7 All the presidents of the kingdom, the governors, and the princes, the counsellors, and the captains, have consulted together to establish a royal statute, and to make []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_128}a firm decree, that whosoever shall ask a petition of any God or man for thirty days, save of thee, O king, he shall be cast into the den of lions.

8 Now, O king, establish the decree, and sign the writing, that it be not changed, according to the law of the Medes and Persians, which altereth not.

9 Wherefore king Darius signed the writing and the decree.

Since the only way of finding an occasion against Daniel was ["concerning the law of his God,"]{.class_1922} the trick was to make keeping the Law illegal. The standard way to make someone who believes the Bible a criminal is to establish a Church-State. In other words, you get laws passed (or executive orders issued or the courts to rule on things) that make it illegal to believe or practice what the Bible says. The present trend in American government is to make it a criminal offense to say what the Bible says. If a Christian populace votes down sex perversion in "marriage," you simply get the liberal judges you appoint to overturn the will of the people. That's how Obama foisted sex perversion on 37 States that recognized marriage as between only one man and one woman.

The three great State churches in the world today are Roman Catholicism, Eastern Orthodoxy, and Islam. Those three godless, depraved, antiscriptural, anti-Christian outfits all pass laws that make Bible believers not just against those religions but criminals in the eyes of the State. For example, in Austria, if you say anything against the Catholic Church in public, you can be turned in to the police, fined as much as \$1,000.00 in American money, and sentenced to a year in jail. That's what can happen to you in Austria for criticizing the Roman Catholic Church. In Islam, Sharia law (Koranic law) dictates that if you criticize Mohammed, you are to be executed; those are called "blasphemy laws." Mohammed practiced that when he was alive ([Hadith,]{.class_1921} Bukhari, 59:369, 4:241), and Moslems are to follow his example ([Koran,]{.class_1921} Sura 4:80).

So these Presidents and Princes go to the King to get him to pass a religious law they know Daniel can't keep if he keeps God's Law. The way they do that is to butter up Darius and appeal to his ego. That Bible says, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_129}["A man that flattereth his neighbour spreadeth a net for his feet"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 29:5). These Princes and Presidents know Darius favors Daniel, so they are going to trap the King with flatteries and force him to execute their competition for power.

Now while it was true that ["All the presidents of the kingdom . . . and the princes"]{.class_1922} had ["consulted together to establish a royal statute"]{.class_1922} (vs. 7), there is nothing in the rest of the chapter about ["the governors . . . the counsellors, and the captains"]{.class_1922} conspiring against Daniel. But the Presidents and Princes needed to present a "united front" before the King to get the law passed, so they do one of two things. Either they "strong arm" their subordinates and make them go along with the plot (knowingly or unknowingly), or they simply lie about the other officials agreeing with them.

The ["royal statute"]{.class_1922} and ["firm decree"]{.class_1922} the Princes and Presidents want passed is: ["whosoever shall ask a petition of any God or man for thirty days, save of thee, O king, he shall be cast into the den of lions"]{.class_1922} (vs. 7). Here the translators have capitalized ["God,"]{.class_1922} even though it refers to ["ANY God,"]{.class_1922} for the same reason they did back in 3:15, and you can see our comments on that verse for the explanation.

Throughout the Scriptures, the word [petition]{.class_1921} is used of a [formal request made to God or a ruler]{.class_1921} (e.g., 1 Sam. 1:7, 27; 1 Kings 2:16, 20; Esth. 5:6--8, 7:2--3, 9:12). It would have been something else if the decree had applied to [every request,]{.class_1921} no matter how small. Imagine having to travel from India or Ethiopia (Esth. 1:1) to Babylon just to get the salt passed at the dinner table.

Verse 8 introduces ["the law of the Medes and Persians, which altereth not."]{.class_1922} This, of course, plays a major role in the events of the book of Esther. ["The law of the Medes and Persians"]{.class_1922} was that once the King had officially passed a law and put his seal to it, nothing and no one could change it, including the King himself. In the Bible, it is a picture of the word of God.

["Heaven and earth shall pass away, but my words shall not pass away"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 24:35).

["For verily I say unto you, Till heaven and earth pass, one jot or one tittle shall in no wise pass from the law, till all be fulfilled"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_130} (Matt. 5:18).

[". . . the scripture cannot be broken"]{.class_1922} (John 10:35).

[". . . the word of the Lord endureth for ever . . . ."]{.class_1929} (1 Pet. 1:25).

The typology here in the passage is the Devil holding God to the letter of His Law. ["The first commandment"]{.class_1922} is ["thou shalt love the Lord thy God with ALL thy heart, and with ALL thy soul, and with ALL thy mind, and with ALL thy strength"]{.class_1922} (Mark 12:30). Nobody except the Son of God has ever kept that commandment satisfactorily. Well, if ["sin is the transgression of the law"]{.class_1922} (1 John 3:4), and ["the wages of sin is death"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 6:23), then the Devil has a right to [kill you]{.class_1921} (Heb. 2:14).

That's why Jesus had to die: He took your place to satisfy the demands of the Law. Someone had to die under the Law. Either it had to be you as the sinner or a sinless sacrifice in your place. Jesus Christ became that sinless sacrifice (1 Pet. 1:18--19, 3:18; 2 Cor. 5:21). I know it comes as a shock to this love-glutted generation, but God wouldn't violate His word to get you out of Hell. God is just as much holy, righteous, and just as He is loving, gracious, and merciful. [Both]{.class_1921} had to be satisfied in order to save you.

The flattery accomplishes its purpose. Darius' ego is coddled, and he signs the decree (vs. 9). The Presidents and Princes now just sit back and wait for their plan to reach its anticipated conclusion.

10 Now when Daniel knew that the writing was signed, he went into his house; and his windows being open in his chamber toward Jerusalem, he kneeled upon his knees three times a day, and prayed, and gave thanks before his God, as he did aforetime.

11 Then these men assembled, and found Daniel praying and making supplication before his God.

12 Then they came near, and spake before the king concerning the king's decree; Hast thou not signed a decree, that every man that shall ask a petition of any God or man within thirty days, save of thee, O king, shall be cast into the den of lions? The king answered and said, The []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_131}thing is true, according to the law of the Medes and Persians, which altereth not.

13 Then answered they and said before the king, That Daniel, which is of the children of the captivity of Judah, regardeth not thee, O king, nor the decree that thou hast signed, but maketh his petition three times a day.

14 Then the king, when he heard these words, was sore displeased with himself, and set his heart on Daniel to deliver him: and he laboured till the going down of the sun to deliver him.

15 Then these men assembled unto the king, and said unto the king, Know, O king, that the law of the Medes and Persians is, That no decree nor statute which the king establisheth may be changed.

16 Then the king commanded, and they brought Daniel, and cast him into the den of lions. Now the king spake and said unto Daniel, Thy God whom thou servest continually, he will deliver thee.

17 And a stone was brought, and laid upon the mouth of the den; and the king sealed it with his own signet, and with the signet of his lords; that the purpose might not be changed concerning Daniel.

There are several things we can get from verse 10. First, Daniel did right although he knew the consequences: ["When Daniel knew the writing was signed."]{.class_1922} When the Sanhedrin told Peter and John to stop preaching in the name of Jesus, they told those Pharisees and Sadducees, ["Whether it be right in the sight of God to hearken unto you more than unto God, judge ye"]{.class_1922} (Acts 4:19), and just to make sure the council judged ["righteous judgment"]{.class_1922} (cf. John 7:24), the apostles told them in the next chapter, ["we ought to obey God rather than men"]{.class_1922} (Acts 5:29). One of the ways the believer can overcome the Devil is not to love his life above his Saviour (Luke 14:26 cf. Rev. 12:11).

Second, Daniel didn't make a big showy "stand." ["He went into his house,"]{.class_1922} in private,[ "as he did aforetime."]{.class_1922} If you stand on the word of God, you won't have to "take your stand" every time some "issue" arises. If you are [consistent]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_132} in believing and proclaiming that Book, you won't have to say, "Look at me! I am about to take my stand!" If you stand on the truths of that Book, you will be right in the line of fire, don't you worry.

A lot of young believers have a lot of zeal but not a lot of wisdom. Some of them think if they are not raising a big stink all the time in their witness that they are compromising. Here at the school one time, we had a fellow with a martyr complex. He figured the way to be like the Apostle Paul was to do something stupid to get himself thrown in jail all the time. So one time he violated one church's private property in order to street preach and then mouthed off to the cops when they tried to get him to move. That's not the way to do it.

Here at PBI, we do everything we can to abide by the law. When the cops said we couldn't be in the median preaching, we moved over to the corners of the intersection on the public sidewalk. When an ordinance was passed that anyone on the corner preaching or selling newspapers had to wear an orange safety vest, we had all our street preachers wear them. People complain about our boys "yelling" at traffic; that's because the local ordinances won't allow us to use bullhorns. We abide by the law. We even give the community a break during the Fall and Winter months, street preaching only in the Spring and Summer. That's not "compromise"; that's common sense to keep the door open. The key is being [consistent]{.class_1921} in what you do.

You don't have to make a big public demonstration to get noticed. Stu Hamblen was one of the original "singing cowboys" in this country, and he got saved in the 1949 Billy Graham Crusade out in Los Angeles. Stu Hamblen hadn't been saved very long when he was out eating with the cowboy evangelist Harvey Springer. Bro. Springer asked Stu to pray to bless the food. Well, Stu Hamblen loved the Lord and wanted to be a good witness, so he took off his ten-gallon cowboy hat and slapped it down on the table, causing everyone in the restaurant to look his way to see what all the commotion was. Then he got down on his knees beside the table and prayed one of those old-time Methodist prayers at the top of his lungs: "O GOD, I PRAY YOU WILL BLESS THIS FOOD IN JESUS' []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_133}NAME! AMEN!"

The Lord may overlook something like that in a babe in Christ, and He might even bless it, but that's not the way to do it. You aren't to pray like that in public to be seen of men (Matt. 6:5). Don't you worry, if you say a normal prayer over your food at a public venue these days, you'll get noticed.

Daniel didn't have to order or alter his behavior for anyone. He simply did right as he had always done. That's what got him noticed in the first place, before any law was passed. You don't have to be obnoxious or boisterous to be a good witness; just be [consistent.]{.class_1921}

Next, notice the "Jewishness" of Daniel's prayer. He opened his windows ["toward Jerusalem"]{.class_1922}; he prayed toward the place where God chose to place His name, even though the Temple at that time was a pile of ashes and rubble. That was a sign of [repentance]{.class_1921} (1 Kings 8:46--50 cf. Dan. 9:1--19). He prayed ["three times a day"]{.class_1922} as David did (Psa. 55:17).

When Mohammed started out his "ministry," he tried to convince the Jews of Medina that he was a "prophet," so he joined them in praying toward Jerusalem. The[ Jewish Encyclopedia]{.class_1921} (1906) observed that Mohammed's "gospel" contained "NOTHING that was not contained in Judaism or in Christianity"; in other words, [Mohammed never had an original thought in his life.]{.class_1921} The reason Moslems pray five times a day is because David and Daniel prayed three times a day; Mohammed was just trying to "one up" the Bible, not being able to come up with anything different or original himself. When the Jews finally saw him for the phony he was, Mohammed decided to [kill]{.class_1921} them, [take their land,]{.class_1921} and pray toward the "god house" in Mecca (the Ka'aba), where he had elevated one god out of the 360 gods there to be "the God" ("Allah").

As Christians, our "windows" shouldn't be "open" to Babylon or Rome spiritually, although that is the case for many these days. They shouldn't be "open" to Egypt or Sodom morally, although more and more churches are facing that direction. They certainly should not be "open" to Mecca in any kind of "Chrislam." They shouldn't even be open to the earthly Jerusalem of today in any kind of "Hebrew Roots" movement (you will get all the "Hebrew roots" you can stand for a thousand years during Christ's reign). Our "windows" are always supposed to be open toward [New Jerusalem]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_134} (Gal. 4:26; Phil. 3:20).

Notice the two basic elements of prayer in verses 10--11. Prayer is [asking]{.class_1921} (["making supplication,"]{.class_1922} vs. 11) and giving thanks (vs. 10). Paul told the Philippians, ["in every thing by prayer and supplication with thanksgiving let your requests be made known unto God"]{.class_1922} (Phil. 4:6). The command for the New Testament believer is: ["Pray without ceasing. In every thing give thanks"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 5:17--18).

When Daniel heard he was going into the lions' den for praying, he didn't stop praying. He said, "That's something to pray about," and he got to praying. I'll tell you how not to fold under pressure: practice when everything is going smoothly. Daniel was able to pray in the face of a death sentence because he had trained himself to pray.

There's an illustration about a soldier in South Africa during the Boer War who got caught sneaking back into camp about an hour after Taps. When asked by his CO what he had been doing, he confessed that he snuck out every night to pray for an hour. In disbelief, the CO said, "You're in the habit of spending that long in private prayer?!" "Yes, sir," said the young soldier. "Well, then," said the CO, "down on your knees, because you never needed prayer more than you need it right now." And down that young fellow went and prayed for thirty minutes right in front of his CO. When that kid got up, his CO said, "You're dismissed. If you hadn't drilled so often, you wouldn't have done so well in review."

So Daniel prayed to God ["as he did aforetime,"]{.class_1922} and the Princes and Presidents were ["assembled"]{.class_1922} together to catch him at it (vs. 11). They knew Daniel's integrity and devotion so much that they knew exactly what he was going to do, and he did it. So off they run to the King to "tattle" on Daniel. That's a picture of the old accuser bringing charges against us before God (Rev. 12:10 cf. Job 1:9--10, 2:4--5).

Notice in verse 13, Daniel is identified by his [tribal ]{.class_1921}affiliation: ["Judah,"]{.class_1922} the same tribe as Jesus Christ. You will also remember back in our comments on 1:3 that Daniel was ["of the king's seed,"]{.class_1922} like Jesus Christ. Daniel is unequivocally a type of Jesus Christ in this []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_135}account.

Now look at verse 14. Darius ["was sore displeased with himself"]{.class_1922} (vs. 14); he realized he had been "played" by the Presidents and Princes. He was intent on delivering Daniel and ["laboured"]{.class_1922} to do so. He worked at finding a way around the law he had signed, and there was no "loophole."

That's a picture of God the Father trying to find a way out of His Son dying for the sins of men. The Liberals and infidels mock the doctrine of the vicarious atonement; they call it "child abuse" on the part of God the Father. But the truth of the matter is, if there had been any other way of saving you apart from the death of His Son, God would have taken it.

When Jesus prayed in the Garden of Gethsemane, ["O my Father, if it be possible, let this cup pass from me: nevertheless not as I will, but as thou wilt"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 26:39), ["all things"]{.class_1922} may have been ["possible"]{.class_1922} for God (Mark 14:36), but not within His will and character (cf. Num. 23:19). Within the confines of God's justice and holiness, there was no other way to save us than by the substitutionary death of Jesus Christ. That was no more "child abuse" than a young man voluntarily entering the Army and dying overseas in action to keep you free back here in the United States.

In verse 15, the Presidents and Princes remind the King that ["the law of the Medes and Persians"]{.class_1922} may not be changed, so in verse 16, Darius carries out the sentence. [God holds Himself to His word.]{.class_1921} Acts 2:23 says Jesus was delivered to His enemies for death ["by the determinate counsel and foreknowledge of God."]{.class_1922} That's why that Bible is the [final authority]{.class_1921} in all matters of faith and practice for the believer. If God Almighty thinks so much of that Book that even He won't break it to get you out of Hell, what are you doing adding to it, cutting it up, changing it, and exalting your opinions and preferences over it?

Now there is a classic illustration of the Lord holding Himself to what He said. In the Dark Ages, there was a King who had a law that if anybody in his kingdom were caught stealing, he would have two eyes put out. One day the King's own son was brought to him; he had been caught red-handed stealing. Everyone in the King's court demanded he carry out the sentence against the son. So the King had []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_136}one of his son's eyes poked out, and then to all the courtiers' amazement, he had one of his own eyes poked out. The law said two eyes had to be put out for theft, and two eyes had been. The law had been satisfied. That's a picture of the vicarious atonement of Christ. The Law demanded death for sin (see Ezek. 18:4, 20), so the Lord allowed His Son to die in your place.

Daniel is ["cast . . . into the den of lions,"]{.class_1922} but before he is sealed in, the King yells down to him, ["Thy God whom thou servest continually, he will deliver thee"]{.class_1922} (vs. 16). Darius had faith; of course, it was kind of shaky. He went back to the palace and fasted (and undoubtedly prayed) all night long without sleeping (vs. 18). And early the next morning, he ran down to the lions' den and ["cried with a lamentable voice"]{.class_1922} (i.e., in a voice full of sorrow and grief), ["is thy God, whom thou servest continually, able to deliver thee from the lions?"]{.class_1922} (vss. 19--20). It reminds one of the words of the father of the possessed boy in Mark 9:24---["Lord, I believe; help thou mine unbelief."]{.class_1922}

The old hymn goes: "He is able to deliver thee." Of course, as we said back in our remarks on 3:18, that is conditioned on God's will and purpose. In Christ's case, He had to go through the horrors of the cross before He could get the deliverance. But He had the promise of His Father ["before the world began"]{.class_1922} that He would be ["loosed"]{.class_1922} from ["the pains of death"]{.class_1922} (Tit. 1:2 cf. Acts 2:24).

If there is any doubt in your mind that what you are reading is a picture of the death, burial, and resurrection of Christ, verses 16--17 should settle the matter for you. When Daniel was cast into the den, he shouldn't have lived long enough for Darius to say anything to him. Look down at verse 24. When those Princes, Presidents, and their families are finally cast into the lions' den, ["the lions . . . brake all their bones in pieces."]{.class_1922} Do you know what the Bible says about the death of Christ?[ "A bone of him shall not be broken"]{.class_1922} (John 19:36).

And in verse 17, ["a stone was brought, and laid upon the mouth of the den; and the king sealed it with his own signet."]{.class_1922} When Christ was buried, a stone was rolled over ["the door of the sepulchre"]{.class_1922} (Mark 15:46), and a seal was placed on it by Pilate (Matt. 27:65--66). Do you see now why Jesus told those Jews, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_137}["Search the scriptures . . . they are they which testify of me"]{.class_1922} (John 5:39)? You can find all kinds of types of the Lord Jesus all through the Old Testament.

18 Then the king went to his palace, and passed the night fasting: neither were instruments of musick brought before him: and his sleep went from him.

19 Then the king arose very early in the morning, and went in haste unto the den of lions.

20 And when he came to the den, he cried with a lamentable voice unto Daniel: and the king spake and said to Daniel, O Daniel, servant of the living God, is thy God, whom thou servest continually, able to deliver thee from the lions?

21 Then said Daniel unto the king, O king, live for ever.

22 My God hath sent his angel, and hath shut the lions' mouths, that they have not hurt me: forasmuch as before him innocency was found in me; and also before thee, O king, have I done no hurt.

23 Then was the king exceeding glad for him, and commanded that they should take Daniel up out of the den. So Daniel was taken up out of the den, and no manner of hurt was found upon him, because he believed in his God.

Now you can't press a type all the way. The Lord wasn't sitting up in Heaven, wringing His hands in worry when Jesus died. He knew He was coming up. But the Father was grief-stricken over the death of His Son. When Jesus died, there was darkness over the earth for three hours (Matt. 27:45; Mark 15:33; Luke 23:44). Bob Jones Sr. used to say of that, that the angels were hanging crepe on the door posts of Heaven, and the chandeliers in the sky went out.

Liberals and infidels don't realize the restraint God exercised when wicked men murdered His Son. If He had intervened, He would have wiped out the entire population of the planet. Back in the Garden of Gethsemane, when the soldiers came to arrest Him, Jesus told Simon Peter, ["Thinkest thou that I cannot now pray to []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_138}my Father, and he shall presently give me more than twelve legions of angels?"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 26:53). A Roman legion consisted of 6,000 men, so ["twelve legions of angels"]{.class_1922} would be 72,000 angels. Jesus said the Father was ready to send more than that if He had asked Him to. One angel in the Old Testament killed 185,000 men in one night (2 Kings 19:35). Given that ratio, 72,000 could kill over [thirteen billion people.]{.class_1921} There weren't that many people on earth in A.D. 33; the best estimate places the world population around 300 million. So I wasn't exaggerating one bit when I said the Lord was ready to wipe out every human being on the face of the earth.

Verse 19: ["Then the king arose very early in the morning, and went in haste unto the den of lions."]{.class_1922} A picture of what took place at the Resurrection. The women came to the tomb ["early in the morning"]{.class_1922} (see Mark 16:1; Luke 24:1). When Mary Magdalene told Peter and John about the empty tomb, they [ran]{.class_1921} to see it (John 20:1--4).

We have already made some comments on verse 20 back under our remarks on verse 16 (which see). Notice what Darius calls the God of Daniel: ["the living God."]{.class_1922} That term first shows up in Deuteronomy 5:26; in that verse, it's a reference to the God who came down on Mt. Sinai and gave the Israelites the Ten Commandments. It stands in contrast to the dead gods of 5:23 (cf. Acts 14:15). We know it can also stand in contrast to the gods who died like men back in Genesis 6--7 (see Psa. 82:6--7).

Did you look up that last reference? Did you notice that those gods who ["die like men"]{.class_1922} are said to ["fall like one of the princes"]{.class_1922}? That's exactly what you are about to see in verse 24 here in Daniel. Those are the ["principalities and powers"]{.class_1922} whom Christ ["spoiled"]{.class_1922} at His resurrection (Col. 2:15). They are part of the ["spiritual wickedness in high places"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:12)---as we will see in 10:20 here in Daniel---that will be punished at the Second Advent (Isa. 24:21). So [both Advents]{.class_1921} show up, in type, here in Daniel 6 (see vs. 26).

Notice the honorific greeting given by Daniel to Darius: ["O king, live for ever"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21). This is the fifth (and last) time it shows up in the book of Daniel (see also 2:4, 3:9, 5:10, and 6:6). It is obviously []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_139}"wishful thinking," for none of the monarchs to whom it is addressed lived forever. In fact, one of them dies within hours of his mother greeting him that way (5:10).

The expression is basically hollow with no substance. The idea is, if the King lives forever, his rule will be forever. It is the vain attempt of earthly monarchs to usurp the coming kingdom of ["the God of heaven"]{.class_1922} (cf. 2:44), who is the only One capable of truly saying such a thing (Deut. 32:40).

What is interesting about the expression is that outside of the Babylonian and Persian Kings (see Neh. 2:3), it is used of [David]{.class_1921} in 1 Kings 1:31. While David did die, he will be [coming back]{.class_1921} to rule forever as ["a prince"]{.class_1922} under his Son (Ezek. 34:24, 37:24--25; Jer. 30:9; Hos. 3:5 cf. 2 Sam 7:12---16; Luke 1:31--33; Mark 12:35--36; Isa. 9:6--7; Rev. 11:15). With David and Christ, the expression is [literal,]{.class_1921} not a delusional fantasy.

Back to Daniel 6: ["My God hath sent his angel, and hath shut the lions' mouths"]{.class_1922} (vs. 22). Before Daniel got pitched into that den of lions, ["the Lion of the tribe of Juda"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 5:5) paid a visit to Leo and Simba, and said, "You lay one tooth or paw on that preacher, and I'll have your head mounted on my wall, got it?" And those lions said, "Yes, Sir; yes, Sir!"

Daniel landed down in that pit, and all those lions got lockjaw. I like the way Bob Jones Sr. used to tell the story. One lion sniffs Daniel and begins to walk away. Daniel says, "Aren't you going to take a bite?" The lion says, "I thought about it, but I lost my appetite completely." One lion walks up to that old prophet and licks his hand. Daniel says, "How about you?" That lion scowls and says, "I just had a terrible attack of indigestion; no, thank you." Some wit said, "The reason those lions wouldn't eat Daniel was because he was 90% backbone and 10% grit."

After a while, the Lord said to Daniel, "You getting tired of standing around down here?" "Yes," said Daniel, "I'm not as young as I used to be. My arthritis is acting up on me, you know." So God said, "Why don't you lie down?" The Lord pulled up one of those lions for Daniel's pillow, and Daniel laid his head back on that lion's mane. The Lord said, "Anything I can get for you before you go to sleep?" "If you wouldn't mind," said Daniel, "could you please turn []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_140}this lion around so I am facing Jerusalem?" And Bob Jones Sr. said, "Daniel was fanned to sleep by the zephyr of an angel's wing and lulled to slumber by the sound of music from a world celestial."

Now the lesson for you, Christian, is that the Lord will go with you into the lions' den just as He does in the fiery furnace (see our remarks under Dan. 3:25). Paul said of his answer before Caesar, ["Notwithstanding the Lord stood with me . . . and I was delivered out of the mouth of the lion"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 4:17). But later on, some of his converts were sent into arenas with the lions, and the Lord didn't deliver them ["out of the mouth of the lion."]{.class_1922} Yet God still preserved them ["unto his heavenly kingdom"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 4:18). Even as the lions were attacking them and devouring them, those Christians stood there in the arena singing praises to God. Some of those Romans up in the stands got under such terrible conviction watching that, that they got saved on the spot.

The sinlessness of Christ (in type) comes up again in verse 22, and you can see our comments on it under verse 4. The Charismatic "televangelists" are always coming up with kooky, nutty ideas that are just as heretical as anything put out by the Catholics, JWs, and Mormons. One of the more recent heresies is the idea that Jesus became a sinner on the cross. While it is absolutely true that ["he was numbered with the transgressors"]{.class_1922} (Mark 15:28), was ["made . . . to be sin for us"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 5:2), and was identified with the Devil in His death (John 3:14), Jesus never sinned in mind, heart, word, or deed; not even on the cross. Second Corinthians 5:21 makes it clear that even as God was making His Son ["to be sin for us,"]{.class_1922} Jesus Christ ["knew no sin."]{.class_1922}

["Daniel was taken up out of the den"]{.class_1931} (vs. 23)---a type of the Resurrection. ["No manner of hurt was found in him."]{.class_1931} And here the type differs from the actuality. In His resurrected body, Jesus Christ bears the scars of His "five bleeding wounds . . . received on Calvary" (see John 20:25--27);[ they remain as a testimony to the nation that pierced Him so they will believe on Him at His return (Zech. 12:10).]{.class_1934}

But the most important thing to note in verse 23 is [why]{.class_1921} Daniel was delivered: ["because he believed in his God."]{.class_1922} Daniel ["stopped the mouths of lions" "through faith"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 11:33), but it was a [personal]{.class_1921} faith (["his God"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_141}). Daniel's faith was not some faith in an impersonal God, like that of the devils (James 2:19). It was not the monotheistic faith of Mohammed in a god who never did anything for him. Daniel trusted in a God who took a personal interest in him, revealed things to him directly (not just through an angel), worked on his behalf, and delivered him miraculously. "Allah" tormented Mohammed in the "revelations" he gave him, he never spoke to Mohammed personally, and as far as the record goes, Allah never did one thing for his "prophet" one way or another (unless you count giving him permission to steal his son's wife).

Jesus Christ's relationship with His Father was [personal]{.class_1921} (Heb. 1:9; John 20:17; 2 Cor. 11:31; Rev. 3:12), and if you are ever going to make it to Heaven, you will have to have a [personal]{.class_1921} relationship with God (Eph. 1:3; 1 Pet. 1:3; John 1:12, 20:28; Phil. 4:19). You don't get that through a starchy cookie and a jug of shinny; you don't get it through the city water system. You get it by personally trusting God's Son as your Saviour, and having the Holy Spirit of God come into you and make you one with your Lord.

24 And the king commanded, and they brought those men which had accused Daniel, and they cast them into the den of lions, them, their children, and their wives; and the lions had the mastery of them, and brake all their bones in pieces or ever they came at the bottom of the den.

The verse shows you what is known in theological circles as the doctrine of "federal headship." That is, the head of a household, a nation, or a race can bring either a blessing or a curse on the whole household, nation, or race. That's what's involved in the sin of Adam (Rom. 5:12), the sin of Ham (Gen. 9:20--25), the faith of Abraham (Heb. 11:8 cf. Gen. 12:1--4), and the sacrifice of Jesus Christ (Rom. 5:15). Here, the families suffer right along with the Presidents and Princes.

That also shows you the families were in on the plot. God doesn't just punish an individual for the sins of the father or leader; the individual has his own sins for which to account. The families of the Presidents and Princes were in collusion with them and certainly []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_142}knew about the plot from the time it was hatched. See a similar thing in Joshua 7:24--26 and Esther 9:7--10.

Now if you thought Daniel surviving the night down in the pit with the lions was not miraculous, look at what happens to the Princes, Presidents, and their families: ["the lions had the mastery of them, and brake all their bones in pieces or ever they came at the bottom of the den."]{.class_1922} That was 122 grown men, not counting 244 (or more) women and children. That's a minimum of 366 people who never made it to the bottom before the lions broke every bone in their bodies. God told those beasts when to bite and when not to bite.

The typology in verse 24 is Satan ["as a roaring lion . . . seeking whom he may devour"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 5:8). The only way you are going to survive against him is by the same kind of faith Daniel had (1 Pet. 5:9). Unlike Daniel, you may have to suffer a while, but you have the promise that Daniel's God will ["make you perfect, stablish, strength, settle you"]{.class_1922} (1 Pet. 5:10).

25 Then king Darius wrote unto all people, nations, and languages, that dwell in all the earth; Peace be multiplied unto you.

26 I make a decree, That in every dominion of my kingdom men tremble and fear before the God of Daniel: for he is the living God, and stedfast for ever, and his kingdom that which shall not be destroyed, and his dominion shall be even unto the end.

27 He delivereth and rescueth, and he worketh signs and wonders in heaven and in earth, who hath delivered Daniel from the power of the lions.

28 So this Daniel prospered in the reign of Darius, and in the reign of Cyrus the Persian.

Darius makes a decree that just about matches Nebuchadnezzar's back in chapter 4 (see 4:1--3). Darius gets "converted." He takes heed to God delivering Daniel (cf. chap. 3) and doesn't require a humbling process (chap. 4). The big difference between Nebuchadnezzar's decrees in 3:29 and 4:1--3 is that Darius decrees the fear of the Lord []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw828.xhtml_page_143}to his subjects, not just fear of what the King would do to them.

["Then king Darius wrote unto all people, nations, and languages, that dwell in all the earth"]{.class_1922} (vs. 25). Consider, if you will, the far-reaching consequences of what Daniel did. Because Daniel did right, every province in the Persian Empire, along with every race and language represented in those provinces, got to hear of the God of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob.
