That is what someone says when he is in [agony.]{.class_1921} You'll hear it from someone who has been in a car wreck or someone injured in combat on the battlefield. As the life ebbs away, it gets reduced to "Oh God!" If a fellow doesn't have a God, he'll call for his mother. You will hear that from hardened "thirty-year" men who live like the devil and "cuss a blue streak." They'll get in an artillery bombardment and go half out of their minds and be saying, "Momma, momma, mother." It's absolutely pitiful.

That thing will go "Oh my God" to "Oh God," and when the fellow is dying and taking his last breath, it will be reduced to just "Oh." Back in 1977, George Burns made a dirty movie with John Denver called "Oh God." It was supposed to be a comedy, but that saying's no joke. It's the dying gasp of a sinner about to meet his Maker. Both George Burns and John Denver have gone to give account to Him (Rom. 14:12).

The reader should note the Trinitarian nature of verse 19: ["O Lord]{.class_1922} \[Father\][, hear; O Lord]{.class_1922} \[Son\][, forgive; O Lord ]{.class_1922}\[Holy Spirit\][]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_215}[, hearken and do."]{.class_1922} The Trinity has one name; each member claims the name ["Lord"]{.class_1922} (Jude 4--5; Phil. 2:11; 2 Cor. 3:17).

20 And whiles I was speaking, and praying, and confessing my sin and the sin of my people Israel, and presenting my supplication before the LORD my God for the holy mountain of my God;

21 Yea, whiles I was speaking in prayer, even the man Gabriel, whom I had seen in the vision at the beginning, being caused to fly swiftly, touched me about the time of the evening oblation.

22 And he informed me, and talked with me, and said, O Daniel, I am now come forth to give thee skill and understanding.

23 At the beginning of thy supplications the commandment came forth, and I am come to shew thee; for thou art greatly beloved: therefore understand the matter, and consider the vision.

The word ["whiles"]{.class_1922} in verse 20 is merely an archaic spelling of the word [while.]{.class_1921} Should you come across a [King James]{.class_1921} Bible that has taken the [s]{.class_1921} off the word, that is not a "satanic" change in the text, as some of the more zealous brethren would have you believe. [While]{.class_1921} and [whiles]{.class_1921} are merely different spellings of the same word. You will see the same thing in current speech with the word [anyway]{.class_1921} and [anyways.]{.class_1921}

The ["holy mountain"]{.class_1922} of verses 16 and 20 is Mount Zion in Jerusalem, where the Temple was located (Isa. 66:20; Joel 2:1, 3:17; Zech. 8:3).

Now, Daniel has been praying. From 6:10, we know that he prayed ["three times a day,"]{.class_1922} and those ["three times"]{.class_1922} are defined for you in Psalm 55:17---["Evening, and morning, and at noon."]{.class_1922} The prayer here was an ["evening"]{.class_1922} prayer. Daniel was praying ["about the time of the evening oblation"]{.class_1922}; that's another way of saying ["the time of the offering of the evening sacrifice"]{.class_1922} (1 Kings 18:36). That would be 3:00 p.m. our time (Acts 3:1). It was the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_216}time of Christ's death on the cross (Mark 15:34--37).

Daniel's prayer of confession is interrupted by the appearance of Gabriel (vs. 21), the angel who appeared to him back in 8:16. Once more, note that an angel appears as a ["man,"]{.class_1922} but because the verse said ["being caused to fly,"]{.class_1922} all the medieval Catholic artists assumed angels must have wings (see the same thing in Rev. 14:6). Well, when I used to take meetings out of town I was ["caused to fly"]{.class_1922} four times a month, and the only wings were those on the airplane.

You say, "Ah, Ruckman . . . ." "Ah, Ruckman," yourself. The power of flight doesn't mean the one flying has to have seven-foot wings growing out of his back. The two Jews who dreamed up Superman knew that even if you don't. Gabriel was an angel, and angels don't have wings anywhere in that Bible. Mohammed's 600-winged Gabriel was a delusion given him by ["the god]{.class_1922} \[that's what [Allah]{.class_1921} means\][ of this world"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 4:4), who was a creature that [did]{.class_1921} have wings (Ezek. 28:14 cf. Ezek. 10:5--15).

Verse 22: ["O Daniel, I am now come forth to give thee skill and understanding."]{.class_1922} Of course, this ["skill and understanding"]{.class_1922} came from God, as it had all throughout Daniel's ministry (see 1:17 and our comments), but this time, God is using an angel as an instrument to bring them to Daniel.

["At the beginning of thy supplications the commandment came forth"]{.class_1922} (vs. 23). So while the prayer of Daniel 9 may have been a specific prayer, on a specific day, during a specific time (vs. 21), the implication of the above statement is that Daniel had been praying and confessing for much longer than an hour or even a day. In the next chapter, Daniel gets to praying and fasting for 21 days, and the answer gets delayed. But God heard Daniel's prayer from day one, and the answer was sent out, but opposed by the ["principalities"]{.class_1922} and ["rulers of the darkness of this world"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:12). That seems to be the case here, though no time element is given. Daniel was heard from the time he started praying, but Gabriel didn't come with the answer until an unspecified amount of time later.

That's why Jesus teaches twice in the Gospel of Luke on importunity in prayer (Luke 11:5--8, 18:1--8). In other words, you []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_217}keep on praying until you get a definite answer. The problem might be spiritual opposition to your prayer, so you ["wrestle"]{.class_1922} in prayer ["against spiritual wickedness in high places"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:12). Have you ever noticed there are only [six]{.class_1921} pieces of the Christian's armor given by name in Ephesians 6:14--17? Then it's incomplete; it's not ["the whole armour of God"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:13); it needs a [seventh]{.class_1921} piece. The seventh piece of armor for a Roman legionnaire was the shin greaves. No shin greaves are mentioned in Ephesians 6, because the Christian soldier is to be on his knees in [prayer]{.class_1921} (Eph. 6:18).

So when you enter the arena of prayer, you may not know it, and it may not seem like anything is going on, but you are tangling with something spiritual and invisible between you and ["the throne of grace"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 4:16). The key to winning the match is don't give up, don't throw in the towel. Keep on praying. Fast if you need to, but keep on praying.

Daniel is called ["greatly beloved"]{.class_1922} three times in the book: here in verse 23 and in 10:11 and 10:19. That not only has to do with Daniel's righteousness (Ezek. 14:14, 20), it also has to do with whom Daniel represents. Daniel is confessing the sins of his nation, Israel, and Israel is God's ["beloved"]{.class_1922} in the Old Testament (Psa. 50:5, 108:6; Jer. 11:15, 12:7).

In the New Testament, Jesus Christ is God's ["beloved" ]{.class_1922}(Matt. 3:17, 12:18, 17:5; Luke 20:13), and when you are put in Christ by the Holy Spirit upon salvation, you are ["accepted in the beloved"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 1:6), and are ["beloved of God"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 1:7). God may love a lost man enough to send His Son to die for the man's sins (John 3:16), but He doesn't love any sinner, who rejects the sacrifice of Jesus Christ, enough to keep him from burning forever in the Lake of Fire. "Jesus loves me; this I know, for the Bible tells me so." Not if you turn down the free gift of God's Son,[ no.]{.class_1921}

["Consider the vision."]{.class_1922} Now no ["vision"]{.class_1922} has been given in this chapter. Clarence Larkin, therefore, conjectures that the reference is to some vision Daniel had between verses 2 and 3 that is not recorded in Scripture; but that is stretching things quite a bit, especially when a ["vision"]{.class_1922} is referred to in the context. Verse 21: ["the man Gabriel, whom I had seen in the vision at the beginning."]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_218} The reference is obviously to Gabriel appearing to give Daniel the interpretation of his vision back in chapter 8.

Larkin will say, "That can't be it, because Gabriel explained the vision of chapter 8 to Daniel." That is only partly true. There were still things about that vision that Daniel didn't understand (see our comments on 8:27). So I take the final command of verse 23 to be a reference to Daniel 8; Gabriel is going to give further revelation from God on that vision.

24 Seventy weeks are determined upon thy people and upon thy holy city, to finish the transgression, and to make an end of sins, and to make reconciliation for iniquity, and to bring in everlasting righteousness, and to seal up the vision and prophecy, and to anoint the most Holy.

25 Know therefore and understand, that from the going forth of the commandment to restore and to build Jerusalem unto the Messiah the Prince shall be seven weeks, and threescore and two weeks: the street shall be built again, and the wall, even in troublous times.

26 And after threescore and two weeks shall Messiah be cut off, but not for himself: and the people of the prince that shall come shall destroy the city and the sanctuary; and the end thereof shall be with a flood, and unto the end of the war desolations are determined.

27 And he shall confirm the covenant with many for one week: and in the midst of the week he shall cause the sacrifice and the oblation to cease, and for the overspreading of abominations he shall make it desolate, even until the consummation, and that determined shall be poured upon the desolate.

We now come to the most important, and the most controversial, part of the whole chapter. This is known as the "Seventy Weeks of Daniel" among the prophetic expositors. ["SEVENTY WEEKS are determined upon thy people and upon thy holy city"]{.class_1922} (vs. 24).

It is no coincidence that the revelation of the ["Seventy weeks"]{.class_1922} follows on what Daniel read about the ["seventy years"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_219} of captivity from Jeremiah (see vs. 2 and our comments). This alerts the reader that more is involved here than just seventy seven-day periods of time. The ["weeks"]{.class_1922} of verse 24 have something to do with [years.]{.class_1921} So unlike the 24-hour days of 8:14, 26 (see our comments on those verses), the "days" that make up these ["Seventy weeks"]{.class_1922} are indeed "prophetic days"; i.e., each day represents a year. The precedent was laid down by the Lord in Numbers 14:34 (see also Ezek. 4:6); God made those Israelites wander in the wilderness a year for every day those spies were in the land of Canaan. Seventy weeks would be seventy times seven days per week, which would be 490 "days." So it is a period of 490 years under discussion.

You will remember under our remarks under verse 2 that 490 years were the time of seventy Sabbatical years (Lev. 25:1--4). The Sabbath  (in this case, one of years) should tell you that you are in [Jewish ]{.class_1921}territory (Ezek. 20:12, 20), not that of the Gentiles or the Church. That is exactly what you find in Daniel 9:24---["Seventy weeks are determined upon THY PEOPLE]{.class_1922} \[the Jews\][ and upon THY CITY]{.class_1922} \[Jerusalem\][."]{.class_1922} Contrary to Seventh-day Adventist teaching (Ellen G. White, [The Great Controversy, ]{.class_1921}1911, pg. 410), no part of Daniel's Seventieth Week takes place in the Church Age (Acts 1:5 cf. 1 Cor. 12:13).

Now, Clarence Larkin has an interesting chart in his work on [Dispensational Truth.]{.class_1921} You will have a hard time finding it on the Internet because it is not included in his numbered pages. But if you get a copy of his printed book, you will find it between pages 71 and 72. It is entitled "Prophetic Chronology or 'Seventy Weeks' of Scripture: Showing God's Dealings with the [Hebrew Race."]{.class_1921} In that chart, Larkin shows you how God deals with the Jewish people in four time periods of 490 years each. Of course, just as you are about to see in verses 26--27, there can be gaps of time not counted in the 490 years because of the sin of God's people.

1\. 490 years from the birth of Abraham to the exodus from Egypt, minus fifteen years between the birth of Ishmael and the birth of Isaac. That was the time Abraham was trying to make the promise of God come to pass by his wife Sarah's machinations. God didn't count the time when Ishmael was usurping the promise.

2\. 490 years between the exodus from Egypt and Solomon dedicating the Temple, not counting the time Israel was out of fellowship with God in the book of Judges.

3\. 490 years between Solomon and the decree for the Jews to rebuild Jerusalem; the seventy years of Babylonian Captivity are not counted.

4\. 490 years between the decree to rebuild Jerusalem and the Second Advent, with 2,000 (+/--) years of the Church Age not included in the count. That's because Israel, as a nation, in the Gospels, rejected their Messiah.

Now, Gabriel gives the purpose of the final 490 years in verse 24, and that purpose has six parts to it:

1. ["To finish the transgression."]{.class_1922}

2. ["To make an end of sins."]{.class_1922}

3. ["To make reconciliation for iniquity."]{.class_1922}

4. ["To bring in everlasting righteousness."]{.class_1922}

5. ["To seal up the vision and prophecy."]{.class_1922}

6. ["To anoint the most Holy."]{.class_1922}

If I were an amillennialist or a postmillenialist, and I wanted to rid myself of any future application of the verse so [I]{.class_1921} could bring in the kingdom, I would read it this way: Christ finished the transgression at Calvary. He made an end of sins when He died on the cross. Through His death, He was able to reconcile us to God. ["To seal up the vision and the prophecy"]{.class_1922} was Him fulfilling all the Old Testament at His First Advent. His perfect sacrifice on the cross is what brings us ["everlasting righteousness."]{.class_1922} And as ["the most Holy,"]{.class_1922} Jesus Christ was anointed at His baptism.

See how it's done? You get rid of the prophetic application by spiritualizing everything and relegating it to the past at Christ's First Advent and His death at Calvary; that way there's nothing left for the future. But did you notice I had to "stretch" things a bit in some places? I'll grant you that Christ's death made ["reconciliation for iniquity,"]{.class_1922} and I'll grant you He was anointed by the Holy Spirit at His baptism. But boy, when you say ["FINISH the transgression"]{.class_1922} and ["END of sins,"]{.class_1922} you have said something else. The [payment]{.class_1921} for sins was made and finished at Calvary, but transgressions and sins have gone on non-stop for the last 2,000 years. And if you think you are living ["in everlasting righteousness"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_221} right now, you need to be locked up in a "rubber room" in a straightjacket for your own safety. Also, I can show you prophecy after prophecy in the Old Testament that wasn't fulfilled anywhere in the Gospels or the book of Acts; i.e., if you take what the Holy Spirit said seriously and don't subject it to your own fanciful flights of private interpretation.

The thing to remember is that [nothing]{.class_1921} in verse 24 is to any [Gentile]{.class_1921} or the [Church.]{.class_1921} Everything is doctrinally for a [Jew;]{.class_1921} specifically those Jews in [Jerusalem.]{.class_1921} Everything in verse 24 waits future fulfillment for the nation of Israel, with Jerusalem as its capital. The time when Israel's transgressions are finished and their sins are ended is at Christ's [Second]{.class_1921} Advent (Rom. 11:25--26; Zech. 12:10; Isa. 45:17--25; Ezek. 37:21--24; Joel 3:16--21; Mic. 7:14--19; Zeph. 3:8--13). As we saw back in 8:12--13, though, ["the transgression"]{.class_1922} is a [specific]{.class_1921} transgression: it is the image of the Antichrist set up in the rebuilt temple. At His return in power, Jesus Christ breaks up that idol just like He did Dagon back in 1 Samuel 5; He smashes it to powder just like Moses did to the golden calf (Exod. 32:20) and just like Josiah did to the images of the groves in Israel (2 Kings 23:15; 2 Chron. 34:7).

The ["reconciliation for iniquity"]{.class_1922} is not the reconciliation of the individual sinner to God by the death of Christ (Rom. 5:10; 2 Cor. 5:18--20; Col. 1:20); it is the reconciliation of Israel as a [nation]{.class_1921} with their God, from whom they are now estranged (Hos. 2:2). That reconciliation begins in the Tribulation, with the calling out of a Jewish remnant, and culminates with Christ's return, when the nation is converted in a day (Hos. 2:14--23). This "national" reconciliation is something the "godly Fundamentalist," who teaches at the average Christian school, does not understand, for it requires the reinstitution of [animal sacrifices]{.class_1921} on a rebuilt altar of the Millennial Temple in Jerusalem, with Jesus Christ right there presiding (Ezek. 45:15, 17). It has nothing to do with the once-for-all, finished, completed atonement for sin by Jesus Christ [right now]{.class_1921} (Col. 2:12--14). Those Old Testament holy days, Sabbaths, and offerings are [coming back]{.class_1921} (Col. 2:16--17); they'll return with a Jewish King on the throne of David at the Jewish capital of Jerusalem.

When that Jewish King shows up, He makes []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_222}["a new covenant with the house of ISRAEL, and with the house of JUDAH"]{.class_1922} (Jer. 31:31; Heb. 8:8). You need to get with whom that covenant is made. That is [not]{.class_1921} ["the new testament"]{.class_1922} of Christ's blood shed for the lost sinner in this age (Matt. 26:28; Luke 22:20; 1 Cor. 11:25). That is the new testament as applied to ["ISRAEL"]{.class_1922} and ["JUDAH,"]{.class_1922} not the Church. In that covenant, God puts the LAW ([not the Gospel]{.class_1921}) in the hearts of those Jews (Jer. 31:33). That covenant will be ["an everlasting covenant"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 61:8; Jer. 32:40; Ezek. 16:60, 37:26) that is connected with God's righteousness (Isa. 61:10; Hos. 2:18--19). When that covenant is made, Jerusalem is ["called, The city of righteousness"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 1:26) because the Lord of righteousness is there reigning as King (Jer. 23:6, 33:16).

The sealing of ["the vision and prophecy"]{.class_1922} takes place in 12:21. It is sealed ["to the time of the end,"]{.class_1922} when it is unsealed (Rev. 22:10). But this sealing is only partial when it comes to the Jews. Paul says, ["blindness IN PART is happened to Israel, until the fulness of the Gentiles be come in"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 11:25). Right now, if an individual Jew turns to Christ in belief, the veil that blinds him to the truths in his Scriptures is taken away (2 Cor. 3:14--16). A saved Jew has the Author of Holy Scripture living in him to lead and guide him ["into all truth"]{.class_1922} (John 16:13). He has the Spirit of Christ in Him (Rom. 8:9) to open his understanding to what's in that Book (Luke 24:44) and expound the things in it about the Lord Jesus Christ (Luke 24:25--27; John 15:26).

Having seen how everything in verse 24, so far, deals with Israel at the Second Advent, ["to anoint the most Holy"]{.class_1922} presents a problem. If ["the most Holy"]{.class_1922} refers to Jesus Christ, then Jesus Christ was anointed at His First Advent, at His baptism (Luke 4:18; John 3:34; Acts 10:37--38; Heb. 1:9). Of course, like David in 1 Samuel 16:13, Jesus Christ was anointed King long before He takes the throne. So if ["the most Holy"]{.class_1922} is a reference to Jesus Christ, what you have is another anointing when Christ comes to reign. That is what happened to David, one of the greatest types of Christ in the Bible. Samuel anoints him as a teenager (1 Sam. 16:13). Years later, when he is thirty years old, he is anointed King over Judah (2 Sam. 2:4), and as far as God is concerned, that is when he started the reign []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_223}he was promised back in 1 Samuel 16 (2 Sam. 5:4--5). Seven-and-a-half years later, he is anointed a third time as King over all twelve tribes (2 Sam. 5:3, 5). So Christ has at least one more anointing, and perhaps two.

Now I would be amiss if I didn't point out to you what Clarence Larkin says about ["the most Holy"]{.class_1922}; after all, you will always get more sound Biblical material out of Clarence Larkin than any Catholic or Protestant "catechism." Larkin contends that ["the most Holy"]{.class_1922} isn't Jesus Christ, but ["the most holy place"]{.class_1922} of the Millennial Temple (Ezek. 41:4, 43:12, 44:13, 45:3). That could very well be, since the first Tabernacle erected by Moses had to be anointed before it could be used (Exod. 30:26--29, 40:9--10). [If]{.class_1921} that be the case, I would say ["the most Holy"]{.class_1922} refers to the entire Temple, just as it did the Tabernacle back in Exodus.

Verse 25 divides the seventy weeks into two periods of ["seven weeks"]{.class_1922} and 62 weeks, with a final division of one week in verse 27. That would be 49 years, 434 years, and seven years. Moreover, the final seven years are divided in half: three and a half, and three and a half. The second half of the Seventieth Week is what we call the "Great Tribulation" (Matt. 24:21; Rev. 7:14 cf. Rev. 11:2--3, 12:6, 14, 13:5). There are two systems for how these weeks fall historically and prophetically, and I will try to present them both, and then let you decide.

For years, I preached a message called "The Seven Sevens." Its thesis was that God operated on a "sevens" system: seven days and then something special, the Sabbath; seven weeks after the Feast of Firstfruits and then Pentecost; three feasts in the seventh month---Trumpets, Atonement, and Tabernacles. So you count seven thousand years from Creation (4000 B.C.), and you have a "Sabbatical rest" for the earth during the Millennial reign of Christ. That means the Second Advent should have taken place in A.D. 2000. But I always prefaced that with two conditions: [if our calendar were right]{.class_1921} and [if there weren't any years God wasn't counting]{.class_1921} (see our comments on Job 3:6 in that Commentary)---and it could be [both.]{.class_1921} Obviously the Second Advent did not take place in the year 2000, but that does not make the system laid out in Scripture any less valid.

But that being said, I have no more guesses to make as to the date of Christ's return, either the Rapture or the Advent (and guesses are all I ever made). So when it comes to which system is right for the fulfillment of Daniel's Seventieth Week, I must admit that I am not as certain as I may have been in the past. I will explain both systems and give you the points for both and the problems with both.

The seventy weeks begin with ["the command to restore and to build Jerusalem."]{.class_1922} This presents the first problem with any system of interpreting the seventy weeks. You see, there are [four]{.class_1921} decrees in the Bible that could qualify as that command.

1\. Cyrus sends the Jews back to rebuild the Temple in 536 B.C. (Ezra 1:1--4).

2\. After the work was stopped in Ezra 4:17--24, a second decree to finish rebuilding the Temple was issued by Darius in 519 B.C. (Ezra 6:7--12).

3\. In 458 B.C., Artaxerxes sent Ezra to Jerusalem to reestablish the daily sacrifice and to organize the priesthood (Ezra 7:11--26).

4\. And in 445 B.C. (I personally make it 446 B.C.), Artaxerxes sent Nehemiah to rebuild the walls of Jerusalem (Neh. 2:1--8).

The end of verse 25 tells you exactly what decree is ["the commandment"]{.class_1922}: ["the street shall be built again, and THE WALL, even in troublous times."]{.class_1922} But the year of that decree is what stands in question. Nehemiah 2:1 says it was given ["in the twentieth year of Artaxerxes the king."]{.class_1922} So the question is, when did that twenty years begin?

I have given the standard date for Artaxerxes' decree back up in point 4 above. That date is arrived at by figuring from Artaxerxes' [solo reign]{.class_1921} (he had a joint reign with his father, which we will discuss shortly). Using the date of 445 B.C. to begin the seventy weeks, Larkin has 49 years (["seven weeks"]{.class_1922}) to the close of the Old Testament canon, 434 years (62 weeks) to the Triumphal Entry, a gap of time between Calvary and the Rapture which would be the Church Age, and the whole of Daniel's Seventieth Week in the future. You can see this on my chart "A Future Seventieth Week."

Of course, for these years to work out, you have to use thirty-day months as you find in comparing Genesis 7:11, 24 to Genesis 8:3--4. For the Flood to start on the seventeenth of ["the second month"]{.class_1922} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1271.xhtml_page_225}and the ark to come to rest on the seventeenth of the seventh month (i.e., five months), you would have to have thirty days per month. Sir Robert Anderson was the first to calculate the time based on a thirty-day month in his work [The Coming Prince.]{.class_1921}

This is what I call laboring ["in the word,"]{.class_1922} brother (1 Tim. 5:17). It involves a lot of math which I am not proficient enough to figure or explain. You can read it all in Larkin's [Book of Daniel.]{.class_1921} He shows where Anderson got his figures, how he dealt with leap years and the year of the birth of Christ, how he figured the length of the ministry of Christ and where he was wrong, and influences of secular history on the calendar. Anderson has done more work of a Biblical nature on the subject than commentaries like Clarke, Jamieson, Fausset, Brown, Henry, Dummelow, Ellicott, Barnes, Lange, et al. I highly commend the reader to Larkin's [Book of Daniel]{.class_1921} and Anderson's [The Coming Prince]{.class_1921} on these computations.

But on that same chart, I have also included Bullinger's "take" on the subject. Bullinger starts where Larkin does: in Nehemiah 2. But Bullinger has the Artaxerxes of Nehemiah 2 as the same King as Ahasuerus of Esther. He identifies both as "Astyages" (see our remarks on vs. 1 above). Bullinger has dates for the events of the Exile and afterwards completely different from other chronologists on the subjects. He has the destruction of the Temple by Nebuchadnezzar take place in 477 B.C. instead of 586 B.C. He has Astyages make the decree of Nehemiah 2 in 454 B.C., and Cyrus (Astyages' and Esther's son in Bullinger's system) make the decree of Ezra 1 in 426 B.C. This divides the first ["seven weeks"]{.class_1922} of Daniel 9:25 into 28 years and 21 years. The 62 weeks begin in 405 B.C. with completion of the Temple in Ezra 6:15. From there, Bullinger's chart matches Larkin's, with all seven years of Daniel's Seventieth Week being future, after the Church Age.

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1430.xhtml}

::: {}
![](image_1437.jpg){.class_1438}
:::

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1439.xhtml}

The second system proposed by some Bible-believing brethren, which has caught on in a number of places, is that the decree of Nehemiah 2 is given in 453 B.C., but they arrive at that date differently than Bullinger. Instead of inventing their own chronology, they go back to Artaxerxes' coreign with his father and begin the first twenty years of his reign there. This places the end of the 69 weeks at [Christ's baptism.]{.class_1921}

And this is where this view differs substantially from that of the standard dispensationalists. Instead of placing all of Daniel's Seventieth Week in the future, after the Church Age, it has the first three-and-a-half years fulfilled during Christ's ministry, between His baptism and His death (see our chart on "Division of the Seventieth Week"---"The Split Seventieth Week" part). I will expound more on this view as I work my way through the passage.

Verse 25:[ "unto the Messiah the Prince."]{.class_1922} The word ["Messiah"]{.class_1922} is a transliteration of the Hebrew word [Mashiyach;]{.class_1921} it means "anointed." The New Testament word is [Christ]{.class_1921} (John 1:41) (Gk.---[Christos]{.class_1921}). It can not only refer to the [Lord's]{.class_1921} anointed (Psa. 2:2)---["the Lord's Christ"]{.class_1922} (Luke 2:26)---it can also refer to the [Devil]{.class_1921} (Ezek. 28:14) and [his christ]{.class_1921}---the Antichrist (1 John 2:18, 22, 4:3; 2 John 7). He is pictured in the Old Testament by King Saul, a demon-possessed paranoid called ["the LORD'S anointed"]{.class_1922} (1 Sam. 24:6, 10, 26:9, 11, 16, 23; 2 Sam. 1:14, 16). The word [Messiah,]{.class_1921} in reference to Jesus Christ, appears four times in the Bible: twice in the Old Testament (Dan. 9:25--26) and twice in the New Testament (John 1:41, 4:25).

He is called ["the Prince"]{.class_1922} in verse 25. Both views of Daniel's Seventieth Week tend to interpret the word ["Prince"]{.class_1922} here as an office that is preparatory to being a King. But as we saw back under 1:3, a Prince can refer to any type of ruler. Back in 1:7, the eunuchs had a ["prince" ]{.class_1922}over them. Well, he wasn't "a King in training" as Larkin says; he was their ["master" ]{.class_1922}(1:3). Those ["princes"]{.class_1922} back in chapter 6 weren't going to be Kings; they were the rulers over their provinces. In the Bible, a Prince can refer to the head of a tribe (Num. 34), a Governor (Ezra 1:8 cf. Ezra 5:14), and even a King who is currently reigning (1 Kings 14:7, 16:2).

Those who have read the Epistle Dedicatory to the [King James]{.class_1921} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1439.xhtml_page_228}Bible will remember that the translation was dedicated  "TO THE MOST HIGH AND MIGHTY [PRINCE]{.class_1921} JAMES, [KING]{.class_1921} OF GREAT BRITAIN, FRANCE, AND IRELAND." He was still called a "Prince," even though he had been on the throne as King for eight years.

Here, the word ["Prince"]{.class_1922} is that ["ruler in Israel,"]{.class_1922} prophesied in Micah 5:2. Peter said when those Jews crucified Jesus, they ["killed the Prince of life"]{.class_1922} (Acts 3:15). At His return, He is called ["the prince of the kings of the earth"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 1:5).

Because the anointing of Christ took place at His baptism, proponents of the second view place the "terminus" of the 69 weeks there, and perhaps that is why the two New Testament appearances of the word [Messiah]{.class_1921} (matching the two Old Testament appearances of the word here in vss. 25--26) occur at the beginning of Christ's ministry (John 1:41, 4:25). Traditional dispensationalism places the end of the 69 weeks at Christ's Triumphal Entry not only because that is the time dictated by their date for beginning the 69 weeks, but also because the Triumphal Entry was Christ's public proclamation of His Messiahship.

The order of the events in verses 26 and 27 also lends itself to a future placement of Daniel's Seventieth Week: the ["Messiah"]{.class_1922} is ["cut off"]{.class_1922}---the Crucifixion; the Romans destroy the Temple and Jerusalem in A.D. 70 (["the PEOPLE of the prince that shall come shall destroy the city and the sanctuary"]{.class_1922}). Verse 27 follows those events, so the standard dispensational teaching is that all seven years are in the future.

Of course, there is a problem at the end of verse 26: ["the end thereof shall be with a flood, and unto the end of the war desolations are determined."]{.class_1922} That has nothing to do with Titus in A.D. 70; that takes place in the Tribulation (Rev. 12:15--16). At the end of the Tribulation, the land of Israel is said to be ["utterly desolate"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 5:9, 6:11, 13:9); if you want to see how desolate, read Isaiah 24:1--11 and Jeremiah 4:23--29. So those who hold the second view of Daniel's Seventieth Week will point out that since verse 26 skips from First Advent to Second Advent, that all of verse 27 doesn't necessarily have to take place after verse 26.

Now, there is no doubt the cutting off of Messiah is the Crucifixion at the First Advent. Notice that He is not ["cut off . . . for himself."]{.class_1922} Isaiah prophesied, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1439.xhtml_page_229}["he was cut off out of the land of the living: for the transgression of my people was he stricken"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 53:8). Even a lost, religious Jew prophesied to this (John 11:49--51). This is the vicarious atonement as applied to [the nation of Israel]{.class_1921} (Matt. 1:21).

Notice also the contrast between ["Messiah the Prince"]{.class_1922} in verse 25 and ["the prince that shall come"]{.class_1922} in verse 26. ["The prince that shall come"]{.class_1922} is the ["profane wicked prince of Israel . . . When iniquity shall have an end"]{.class_1922} (Ezek. 21:25 cf. Dan. 9:24); he is the incarnation of ["the prince of this world"]{.class_1922} (John 12:31, 14:30, 16:11), Satan (2 Cor. 4:4). He is the Antichrist, and he is such a good "imitator" of ["Messiah the Prince"]{.class_1922} (see our comments on 1 Cor. 11:1 and Rev. 6:2 in those Commentaries) that he manages to fool some of the most prominent Bible expositors and commentators. The cross-references given are all to [Jesus Christ]{.class_1921} (Matt. 22:7; Acts 6:13--14).

We understand perfectly that God uses Gentile rulers to punish His people, but ["the prince"]{.class_1922} of verse 26 is the one who breaks ["the covenant,"]{.class_1922} causes ["the sacrifice and oblation to cease,"]{.class_1922} and sets up ["the abomination of desolation"]{.class_1922} (vs. 27 cf. Mark 13:14). This is the King who exalts and magnifies ["himself above every god, and shall speak marvellous things against the God of gods"]{.class_1922} (11:36 cf. 2 Thess. 2:4; Rev. 13:6). That's not Jesus Christ; that's the [Antichrist.]{.class_1921}

Now notice in verse 26 that ["Messiah"]{.class_1922} is ["cut off" "AFTER"]{.class_1922} the 69 weeks are done, with no time element given. To this, both views agree (see Scofield's note on 9:24). The question is [how long after?]{.class_1921} The standard teaching is that it is after the Triumphal Entry, but the alternative view places it after the first three-and-a-half years of Daniel's Seventieth Week. This second view ends the 69 weeks with Christ's baptism and then immediately goes into the Seventieth Week of verse 27.

Proponents of that view do so for a couple of reasons. First, ["the prince that shall come"]{.class_1922} was right there in the Gospels. Judas was ["the son of perdition"]{.class_1922} (John 17:12), just as the Antichrist will be (2 Thess. 2:3). When he died, he went ["to his own place"]{.class_1922} (Acts 1:25). That ["place"]{.class_1922} is defined in Revelation 9:11, where the spirit of the Son of Perdition (both ["Abaddon"]{.class_1922} and ["Apollyon"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1439.xhtml_page_230} mean "perdition") is King over the spirits in the Bottomless Pit. In the Tribulation, he comes up ["out of the bottomless pit"]{.class_1922} and goes ["into perdition"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 17:8, 11). Moreover, as an apostle, he had the apostolic signs and wonders (Mark 16:17--18; 2 Cor. 12:12 cf. Matt. 10:1--4), but being ["a devil"]{.class_1922} (John 6:70--71), those were [lying]{.class_1921} signs and wonders as the Antichrist will perform (2 Thess. 2:9).

The second reason is that whenever the Bible gives a time for the Tribulation, it is [always]{.class_1921} three-and-a-half years (Dan. 7:25, 12:7; Rev. 11:2--3, 12:6, 14, 13:5). The standard dispensational teaching is that the first half of Daniel's Seventieth Week is when the Antichrist takes the kingdom ["peaceably . . . by flatteries"]{.class_1922} (see 11:21--24). (See the chart on "Division of the Seventieth Week---The 'Unsplit' Seventieth Week.") Even those who hold to the other view admit that this could happen in the future.

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1459.xhtml}

::: {}
![](image_1466.jpg){.class_1467}
:::

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1468.xhtml}

Now no matter which view you take, there is a gap which precedes the Tribulation. That gap is the Church Age, which was not revealed in the Old Testament. In the first view, that gap falls between the end of the 69th week and the beginning of the Seventieth Week. In the second view, the gap falls between the first half of Daniel's Seventieth Week and the last half of Daniel's Seventieth Week. The Church, therefore, would not be in any part of Daniel's Seventieth Week, for as any student of the Bible knows (except Stam, O'Hair, Greaterex, Bullinger, Sharpe, Moore, and the rest of the "Dry Cleaners"), a way for the Body of Christ was made at Calvary (Eph. 2:16), and the first members were placed in it in Acts 2 (Acts 1:5 cf. 1 Cor. 12:13). Therefore, no "mid-Trib rapture" takes place, since the Rapture of the Body of Christ takes place before the last half of Daniel's Seventieth Week, the actual "Tribulation" (Matt. 24:21).

There are two things, though, that pose a problem with that second view, and they are found in verse 27. The first is ["the covenant"]{.class_1922} that is confirmed by the Antichrist. It is evident that Judas made no covenant ["with many"]{.class_1922} that he broke at the end of Christ's ministry. As a matter of fact, the only "covenant" Judas made was with the chief priests to betray Christ (Matt. 26:15; Luke 22:5). That "covenant" was made at the end of Christ's ministry, and it was carried out.

The proponents of the second view, though, say, "No, the verse doesn't say the Antichrist 'makes' the covenant; it says he ['confirms']{.class_1921} the covenant." True enough, but what would that covenant be? The answer is, the land covenant of a physical kingdom made to Abraham and his seed. They say Judas confirmed this covenant when he went out preaching in the three-and-a-half-year ministry of Christ. This covenant was broken when Judas betrayed Christ to be killed. Moreover, it will be broken a [second ]{.class_1921}time when the Antichrist begins his "ministry" in the second half of Daniel's Seventieth Week.

But that is stretching things a bit. Judas was only one of twelve apostles preaching, and they didn't preach the entire three-and-a-half years from Christ's baptism till His death. There is only one mention of the ["holy covenant"]{.class_1922} in the Gospels, and it is not made by any apostle; it is made by Zacharias, the father of John the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1468.xhtml_page_233}Baptist, before Christ is born (Luke 1:72--73). In fact, it is not until after Christ's ascension that this covenant comes up in the preaching of the apostles, and it is not by Judas (Acts 3:25, 7:8). But even if it were, exactly how the death of Christ breaks that covenant between the Antichrist and Israel is actually impossible to say. We will get into this covenant more when we get to Daniel 11, but I just don't see it happening anywhere in Matthew, Mark, Luke, or John.

The second problem that presents itself in verse 27 for the view of a split Seventieth Week is that no sacrifice or oblation ceased when Christ died. In fact, priests offering sacrifices at the Jewish Temple went on for another 37 years after Christ's death. Of course, it is spiritualized to mean that God no longer accepted the Jewish sacrifices after Christ's death, but that is [not]{.class_1921} what the verse said. It said they ["cease."]{.class_1922} That still awaits future fulfillment (see our comments on 8:12--13).

We have already commented on the ["abomination of desolation"]{.class_1922} under our remarks on 8:13, 25 (which see).

Now there it is. There are some loose ends that don't fit on both sides, and I couldn't tell you definitely for certain which one is correct doctrinally until those wrinkles get ironed out. What we do know for certain is that what Christ calls the Great Tribulation is the last half of Daniel's Seventieth Week, and regardless of whether the first half has already been fulfilled in the Gospels, that bowman on the white horse in Revelation 6:2 is going to need some time to worm his way into power with flattery and talk of peace (Dan. 11:21--24). But regardless of how Daniel's Seventieth Week unfolds, the Christian should be looking for one thing, and it isn't the Antichrist or his kingdom. It is his [Saviour.]{.class_1921}

["And to wait for his Son from heaven, whom he raised from the dead, even Jesus, which delivered us from the wrath to come"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 1:10).

["So that ye come behind in no gift; waiting for the coming of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 1:7).

["For our conversation is in heaven; from whence also we look for the Saviour, the Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class_1922} (Phil. 3:20).

["Looking for that blessed hope, and the glorious appearing of the great God and our Saviour Jesus Christ"]{.class_1922} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1468.xhtml_page_234}(Tit. 2:13).

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml}

# Chapter 10 {.heading_67-0}

10:1 In the third year of Cyrus king of Persia a thing was revealed unto Daniel, whose name was called Belteshazzar; and the thing was true, but the time appointed was long: and he understood the thing, and had understanding of the vision.

Chapters 10--12 are all one vision given to Daniel ["In the third year of Cyrus king of Persia"]{.class_1922} (vs. 1). The restoration of the Jews to their land, about which Daniel read and prayed back in chapter 9, has been accomplished (2 Chron. 36:22--23; Ezra 1:1--2). Daniel, though, does not return when the decree is given; he stays in Babylon and serves Cyrus (6:28). He may have even been the one God used to persuade the King to fulfill Isaiah 44:28--45:1.

By the time of verse 1, Daniel has probably retired from public service (cf. 1:21), but that doesn't mean his ministry is over. Daniel continues to fast and pray for his people. If you are a Christian who is "up in years," that doesn't mean you can't still do something for God. Even if you are bedridden and can't get around, you can still [pray.]{.class_1921} Get you a list of missionaries and hold them up in prayer. That is as important of a ministry as being a pastor or evangelist.

Verse 1 is the last time Daniel's Babylonian name shows up in the book. This old man is that same teenage boy who made up his mind to serve God back in chapter 1. Nothing has changed: he is still serving God into his late eighties and early nineties.

Now the verse says, ["a thing was revealed unto Daniel . . . and the thing was true, but the time appointed was long."]{.class_1922} This is exactly what was said of the vision in Daniel 8 (8:26). What you probably have here is further explanation of all that is involved with that vision (see our remarks under 9:23). So although Daniel did not understand everything at the time (see 8:27 and our comments), he kept studying and praying until God revealed the thing he needed to know.

Let that be a lesson to you in your Bible study. Just because you don't get something about a passage the first time you read it, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_236}doesn't mean the Lord won't reveal the thing to you. Just keep reading your Bible and praying over it. Sam Gipp says something to the effect in one of his sermons, "What if God wanted to show you something on your fortieth time through the Bible, and you stopped at the 39th time?" Good question. God knows when you're ready to receive what He wants to show you in that Book, so don't stop reading and studying it before you get to that point. If you run across something you don't understand, write it down, and as you read across that passage, pray about it every time you come across it. Daniel didn't get a full understanding of his vision until [years]{.class_1921} after it was shown him (8:1 cf. 9:1, 10:1).

2 In those days I Daniel was mourning three full weeks.

3 I ate no pleasant bread, neither came flesh nor wine in my mouth, neither did I anoint myself at all, till three whole weeks were fulfilled.

["I Daniel was mourning three full weeks"]{.class_1922} (vs. 2). This ["mourning"]{.class_1922} isn't just Daniel sitting around crying; [prayer]{.class_1921} is involved (vs. 12). Daniel is praying about something for three weeks straight. This is true importunity in prayer: that's banging at the gates of Heaven till you get an answer (see Luke 11:5--10). That's what Paul meant when he told the Thessalonians to ["Pray without ceasing"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 5:17).

Now you aren't told why Daniel was mourning, but given the motivation of his prayer session back in 9:2--3, it is not unreasonable to believe that Daniel was mourning over the state of those Jews who had returned to Israel. If you look at the date given for Daniel 10 by Ussher, it is the same date as that given for Ezra 4. The Samaritans were weakening ["the hands of the people of Judah, and troubled them in building, And hired counsellors against them, to frustrate their purpose, all the days of Cyrus king of Persia"]{.class_1922} (Ezra 4:4--5).

Verse 3:[ "I ate no pleasant bread"]{.class_1922}; that's another way of saying he didn't eat leavened bread. Unleavened bread was called ["the bread of affliction"]{.class_1922} (Deut. 16:3). So this is not a full fast. Daniel is eating unleavened bread, and instead of having meat and []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_237}wine with his meals, he is just having water with his unleavened bread (cf. 1 Kings 22:27).

["Neither did I anoint myself."]{.class_1922} The ancients would anoint themselves with fragrant oils such as we use deodorants, colognes, and perfumes today. Not to anoint oneself was a sign of deep sorrow (2 Sam. 14:2). The Pharisees misused the practice to draw attention to themselves when they fasted (Matt. 6:16--17).

4 And in the four and twentieth day of the first month, as I was by the side of the great river, which is Hiddekel;

5 Then I lifted up mine eyes, and looked, and behold a certain man clothed in linen, whose loins were girded with fine gold of Uphaz:

6 His body also was like the beryl, and his face as the appearance of lightning, and his eyes as lamps of fire, and his arms and his feet like in colour to polished brass, and the voice of his words like the voice of a multitude.

["The first month"]{.class_1922} is ["the month Nisan"]{.class_1922} (Esth. 3:7), called ["Abib"]{.class_1922} by the Jews (Exod. 13:4 cf. Exod. 12:2). It is the month of the Passover and the Feast of Unleavened Bread (Exod. 12:18, 23:15; Lev. 23:5--8). Daniel had been praying from the third of Nisan to the 24th.

["The great river, which is Hiddekel"]{.class_1922} is the Tigris River, the twin river of the Euphrates. Its northern waters lie ["east of Assyria"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 2:14), and it comes the closest to the Euphrates near Babylon (about thirty miles apart).

As Daniel is praying by the Tigris, he has a vision of a man. The description in verses 5--6 matches that of Jesus Christ in Revelation 1:13--15 (which see). So what Daniel is seeing is a preincarnate appearance of the Lord Jesus Christ.

The scholars take ["Uphaz"]{.class_1922} as another name for [Ophir]{.class_1921} (cf. Jer. 10:9). The reason that is significant is that the walls of the Temple were overlaid with ["the gold of Ophir"]{.class_1922} (1 Chron. 29:3--4), and John 2:21 speaks of the temple of Christ's body. Moreover, the Bride of Christ is clothed ["in gold of Ophir"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 45:9). And in the Tribulation, ["a man"]{.class_1922} is ["more precious" "than the golden wedge of Ophir"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_238} (Isa. 13:12).

["Ophir"]{.class_1922} was originally a man's name, and he was the brother of ["Havilah"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 10:29). For some strange reason, ["gold"]{.class_1922} shows up [twice]{.class_1921} in the same chapter as the [creation of man,]{.class_1921} and that ["gold"]{.class_1922} is found in ["the whole land of Havilah"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 2:11), the brother of Ophir.

The New Jerusalem is said to be ["the mother of"]{.class_1922} every saved believer that makes up the Bride of Christ in this age (Gal. 4:26 cf. Eph. 5:30--32), but in Revelation 21:2, it is identified with the Bride of Christ herself. Do you know what the New Jerusalem is made of? Revelation 21:8---["the city was PURE GOLD."]{.class_1922} There is something about [gold]{.class_1921} that is connected with the glorified body of a believer in Christ.

But I sense we have waded into waters too deep for the average "reverent, godly Biblicist." We will leave the babies in the kiddie pool where they won't drown. The golden girdle is associated with the garments of the high priest (Exod. 28:8, 39:5), as is the linen clothing (cf. Exod. 28:39--42, 39:27--28; Lev. 6:10, 16:4, 32).

["The beryl"]{.class_1922} of verse 6 was a gemstone from Tarshish. While it can be green or blue, the color here is probably the [yellow]{.class_1921} beryl (see our comments above on gold) or a [fire]{.class_1921} color (see our comments on Song of Sol. 5:14 in that Commentary). The stone is associated with the cherubim (Ezek. 1:16, 10:9), and was part of Lucifer's covering before his fall (Ezek. 28:13). It was one of the stones representing one of the tribes of Israel (probably Dan) on the breastplate of the high priest, and it is one of the foundation stones of the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:19--20), representing one ["of the twelve apostles of the Lamb"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 21:14). So between the golden girdle and the beryl-like body, you have a picture of Jesus Christ as God's High Priest (Heb. 3:1).

["His face as the appearance of lightning"]{.class_1922} (vs. 6). This is Jesus Christ in His glorified state as he appeared on the Mount of Transfiguration (Matt. 17:2; Luke 9:29). Christ's transfiguration was a picture of His Second Advent (Matt. 16:28; 2 Pet. 1:16). ["His eyes as lamps of fire."]{.class_1922} And that is how He will appear at His Second Advent (Rev. 19:12).

But the imagery of Christ's arms and feet, and His voice, is like []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_239}the Angel of the Lord that shows up in Revelation 10:1--3. That is not the Second Advent; that is an appearance of Christ [before]{.class_1921} the Second Advent (see Rev. 14:14). I do not profess to know when during the Tribulation this appearing takes place, but at some point, Jesus manifests Himself to Israel, and a remnant will be converted. This appearance is typified in the Bible by Joseph revealing himself to his brothers in Genesis 45:1--6, by God appearing to Job in Job 38 before ["turning his captivity"]{.class_1922} in Job 42:10, and Paul on the road to Damascus (Acts 9:3--6).

7 And I Daniel alone saw the vision: for the men that were with me saw not the vision; but a great quaking fell upon them, so that they fled to hide themselves.

8 Therefore I was left alone, and saw this great vision, and there remained no strength in me: for my comeliness was turned in me into corruption, and I retained no strength.

9 Yet heard I the voice of his words: and when I heard the voice of his words, then was I in a deep sleep on my face, and my face toward the ground.

10 And, behold, an hand touched me, which set me upon my knees and upon the palms of my hands.

It wasn't without cause that I compared Daniel to Paul here in this passage. Just as those with Saul of Tarsus did not see the risen Christ nor hear the words He spoke (Acts 9:7 cf. Acts 22:9), but ["were afraid"]{.class_1922} at what they did see and hear, so also did the men with Daniel. They fled, leaving Daniel alone.

Notice in verses 8--9 that Daniel doesn't act like this modern bunch of Charismatic kooks who claim to visit Heaven and talk with God and Jesus. In the [Bible]{.class_1921} (not some book written by someone who ate too much pizza before going to bed), people who have encounters with God or Jesus Christ in His glory don't treat Him like their "best Bud." They don't go fishing with Him or talk about sports or get the "nickel tour" of Glory. [They are reduced to a state of helplessness.]{.class_1921}

Job said, ["I abhor myself, and repent in dust and ashes"]{.class_1922} (Job 42:6). Isaiah said, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_240}["Woe is me! for I am undone; because I am a man of unclean lips"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 6:5). When Ezekiel saw ["the glory of the LORD,"]{.class_1922} he fell on his face and couldn't get back up until the Holy Spirit empowered him to do so (Ezek. 1:28--2:2). When Peter, James, and John heard God the Father speak on the Mount of Transfiguration,[ "they fell on their face, and were sore afraid"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 17:6). Paul was knocked off his horse to the ground (Acts 9:3--4). When John saw in Revelation 1 what Daniel saw here in Daniel 10, John fell at Christ's ["feet as dead"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 1:13--17), which is what the picture is here in Daniel 10:8 (["corruption"]{.class_1922}---1 Cor. 15:53).

Now I am not a Charismatic. I don't recommend you seek an encounter like that with the Lord. You say, "Why not, Ruckman?" [Because you might make contact with the Devil.]{.class_1921}

["And no marvel; for Satan himself is transformed into an angel of light"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 11:14).

Just because you see some supernatural being radiating a brilliant light doesn't mean you are seeing Jesus Christ or even an angel of God. You are commanded in that Book to ["try the spirits whether they are of God"]{.class_1922} (1 John 4:10), and the authority to which even God Almighty subjects Himself is [His written words]{.class_1921} (2 Pet. 1:17--20). You are to judge [everything]{.class_1921} by that Book---especially some "vision." That is why Daniel 10 ends with Jesus Christ, as the Angel of the Lord, showing Daniel ["that which is noted in the SCRIPTURE OF TRUTH"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21).

I recall one experience I had up in the mountains of Carolina which made an indelible impression on me. There was a lady dying of cancer way back up in the mountains where there was no medicine or doctors or even electricity. The places I preached in those days had no refrigerators or radios or telephones---[nothing.]{.class_1921} The only lights they had were kerosene lamps.

I was asked to go into the room where she was bedridden and pray with her. She had a sore on the side of her face about the size of a half dollar, and the stench of that open cancer filled her room. But when I opened the door to go in and pray with her, I couldn't stand up. I had to crawl into that room on my hands and knees, with my head bowed to the floor. I crawled up to the side of that woman's bed, talked with her, prayed with her, and crawled back out. I never []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_241}lifted my head up from that floor one time while I was in there.

You say, "Why not, Ruckman?" I couldn't. The power of God was so thick in that room that I couldn't look up. You say, "What do you think you would have seen if you had?" I don't know, but I wasn't about to find out. But I am not going to use an experience like that to override anything I read in that Book.

You have to have some discernment about these things. Inevitably, an evil spirit will go against that Book in some way. One of the tests you can put on it is to bypass the spirit and go straight to the "front office" and ask the Lord if that spirit confesses ["Jesus Christ is come in the flesh"]{.class_1922} (1 John 4:2--3; 2 John 7), and I wouldn't accept a "pat answer" either. I would press the issue to make sure the confession is a [Scriptural]{.class_1921} one.

Another way is the "impression" the spirit leaves you. Is it an oppressive, demanding spirit? When I went into that woman's room, it was a calm, insistent spirit that led me to [prayer.]{.class_1921} I was ministered to by that spirit, as well as getting a chance to minister to that dying sister. I wasn't interested in promoting [myself,]{.class_1921} like Mohammed was after his encounters with "Gabriel." That buzzard claimed to have the same authority as "Allah" (read Sura 4:80), and he would kill you for making fun of him. [That wasn't the Spirit of God]{.class_1921} (Matt. 5:44; Rom. 12:14; 1 Cor. 4:12--13; 1 Pet. 3:9).

Now, when Christ speaks to Daniel, Daniel collapses face down on the ground and passes out cold. The ["deep sleep"]{.class_1922} of verse 9 is a picture of [death]{.class_1921} (cf. Rev. 1:17). It takes the touch of the Angel of the Lord to get Daniel back up on his hands and knees (vs. 10). Notice how often this is mentioned: Gabriel had to do the same thing to him back in 8:18; Gabriel touched Daniel again as he was praying back in 9:21. Jesus had to touch those disciples cowering at the voice of God there on the Mount of Transfiguration to get them up. Jesus lays His right hand on John to get him up there in Revelation 1:17.

The picture over and over again is one of [resurrection.]{.class_1921} Jesus takes Jairus' daughter by the hand to raise her from the dead; He touches the bier of the widow of Nain's son to get that dead young man to sit up and talk. Throughout the Gospels, the touch of Jesus Christ was a [healing]{.class_1921} touch (Matt. 8:3, 15, 9:29); it was a [reviving]{.class_1921} touch (see references above).

11 And he said unto me, O Daniel, a man greatly beloved, understand the words that I speak unto thee, and stand upright: for unto thee am I now sent. And when he had spoken this word unto me, I stood trembling.

12 Then said he unto me, Fear not, Daniel: for from the first day that thou didst set thine heart to understand, and to chasten thyself before thy God, thy words were heard, and I am come for thy words.

13 But the prince of the kingdom of Persia withstood me one and twenty days: but, lo, Michael, one of the chief princes, came to help me; and I remained there with the kings of Persia.

14 Now I am come to make thee understand what shall befall thy people in the latter days: for yet the vision is for many days.

Daniel is called ["a man greatly beloved"]{.class_1922} in verse 11; he is also called that in 9:23 and verse 19 here in chapter 10. Daniel has quite a reputation up in Heaven: he is righteous (Ezek. 14:14), wise (Ezek. 28:3), and ["greatly beloved"]{.class_1922} by God. That's a great type of the Lord Jesus Christ. Three times in the Gospel of Matthew, Jesus is called ["my beloved"]{.class_1922} by the Father (Matt. 3:17, 12:18, 17:5); ditto the Gospel of Luke (Luke 3:22, 9:35, 20:13).

Do you know why God accepts you, child of God? Because you are ["in the beloved"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 1:6). If you are [in Jesus Christ,]{.class_1921} you are in ["the love of God"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 8:39), and if you're [not in Jesus Christ,]{.class_1921} you are under ["the wrath of God"]{.class_1922} (John 3:36). If you are saved, you are ["beloved of the Lord"]{.class_1922} (2 Thess. 2:13), and if you're not saved, God doesn't even know you, much less love you, as a son (Matt. 7:21--23).

Like John, Daniel represents a [group of people]{.class_1921} beloved by God. In the New Testament, John is known as the ["beloved apostle"]{.class_1922} (see John 13:23, 20:2, 21:7, 20, 24); he is a picture of the Church, the Body and Bride of Christ (Rom. 1:7; Eph. 5:25; Col. 3:12; 2 Thess. 2:13, 16; 1 John 4:10, 19; Rev. 4:1). In the Old Testament, Daniel, the ["greatly beloved,"]{.class_1922} represents the nation of Israel (Deut. 7:7--8, 10:15, 33:3; Jer. 12:7, 31:3; Hos. 11:1; Mal. 1:2). Here, Daniel, as the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_243}representative for his people, receives the revelation of what happens to Israel in the last days (vs. 14).

Practically speaking, wouldn't you like to have the reputation in Glory that Daniel had? There are people like that throughout the Bible. Here's Gideon in Judges 6. He was just a timid farm boy from a poor family in a small town in Ephraim, but up in Heaven, he was known as a ["mighty man of valour"]{.class_1922} (Judg. 6:11--12). The angel greeted Mary, ["Hail, thou that art highly favoured"]{.class_1922} (Luke 1:27--28). For all his faults, Jacob was still known as "a Prince of God" (Israel) because he had ["power with God" ]{.class_1922}in prayer (Gen. 32:28).

Of course, if you are well known up in Heaven, you will be well known down below, I guarantee you. If you are living right and doing something for God, the Devil knows it and doesn't appreciate it one bit. God asked Satan, ["Hast thou considered my servant Job, that there is none like him in the earth, a perfect and an upright man, one that feareth God, and escheweth evil?"]{.class_1922} (Job 1:8). Yeah, the Devil sure had considered Job and was just waiting for the Lord to give him the go-ahead to take everything Job had.

For two years, Paul was in Ephesus, beating down the doors, winning souls to Christ (Acts 19:10, 20:20). He was preaching down at the "free speech zone" of the local State College (Acts 19:9). And he was healing people and casting out devils with handkerchiefs and aprons that had touched his body (Acts 19:11--12). Some vagabond Jewish exorcists decided to ride the coattails of Paul's reputation and invoked his name while trying to exorcise an evil spirit. That unclean spirit said, ["Jesus I know, and Paul I know, but who are ye?"]{.class_1922} (Acts 19:15). The evil spirit knew who Paul was.

Do you know what you will find in your Christian life? If you just coast along making a living, getting along with the family, paying your bills, enjoying whatever leisure you can, you won't have much trouble. But the moment you start passing out tracts, witnessing, preaching on the street, and trying to win lost sinners to Jesus Christ, all hell will break loose. Why is that? Well, let me ask you this: how would you feel if someone kidnapped your children? Would you be kindly disposed toward that person? Well, how do you think the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_244}Devil feels when you steal one of his kids away from him (John 8:44; Eph. 2:1--3)?

Christian, do you have a reputation with God? Does the Devil know who you are because you are always causing trouble for him? Think back to ancient history for a moment. If I asked you to name a famous person from the Fertile Crescent, circa 1900 B.C., you might come up with the name of some King like Hammurabi if you paid attention in World History class in school. But far more well known are a Bedouin cattle herder and his wife. Do you know why people know the names of Abraham and Sarah? Because they believed God and lived by faith (Heb. 11:8--11). So the Lord recorded their names in His Book for everyone from 1500 B.C. onward to read.

Christian, you are going to find out, when you get to Heaven, that the famous people in the world's eyes are complete blanks up there. The "rich and famous" up in the New Jerusalem will be those who believed God, denied themselves, and served Him down here---whether anybody knew it or not. You will find out the names of a lot of praying mothers and grandmas, faithful missionaries and witnesses, and those who gave toward the propagation of the Gospel and the Book that no one down here knew; whereas if you bring up the names of the Bushes, Obama, the Clintons, Trump, Lucas, Spielberg, Clooney, DeCaprio, Pitt, Hanks, Cyrus, Perry, Swift, et al., the angels will be scratching their heads in bewilderment, asking, "Who?" You will be better off with God knowing you than to be in the Top 40, the Hit Parade, Who's Who, or "Man of the Year" (I suppose in Obama's America, you would have to change that to "Thing of the Year").

Back to verse 11: ["And when he had spoken this word unto me, I stood trembling."]{.class_1922} Trembling is a sign of [fear]{.class_1921} (and I don't mean "godly reverence"---see Heb. 12:28). That's the right response to the words of God, if you want God's favor (Isa. 66:2; Ezra 10:3; Psa. 119:120; Acts 9:6, 16:29--30; 2 Cor. 7:15; Phil. 2:12). You will either tremble at [God's words,]{.class_1921} or you will tremble at [God's wrath]{.class_1921} (Isa. 51:17, 22).

That is one of the things that struck me about Christian scholarship: no scholar (I would say 99% of them at least) has enough esteem for the written words of God---in any language!---to []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_245}tremble at them. If they did, they wouldn't even think of changing them according to their own (or someone else's) whims, opinions, and preferences. You don't fear what's written in that Book if you can make 500 ([New Scofield Reference Bible]{.class_1921}) to 64,000 ([NIV]{.class_1921}) changes in it.

Verse 12: ["Fear not, Daniel."]{.class_1922} Someone started the teaching one time that there are 365 "Fear nots" in the Bible, one for each day of the year. That sounds good, and of course, it was picked up and spread around by all the preachers. But with the advent of computers, it has been proved not to be true (kind of like demon oppression, demon obsession, and demon possession); there are only about 122 times, if you include all the variations (and not every one of those is a command by God). Nevertheless, there are a lot of them there. There is a time to be afraid, and there is a time not to be afraid. One of the strangest passages you will read in that Book is Exodus 20:20.

"And Moses said unto the people, Fear not: for God is come to prove you, and that his fear may be before your faces, that ye sin not."

"Don't be scared; God is just come to scare you." But did you notice the purpose of the fear of God you are to have: ["THAT YE SIN NOT."]{.class_1922} Job 28:28---["the fear of the Lord, that is wisdom; and to DEPART FROM EVIL is understanding."]{.class_1922} You don't need to fear God being fickle and capricious, like the heathen gods were, where even if you did everything right, they could still "get you." But you had better fear a holy, righteous God enough to believe Him and do what He says in His Book.

Now, verse 13 is a "wild scene," and it all has to do with the nature of [angels.]{.class_1921} It should be obvious to anyone that ["the prince of the kingdom of Persia"]{.class_1922} is [not]{.class_1921} Cyrus, for no flesh-and-blood ruler could stand up to the Angel of the Lord (Gen. 32:24--29; 2 Kings 19:35). ["The prince of Persia" ]{.class_1922}and[ "the prince of Grecia"]{.class_1922} are the ["principalities"]{.class_1922} of Ephesians 6:12; they are the ["spiritual wickedness in high places"]{.class_1922} (see our comments on 4:26 and note especially our remarks on the ["high places"]{.class_1922} of Isa. 24:21).

The word [angel,]{.class_1921} in your [King James]{.class_1921} Bible, goes beyond the Hebrew word [malak,]{.class_1921} which can mean "messenger" (see Mal. 3:1). []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_246}The standard Fundamentalist teaching is that angels are God's "messengers," and the Hebrew word [malak]{.class_1921} is used to prove that.

That's a rather lazy way to do Bible study. There are plenty of angels in that Book that don't bring a "message" to anyone. Angels can be sent to kill (2 Kings 19:35; 2 Sam. 24:15--16). They can be sent to strengthen (Luke 22:43). They can be sent to prosper the way you take (Gen. 24:40). They can be sent to keep you in the way you are going and to get you to the place God wants you to be (Exod. 23:20). They can be sent to stop you in the way you are taking (Num. 22:22). We saw twice here in Daniel where an angel was sent to deliver those who served God (3:28, 6:22). An angel was sent to roll the stone from the door of Christ's tomb when He arose (Matt. 28:2). Once a year before Christ began His ministry, an angel came down to the pool of Bethesda and troubled the waters so someone could be healed (John 5:4). And angels can just "minister" in general (Mark 1:13), which is the actual purpose for which they were created (Heb. 1:7, 14). That is a "might sight" more than just being "messengers."

Now if you want a definition of an angel that will fit every occurrence in that Book, it would be an [appearance.]{.class_1921} The Angel of the Lord is an [appearance]{.class_1921} of God. The ["angels"]{.class_1922} of those ["little ones"]{.class_1922} in Matthew 18:10 are the [appearances]{.class_1921} of those children up in Heaven. The ["angels"]{.class_1922} of those seven churches in Revelation 1, 2, and 3 are the [appearances]{.class_1921} of those churches before Jesus Christ.

Another way of putting it is a [representation.]{.class_1921} So just as children and churches have a spiritual representation of themselves before God, so do nations. Here in Daniel 10, the Princes of Persia and Greece are spiritual representatives of those nations that appear up in heavenly places. Of course, these Princes are spiritual beings that represent, empower, and influence nations under [Satan's]{.class_1921} authority (Luke 4:6; 2 Cor. 4:4). They stand in opposition, here in verse 13, to Princes who seek to influence nations for God (["Michael, one of the chief princes"]{.class_1922}). These spiritual rulers were originally created by Jesus, for His pleasure (Col. 1:16; Rev. 4:11). Once Christ had accomplished our atonement and been received back into Glory to be seated at His Father's right hand, those principalities and powers that were once answerable to God the Father became subject to His Son (1 Pet. 3:22; Eph. 1:20--21). That is why, one day, even Satan and []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_247}his hierarchy will bow before Jesus Christ and confess Him as Lord (Phil. 2:9--11).

Now, God heard Daniel's prayer the first day he started praying (vs. 12), but he didn't get an answer until 21 days later because the Prince of Persia withstood the Angel of the Lord for 21 days. The question is, how is that even possible? After all, isn't God "omnipotent" (all powerful)?

The answer is found in Zechariah 3:2.

"And the LORD said unto Satan, the LORD rebuke thee, O Satan; even the LORD that hath chosen Jerusalem rebuke thee . . . ."

Satan has been called front and center before God to resist a saint of God, just as he had been back in Job 1:6--12 and 2:17. But in Zechariah, the second member of the Godhead shows up at the meeting. But notice, Satan has so much power that one member of the Trinity has to refer him to another member of the Trinity to rebuke him, just as Michael the archangel had to do in Jude 9.

The reason for this was that, before Christ's incarnation, the Devil contended that God knew nothing about man's sin and temptation from [experience.]{.class_1921} In the Old Testament, Christ took the form of the Angel of the Lord, not of a man. So before His incarnation, God the Son referred Satan to God the Father. But after the incarnation, Christ tells the Devil where to "head in" (Luke 4:8).

Folks, there is stuff in that Bible no science fiction or fantasy movie can touch. You talk about "Star Wars," when you go to prayer, you are participating in a warfare going on over your head in the heavens. That's why Paul says, ["we wrestle not against flesh and blood, but against principalities,"]{.class_1922} etc. (Eph. 6:12).

Back to verse 13---["but, lo, Michael, one of the chief princes, came to help me."]{.class_1922} Now, someone in the intertestamental period (if we are to believe the scholars) pretending to be Enoch, read Daniel 10:13 and figured that since Michael was ["one of the chief princes"]{.class_1922} and since he was an ["archangel"]{.class_1922} (Jude 9), that there were more than one archangel. So taking his cue from the Apocryphal book of Tobit (specifically Tobit 12:15), he invented [seven]{.class_1921} archangels.

But did you notice, old "Enoch" had to go to a [New Testament]{.class_1921} book written around A.D. 66 to get the word [archangel ]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_248}(ditto the author of 2 Esdras)[.]{.class_1921} The word [archangel]{.class_1921} appears [nowhere]{.class_1921} in the Old Testament; it is a [New Testament]{.class_1921} term (1 Thess. 4:16; Jude 9). I guarantee you, the fragment of Enoch 1:9 found in Cave 4 of Qumran didn't come from the Third Century B.C. Whoever "Enoch" was, he had the writings of Paul and Jude before him as he [lied]{.class_1921} (he [wasn't]{.class_1921} the Old Testament patriarch Enoch). You know that to be the case because after all the unpublished fragments and scrolls from Qumran were made public, in 1995, a certain Dr. Jose O'Callaghan discovered fragments containing readings from Luke, Mark, Acts, Romans, 1 Timothy, and James. The same cave that contained the fragment of the Book of Enoch (Cave 4) contained a reading from Luke. When it comes to the irresistible desire to elevate their authority above that of the Holy Scriptures ([AV]{.class_1921} 1611), the scholars will lie, withhold evidence, and anything else to cast doubt in your mind as to the veracity of what God said (following the example of their father \[John 8:44\] in Gen. 3:1).

In both instances where the word ["archangel"]{.class_1922} shows up in your Bible, there is only ONE: ["THE archangel."]{.class_1922} There may be several ["chief princes,"]{.class_1922} but there is only one chief angel (which is what [archangel]{.class_1921} means): it is Michael.

Michael is said to be ["YOUR prince"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21), a reference to Daniel, a [Jew.]{.class_1921} He is ["the great prince which standeth for the children of THY PEOPLE"]{.class_1922} (12:1); i.e., [Daniel's]{.class_1921} people---the [Jews.]{.class_1921} So in the Tribulation, when Satan persecutes the remnant of Israel (Rev. 12:13), ["Michael and his angels"]{.class_1922} fight against the Devil and his angels (Rev. 12:7--9). This is what is happening [in type]{.class_1921} in Daniel 10. Daniel is wrestling in prayer for his people, Satan's Princes are withstanding the Angel of the Lord who brings the answer to Daniel's prayer, and the archangel Michael joins with the Angel of the Lord to fight against Satan's principalities in order to get the answer to Daniel.

["I remained there with the kings of Persia."]{.class_1922} This is one of those places in Daniel where I have to admit, ["Ich weiss nicht"]{.class_1921} (German for "I don't know"). There is only one physical King at this time over the Persian Empire: it is Cyrus (vs. 1). I suppose it could be a reference to the Kings given in Ezra 4:5--6 whom Satan and his []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_249}principalities were moving to hinder the Jews from building the Temple, but that is stretching the text a bit. The Angel of the Lord had ["remained there with the kings of Persia"]{.class_1922} until he could come to make Daniel understand what would befall the Jews ["in the latter days"]{.class_1922} (vs. 14). So in the text as it stands, it couldn't be any physical King of Persia after Cyrus.

But as I pointed out to you in my remarks on the meaning of the word[ Prince]{.class_1921} back in 9:25--26, a Prince can be a King who currently reigns. Over in Ezekiel 28, ["the prince of this world"]{.class_1922} (John 12:31, 14:30, 16:11), who is ["the prince of the power of the air,"]{.class_1922} is addressed in the person of ["the king of Tyrus,"]{.class_1922} who is called ["the prince of Tyrus"]{.class_1922} (Ezek. 28:2--15). So these ["kings of Persia"]{.class_1922} could be ["the rulers of the darkness of this world,"]{.class_1922} the ["spiritual wickedness in high places"]{.class_1922} set over ["the kingdom of Persia."]{.class_1922}

Brethren, there is some truth to the things in the second and third heavens affecting things on earth. Of course, the astrologists, the psychics, the clairvoyants, the Rosicrucians, the Satanists, and the Wiccans (witches) have it all wrong. I don't profess to understand all these things, but if there is one place where you will find the truth about these matters, it's in a [King James Authorized Version]{.class_1921} of the Holy Bible. In that Book, angels are connected with stars and "luminaries" (the seven main heavenly bodies that can be seen with the naked eye: the sun, the moon, Mercury, Venus, Mars, Jupiter, and Saturn). That means they have some influence over the seasons (Gen. 1:14). They represent children, churches, and governments; and they exercise influence over them. What happens in the spiritual realm between Satan with his hierarchy and the angels of God affects what goes on here on earth. Now, you shouldn't get preoccupied with these things. I mean, ["it is a good thing that the heart be established with grace; not with meats, which have not profited them that have been occupied therein"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 13:9). But you certainly should be aware of them and believe them, because the Holy Spirit revealed them to you in His Book.

Verse 14 is the answer to Daniel's prayer, whether that was for what he was praying or not. Romans 8:26 says, ["Likewise the Spirit also helpeth our infirmities: for we know not what we should pray for as we ought."]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_250} We don't know exactly for what Daniel was fasting and praying, but the Lord knew that what Daniel needed in response to his prayers was an explanation of what was going to happen to the Jews ["in the latter days"]{.class_1922} (vs. 14). As I have told you on many an occasion, the Lord is more concerned with the day His Son gets the throne of this earth than He is with your salvation.

15 And when he had spoken such words unto me, I set my face toward the ground, and I became dumb.

16 And, behold, one like the similitude of the sons of men touched my lips: then I opened my mouth, and spake, and said unto him that stood before me, O my lord, by the vision my sorrows are turned upon me, and I have retained no strength.

17 For how can the servant of this my lord talk with this my lord? for as for me, straightway there remained no strength in me, neither is there breath left in me.

18 Then there came again and touched me one like the appearance of a man, and he strengthened me,

19 And said, O man greatly beloved, fear not: peace be unto thee, be strong, yea, be strong. And when he had spoken unto me, I was strengthened, and said, Let my lord speak; for thou hast strengthened me.

The first time Daniel heard the voice of the Angel of the Lord, he fainted dead away (vs. 9). Here in verse 15, he bows his head to the ground and is rendered speechless (["dumb"]{.class_1922} in the sense of being unable to speak).

Elsewhere in Scriptures, this dumbness was a sign to the Jews (Ezek. 24:27; Luke 1:20). In Ezekiel's case, it was a sign to the Jews who escaped the destruction of Jerusalem by Nebuchadnezzar that Ezekiel had told them the truth when he prophesied of it ahead of time. In Zacharias' case, it was because he didn't believe Gabriel about his wife Elizabeth giving birth to John the Baptist.

Now, Daniel has been struck dumb by the words of the Angel of the Lord, and it's not a natural thing because it takes the touch of the Angel of the Lord to restore his speech. Because verse 16 says []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_251}["one like the similitude of the sons of men,"]{.class_1922} and because Daniel addresses the Angel as ["lord"]{.class_1922} with a lower case [l,]{.class_1921} the commentators assume it can't be the Lord Jesus Christ appearing in His Old Testament state as the Angel of the Lord, so they make this Angel here in chapter 10 Gabriel, even though Gabriel is only identified in 8:16 and 9:21. Even Larkin does this.
