But look at Judges 13. That is the Angel of the Lord coming to Manoah and his wife about the birth of Samson, and the text states so clearly (Judg. 13:3, 13, 15--18, 20--21). But look at how both Manoah and his wife perceive the Angel: ["A man of God"]{.class_1922} (Judg. 13:6), ["the man of God"]{.class_1922} (Judg. 13:8), ["the man"]{.class_1922} (Judg. 13:10), ["the man"]{.class_1922} (Judg. 13:11). In fact, they didn't even realize it was the Angel of the Lord until He went up to Heaven in the flame of a sacrifice on an altar (Judg. 13:20--21). If they had addressed Him as Lord, the text could have legitimately used the lower-case [lord.]{.class_1921}

As a matter of fact, that is exactly what happened over in Joshua 5:14. The ["captain of the host of the LORD"]{.class_1922} is obviously an Old Testament appearance of the Lord Jesus Christ (cf. Heb. 2:10). But having no clear revelation yet until verse 25 that this is a "theophany," Joshua does obeisance but addresses the Captain as ["my lord,"]{.class_1922} small [l.]{.class_1921} You see the same thing in Zechariah 1:9.

The one touching Daniel to open his mouth (vs. 16) and strengthen him (vs. 18) is the ["man"]{.class_1922} Daniel saw back up in verse 5 and the same one who touched Daniel and raised him up in verse 10. We commented on that touch back under verse 10, which see.

Did you notice that the Angel of the Lord touches Daniel three times (vss. 10, 16, 18)? It is an allusion to the Trinity. Jesus Christ is ["the fulness of the Godhead bodily"]{.class_1922} (Col. 2:9).

["By the vision my sorrows are turned upon me."]{.class_1922} Seeing Jesus Christ in His glory troubles Daniel to the point of sorrow (cf. 7:15). ["And I have retained no strength."]{.class_1922} The picture is death, as it was back in verse 8 (cf. Psa. 88:4). Look at the end of verse 17: ["neither is there breath left in me."]{.class_1922} Daniel is a picture of Israel in this age (Ezek. 37:8, 11--12). Right now, lost Israel is ["dead in trespasses and sins"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 2:1), but God plans on a full restoration of Israel---physically, politically, and spiritually. So Paul says, ["what []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_252}shall the receiving of them be, but LIFE FROM THE DEAD?"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 11:15). When that happens, and Jesus Christ reveals Himself to the remnant of Jews in the Tribulation (see our remarks under vs. 6), they'll ["look on me whom they have pierced]{.class_1922} \[i.e., [Jesus Christ]{.class_1921}---Rev. 1:7\][, and they shall mourn for him, as one mourneth for his only son, and shall be in bitterness for him, as one that is in bitterness for his firstborn"]{.class_1922} (Zech. 12:10). There is the sorrow of Daniel 10:16.

Once ["the day of vengeance of our God"]{.class_1922} is accomplished by Jesus Christ at His Advent, then His ministry will be ["to comfort all that mourn"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 61:2); that ["comfort"]{.class_1922} is specifically to ["them that mourn in Zion, to give unto them beauty for ashes, the oil of joy for mourning, the garment of praise for the spirit of heaviness"]{.class_1922} (Isa. 61:3). So here in Daniel 10, the Angel of the Lord touches Daniel, strengthens him so he can now receive the words (cf. 1 Cor. 2:13--14), and comforts him.

["O man greatly beloved]{.class_1922} \[Deut. 7:8, 33:3; Psa. 47:4; Isa. 43:4; Jer. 31:3\][, fear not]{.class_1922} \[Isa. 43:1, 5, 44:2; Jer. 30:10--11, 46:27--28\][: peace be unto thee ]{.class_1922}\[Isa. 52:7, 54:4, 13; Jer. 33:6--9; Ezek. 34:25, 37:26\][, be strong, yea, be strong ]{.class_1922}\[Isa. 35:4--6, 41:10; Ezek. 34:15--16\][."]{.class_1922} All the references I just gave you deal with the restoration of Israel at the return of Christ; that is the typology in the person of Daniel here (see our comments on vs. 14).

Now the double command of verse 19 is: ["be strong, yea, be strong."]{.class_1922} When I sign a Bible for a man or boy, I always sign it with the reference Joshua 1:9. But the strength Daniel gets isn't his own. It was the touch of Jesus Christ that made him strong again (vs. 18). So in the New Testament, the command isn't just to ["be strong"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 16:13), it is ["be strong IN THE LORD"]{.class_1922} (Eph. 6:10) and ["be strong IN THE GRACE THAT IS IN CHRIST JESUS" ]{.class_1922}(2 Tim. 2:1).

It is going to take two things to get God's strength. It is going to take [prayer.]{.class_1921}

["In the day when I cried thou answeredst me, and strengthenedst me with strength in my soul"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 138:3).

And it is going to take something that doesn't appeal to me in the least. It is going to take [infirmities:]{.class_1921} physical weakness on your part []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_253}that drives you to rely on the Lord and His strength.

["And he said unto me, My grace is sufficient for thee, for my strength is made perfect in weakness. Most gladly therefore will I rather glory in my infirmities, that the power of Christ may rest upon me"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 12:9).

Paul told the Colossians: ["Strengthened with all might, according to his glorious power, UNTO ALL PATIENCE and longsuffering with joyfulness"]{.class_1922} (Col. 1:11).

God strengthens you ["unto all patience."]{.class_1922} Do you know how you get patience? [Trouble!]{.class_1921}

["And not only so, but we glory in tribulations also: knowing that tribulation worketh patience"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 5:3).

["Knowing this, that the trying of your faith worketh patience"]{.class_1922} (James 1:3).

Brethren, I don't like it any more than you do, but if you want the strength promised you in Christ Jesus by the Holy Spirit (Phil. 4:13; Eph. 3:16), you are going to have to [suffer.]{.class_1921} You are going to have to have trouble somewhere, somehow. Do you know why Paul had the power to do what he did for God? It was because he was mocked, cussed, beaten, imprisoned, robbed, lied about, shipwrecked, ill-clothed, ill-fed, etc. (2 Cor. 11:23--27, 12:10). If you are going to know the power of Christ's resurrection, you are going to have to be intimately acquainted with the fellowship of Christ's sufferings (Phil. 3:10).

20 Then said he, Knowest thou wherefore I come unto thee? and now will I return to fight with the prince of Persia: and when I am gone forth, lo, the prince of Grecia shall come.

21 But I will shew thee that which is noted in the scripture of truth: and there is none that holdeth with me in these things, but Michael your prince.

Verse 20 places you right back at the vision of Daniel 8 (see 8:20--21): the kingdoms of Persia and Greece. (This is why I said the Angel of the Lord had come to give the final explanation of the vision of Daniel 8.) These are the spiritual principalities influencing the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_254}Kings of those realms, for the Angel of the Lord had no problem at all taking down a flesh-and-blood man (see Acts 12:23).

["Knowest thou wherefore I come unto thee?"]{.class_1922} Well, He said He had come to make Daniel understand what would happen to the Jews ["in the latter days"]{.class_1922} (vs. 14), but He hasn't explained anything about that yet. He is going to, though, and that is what follows in chapters 11 and 12. Chapter 10 ends with the source of those chapters: ["I will shew thee that which is noted in the SCRIPTURE OF TRUTH"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21).

This is the first mention of the word [Scripture]{.class_1921} in the Scripture. Now, what is Scripture? Well, do you see the word [script]{.class_1921} contained in the word [Scripture?]{.class_1921} A script is something [written down.]{.class_1921} This involves what is known as "inspiration." Second Timothy 3:16 says, ["All scripture is given by inspiration of God."]{.class_1922} The question is, how does this occur? Look at 2 Peter 1:20--21.

"Knowing this first, that no prophecy of the scripture is of any private interpretation. For the prophecy came not in old time by the will of man: but holy men of God SPAKE as they were moved by the Holy Ghost."

The word [inspire]{.class_1921} means to "breath in." So technically speaking, the "original autographs" were not "inspired" as the professors at the Fundamental Bible Colleges and Universities will tell you. God breathed (that's the Greek word for ["inspiration of God"]{.class_1922} in 2 Tim. 3:16---[theopneustos]{.class_1921}) His words into a prophet, who [spoke]{.class_1921} the words God gave him. Those words were, in turn, written down by a scribe, thus becoming "Scripture." You can see the whole process illustrated in Jeremiah 36:4.

"Then Jeremiah called Baruch the son of Neriah; and Baruch wrote from the mouth of Jeremiah all the words of the LORD, which he had spoken unto him, upon a roll of a book."

Now do you know why all of this is so important? Because the standard teaching of the Fundamentalists and Conservatives is that only the "original autographs" were "inspired." There are only three things wrong with that statement. Second Timothy 3:16 doesn't say anything about "originals," it doesn't say anything about "autographs," and it doesn't say anything about anything being []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_255}"inspired."

Read the statement again: ["ALL scripture . . . ."]{.class_1922} To what ["scripture"]{.class_1922} was Paul referring? Well, it sure wasn't any "original autographs." According to 2 Timothy 3:15, the verse right before it in the context, the Scriptures were the ones Timothy knew from a child. I guarantee you Timothy didn't have the original copy of Isaiah. If he did, that means his momma or grandma stole it from the Ethiopian eunuch (Acts 8:27--35), who had bought it on the black market after it had been stolen from the synagogue at Nazareth (Luke 4:16--21).

You see into what nonsense you get when you make ["all scripture"]{.class_1922} mean "only the original autographs." I just gave you two references in the [Scriptures]{.class_1921} where the same [Scripture]{.class_1921} (Isaiah) was called ["scripture"]{.class_1922} by the [Scriptures,]{.class_1921} and neither manuscript was Isaiah's "original" (not unless you are "one brick short of a load"). Brethren, the word ["scripture"]{.class_1922} (or ["scriptures"]{.class_1922}) in the Scriptures is NEVER a reference to any "original." The Fundamentalists are full of beans.

Now given how the Scriptures are ["given by inspiration,"]{.class_1922} is there any way one could prove that "only the originals are inspired, and therefore, only the originals are infallible and inerrant"? I just showed you where the inspiration takes place in the [speaking,]{.class_1921} not the writing. Are you going to tell me the scribe couldn't have misheard a word and written it down wrong in the "original manuscript"? You Fundamental scholars can present a list "a mile long" of "transcriptionist errors" the same scribe could make in copying that original manuscript. Was he suddenly free from human error because he was writing what he [heard]{.class_1921} rather than writing what he [saw?]{.class_1921}

Moreover, if you did have the "original," would you have what God wants you to have as "Scripture"? You take the example at which we just looked in Jeremiah 36. Do you know what happened to Jeremiah's "original"? Jehudi cut it up with his penknife and burned it. So you know what God did? He did what every Fundamental scholar, professor, and preacher who wants to lord his own authority over the authority of that Book says He didn't do: the Holy Spirit "doubly inspired" the book of Jeremiah.

["Then took Jeremiah another roll, and gave it to Baruch the scribe, the son of Neriah; who wrote therein from the mouth of Jeremiah all the words of the book which Jehoiakim king of Judah had burned in the fire: and there were ADDED BESIDES UNTO THEM MANY LIKE WORDS"]{.class_1922} (Jer. 36:32).

Not only "double inspiration," but an "inspiration" that didn't match the first one. There were [additional]{.class_1921} words in the "doubly inspired" copy of Jeremiah. So if you did get hold of Jeremiah's "original," you would be missing some words God wanted you to have. Maybe it would be 500 words like a [New King James;]{.class_1921} maybe it would be 36,000 words like a [New American Standard;]{.class_1921} maybe it would be 64,000 words like a [New International.]{.class_1921} Regardless of the number, [you still wouldn't have all the words God intended you to have.]{.class_1921} You see what I mean, jelly bean?

I have in my [King James]{.class_1921} Bible the Holy Scriptures in English. God has used that Book more than He ever did any "original manuscript" in the history of Israel or the Church. I believe it is ["given by inspiration"]{.class_1922}; certainly not as the "originals" were, but ["given by inspiration,"]{.class_1922} nonetheless. I believe I have the very words in that Book God wants me to have in English.

You say, "I don't like that Book, Ruckman. It's outdated and archaic." All right, then, what book is the Holy Scriptures in English? You say, "Well, the [NIV]{.class_1921} is good; the [NKJV]{.class_1921} is updated; the [NASV]{.class_1921} is thoroughly reliable; the [ESV]{.class_1921} is sound . . . ." I didn't ask you that. I asked you, "WHAT IS THE HOLY SCRIPTURES IN ENGLISH?"

You see, as soon as you say one or another, you have to face that verse: ["ALL SCRIPTURE is given by inspiration of God."]{.class_1922} If the "Bible" you pick is "Scripture," then it ["is given by inspiration of God."]{.class_1922}

You say, "Oh, no, only the originals are inspired." Then why not just admit to the Body of Christ that [you have no Scripture.]{.class_1921} You have "reliable translations" (maybe even "thoroughly reliable" ones), "updated versions," and "the work of Conservative scholarship"; but you don't have the Holy Scriptures, because ["ALL SCRIPTURE is given by inspiration of God."]{.class_1922} All you have are the opinions, preferences, and guesswork of [men;]{.class_1921} not the living words of the living God (cf. 1 Thess. 2:13) in a Book to which []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_257}[you are subject]{.class_1921} and not one that is [subject to you.]{.class_1921}

Now the Scripture is called ["the scripture of truth"]{.class_1922} in Daniel 10:21. That Bible is called ["the word of truth"]{.class_1922} by the Holy Spirit in His Book (Psa. 119:43; 2 Cor. 6:7; Eph. 1:13; 2 Tim. 2:15). That ["word"]{.class_1922} is not some nebulous "message" or collection of principles, thoughts, or "fundamentals." ["The word of truth"]{.class_1922} is made up of ["WORDS of truth"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 22:21; Eccl. 12:10).

The words of God in the Holy Scriptures are [absolute truth]{.class_1921} for [any time, anywhere.]{.class_1921}

["All thy commandments are truth"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 119:151).

["Thy law is the truth"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 119:142).

["Sanctify them through thy truth: thy word is truth"]{.class_1922} (John 17:17).

["Thy word is true from the beginning: and every one of thy righteous judgments endureth for ever"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 119:160).

You are living in a day when Christians have abandoned the truth of the Scriptures for their relatives, their friends, their colleagues, their jobs, their governments, their own convenience, and a "God" they have fashioned out of their own imaginations and preferences. But the God of that Bible doesn't change in His attitudes of sin, judgment, righteousness, holiness, and grace (Mal. 3:6; Heb. 13:8, 6:17--19). Just because you don't live under an Old Testament theocracy doesn't mean what God calls sin and abomination has changed. Why? Because God's words are still [the truth.]{.class_1921}

Now do you know what you have in a [King James ]{.class_1921}Bible? You have the [truth,]{.class_1921} the [whole truth,]{.class_1921} and [nothing but the truth]{.class_1921}. That can't be said of any other "Bible" on the market.

Sure, any "Bible" has enough of the truth in it to get you saved. If you have a modern version, you have what the Neo-orthodox always talked about: you have a "Bible" that [contains]{.class_1921} the word of God but is [not actually]{.class_1921} the word of God. That means it [contains]{.class_1921} truth, along with some garbage as well.

The new versions don't have the "[whole truth."]{.class_1921} They will leave out the blood in Colossians 1:14. They will eliminate half of Romans 8:1. They will trim off three-quarters of 1 John 5:7. And verses like Mark 9:44, 46 and Matthew 17:21 drop clean out of sight.

They don't have "[nothing but the truth."]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_258} They will attack the virgin birth of Christ in Luke 2:33 by making ["Joseph"]{.class_1922} Christ's ["father."]{.class_1921} They will attack His incarnation by changing ["child"]{.class_1922} to ["servant"]{.class_1921} in Acts 4:27, 30 (even the ["New" King James]{.class_1921} does that). They attack His Deity in 1 Timothy 3:16 by converting ["God"]{.class_1922} into some ambiguous ["He Who"]{.class_1921} or simply ["Who."]{.class_1921} And they create [two Gods]{.class_1921} in John 1:18 (a begotten One and an unbegotten One) by changing ["the only begotten Son"]{.class_1922} to ["the only begotten God"]{.class_1921} (see the [NASV]{.class_1921} reading for John 1:18).

The [King James]{.class_1921} not only is true "generally"; it is true in every detail and complete in the truth it presents. It is [the truth,]{.class_1921} the [whole truth,]{.class_1921} and [nothing but]{.class_1921} [the truth.]{.class_1921}

Now, verse 21 is enigmatic, to say the least. You see, what the Angel of the Lord shows Daniel that ["is noted in the scripture of truth"]{.class_1922} is what follows in chapters 11 and 12. While you can certainly cross-reference the material in those chapters to Scriptures written previous to Daniel, you don't find the Angel of the Lord quoting anything from Genesis, Exodus, Leviticus, Numbers, Deuteronomy, Psalms, Isaiah, Jeremiah, Ezekiel, or any other Old Testament book written before Daniel 10.

The safest way to handle the passage is to go back to the vision of Daniel 8, which was written during ["the third year of the reign of king Belshazzar"]{.class_1922} (8:1); that vision was said to be ["true"]{.class_1922} (8:26). ["The thing"]{.class_1922} the Angel of the Lord is about to reveal to Daniel about that vision is said to be ["true"]{.class_1922} (vs. 1). So this could be the Lord Jesus Christ giving understanding on the Scripture previously revealed to and recorded by Daniel.

But the fact is, God had a Book written before Moses ever set ink to paper (Exod. 32:32). David wrote, ["For ever, O LORD, thy word is settled in heaven"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 119:89). Unable even to acknowledge the individual words that make up God's word---even the Book up in Heaven before the throne---Adam Clarke says, "Thy PURPOSES are all settled above." After that, you can write H-O-G-W-A-S-H!

That ["word"]{.class_1922} that God has ["magnified"]{.class_1922} above even the name of His own Son (Psa. 138:2 cf. Phil. 2:9) is composed of ["words"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 138:4). Every one of those words are said to be ["pure"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 30:5). []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_259}"Purposes" your Aunt Sally's house cat!

[IF]{.class_1921} (and that is a big [if]{.class_1921}) ["the scripture of truth"]{.class_1922} in Daniel 10:21 is a reference to that Book up in Heaven, then you have three manifestations of the Scripture. You have the Book in its entirety up in Glory. You have the individual revelations of the Scripture ["given by inspiration"]{.class_1922} down here on earth to ["holy men of God"]{.class_1922} from between 1800 B.C. (Job) to A.D. 96 (Revelation). These writings were copied, eventually collected in one Book which we call "the Bible," and then translated into over 160 languages, the greatest of these translations being the [King James Authorized Version]{.class_1921} in the English tongue.

Of those copies and translations made by men, the Holy Spirit said, ["the words of the LORD are pure words: as silver tried in a furnace of EARTH]{.class_1922} \[not up in Heaven\][, purified seven times. Thou shalt keep them, O LORD, thou shalt preserve them from this generation for ever"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 12:6--7). God took those "originals" and purified them here on earth to give you His final authority in the universal language of the last days before the return of Christ: English. God put the Scriptures through seven steps of purification: Hebrew, Aramaic, Greek, Old Syriac, Old Latin, German, English. He put the English Bible through seven steps of purification: Tyndale, Coverdale, [Matthew, Great, Geneva, Bishops', King James.]{.class_1921}

Proponents of "Scholarship Onlyism" (aka "Dead Duck Otherism") don't mind that ["word . . . settled in heaven."]{.class_1922} Why not? [You can't check it out.]{.class_1926} They don't mind the "originals"; [you can't check them out.]{.class_1926} But that old, black-backed, 66-caliber [Authorized Version]{.class_1926} of the Protestant Reformation "am sumptin' else." It is the standard by which they have to measure whatever they do, even though they can't stand it. They don't try to overthrow the authority of the Book in Heaven. They don't try to overthrow the authority of the "originals"; in fact, they will pledge their hearts and souls to a lost pile of papers no one has ever seen because they can make them say anything they want (and they do, whether in Hebrew and Greek, or translations from those texts). But they will do their "dead level best," laboring day and night, to get rid of that roaring lion of 1611, because it "eats their lunch." You can tell what ["the scripture of truth"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1484.xhtml_page_260} is by the opposition it receives from all quarters---[Fundamental, Conservative, and Evangelicals foremost.]{.class_1926}

[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml}

# Chapter 11 {.heading_67-0}

Daniel 11 is the longest chapter in the prophetic half of Daniel and, I must profess, a difficult chapter on which to comment; I don't profess to understand it. According to Scofield, Larkin, and most of the commentators, the material is the historic events that take place in the intertestamental period. I am sure that is [partially]{.class_1921} true, but we should never forget what Daniel was told back in 10:14---["I am come to make thee understand what shall befall thy people IN THE LATTER DAYS."]{.class_1922} So the main purpose of the chapter is to give you what happens to the Jews before the [Second Advent]{.class_1921} of Jesus Christ, not the First.

Of course, as we have pointed out on many an occasion (e.g., see our comments on Acts 7:55--56 in that Commentary), in the Gospels, everything was set up for both Advents being fulfilled; it all depended on what the Jews did with John the Baptist, the Lord Jesus Christ, and finally, the message of Stephen in Acts 7. But the Jews rejected all three, so the Second Advent was postponed 2,000--plus years (see Mark 9:11--12). That is one of the things that is problematic about the first half of Daniel's Seventieth Week and when to locate it. Did the Jews' rejection of their Messiah put both halves of the Seventieth Week into the future? I will have to plead ["Ich weiss nicht"]{.class_1921} on that one.

Undoubtedly what you have here in Daniel 11 is [double application]{.class_1921} of the text, as we have seen previously in chapters 7 and 9. There will be an application which, to us, will be [historical;]{.class_1921} i.e., the events prophesied, which were still future to Daniel, took place between 534 B.C. (Ussher's date for the passage) and the First Advent. However, just as there was [prophetic]{.class_1921} application to the beasts of Daniel 7 and 8, as sure as you live and breathe, what you are reading here in chapter 11 are events that will take place before the Second Advent. So all the comings and goings, the fussing and fighting, and the political intrigue going on between the Ptolemies, the Seleucids, Antiochus Epiphanes, and Cleopatra are types of what will take place between now and the end of the Tribulation.

Now I want to give the reader a word of warning: you need to be []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_262}careful about "jumping the gun" on declaring prophecies such as you are about to read here as being "fulfilled" by current events in the news. That is what a lot of the prophecy boys do. They will latch onto some news item in the Middle East and declare it a fulfillment of some Old Testament prophecy, and then everything "blows over" with nothing happening as far as end-time events are concerned. That's the mindset from which all the prophetic books on Anwar Sadat's peace treaty with Israel, Saddam Hussein and the Gulf War, and the "Blood Moons" come. That's just a bunch of pastors and teachers trying to make a name for themselves off Christian suckers. Some of them get all caught up with "prophecy fulfilled in our time" to the point that they have the Body of Christ going through the Tribulation now. Just because you are paying over two dollars a gallon for gas and the queers, dykes, and perverts are taking over the country doesn't mean you are in the Tribulation yet. Some of your brethren overseas have been through more hell than you have for the sake of Christ, and they're not in the Tribulation.

Of course, I don't want to put a wet blanket on any Christian studying Bible prophecy. There are definitely signs of Christ's return to which you can point (see our remarks in Luke 21 in that Commentary). The Christian can certainly be encouraged by these signs, even though they are not for him (1 Cor. 1:22). Any sign pointing towards the Second Advent means the Rapture is that much closer. But you had better be careful about being dogmatic about some things.

There was a preacher years ago named McBurney who said if Mussolini did not turn out to be the Antichrist, he would quit preaching. [I trust he quit preaching.]{.class_1921}

Back in the 80s, there was a guy named Edgar Whisenant who wrote a booklet that a lot of the Charismatic brethren bought into; it was titled [88 Reasons Why the Rapture Will Be in 1988.]{.class_1921} That bird sold four-and-a-half million copies of that book, and of course, nothing happened. So he wrote three more books on why it would [definitely]{.class_1921} occur in 1989, 1993, and 1994; but by then, he had become a laughingstock. There were Christians who took him so seriously that they went out and "maxed out" their credit cards, figuring they would leave the bill to the Antichrist. Boy, were they []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_263}surprised!

That didn't stop Harold Camping, though, from predicting the Lord's return on May 21, 2011 (and then on October 21, 2011). Christians gave him millions of dollars to launch a publicity campaign announcing his predictions, only to have the atheists and infidels throw parties when it didn't happen.

That's why, brethren, I never made anything but [guesses]{.class_1921} as to the date of the Rapture. You can't be dogmatic about things like that because there are things about the Lord's plans you don't know. My booklet on [Millions Disappear]{.class_1921} is good for [whenever]{.class_1921} the Lord comes back. There are general truths and admonitions about the Second Coming that are good for anytime, anywhere.

So with all that being said, let's get into the text.

11:1 Also I in the first year of Darius the Mede, even I, stood to confirm and to strengthen him.

2 And now will I shew thee the truth. Behold, there shall stand up yet three kings in Persia; and the fourth shall be far richer than they all: and by his strength through his riches he shall stir up all against the realm of Grecia.

3 And a mighty king shall stand up, that shall rule with great dominion, and do according to his will.

4 And when he shall stand up, his kingdom shall be broken, and shall be divided toward the four winds of heaven; and not to his posterity, nor according to his dominion which he ruled: for his kingdom shall be plucked up, even for others beside those.

The speaker is still the Angel of the Lord from chapter 10. He refers Daniel back to ["the first year of Darius the Mede"]{.class_1922} (vs. 1). So during Daniel 6 and 9, the Angel of the Lord was at work for Daniel and his people.

The Angel of the Lord says, ["even I, stood to confirm and to strengthen him."]{.class_1922} That can be interpreted in two ways. In the context of 10:21, it could refer to ["Michael your prince"]{.class_1922} who held with the Angel of the Lord in the things concerning the Princes of Persia and Greece. If that be the case, then that would be Jesus []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_264}Christ as the Angel of the Lord confirming and strengthening Michael in the matter of the return of Israel to the land. But the immediate antecedent for ["him"]{.class_1922} in the verse would be ["Darius the Mede."]{.class_1922} That would mean that it was God Almighty who deposed Belshazzar, set Darius on the throne of Babylon, and strengthened him in his kingdom.

Verses 2 and 3 give the transition from the silver chest to the brass waist (chap. 2), from the winged lion to the bear (chap. 7), from the ram to the rough he-goat (chap. 8). Before Persia passed as the leading world empire, there would be three more Kings after  Cyrus (10:1), and the fourth would ["by his strength through his riches . . . stir up all against the realm of Grecia"]{.class_1922} (vs. 2). The three Kings are given in Ezra 4. They are: ["Ahasuerus"]{.class_1922} (Ezra 4:6), ["Artaxerxes"]{.class_1922} (Ezra 4:7--8), and ["Darius"]{.class_1922} (Ezra 4:24). The fourth King would be Xerxes I, who invaded Greece in 480 B.C. The problem with identifying the three Kings in history is that, as Bullinger points out in Appendix 57 of his [Companion Bible]{.class_1921} on "The Genealogy of the Persian Kings," you are dealing with [titles]{.class_1921} in Ezra 4, not the actual names of the monarchs. Out of three secular lists of Persian Kings, you find as many variations in the actual names. Larkin gives them as Cambyses, "Pseudo" Smerdis, and Darius Hystaspes; and that is as good an identification as any.

Verse 3 skips over seven or eight Persian Kings (depending on whose list you use), a period of about 165 years, to the rise of Alexander the Great---the ["mighty king . . . that shall rule with great dominion, and do according to his will."]{.class_1922} This King is ["the great horn"]{.class_1922} of ["the rough goat"]{.class_1922} of 8:21. ["His kingdom"]{.class_1922} is ["broken"]{.class_1922} and ["divided toward the four winds of heaven"]{.class_1922} as you read back in 8:8, 22 (see our comments on those verses).

Alexander's kingdom is broken up after his death, and his Generals get the four kingdoms into which it is divided. His son doesn't get what his father conquered (["not to his posterity, nor according to his dominion which he ruled"]{.class_1922}---vs. 4). So what you are about to read applies historically (from our perspective) to wars between two of the kingdoms of Alexander's empire: Egypt in the south and Syria in the north. South and north of what? ["The glorious land"]{.class_1922} (vss. 16, 41, 45)---[Israel.]{.class_1921} There are 83 prophecies []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_265}fulfilled during the intertestamental period; there are seventy more yet to be fulfilled during the Tribulation (see especially vss. 24--38). Undoubtedly, the reason for the double application is so the Jews will expect the fulfillment of the latter after seeing the fulfillment of the former.

5 And the king of the south shall be strong, and one of his princes; and he shall be strong above him, and have dominion; his dominion shall be a great dominion.

6 And in the end of years they shall join themselves together; for the king's daughter of the south shall come to the king of the north to make an agreement: but she shall not retain the power of the arm; neither shall he stand, nor his arm: but she shall be given up, and they that brought her, and he that begat her, and he that strengthened her in these times.

["The king of the south"]{.class_1922} (vs. 5) would be  Ptolemy I (also known as Ptolemy Souter or Ptolemy Lagidae \[or some spelling variation thereof, depending on what source you use\]). ["One of his princes"]{.class_1922} was Seleucus Nicator, the General of Alexander's cavalry who helped establish Ptolemy as Pharaoh of Egypt. After the two of them conquered Babylon, Seleucus took control of the eastern part of Alexander's empire, which stretched from Syria to the Indus River. That is why verse 5 says, ["he]{.class_1922} \[i.e., the Prince under Ptolemy\][ shall be strong above him, and have dominion; his dominion shall be a great dominion."]{.class_1922} The territory Seleucus ruled was greater than the territory Ptolemy ruled. Of course, this resulted in war between the sons (Ptolemy Philadelphus and Antiochus Soter) when they took over.

Verse 6: ["And in the end of years."]{.class_1922} And now we have a problem. ["The end"]{.class_1922} points you to events preceding the Second Advent, not the First. The commentators who read the verse as the Egyptian--Syrian wars that took place between the Testaments will say ["the end of years"]{.class_1922} would be the consummation of the time when verses 5--15 would be fulfilled. But ["the end"]{.class_1922} in verses 27, 35, 40 points, in each case, to the Tribulation. Undoubtedly what you []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_266}are about to read has some prophetic application that will be fulfilled in the Tribulation. Notice how often the words [Egypt]{.class_1921} and [Assyria]{.class_1921} (which was part of the Seleucid Empire) appear together in the Prophets: Isaiah 7:18, 10:24, 11:11, 16, 19:23--25, 20:4, 27:13, 52:4; Jeremiah 2:18, 36; Hosea 7:11, 9:3, 11:5, 11, 12:1; Zechariah 10:10--11. Of course, how to put it all together I will have to plead ["Ich weiss nicht"]{.class_1921} to.

In the intertestamental interpretation, what you have is Ptolemy II (Philadephus) giving his daughter Berenice in marriage to Antiochus Theus in order to bring peace to the two kingdoms. Sometimes you will see Berenice called "Cleopatra" because all the Princesses and Queens of the Ptolemaic line took that as a title (like [Pharaoh]{.class_1921} and [Ptolemy]{.class_1921} for the male heirs). The condition was that Antiochus had to divorce his present wife (Laodice, after whom Laodicea was named) and denounce her children as heirs to his throne in favor of Berenice's child.

["But she shall not retain the power of the arm; neither shall he stand, nor his arm . . . and he that begot her." "The arm"]{.class_1922} would be what gave her strength in this deal; that would be the army of her daddy backing up her claim to the throne. When he died (["he that begat her"]{.class_1922}), Antiochus' "ex" made her move and poisoned her former husband, had her "replacements" (Berenice and her kid) killed, and placed her son (Seleucus Callinicus) on the throne.

7 But out of a branch of her roots shall one stand up in his estate, which shall come with an army, and shall enter into the fortress of the king of the north, and shall deal against them, and shall prevail:

8 And shall also carry captives into Egypt their gods, with their princes, and with their precious vessels of silver and of gold; and he shall continue more years than the king of the north.

The ["branch of her roots"]{.class_1922} (vs. 7) is obviously someone in Berenice's "family tree." The ["roots"]{.class_1922} would be her parents, and the ["branch"]{.class_1922} would be a sibling. Scofield, Larkin, and the commentators identify this ["branch"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_267} as Berenice's brother, Ptolemy Euergetes (Ptolemy III). In revenge for his sister's death, he invaded Syria (the Third Syrian War) all the way to Seleucia on the Tigris, ["the fortress of the king of the north"]{.class_1922} in verse 7.

["And shall also carry captives into Egypt their gods"]{.class_1922} (vs. 8). As Nebuchadnezzar had done to the Temple vessels of Jerusalem, the Persian Kings had carried the idols of the Egyptian gods, along with the gold and silver vessels used in their service, back to Persia when they conquered Egypt. Ptolemy III brought these idols and their vessels back to Egypt and restored them to their temples, thus gaining the surname of [Euergetes,]{.class_1921} meaning "benefactor." It is amusing to see how some writers try to describe these false gods. One source calls them "Egyptian works of art." One Christian author called them "sacred statues." They were [idols, false gods;]{.class_1921} like Mary, the crucifix, the Virgin of Guadaloupe, the Black Peter, St. Christopher medallions, our Lady of Lourdes, "Christ the Redeemer" in Rio de Janeiro, and the ninety-foot "Our Lady of the Rockies" in Butte, Montana. "Works of art," "sacred statues"; aren't we cute?

["And he]{.class_1922} \[i.e., ["the king of the south"]{.class_1922}\][ shall continue more years than the king of the north."]{.class_1922} Ptolemy III outlived Seleucus II by four years.

9 So the king of the south shall come into his kingdom, and shall return into his own land.

10 But his sons shall be stirred up, and shall assemble a multitude of great forces: and one shall certainly come, and overflow, and pass through: then shall he return, and be stirred up, even to his fortress.

11 And the king of the south shall be moved with choler, and shall come forth and fight with him, even with the king of the north: and he shall set forth a great multitude; but the multitude shall be given into his hand.

We come now to a section that can be confusing, because the antecedents to the pronouns are not very clear. Knowing Hebrew doesn't help either. So a careful reading and comparing of the text with its fulfillment is what it will take to figure everything out.

Now, the ["his kingdom"]{.class_1922} could be the same as []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_268}["his own land"]{.class_1922} in verse 9, and commentators like Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown, and Gill, will read it that way. Most of the commentators, though, will say the ["his kingdom"]{.class_1922} is the kingdom of Syria in the north, while the ["his own land"]{.class_1922} is Egypt, the land of ["the king of the south."]{.class_1922} Larkin reads it that way. There could be some merit in that view. The King of Egypt [comes]{.class_1921} into that ["kingdom,"]{.class_1922} but he [returns]{.class_1921} to that ["land,"]{.class_1922} and that ["land" ]{.class_1922}is distinguished from that ["kingdom"]{.class_1922} by the word ["own."]{.class_1922}

But if you want to see why Larkin and others take that interpretation, look at verse 10: ["But HIS SONS shall be stirred up."]{.class_1922}[ Whose]{.class_1921}[ "sons"]{.class_1922}? Well, it can't be the sons of ["the king of the south"]{.class_1922} because that King goes out to fight with one of those sons in verse 11, and that son is ["the king of the north."]{.class_1922}

So verse 9 is a summary of verses 7--8. Ptolemy III goes into Seleucus II's territory and tears it up. Ptolemy then returns to Egypt without deposing Seleucus II. Larkin tells us it was to quell an insurrection back in Egypt.

After the death of Seleucus II, his two sons---Seleucus III and Antiochus III---begin to amass an army to invade Egypt, but only ["one shall certainly come"]{.class_1922} (vs. 10). That was Antiochus III, because Seleucus III had been poisoned to death by two of his Generals. Antiochus III "overflowed" his boundaries and passed through and took the territories Ptolemy III had taken in Lebanon and Palestine.

This Fourth Syrian War ended with a great battle between Ptolemy IV and Antiochus III at the Egyptian garrison of Raphia, near Gaza; that would be the ["his fortress"]{.class_1922} of verse 10. Ptolemy IV was known as a weak King, so when he ["moved with choler"]{.class_1922} (i.e., [fury]{.class_1921}---see our remarks under 8:7) against Antiochus, it was "out of character" for him. He ended up winning the battle, and Antiochus' ["multitude"]{.class_1922} was ["given into his hand"]{.class_1922} (vs. 11); i.e., the hand of the King of Egypt.

Now I trust you understand what you are reading here. This is history recorded ahead of time in such explicit detail that the Liberal would swear it had to be written after the fact. The reason he figures that is because no other religious book in the world (e.g., Mohammed's [Koran]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_269}) even attempts to do anything like it. No other "scriptures" of other religions will give you eighty details ahead of time that can be verified as taking place [in history.]{.class_1921} The Bible will, and it gets it right every time.

12 And when he hath taken away the multitude, his heart shall be lifted up; and he shall cast down many ten thousands: but he shall not be strengthened by it.

13 For the king of the north shall return, and shall set forth a multitude greater than the former, and shall certainly come after certain years with a great army and with much riches.

14 And in those times there shall many stand up against the king of the south: also the robbers of thy people shall exalt themselves to establish the vision; but they shall fall.

15 So the king of the north shall come, and cast up a mount, and take the most fenced cities: and the arms of the south shall not withstand, neither his chosen people, neither shall there be any strength to withstand.

Ptolemy IV had a great victory at Raphia; he ["cast down many ten thousands"]{.class_1922} (vs. 12). But Ptolemy allowed himself to be ["lifted up"]{.class_1922} with pride in ["his heart."]{.class_1922} He didn't follow through on his victory because he fancied himself invincible, so he wasn't ["strengthened"]{.class_1922} by the great victory he had won. He gave himself over to sensuality and ended up losing half his kingdom in a rebellion by his own subjects.

When Ptolemy IV died, Antiochus III once more invaded Lebanon and Palestine to retake his holdings there after retreating from his defeat at Raphia. This was the Fifth Syrian War, and it ended with Antiochus being victorious over the Egyptian forces at the Battle of Panium near the headwaters of the Jordan.

Among the ["many"]{.class_1922} that stood up ["against the king of the south"]{.class_1922} (vs. 14) with Antiochus was Philip V of Macedon. The two made an alliance to take and divide the territories held by Egypt. Rome was rising in power at this point and issued an ultimatum that they were not to invade Egypt itself.

It is not clear, historically, who []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_270}["the robbers of thy people"]{.class_1922} are. All the commentators and expositors agree that the ["thy people"]{.class_1922} identifies both who the robbers are as well as whom they are robbing. These are [Jews]{.class_1921} (they are ["of"]{.class_1922} Daniel's people) robbing [Jews.]{.class_1921} Larkin says they are unscrupulous Jews who bring trouble to their own people by joining Antiochus against the Egyptians. They were trying to curry favor with Antiochus in order to gain positions of power once Antiochus took charge. According to Larkin, once Antiochus took over Palestine, he turned on these "robber Jews" and, assumably, had them killed.

The problem with that view is, there is no historic evidence that happened. According to Josephus, Antiochus the Great actually helped out the Jews. He rebuilt parts of Jerusalem destroyed in his battle against the Egyptian garrison there, he forbade bringing unclean animals into Jerusalem, he freed Jerusalem from taxation, and gave supplies and funds to the Temple.

Another view, which seems to fit the facts better, is that before Antiochus came in, Jerusalem was controlled by a family called the "Tobiads" who taxed Jerusalem and the Jews excessively for the Egyptians. The Jews grew so tired of this that when Antiochus whipped Ptolemy's forces, the Jews welcomed him into Jerusalem, supplied his army, and helped him defeat the garrison of the Egyptians in Jerusalem. Without intending to, the Tobiads helped bring about the vision given to Daniel of the overthrow of ["the king of the south."]{.class_1922}

Now, I just gave the historic view of verse 14, but as I said, there is probably a future application as well. Over in Ezekiel 7:22, the Lord talks about ["robbers"]{.class_1922} entering into His ["secret place"]{.class_1922} (i.e., the Holy of Holies) and defiling it. That is what happens down in verse 31 here in Daniel 11. So the prophetic application begins to grow stronger here. The further we get into the chapter, the stronger this prophetic application becomes. These historic characters and events are types of what is to come in the Tribulation.

Not being allowed by the Romans to invade Egypt, Antiochus turned to take the Egyptians' holdings in Caria and Cilicia along the southern coast of Asia Minor. That is the historic fulfillment of verse 15, but as we will see in the next verse, allusions are being made to []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_271}the Antichrist.

16 But he that cometh against him shall do according to his own will, and none shall stand before him: and he shall stand in the glorious land, which by his hand shall be consumed.

17 He shall also set his face to enter with the strength of his whole kingdom, and upright ones with him; thus shall he do: and he shall give him the daughter of women, corrupting her: but she shall not stand on his side, neither be for him.

18 After this shall he turn his face unto the isles, and shall take many: but a prince for his own behalf shall cause the reproach offered by him to cease; without his own reproach he shall cause it to turn upon him.

19 Then he shall turn his face toward the fort of his own land: but he shall stumble and fall, and not be found.

Historically, verse 16 is the conquest of Palestine by Antiochus. ["The glorious land"]{.class_1922} is another name for the Promised Land, Israel (cf. 8:9). In order for Antichous to be able to launch an attack against Egypt, he had to have a clear corridor through which to move his troops; hence, the need to have control over the land of Israel.

Larkin doesn't make any comment on the last clause of verse 16: ["which by his hand shall be consumed."]{.class_1922} As I pointed out above, Antiochus III ("the Great") wasn't particularly oppressive in his dealings with the Jews. Seeing the problem, some of the commentators, like Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown, try to "Hebrewfy" it away. SOP for the Alexandrian Cult---when you don't understand something in the Bible, [change it to bring it down to your own level of ignorance.]{.class_1921}

I don't profess to have all the answers, but I will say this. The "consuming" could be a reference to the desolations caused by the battles between the Syrians and the Egyptians. No matter how "benevolent" a ruler may be, he can't prevent the ravages of war. Also, though Antiochus the Great may not have personally "consumed" the land, his son, Antiochus Epiphanes, the next []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_272}["king of the north,"]{.class_1922} did. The Holy Spirit could be looking ahead to that King. But far more likely is the possibility that this is a prophetic reference to the Antichrist in the type of ["the king of the north"]{.class_1922} (see vs. 41).

Now, as I pointed out under my remarks on verses 14--15, though Antiochus wanted to invade and take over Egypt, Rome wouldn't allow it. So Ptolemy V made a treaty with Antiochus and, as a seal of that treaty, was given the daughter of Antiochus to be his wife. This was Cleopatra I (not the one who messed around with Marc Antony; that was Cleopatra VII). Antiochus hoped to gain control of Egypt through her and her children, but she ended up siding with her husband (eventually becoming the only sole woman ruler of Egypt in the Ptolemaic line). That is what is going on historically in verse 17.

The ["upright ones"]{.class_1922} is a reference to the Jews, as opposed to the Gentiles. These are the Jews who support Antiochus the Great in his campaign against Egypt (see our remarks under vs. 14). The title sheds some light on one of the famous "extra-canonical" writings mentioned in Scripture. The Hebrew word for ["upright ones"]{.class_1922} is [yashar,]{.class_1921} transliterated in your Bible as ["Jasher,"]{.class_1922} as in ["the book of Jasher"]{.class_1922} in Joshua 10:13 and 2 Samuel 1:18. All ["the book of Jasher"]{.class_1922} is, is an historic record of the Jews in the land between the conquest of the land under Joshua to the reign of Saul. It is obviously used as an historic source for at least parts of the books of Joshua and 2 Samuel (and probably Judges, Ruth, and 1 Samuel as well), but it is no more "Scripture" than ["the chronicles of the kings"]{.class_1922} of Israel and Judah referenced throughout 1 & 2 Kings (e.g., 1 Kings 14:19, 29; 2 Kings 1:18, 8:23). If you ever see [The Book of Jasher]{.class_1921} for sale at a "Christian" bookstore, all you are getting is a forgery put out by the Mormons; you aren't getting any "light" on the Scriptures from archaeology.

Verses 18 and 19 cover the end of the reign of Antiochus the Great. Failing to "get his foot in the door" of the throne of Egypt through his daughter, and not being allowed by the Romans to conquer Egypt, he turned to take the rest of Alexander's old empire in Thrace (upper Asia Minor and Macedonia) and Greece. With a fleet []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_273}of 300 ships, he began attacking the islands and coastal cities off Asia Minor and Greece. He invaded Greece in 192 B.C. and was driven out the next year by the Roman armies under Manius Glabrio. The year after that, he was defeated at Magnesia in Asia Minor by Scipio Asiaticus;[ ]{.class_1921}Scipio is the ["prince"]{.class_1922} of verse 18 who caused ["the reproach"]{.class_1922} of Antiochus III ["to cease."]{.class_1922}

Antiochus fled to his capital in Antioch of Syria, ["the fort of his own land"]{.class_1922} in verse 19. In the ensuing peace treaty with Rome (the Treaty of Apamea), he lost nearly all of his holdings and conquests in Asia Minor. He was also forced to pay the costs of the war for the Romans: 500 talents of silver as a down payment, 2,550 more when the treaty was ratified by the Roman Senate, and a thousand more annually for twelve years. It was this tribute that led to his demise. The people of Elam killed him when he tried to plunder their temple to Bel (["he shall stumble and fall, and not be found"]{.class_1922}).

20 Then shall stand up in his estate a raiser of taxes in the glory of the kingdom: but within few days he shall be destroyed, neither in anger, nor in battle.

21 And in his estate shall stand up a vile person, to whom they shall not give the honour of the kingdom: but he shall come in peaceably, and obtain the kingdom by flatteries.

Now that is just about enough of Syrian politics, but the lion's share of the commentators and expositors, including Larkin and Scofield, will keep right on with the historic application. The common interpretation is to apply verses 20--35 to Antiochus Epiphanes (Larkin makes the break at vs. 32 and runs vss. 33--35 to the birth of Christ). Now I don't deny at all that Antiochus Epiphanes is a type of what is to show up in the next several years, but what you are about to read has nothing [doctrinally]{.class_1921} to do with the Maccabean revolt. I will [briefly]{.class_1921} describe the historic application, and then we will get into the doctrinal, prophetic application.

The ["raiser of taxes"]{.class_1922} in verse 20 would be Antiochus III's son Seleucus Philopater. He tried to raid the Temple treasury in Jerusalem in order to pay his daddy's war debt. He was assassinated []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_274}by his chief tax collector and was succeeded by his younger brother Mithsidates, who seized the throne, took his daddy's name, and proclaimed himself deity ([Ephiphanes,]{.class_1921} Gk. "God manifest"). So you can see why Antiochus IV makes such a good type of the Antichrist: he claimed to be God in the flesh and defiled the Jewish Temple. Although he had delusions of godhood, his citizens made a play on the title he gave himself and called him "Epimanes"---the [madman.]{.class_1921} His own people considered him a ["vile"]{.class_1922} character (vs. 21).

Antiochus was not the rightful heir to the throne, so he had to ["obtain"]{.class_1922} it ["by flatteries."]{.class_1922} He flattered two Kings of Pergamum (Eumemes and Attalus) to help him get rid of his political enemies. Then he flattered the Romans to proclaim him the rightful King of Syria.

Then, depending on which commentator you pick up, ["the prince of the covenant"]{.class_1922} is either the King of Egypt with whom Antiochus the Great had made a covenant (the position of Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown), or it is Onias, the Jewish high priest. And ["the league"]{.class_1922} of verse 23 is either the one made between Syria and Egypt (Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown), or it is the one Antiochus Epiphanes made with the Kings of Pergamum (Larkin).

Antiochus finally ended up attacking Ptolemy Philometor and defeating him (vss. 25--26). Ptolemy's brother was made King of Egypt by Antiochus, and Antiochus had a "peace summit" with Ptolemy. Antiochus used the "peace accords" as an excuse to [attack]{.class_1921} Alexandria (and lost). Ptolemy used them to reconcile with his brother and became coregent with him; then they both [attacked]{.class_1921} Antiochus. That is supposed to be the fulfillment of verse 27.

Antiochus took what spoils of war he had gained and went back to Syria via Israel. The Jews had been watching "cable news" and reading the Associated Press, the Gannet string of newspapers, and [Time, Life,]{.class_1921} and [Newsweek,]{.class_1921} and had gotten "preliminary reports" that Antiochus had died in battle. Antiochus was not flattered at all to learn that the Jews had "great joy" over the "greatly exaggerated" reports of his demise. So he proceeded to kill 40,000 of them, take a bunch of them as slaves, and carried off Temple treasure valued at about 1,800 talents of silver. That's the historic interpretation of verse 29.

["The time appointed"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_275} of verse 29 is supposed to be a reference to Antiochus' attack on Alexandria in the Spring of 168 B.C. This campaign didn't go as any of his previous ones. ["The ships of Chittim"]{.class_1922} (vs. 30) turned out to be a Roman fleet, and the commander gave him the ultimatum to leave Rome's "friends" alone and go home. [Antiochus went home.]{.class_1921}

Frustrated in his purpose to take Egypt, he took out his frustrations once more on the Jews. This is his famous desecration of the Temple. He went into the Temple, sacrificed a pig on the altar, sprayed its blood in the Holy of Holies, set up an altar to Zeus (Jupiter), and began offering sacrifices to the idol. He made a law that all Jews throughout the land were to forsake their religion and worship as Greeks, and that is where the Maccabean revolt comes in. Some of the Jews gave in, but the Maccabees did not. Both Scofield and Larkin apply verses 32--34 to the Maccabean period.

Now, a lot of that content on Antiochus Epiphanes is given in the Roman Catholic Apocryphal books of 1 & 2 Maccabees; they contain some accurate history as well as some [bunk.]{.class_1921} The Catholics get their "proof texts" for Purgatory and prayers to dead saints from 1 & 2 Maccabees. Luther and the [AV]{.class_1921} translators recognized the Apocryphal books as giving historic insights into the intertestamental period [but as not inspired Scripture,]{.class_1921} and put them between the Testaments as recommended reading [that is not inspired Scripture.]{.class_1921} As Bible believers, we can respect the judgment of the [AV]{.class_1921} translators as to what is Scripture and what is not. When it comes to the value of the Apocryphal books, we don't have to worry about what they thought one way or another. Where 1 & 2 Maccabees don't contradict revealed Scripture, we will take what they say with a grain of salt; where they contradict what the Holy Spirit said in His Book, we won't pay any more attention to them than we would a stale gummi bear from last year.

Let's go back, now, to verse 20 and pick it up and come through again, this time looking at the reality instead of the type. First of all, let's look at that ["raiser of taxes"]{.class_1922} (T-A-X: watch out for words that end in X; see chap. 4 of [The Mark of the Beast]{.class_1921}). When Jesus Christ came the first time, ["a decree"]{.class_1922} went forth ["from Caesar Augustus,"]{.class_1922} the King of [Rome,]{.class_1921} a type of [Babylon]{.class_1921} (Rev. 17), ["that all the world should be TAXED"]{.class_1922} (Luke 2:1). That [tax]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_276} has been changed in the new "Bibles" (including the [NKJV,]{.class_1921} which is NOT a [King James]{.class_1921} Bible) to a [census]{.class_1921} or an [enrollment]{.class_1921} so you will lose the cross-references to Caesar as one of the seven heads on the Beast (Rev. 13:1; see our remarks on 7:7).

Right before the First Advent, there is ["a raiser of taxes,"]{.class_1922} so before Christ's Second Advent, there will be ["a raiser of taxes."]{.class_1922} So the push by the UN, Obama, Pelosi, Hillary, and the Democrats is for a [global]{.class_1921} tax for the "redistribution of wealth" (i.e., you take money away from the United States and give it to a third-world dictator, more likely than not a [Moslem]{.class_1921} dictator, these days). Republicans want to do the same thing, only slower. Sooner or later, you can expect to see an [International]{.class_1921} Revenue Service.

Now look at what happens to this ["raiser of taxes"]{.class_1922} in verse 20: ["but within few days he shall be destroyed."]{.class_1922} He is killed, but ["neither in anger, nor in battle."]{.class_1922} That ["anger"]{.class_1922} is like that ["choler"]{.class_1922} back up in verse 11: it is the fury associated with [war.]{.class_1921} So this ["raiser of taxes"]{.class_1922} dies, and ["a vile person"]{.class_1922} takes his place (vs. 21).

You say, "Then how can verse 20 be referring to the Antichrist?" Because when he comes, the Antichrist has [two]{.class_1921} manifestations.[ ]{.class_1921}The first is the ["man of sin,"]{.class_1922} and the second is ["the son of perdition"]{.class_1922} (2 Thess. 2:3). The Beast comes on the scene as the Man of Sin, an economic-political figure. At some point, one of the heads of that Beast (probably the [Roman]{.class_1921} one) is ["as it were wounded to death."]{.class_1922} He is "resurrected" as the Son of Perdition, a religious figure (2 Thess. 2:4), with the spirit of Judas Iscariot (John 17:12; Acts 1:25 cf. Rev. 9:11) and the soul of the Devil (Rev. 13:2, 4).

Back to verse 21: ["And in his estate shall stand up a VILE person."]{.class_1931} Do you know what is so interesting about that description? Twice in your Bible the word ["vile"]{.class_1931} is directly connected to the practice of [sex perversion]{.class_1932} (Judg. 19:24; Rom. 1:26). So do you know what you find about this ["vile person"]{.class_1931} down in verse 37 here in Daniel 11? [He's a sex pervert.]{.class_1932} We shall reserve further comment on that for verse 37. Suffice it for right now to say: ["as it was in the days of Lot . . . Even thus shall it be in the day when the Son of man is revealed"]{.class_1931} (Luke 17:28--30).

["To whom they shall not give the honour of the kingdom."]{.class_1922} Whoever this person is, he is not the first choice of all the "one-worlders" like the Bilderbergers, the Rothschilds, the Illuminati, the Club of Rome, the Bohemian Grove, etc. This fellow worms his way into power ["by flatteries."]{.class_1922}

Now those last two words are interesting. Do you know what Job said nearly 300 years before Moses wrote anything? Job said, ["He that speaketh flattery to his friends, even the eyes of his children shall fail"]{.class_1922} (Job 17:5). According to the oldest book in that Bible, flattery is connected with losing your eyesight. Of course, I understand that can be taken figuratively (Deut. 28:65; Lam. 4:17), but in the case of the Antichrist, it is [literal.]{.class_1921}

["Woe to the idol shepherd that leaveth the flock! the sword shall be upon his arm, and upon his RIGHT EYE: his arm shall be clean dried up, AND HIS RIGHT EYE SHALL BE UTTERLY DARKENED"]{.class_1922} (Zech. 11:17).

["He shall come in peaceably."]{.class_1922} That white horse rider in Revelation 6:2 conquers through peace: he has no arrows for his bow. "Peace," when God is about to "lower the boom," is the message of the false prophets in the Old Testament (Jer. 4:10, 6:14, 8:11, 14:13, 23:17; Ezek. 13:10). That is one of the things that characterizes ["the times and the seasons"]{.class_1922} before the Lord's return (1 Thess. 5:1).

["For yourselves know perfectly that the day of the Lord so cometh as a thief in the night. For when they shall say, PEACE AND SAFETY; then sudden destruction cometh upon them, as travail upon a woman with child; and they shall not escape"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 5:2--3).

22 And with the arms of a flood shall they be overflown from before him, and shall be broken; yea, also the prince of the covenant.

23 And after the league made with him he shall work deceitfully: for he shall come up, and shall become strong with a small people.

24 He shall enter peaceably even upon the fattest places of the province; and he shall do that which his fathers have []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_278}not done, nor his fathers' fathers; he shall scatter among them the prey, and spoil, and riches: yea, and he shall forecast his devices against the strong holds, even for a time.

The ["flood"]{.class_1922} of verse 22 is said to be ["water"]{.class_1922} the Devil casts ["out of his mouth"]{.class_1922} at the remnant of the Jews hiding out in the wilderness from the Antichrist during the Tribulation (Rev. 12:14--15). In Revelation, ["the earth"]{.class_1922} helps those Jews by opening up and swallowing the water (Rev. 12:16), but that flood overflows the land of Israel, its cities, and its inhabitants in Jeremiah 47:2. There is a chance that the floodwaters of Revelation 12:15--16 could be symbolic of the [armies]{.class_1921} of the Antichrist (["the ARMS of a flood"]{.class_1922}), for Isaiah 8:7--8 says this:

["Now therefore, behold, the Lord bringeth up upon them the WATERS OF THE RIVER, strong and many, EVEN THE KING OF ASSYRIA ]{.class_1922}\[a reference to the Antichrist---Isa. 10:5, 14:25, 30:31, 31:8; Ezek. 31:3; Mic. 5:5--6\][, and all his glory: and he shall come up over all his channels, and go over all his banks: And he shall pass through Judah; he shall overflow and go over, he shall reach even to the neck; and the stretching out of his wings shall fill the breadth of thy land, O Immanuel]{.class_1922} \[Jesus Christ---Isa. 7:14; Matt. 1:21--23\][."]{.class_1922}

This would fit what we read back in 9:26 here in Daniel (which see). That would place ["the covenant"]{.class_1922} of verse 22 as ["the covenant"]{.class_1922} that is confirmed and broken by the Antichrist back in 9:27. But who that ["prince of the covenant" ]{.class_1922}would be, I am not sure. It is not the Antichrist, because he is the one coming in with a flood and doing the breaking; ["the prince of the covenant"]{.class_1922} is ["broken"]{.class_1922} by him. It is not Jesus Christ, because this has nothing to do with the First Advent, and it's not He at His Second Advent, because then, He does the breaking (Psa. 2:9). I suppose you could say it will be a ["prince"]{.class_1922} with whom the Antichrist confirms ["the covenant"]{.class_1922} (cf. vss. 23, 27), but I am not sure about that.

I will tell you what it looks like to me. From passages like Revelation 12:5; Job 3:3; Lamentations 4:20; and 1 Samuel 1:11, there seems to be a Jewish leader whom God raises up during the []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_279}Tribulation to oppose the Antichrist, but whom the Antichrist slays. The reference in Lamentations 4:20 is really strong in that regard, for Israel is in the land where Job was persecuted (Lam. 4:21 cf. Job 1:1)---Edom. That's where Selah Petra is located, where Israel will flee during the Tribulation (see our comments on Psa. 3:4 in that Commentary). God is feeding them there in the wilderness, just as He did back in Exodus and Numbers (Lam. 5:9; Mic. 7:14--15; Rev. 12:6, 14).

Now notice this "back and forth" in the narrative. The Antichrist comes in ["peaceably"]{.class_1922} (vs. 21), but then overflows with his army and breaks ["the prince of the covenant"]{.class_1922} (vs. 22). Then it's back to working ["deceitfully"]{.class_1922} and becoming ["strong with a small people"]{.class_1922} (vs. 22) by entering ["peaceably"]{.class_1922} into the land (vs. 24). Like many other places in the Scriptures, the Holy Spirit doesn't necessarily record events in chronological or sequential order (see our remarks on 7:9--14).

[If]{.class_1921} ["the league"]{.class_1922} in verse 23 is the same as ["the covenant"]{.class_1922} of verse 27, that would lend credibility to the idea that Daniel's Seventieth Week is still all in the future (see our comments on 9:27), for that ["league"]{.class_1922} is ["MADE,"]{.class_1922} not just confirmed. Over in Ezekiel 17:13--19, the last King of Judah, Zedekiah, made a covenant with the King of Babylon, and he broke it by going to Egypt for military help against Nebuchadnezzar. Because of that, Zedekiah ends up losing his life. As we saw back in chapter 3 here in Daniel, Nebuchadnezzar is one of the greatest types of the Antichrist there is in the Bible. So Ezekiel 17 has the basic elements, in type, that you find here in Daniel 11: the Antichrist, a Jewish ruler who lies, Pharaoh (["the king of the south"]{.class_1922}vs. 25), and a broken covenant.

So the Antichrist makes a league and a covenant with those Jews. He does so with overtures of peace and by "buttering them up" (flatteries---vss. 32, 34). He becomes ["strong"]{.class_1922} even though he doesn't have a "show of force"---["with a small people"]{.class_1922} (vs. 23). He breaks the league and covenant, and scatters the Jews (some fleeing into the wilderness to be fed by God---see our remarks under vs. 22) and spoils the riches and resources of the land. The last part of verse 24 shows this will not be done on a "whim," but will be well thought out and planned ahead of time, even while he is making the league (["he shall forecast his devices against the strong holds"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_280}).

Notice the expressions ["his fathers"]{.class_1922} and ["his fathers' fathers"]{.class_1922} in verse 24. That's a [Jewish]{.class_1921} expression for the [Jewish]{.class_1921} forefathers (e.g., Exod. 10:6; Lev. 25:41; Num. 1:4, 44; 1 Kings 2:10, 11:43, 14:20, 31; 2 Kings 20:21, 21:22; 1 Chron. 26:31; Acts 13:36). Look down at verse 37: ["Neither shall he regard the God of HIS FATHERS."]{.class_1922} So we have two things that identify the Antichrist in this chapter. First, he's ["the king of the north"]{.class_1922}---Syria. Second, his ancestry is Jewish---["his fathers."]{.class_1922} So I say the Antichrist is a [Syrian Jew.]{.class_1921} Isaiah 14:20 says of the Antichrist, ["thou hast destroyed THY LAND]{.class_1922} \[Israel\][, and slain THY PEOPLE]{.class_1922} \[the Jews\][."]{.class_1922} Ezekiel 21:25 identifies him as the ["profane wicked prince of ISRAEL."]{.class_1922} The Antichrist is a [Jew.]{.class_1921}

That is why you have some Christians these days becoming anti-Semitic. They figure that since most of those Jews are Christ-rejectors and the Antichrist is Jewish, then they ought to be against that Jew. So they identify Babylon the Great as Jerusalem. But that can't be, because even in its apostasy, the Holy Spirit calls that city ["the holy city"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 11:2, 8). Babylon is [never]{.class_1921} called that, in any form. You had better watch out for that anti-Semitism. God promised to restore that city (Ezek. 48; Zech. 14), and He promised to save that people (Rom. 11:26--27). God will whip them enough without you adding your two-cents worth.

25 And he shall stir up his power and his courage against the king of the south with a great army; and the king of the south shall be stirred up to battle with a very great and mighty army; but he shall not stand: for they shall forecast devices against him.

26 Yea, they that feed of the portion of his meat shall destroy him, and his army shall overflow: and many shall fall down slain.

27 And both these kings' hearts shall be to do mischief, and they shall speak lies at one table; but it shall not prosper: for yet the end shall be at the time appointed.

Verse 25 is a campaign of the Antichrist against ["the king of the south."]{.class_1922} So far, ["the king of the south"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_281} has been a reference to the ruler of Egypt, but if you translated that into our modern political set-up, it could include a Moslem coalition made up of Egypt, Sudan, Libya, Ethiopia, and perhaps Saudi Arabia. Ancient Egypt had holdings in all those countries. If that be the case, ["the north"]{.class_1922} which the Antichrist is ["the king of"]{.class_1922} would be that ten-nation federated kingdom of those iron-clay toes in the image back in chapter 2. That's a restored Roman Empire centered in Europe, north of Palestine. So you have the Antichrist and his forces coming down and fighting against Egypt and its modern allies, and Egypt loses. Egypt loses due to traitors and a "fifth column" in its own midst (vs. 26).

Once more, this expression ["forecast devices"]{.class_1922} shows up (see vs. 24). It is an old way of saying "plan your strategy against the enemy ahead of time," but isn't that word ["devices"]{.class_1922} interesting? Today those ["devices"]{.class_1922} are computers, satellites, surveillance equipment, drones, etc. We would call "forcasting devices against," today, in modern parlance, "computer simulations."

["And both these kings' hearts]{.class_1922} \[i.e., the King of the north and the King of the south\][ shall be to do mischief, and they shall speak lies at one table"]{.class_1922} (vs. 27). There's your "peace conference" and "peace summit"---just a couple of troublemakers sitting around a table lying to each other. The Antichrist is just being "like father, like son" (John 8:44), but did you know that under Sharia (Koranic law), a Moslem is allowed to [lie]{.class_1921} if it will advance Islam? That's called "taqiyya"; it means a Mohammedan can lie anywhere, at any time, if he believes it will help protect or advance his religion. That is why you can never trust any "good Moslem"; lying is part of his religious duty.

["For yet THE END shall be at the time appointed." "The end"]{.class_1922}---so this is a covenant made at some point immediately preceding the Second Advent; it has nothing to do [doctrinally]{.class_1921} with Antiochus Epiphanes. ["The time appointed"]{.class_1922} is the time when he comes back through Israel to set up ["the abomination of desolation"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 24:15; Mark 13:14 cf. Dan. 9:29--31).

28 Then shall he return into his land with great riches; []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_282}and his heart shall be against the holy covenant; and he shall do exploits, and return to his own land.

29 At the time appointed he shall return, and come toward the south; but it shall not be as the former, or as the latter.

30 For the ships of Chittim shall come against him: therefore he shall be grieved, and return, and have indignation against the holy covenant: so shall he do; he shall even return, and have intelligence with them that forsake the holy covenant.

31 And arms shall stand on his part, and they shall pollute the sanctuary of strength, and shall take away the daily sacrifice, and they shall place the abomination that maketh desolate.

Verse 28 says the Antichrist returns ["into his land"]{.class_1922} without ever telling you what that ["land"]{.class_1922} is. If you take it in its historic context, it would be the Hellenistic kingdom of Syria, which stretched from Syria in the west to India in the east, with Babylon in the middle. So there is a good chance that ["his land"]{.class_1922} is a reference to a restored Babylon. While there is no doubt that Revelation 17 is a reference to Rome as [religious]{.class_1921} Babylon, some of the prophecy writers, like Clarence Larkin, believe Babylon itself will be rebuilt as the new economic capital of the world (Rev. 18). Babylon was located in what is, today, the modern State of Iraq. Saddam Hussein actually started rebuilding Babylon in 1983. [If]{.class_1921} (and I say "if" because the Bible isn't definite about some of these things) ["the north"]{.class_1922} is a reference, prophetically, to the ten-nation revived Roman Empire, there is a possibility that a revived Babylon will be chosen as its political capital.

Now, why would I say that Babylon is the ["his land"]{.class_1922} of the text? Look at verse 30: ["For the ships of Chittim shall come against him."]{.class_1922} The cross-reference to that is found in Balaam's prophecy in Numbers 24:24.

"And ships shall come from the coast of Chitim, and shall afflict Asshur, and shall afflict Eber, and he also shall perish for ever."

Asshur and Eber are descendants of Shem connected with the kingdoms of the Assyrians and Chaldeans (1 Chron. 1:17; Gen. 10:21--24); their names are used for the lands they inhabited. Asshur would be Assyria, for he built Nineveh, the capital of Assyria (Gen. 10:11). The land of Eber would be the land where his descendants originally lived: Ur of the Chaldees (Gen. 11:16--28). Nineveh was located on the northern part of the Euphrates, and Ur was located on the southern part of the Euphrates, with Babylon in between. So the land of Babylon is the land of the Antichrist, exactly as it was for Nimrod, Sennacherib, Nebuchadnezzar, Darius, and Alexander.

The ["Chittim"]{.class_1922} of verse 30 originally referred to the Phoenician colony on the island of Cyprus. With the Phoenicians traveling all over the Mediterranean and founding colonies along the coasts, it eventually came to refer to anybody dwelling along the coast line of the Mediterranean. So in the Tribulation, ["the ships of Chittim"]{.class_1922} can be from Turkey, Greece, Italy, France, Spain, Morocco, Libya, Egypt, or any of thirteen other countries in the Mediterranean area. With modern warfare, a fleet could sit off the coast of Lebanon or Syria, or even in the Persian Gulf, and launch missiles, fighter jet sorties, or drone strikes all up and down the Euphrates.

Back to verse 29. So having whipped Egypt, the Antichrist makes a covenant with Egypt that somehow involves Israel. Of course, he has no intention of keeping any part of it, with either Egypt or Israel: ["his heart shall be against the holy covenant."]{.class_1922} In God's appointed time (cf. 8:19, 10:1), the Antichrist launches a second campaign against Egypt, but is foiled by an armada of vessels from the Mediterranean nations. Being unable to take Egypt, he turns his attention toward Israel to vent his ["indignation against the holy covenant"]{.class_1922} (vs. 30). The word ["intelligence"]{.class_1922} in verse 30 has the same meaning it has today in military and political circles: it is information gathered that is of value militarily or politically. ["Them that forsake the holy covenant"]{.class_1922} are those Jews who have sided with the Antichrist against their own people (vss. 32, 34).

The Antichrist enters Jerusalem in armed force. He goes to the rebuilt temple, takes ["away the daily sacrifice,"]{.class_1922} and sets up his own image in the Holy of Holies (vs. 31). At this point, Larkin is faced with the same problem Scofield had with the ["little horn"]{.class_1922} back in []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_284}8:9. Rather than admit that verse 31 has nothing to do doctrinally with Antiochus Epiphanes, he has ["the abomination that maketh desolate"]{.class_1922} here different from ["the abomination that maketh desolate"]{.class_1922} in 12:11. The reason is, he has to have some reference to the future ["abomination of desolation, spoken of by Daniel the prophet"]{.class_1922} which had not yet taken place at the time of Christ (Matt. 24:15; Mark 13:14). What Larkin got with the little horns of 7:8 and 8:9 (that they were both prophecies of the Antichrist), he missed with the abominations in 11:31 and 12:11.

32 And such as do wickedly against the covenant shall he corrupt by flatteries: but the people that do know their God shall be strong, and do exploits.

33 And they that understand among the people shall instruct many: yet they shall fall by the sword, and by flame, by captivity, and by spoil, many days.

34 Now when they shall fall, they shall be holpen with a little help: but many shall cleave to them with flatteries.

35 And some of them of understanding shall fall, to try them, and to purge, and to make them white, even to the time of the end: because it is yet for a time appointed.

Now, I take those who ["do wickedly against the covenant"]{.class_1922} to be [Jews]{.class_1921} whom the Antichrist corrupts ["by flatteries"]{.class_1922} (vs. 32). The reason I take that position is that they are contrasted with ["the people that do know their God"]{.class_1922}; those are those Tribulation [Jewish]{.class_1921} saints back in 7:27 (which see). In the Tribulation, there will be Jews who side with the Antichrist against their own people (Matt. 24:10; Mark 13:12; Luke 21:16).

["The people that do know their God"]{.class_1922} would be the 144,000 Jews sealed to go through the Tribulation in Revelation 7:4--8. While nothing is said in Revelation 7 about what they do besides being ["servants"]{.class_1922} of God (Rev. 7:3), the implication of verse 33 here in Daniel 11 is that they ["shall instruct many."]{.class_1922} There are a couple of places in the Scriptures where some insight into the ministry of the 144,000 is mentioned. There is an enigmatic statement by the Lord Jesus to the apostles in Matthew 10:23---["Ye shall not have gone []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_285}over the cities of Israel, till the Son of man be come."]{.class_1922} Neither the apostles nor Jesus Christ preached in every city of Israel during His earthly ministry. Unless there is a "second coming" of the apostles, then that is a prophetic statement on the ministry of the 144,000.

Jesus said, ["And this gospel of the kingdom shall be preached in all the world for a witness unto all nations; and then shall the end come"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 24:14).

That ["gospel of the kingdom"]{.class_1922} is not ["the gospel of the grace of God"]{.class_1922} Paul preached (Acts 20:24).
