The ["gospel of the kingdom"]{.class_1922} is the message that the King is coming, so you had better get ready for Him by repenting (Matt. 4:17), believing in Him, and keeping[ "the commandments of God"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 12:17, 14:12). You are not looking for "the King is coming"; you are looking for your Saviour to come back and take you out of here to be with Him (Tit. 2:13; 1 Thess. 1:10, 4:15--17).

Paul is a [type]{.class_1921} of the 144,000, though, in that he was ["a servant of God"]{.class_1922} (Tit. 1:1) who preached to Gentiles. These 144,000 Jewish evangelists will win ["a great multitude . . . of all nations, and kindreds, and people, and tongues . . . out of great tribulation"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 7:9, 14; note that ["After this"]{.class_1922} in Rev. 7:9 that follows the sealing of the 144,000). Like their apostolic type (Paul), they will exercise the apostolic signs and wonders (2 Cor. 12:12 cf. Mark 16:17--18). That will be the ["exploits"]{.class_1922} they ["do"]{.class_1922} (vs. 32). Part of those ["exploits"]{.class_1922} will undoubtedly be a repeat of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego in the fiery furnace, and Daniel in the lions' den.

Now, the 144,000 are protected during the Great Tribulation, but their converts aren't. ["They shall fall by the sword, and by the flame, by captivity, and by spoil, many days]{.class_1922} \[the three-and-a-half years of the Great Tribulation\]["]{.class_1922} (vs. 33). These are Tribulation saints, both Jew and Gentile, who die for the sake of Jesus Christ and His word at the hands of the Antichrist and his crowd (Rev. 6:9--11, 7:14, 14:12--13, 15:2, 20:4).

During this time of intense persecution and martyrdom, ["they shall be holpen ]{.class_1922}\[an archaic form of the past participle for help\][ with a little help"]{.class_1922} (vs. 34). That help is given in Revelation 12. The saved Jews will flee ["into the wilderness"]{.class_1922} where there is []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_286}["a place prepared of God,"]{.class_1922} and they are fed miraculously by God just like the Israelites were when they came out of Egypt (Rev. 12:6, 14 cf. Mic. 7:14--15). Moreover, when the Devil casts that water out of his mouth to flood out those Jews and drown them, ["the earth"]{.class_1922} helps by opening up to swallow ["the flood"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 12:15--16). Outside of that, there are only a few "righteous Gentiles," here and there across the globe, who give the Jews around them food, water, shelter, clothes, and comfort in sickness and imprisonment (Matt. 25:32--36). The reason there are so few is because to help a Jew out in the Tribulation is to expose yourself to the persecution of the Antichrist.

The foreshadow of that was Hitler and then the Communists. If the Nazis caught you helping the Jews, you would be sent off to a concentration camp; that is what happened to Corrie Ten Boom and her family ([The Hiding Place]{.class_1921}). In Nazi Germany, the children were encouraged to turn in the parents, and neighbors were rewarded for "ratting out" their neighbors if they saw or heard anything against the Nazi agenda. The Communists did the same thing, and also "bugged" the phones of any suspected political dissenters. The Romanian Communist dictator Nicolae Ceausescu would use the television sets to spy on people. With the advent of cell phones and computers, it is easier than ever for the government to keep track of where you are and what you are doing. In the Tribulation, people are under electronic and computerized surveillance that won't allow them to let out a squeak against the Antichrist without the secret police making a "midnight call."

In the Tribulation, there are "infiltrators" who ["cleave"]{.class_1922} to congregations of believers ["with flatteries."]{.class_1922} Jude says they creep in ["unawares"]{.class_1922} (Jude 4); Peter says they ["privily . . . bring in damnable heresies"]{.class_1922} (2 Pet. 2:1). ["They speak great swelling words of vanity"]{.class_1922} (2 Pet. 2:18), ["having men's persons in admiration because of advantage"]{.class_1922} (Jude 16). Paul says they serve ["their own belly"]{.class_1922} and ["deceive the hearts of the simple"]{.class_1922} by ["GOOD words and FAIR speeches"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 16:18). They aren't rude and crude like "Ruckman" (2 Cor. 11:6, 10:10); their words ooze with a syrupy sweetness that would give you diabetes. They wouldn't even think of offending anyone with what they say, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_287}but they will slit your spiritual throat from ear to ear---in the Tribulation, it will be someone's [physical]{.class_1921} throat (Rev. 20:4).

Now the ["fall"]{.class_1922} of verse 35 is different from the ["fall"]{.class_1922} of verse 33. In verse 33, they are falling into slavery (["captivity"]{.class_1922}), extreme poverty from being robbed of everything (["spoil"]{.class_1922}), or [falling down dead]{.class_1921} (["sword," "flame"]{.class_1922}). In verse 35, the ["fall"]{.class_1922} is for the purpose of [testing]{.class_1921} and [purging]{.class_1921} so someone comes out ["white"]{.class_1922} in ["the end"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 6:11, 3:5, 7:9, 14). You see, there are not only ["virgins"]{.class_1922} who are ["sealed"]{.class_1922} in the Tribulation (Rev. 11:1--4 cf. Rev. 7:4), there are ["virgins"]{.class_1922} who are [not]{.class_1921} sealed (Matt. 25:1--13). They aren't waiting to [marry]{.class_1921} the Bridegroom like the [one]{.class_1921} ["chaste virgin"]{.class_1922} (2 Cor. 11:2), the Church (Eph. 5:23--32); they are waiting to [meet]{.class_1921} Him so they can go in with Him to His marriage to His Bride (Matt. 25:10). If they don't watch (Matt. 25:13) and retain the Holy Spirit (Matt. 25:8) by enduring to ["the end"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 24:13), they can be left behind when the Bridegroom comes (Matt. 25:10--12). Although they start out with the oil in their lamps and their lamps burning (a type of the Holy Spirit), they end up with[ no oil]{.class_1921} and their [lamps out]{.class_1921} (i.e., they lost the Holy Spirit just as David could have back in Psalm 51:11). That is [not]{.class_1921} your case: you can't lose the Holy Spirit (Eph. 4:30). But believers in the Tribulation sure can. Christ tells those virgins who started out with oil in their lamps but let it burn out:[ "I know you not"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 25:12)---[they're lost.]{.class_1921} Brethren, get it and get it straight: salvation in the Old Testament and the Tribulation (and the Millennium, for that matter) is NOT the same as salvation in the Church Age; I don't care what "good," "godly," "dedicated," "Fundamental" so-and-so says it is.

36 And the king shall do according to his will; and he shall exalt himself, and magnify himself above every god, and shall speak marvellous things against the God of gods, and shall prosper till the indignation be accomplished: for that that is determined shall be done.

37 Neither shall he regard the God of his fathers, nor the desire of women, nor regard any god: for he shall magnify himself above all.

38 But in his estate shall he honour the God of forces: []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_288}and a god whom his fathers knew not shall he honour with gold, and silver, and with precious stones, and pleasant things.

39 Thus shall he do in the most strong holds with a strange god, whom he shall acknowledge and increase with glory: and he shall cause them to rule over many, and shall divide the land for gain.

There is no doubt now that the passage is about the Antichrist. After their excursion into the Maccabean history of Antiochus Epiphanes, Scofield and Larkin acknowledge that verse 36 to the end of the chapter deal with the Antichrist; even Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown come around.

The clincher is the term ["the king"]{.class_1922} in verse 36; it's emphatic. It is not just ["the king of the north"]{.class_1922}; it is ["THE king."]{.class_1922} Those ten Kings who rule with the Antichrist ["give their kingdom unto the beast"]{.class_1922} so that he is the one in charge of "the whole kit and caboodle" (Rev. 17:12, 17).

This King operates ["according to his will; and he shall exalt himself, and magnify himself above every god."]{.class_1922} The first words the Devil ever spoke, as recorded in the Bible, were:[ "I WILL ascend into heaven, I will EXALT MY THRONE ABOVE the stars of God . . . I will ASCEND ABOVE the heights of the clouds; I WILL BE LIKE THE MOST HIGH" ]{.class_1922}(Isa. 14:13--14). When Satan enters the Man of Sin, the Bible says he ["opposeth and exalteth himself above all that is called God, or that is worshipped; so that he as God sitteth in the temple of God, shewing himself that he is God"]{.class_1922} (2 Thess. 2:4). Satan's sin, though, started with the [will.]{.class_1921}

Do you know why a man goes to Hell; I mean, ultimately? It's because of his [will.]{.class_1921} That Bible says, ["whosoever WILL, let him take the water of life freely"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 22:17). Jesus said, though, ["ye WILL NOT come to me, that ye might have life"]{.class_1922} (John 5:40). ["Wilt thou go with this man?"]{.class_1922} (Gen. 24:58). You either will or you won't. There's no "Irresistible Grace" to it (see Acts 7:51).

When D. L. Moody was over in London, he held a special meeting for atheists; about 5,000 came out. When he got through preaching, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_289}he held an invitation and had the back doors open so anyone who wished could leave. No one left (a miracle in itself), but no one came forward either.

With 5,000 atheists just sitting there staring at him, Moody explained what it meant to [receive]{.class_1921} Christ and then asked, "Who will receive Him? Just say, 'I will.'" One fellow among those atheists said, "I can't." So Moody went on to explain what it meant to [believe]{.class_1921} Christ (after all, John 1:12 is the touchstone of salvation: to receive Christ is to believe what He did for you on the cross). He then asked, "Who will say, I will believe Him?" One of the leaders of those atheists yelled out, "I won't!"

D. L. Moody broke down in tears and said, "It is 'I will' or 'I won't' for every man in this hall tonight." He told the story of the Prodigal Son and said, "The battle is in the will, and only there. When the young man said, 'I will arise,' the battle was won, for he had yielded his will; and on that point all hangs tonight. Men, you have your champion there in the middle of the hall, the man who said, 'I won't.' I want every man here who believes that man is right to follow him and to rise and say, 'I won't.'"

[No one stood up,]{.class_1921} so Moody changed his invitation: "Now who'll say, 'I will'?" Five hundred of those atheists jumped to their feet with the shout of "I will." That was Monday night of those meetings; by Friday, almost 2,000 of those atheists had come to Christ.

Now I know you would have a hard time today getting this bunch of hedonistic hypocrites to say "I will" to Jesus Christ, but the point of that account is still well taken. There are only two responses to the claims of Christ: you [will]{.class_1921} receive Him or you [won't.]{.class_1921} If you [will]{.class_1921} receive Him, then you'll go to Heaven, and if you [won't,]{.class_1921} well, then go to Hell. You can't avoid the consequences of your choice.

["And shall speak marvellous things against the God of gods." ]{.class_1922}This is the ["little horn"]{.class_1922} of 7:8, 20; this is the Beast of Revelation 13:5--6. Revelation 17:3 says he is ["FULL of names of blasphemy."]{.class_1922} Blasphemy becomes the hallmark of the followers of the Antichrist in the Tribulation (Rev. 16:9, 11, 21).

["And shall prosper till the indignation be accomplished: for that that is determined shall be done."]{.class_1922} That's rough, boy. That means that just as God determined that His Son die for the sins []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_290}of man­kind (Acts 2:23, 4:28), He has determined to allow Satan free reign on this earth for three-and-a-half years. The Lord isn't just going to allow it to happen, He's going to let it ["prosper."]{.class_1922} He will even help it along (2 Thess. 2:11--12).

Now don't misunderstand what I am about to say. I am no Calvinist (I am no Arminian, either). I believe man is free in his will to accept or reject Christ (John 1:12); I believe election is conditioned on God's foreknowledge (1 Pet. 1:2) of a man getting in Christ at salvation (Eph. 1:4 cf. 1 Cor. 12:13); I believe Christ died for [all]{.class_1921} sinners, not just those who accept Him (1 John 2:2; 2 Pet. 2:1); I believe a sinner can resist the Holy Ghost (Acts 7:51); and I believe in the Eternal Security of the believer, not the "Perseverance of the Saints" (yes, there is a difference; see Laurence Vance's work [The Other Side of Calvinism]{.class_1921}). But I tell you what, it sure looks sometimes, as I read through that Book, that God has reserved a specific generation of Christ-rejectors for damnation in the Tribulation (see Prov. 30:11--14). Of course, He gives folks then a chance to be saved (Matt. 24:14), but you will really have to be committed to make it (Matt. 24:13). If you won't get saved by grace through faith without works now, I can't see how in the world you are going to make it then by not only faith in Christ but keeping the commandments (Rev. 12:17, 14:12). If you ever wanted to prove what a really good person you are, that will be your chance. Of course, you will have to make it through starvation (Rev. 13:16--17) and beheading (Rev. 20:4), but more power to you. Me, ["I pray thee have me excused"]{.class_1922} (cf. Luke 14:18--19). I'm trusting Christ [right now]{.class_1921} because [I'm chicken:]{.class_1921} I don't want to go to Hell, and I don't want to go through the Tribulation. I have nothing whatsoever to prove, as far as my own goodness is concerned; I will take ["the free gift"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 5:15--18), thank you very much.

We have already discussed the expression ["his fathers"]{.class_1922} (vss. 37--38) back under verse 24, which see. The ["fathers"]{.class_1922} are Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, the patriarchs of Israel. But not only will the Antichrist not ["regard the God of his fathers,"]{.class_1922} he won't regard ["the desire of women"]{.class_1922} (vs. 37).

Now what does that mean? Well, in a day and age when sexual perversity was hidden away "in the closet," a lot of the old-time []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_291}commentators would say this:

1\. The desire of Jewish women was to give birth to the Messiah. Since this is the Antichrist, he would have no regard at all for Jesus Christ. That is a rather stupid piece of exposition. If Jewish women don't believe the Messiah has come yet, the Devil certainly does. To Satan, the promise of the virgin birth in Genesis 3:15 is a moot point these days, since it has already come and gone. He had his chance in Luke 2 and Matthew 2, and he blew it both times.

2\. ["The desire of women" ]{.class_1922}is the desire for the husband to be the ruler of the household (Gen. 3:15). That interpretation really doesn't go anywhere, unless you take it to mean the Antichrist pushes "women's lib."

3\. Adam Clarke gets the point that ["the desire of women"]{.class_1922} is a man's [sexual ]{.class_1921}desire toward a woman (Deut. 5:21, 21:11; Song of Sol. 7:10; Ezek. 24:16--18), but he applies it to the clerical celibacy of the Roman Catholic Church (1 Tim. 4:3). That is good, but it still doesn't "hit the bullseye," especially after what we have learned in the last twenty to thirty years about the "sexual preferences" of Catholic Priests.

4\. The problem was, even writers like Scofield and Larkin didn't take Christ's word in Luke 17:28--30 seriously. They couldn't imagine a society today being as sexually depraved as Sodom and Gomorrah. Sexual perversion was around when I was growing up; sure it was. But it hadn't "come out of the closet" yet. Now, although the Antichrist []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_292}["shall speak marvelous things against the God of gods"]{.class_1922} and will ["magnify himself above every god"]{.class_1922} (vs. 36), and although he won't ["regard the God of his fathers,"]{.class_1922} or ["any god"]{.class_1922} for that matter (vs. 37), there is an [exception.]{.class_1921} There is one "God" whom he does honor: that "God" is called ["the God of forces"]{.class_1922} (vs. 38). ["And he shall cause THEM to rule over many."]{.class_1922} Uh oh, there is no plural antecedent for the ["them."]{.class_1922} I suppose you could say the ["strong holds"]{.class_1922} could be the antecedent because it is plural, but ["strong holds"]{.class_1922} don't rule over anybody. 40 And at the time of the end shall the king of the south push at him: and the king of the north shall come against him like a whirlwind, with chariots, and with horsemen, and with many ships; and he shall enter into the countries, and shall overflow and pass over.

41 He shall enter also into the glorious land, and many countries shall be overthrown: but these shall escape out of his hand, even Edom, and Moab, and the chief of the children of Ammon.

42 He shall stretch forth his hand also upon the countries: and the land of Egypt shall not escape.

43 But he shall have power over the treasures of gold and of silver, and over all the precious things of Egypt: and the Libyans and the Ethiopians shall be at his steps.

What you have here is a battle between the Antichrist and Egypt that takes place during the Tribulation. Once more, the Antichrist beats the Egyptian coalition (vs. 25). This time, he doesn't just spoil Egypt, he "owns" it ([]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_296}["he shall have power . . . over all the precious things of Egypt"]{.class_1922} ).

44 But tidings out of the east and out of the north shall trouble him: therefore he shall go forth with great fury to destroy, and utterly to make away many.

45 And he shall plant the tabernacles of his palace between the seas in the glorious holy mountain; yet he shall come to his end, and none shall help him.

The passage is a reference to Armageddon. Those ["tidings out of the east"]{.class_1922} (vs. 44) are about those ["kings of the east"]{.class_1922} crossing the dry river bed of the Euphrates, headed on their way to Armageddon (Rev. 16:12--16). ["He stretcheth out the north over the empty place, and hangeth the earth upon nothing"]{.class_1922} (Job 26:7).

["Beautiful for situation, the joy of the whole earth, is mount Zion, on the sides of the north, the city of the great King"]{.class_1922} (Psa. 48:2). That's not Mount Zion over in Jerusalem; that's the one "upstairs" (Heb. 12:22; see also Isa. 14:13).

["For promotion cometh neither from the east, nor from the west, nor from the south. But God is the judge . . ."]{.class_1922} (Psa. 75:6--7). []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1632.xhtml_page_297}19:11--14).

CHAPTER 12

12:1 And at that time shall Michael stand up, the great prince which standeth for the children of thy people: and there shall be a time of trouble, such as never was since there was a nation even to that same time: and at that time thy people shall be delivered, every one that shall be found written in the book.

We have discussed angels representing nations as "Princes," and Michael specifically as the angelic Prince of Israel, in our remarks on 10:13, 21 (which see). ["Which standeth for the children of thy people"]{.class_1922}---we have already read about Michael's war with the Devil in Revelation 12:7.

["That time"]{.class_1922} is obviously the time of the Tribulation back in the last 26 verses of chapter 11. "[Such as never was since there was a nation even to that same time."]{.class_1922} This is what Jesus called ["great tribulation"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 24:21), but He took it all the way back to Genesis 1, not just Genesis 10 when the nations began.

["And at that time thy people shall be delivered, every one that shall be found written in the book."]{.class_1922} This ["book"]{.class_1922} appears throughout Scripture. It starts out in Exodus 32:32--33 and ends up in Revelation 22:19. In the New Testament, it is called ["the book of life"]{.class_1922} (Phil. 4:3; Rev. 3:5, 13:8, 17:8, 20:12, 15, 21:27, 22:10). It is the criterium for whether or not you end up in the Lake of Fire at the White Throne Judgment (Rev. 20:12, 15). The problem is, someone, at some time, can have his name blotted out of that book after it has been written there (Exod. 32:32--33; Psa. 69:28; Rev. 3:5, 22:19). The question is, is that [you]{.class_1921} as a member of the Body of Christ in this age, as the Charismatics (many of them), Methodists, Pentecostals, Freewill Baptists, and Holiness teach?

There is no doubt that if you trust Christ as your personal []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_300}Saviour, your name is in that book (Luke 10:20; Phil. 4:3). You receive eternal life as a free gift by faith in the Author of that book (Rom. 6:23; 1 John 5:13). Moreover, you have the promise of God that nothing will ever change your status in that book because not only is your name there, [you are in the Author]{.class_1921} (Rom. 8:38--39; 1 Cor. 1:8; Eph. 4:30; Phil. 1:6). You take Revelation 3:5. That's no threat to the born-again child of God, for he has already overcome the moment he got saved (1 John 4:4, 5:4--5).

That being said, someone's name [can]{.class_1921} be blotted out. Those Jews in Exodus 32 could have their names blotted out by [idolatry]{.class_1921} (Exod. 32:31--32). Someone's name can be blotted out if he isn't righteous (Psa. 69:28). That's not you if you are saved, because you have the righteousness of God through faith in Christ (Rom. 10:3--4). But in the Tribulation, the saints not only have to trust Christ, they have to keep the commandments (Rev. 12:17, 14:12). The revisers and translators of the modern versions (and the preachers who correct the Bible from the pulpit) better be glad they don't live in the Tribulation, because changing the Book then can get ["his part"]{.class_1922} taken away ["out of the book of life"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 22:19).

Now Daniel 12:1 isn't written to any Christian from Acts 2 to the Rapture of the Church. It is written to Daniel's ["people"]{.class_1922}---the [Jews. ]{.class_1921}This[ ]{.class_1921}["book"]{.class_1922}[ ]{.class_1921}is called ["a book of remembrance"]{.class_1922} in Malachi 3:16, and it is for the Jews who fear the Lord and think on His name. In the Tribulation, for a Jew's name to remain in that book, he must fear God and think on His name (and that name includes the name of His [Son]{.class_1921}---1 John 5:20 cf. Rev. 12:17, 14:12) to the point where they won't bow to the image of the Antichrist and worship it or take his mark; that's when they "overcome" (Rev. 15:2). They accomplish that not only ["by the blood of the Lamb"]{.class_1922} but ["by the word of their testimony"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 12:11). 2 And many of them that sleep in the dust of the earth shall awake, some to everlasting life, and some to shame and everlasting contempt.

3 And they that be wise shall shine as the brightness of the firmament; and they that turn many to righteousness []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_301}as the stars for ever and ever.

Two resurrections, both of them rejected by the Sadducees (Mark 12:18; Acts 23:8). As a Pharisee, Paul believed in both resurrections even before he was saved, because he believed ["all things which are written in the law and in the prophets"]{.class_1922} (Acts 24:14--15). Salvation, though, opened up a whole new understanding of those two resurrections for him. He could distinguish a resurrection ["from the dead"]{.class_1922} (1 Cor. 15:20; Mark 9:9--10) that takes place before the "general resurrection" taught by the Jews (John 11:24), as well as every lost Catholic, Mohammedan, Episcopalian, etc. (see our comments on Luke 20:35 in that Commentary). He could see that the resurrection of the just is in [stages:]{.class_1921} the firstfruits (1 Cor. 15:20, 23; Matt. 27:52--53), the harvest (1 Cor. 15:23; 1 Thess. 4:13--17), and the gleanings (Rev. 20:4--5).

It was revealed to John that these two resurrections are a ["thousand years"]{.class_1922} apart, and that ["the first resurrection"]{.class_1922} takes place before the thousand-year reign of Christ begins (Rev. 20:4--6). So the Bible position on the return of Christ is [premillennial]{.class_1921}: He comes back and resurrects the saved [before]{.class_1921} His Millennial reign. That means all Postmillennialists and Amillennialists are [full of beans]{.class_1921} (see our comments on 2 Tim. 2:18 in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on the Pastoral Epistles]{.class_1921}). For the Church, the Body of Christ, it is [pre-Tribulational,]{.class_1921} for the dead in Christ get resurrected at the Rapture, and the Rapture takes place before ["the time of JACOB'S trouble"]{.class_1922} starts. For further study, get our work [The Two Raptures]{.class_1921} so you don't get the "harvest" and the "gleanings" of ["the first resurrection"]{.class_1922} confused like this modern bunch that has Christians going through the Tribulation to prove just how "holy" they (i.e., the ones who believe in a "mid-Trib" or "post-Trib" rapture of the Body of Christ) really are.

Now, verse 2, in the context, is specifically about [Jews in the Tribulation]{.class_1921} (vs. 1). When Jesus taught on these resurrections, He based them both on [works.]{.class_1921} If a Jew does ["good"]{.class_1922}---WORKS---he comes up at ["the resurrection of life,"]{.class_1922} and if he does ["evil,"]{.class_1922} he comes up at ["the resurrection of damnation"]{.class_1922} (John 5:29). Is that [your]{.class_1921} salvation?

[Not on your life, brother!]{.class_1921}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_302} If you die before your Saviour comes back, your resurrection will be based on your position ["in Christ"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 4:16), not on anything you've ["done"]{.class_1922} (Tit. 3:5). The only thing you "do" is accept the free gift purchased by your Saviour by His blood (Rom. 5:1, 9--10, 6:23). Salvation in the Tribulation is NOT like it is right now. You had better learn to rightly divide that Book (2 Tim. 2:15) and always interpret an incomplete passage by a complete passage, or you will make the biggest mess you ever saw. Daniel 12 and John 5 are the [incomplete]{.class_1921} revelation; Revelation 20 sets everything in order. And for the born-again child of God in this age, the passages on [his]{.class_1921} resurrection (not some Jew or his convert trying to keep ["the faith of Jesus"]{.class_1922} and the commandments) are 1 Corinthians 15 and 1 Thessalonians 4.

And then a great inspirational verse on soulwinning:[ "And they that be wise shall shine as the brightness of the firmament; and they that turn many to righteousness as the stars for ever and ever"]{.class_1922} (vs. 3). That Bible says, ["he that winneth souls is wise"]{.class_1922} (Prov. 11:30).

Of course, you understand the [doctrinal]{.class_1921} context is for Jews in the Tribulation, but you can still apply the verse [devotionally]{.class_1921} to you. Paul wrote, ["For what is our hope, or joy, or crown of rejoicing? Are not even ye in the presence of our Lord Jesus Christ at his coming?"]{.class_1922} (1 Thess. 2:19). So the souls you win to Christ make up a ["crown of rejoicing"]{.class_1922} for you when the Lord comes back. Over in 1 Corinthians 15:40--41, Paul likens the resurrection body of the believer to a celestial body like the sun, the moon, or the stars. He says that body will be like that of his resurrected Saviour in its glory (Phil. 3:21). Well, the glorified body of Jesus Christ was white and glistening as the sun (Matt. 17:2; Luke 9:29), and the sun is supposed to be a star. So the old hymn writer put all of that together and wrote, "Will there be any stars, any stars in my crown . . . . ?" The second verse says, "Let me watch as a winner of souls; That bright stars may be mine in the glorious day." That's the business.

Do you know why a Christian is wise if he wins souls? Because he knows a good investment from a bad one. The wise Christian invests in the [eternal,]{.class_1921} not the [temporal]{.class_1921} (2 Cor. 4:18). Souls are eternal; they []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_303}are the only thing you will be able to take with you to Heaven. The rest will burn (2 Pet. 3:10--12).

John R. Rice used to have a good sermon on the sevenfold disobedience of a Christian who is not trying to win souls.

1\. [He is guilty of disobeying Christ's last commandment to His Church before returning to Heaven---the Great Commission (Acts 1:8).]{.class_1921} Every Christian is to be a witness for his Lord. My thesis for my doctorate at Bob Jones University was if a man is not actively trying to win souls to Christ, he is an heretic, no matter what his profession of faith.

2\. [He shows a lack of love for Christ.]{.class_1921} If you love the Lord as you should, you will try to bring souls to Him, and if you aren't doing that, you don't love Him as you ought.

3\. [He doesn't follow Christ.]{.class_1921} Jesus said, ["Follow me, and I will make you fishers of men"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 4:19). If you aren't trying to catch men for the Saviour, then you aren't following Him.

4\. [He is not abiding in Christ.]{.class_1921} Of course, as a Christian, you are in Christ, and Christ is in you (Col. 1:27). But you can abide in Christ in the sense of living in fellowship with Him. Jesus said, ["He that abideth in me, and I in him, the same bringeth forth much fruit"]{.class_1922} (John 15:5). Living in fellowship with the Lord will enable you to win people to Christ.

5\. [He disregards a sacred trust.]{.class_1921} Christian, the Lord has entrusted you with the greatest news the world has ever heard. The greatest news this world ever received, it got from a graveyard. ["He is not here: for he is risen, as he said"]{.class_1922} (Matt. 28:6).

The word [gospel]{.class_1921} means "good news." The good news for a sinner is that he doesn't have to stay dead; either spiritually, physically, or for eternity. If a man will receive Christ, he will pass ["from death unto life"]{.class_1922} spiritually (John 5:24). You have a living Saviour who rose from the dead and conquered death. When you get saved, you are put in Him. You enter spiritually into His death for your sins, and you are raised with Him to ["walk in newness of life"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 6:4; Col. 2:12--13). And not only that, the same Holy Spirit of God who ["raised up Jesus from the dead"]{.class_1922} lives in you and will raise your dead body up one day (Rom. 8:11). And best of all, because you are alive in Christ, ["the second death"]{.class_1922} ([Hell]{.class_1921}) won't be able to touch []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_304}you (Rev. 20:6).

That's the good news with which you have been entrusted. If you keep your mouth shut about it, you are like that ["wicked servant"]{.class_1922} in the Parable of the Pounds in Luke 19:20--23 who wrapped his master's pound up in a napkin and buried it, instead of trading with it to make a profit for his master. You are useless to the Lord; you have not fulfilled the sacred trust He gave you.

6\. [He is guilty of spiritual manslaughter.]{.class_1921} Here is what God told Ezekiel:

["When I say unto the wicked, Thou shalt surely die; and thou givest him not warning, nor speakest to warn the wicked from his wicked way, to save his life; the same wicked man shall die in his iniquity; but his blood will I require at thine hand"]{.class_1922} (Ezek. 3:18).

Paul took that warning seriously. For two years he banged away at the doors of the Ephesians until everyone in that city had heard the Gospel (Acts 19:10, 20:20). He could say, ["I am pure from the blood of all men. For I have not shunned to declare unto you all the counsel of God"]{.class_1922} (Acts 20:26--27).

If you don't witness, you become guilty of letting sinners die and go to Hell without warning or the opportunity to escape. Under the Law, that's not murder with malice aforethought, but it is manslaughter: letting a person die without intending to do so, when you might have done something to prevent it.

7\. [He is a fool.]{.class_1921} If ["he that winneth souls is wise,"]{.class_1922} then it stands to reason that the opposite is also true: he that doesn't win souls is a [fool.]{.class_1921}

Now I don't know about you, brethren, but I made up my mind a long time ago that I wouldn't hit the Judgment Seat of Christ empty-handed. Imagine working down here your whole life and having nothing but ashes to show for it (1 Cor. 3:15). Invest your life in something that matters: something to get someone to Jesus Christ.

4 But thou, O Daniel, shut up the words, and seal the book, even to the time of the end: many shall run to and fro, and knowledge shall be increased.

Once more, what Daniel is given is ["shut up"]{.class_1922}[]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_305} (see 8:26). This time, though, in addition to being ["shut up,"]{.class_1922} it is also [sealed]{.class_1921}[ "to the time of the end."]{.class_1922} One is reminded immediately of that seven-sealed book in Revelation 5 that only Jesus Christ is worthy to open. That book may or may not be the book of Daniel (it could also be the book of Revelation itself), but whether that book in Revelation 5 is the book of Daniel or not, the two are certainly alike in that both are unsealed [after]{.class_1921} the Church has left the earth (Dan. 12:1 cf. Rev. 4:1).

Now if you want to know why there are things in Daniel which I can't explain, that's the reason. That book is sealed until we're "outta here." After the Rapture of the Church, all that stuff will begin to come out, and a saint in the Tribulation will be able to unlock all kinds of things in Daniel.

(It is interesting to note, here, that Scofield defines ["the time of the end"]{.class_1922} as the time between when the Antichrist violates his covenant with the Jews to his destruction at the Second Advent; i.e., the three-and-a-half years of the Great Tribulation \[see the discussion on the two halves of Daniel's Seventieth Week under 9:27\].)

The last part of verse 4 is one of the greatest prophecies on ["the last days"]{.class_1922} (i.e., the end of the Church Age leading into the Tribulation---2 Tim. 3:1, 7) you will find in the Bible. Like the ["many"]{.class_1922} of verse 2, more people are in view here than just Jewish Tribulation saints. Larkin tries to limit the running ["to and fro"]{.class_1922} to Jews in the Tribulation running from the Antichrist; the increase of knowledge is an increase of knowledge on the book of Daniel itself. And of course, there is a wide range of variations on this theme.

But with Paul's warnings against knowledge in the last days (1 Cor. 8:1; 1 Tim. 6:20; 2 Tim. 3:7), there is no need to ignore what is perfectly evident to anyone: locomotion and knowledge in general [have]{.class_1921} increased in these last days.

At the time Daniel and John wrote their prophecies, the fastest a man could travel on land was the speed of a horse: 30--40 mph at a full gallop, and then only for a mile or two at the most. In 1830, Martin Van Buren (then the Governor of New York) complained to the President of the United States of "railroad carriages . . . pulled at the [enormous]{.class_1932} speed of 15 miles per hour." Around that same time, []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_306}the professor of Natural Philosophy and Astronomy at the University College London said, "Rail travel at high speed is not possible because passengers, unable to breathe, would die of asphyxia." If 15 mph was considered an "enormous speed," I don't know what the good professor would have considered "high speed." There are trains today (called "bullet trains") which travel at [200 mph.]{.class_1932}

For thousands of years, the fastest a ship could travel on the sea was the speed of the wind or currents in the water. When Robert Fulton presented his idea for a steamboat that could sail on its own power against the wind and the currents, Napoleon Bonaparte called it nonsense. Today, a gas-turbine or diesel-powered cruise ship can travel at speeds of about 24 knots, about three times the average speeds of sailing ships and steamers.

But nowadays, nobody depends on ships to get across the ocean, not if they need to be at their destination right away. They fly by jet. Whereas the old sailing vessels could take 80--100 days to cross the Atlantic, you can do it now in 7--8 hours. But that's not how the airplane started out.

In 1895, the British physicist Lord Kelvin said, "Heavier-than-air flying machines are [impossible."]{.class_1921} Eighteen months before the Wright brothers made their historic flight at Kitty Hawk, North Carolina in December of 1903, the American mathematician Simon Newcomb said, "Flight by machines heavier than air is unpractical and insignificant, if not utterly impossible." And an engineer at Boeing in 1933, after the first flight of the ten-passenger 247, said, "There will never be a bigger plane built." Why, there are jets now that can carry up to 500 passengers.

People are running ["to and fro"]{.class_1922} all over this globe in ways unheard of in Daniel's day. There are 204,000 planes in the air, 260 million vehicles on the roads, 25,000 locomotives on the rails, and 8,000 boats and ships on the water (as of 2014) in America alone. I would say that qualifies as a fulfillment of the prophecy, wouldn't you?

And to limit the increase of knowledge to just the book of Daniel, or even prophecy in general, is absurd. Up until A.D. 1900, knowledge doubled every [century.]{.class_1921} By 1945, it was every [25 years.]{.class_1921} []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_307}Today, depending on the field of study, knowledge doubles every [thirteen to 24 months.]{.class_1921} According to some predictions, it could soon be every [twelve hours.]{.class_1921} God knows what man is capable of doing, and He acknowledges it (Gen. 11:6). He doesn't underestimate His creation. Men know just as much as God lets them, and He lets them learn a lot. Knowledge has increased in all areas, but it hasn't led to a great deal of [truth]{.class_1921} (2 Tim. 3:7). That's the mark of ["the last days"]{.class_1922} (2 Tim. 3:1).

5 Then I Daniel looked, and, behold, there stood other two, the one on this side of the bank of the river, and the other on that side of the bank of the river.

6 And one said to the man clothed in linen, which was upon the waters of the river, How long shall it be to the end of these wonders?

7 And I heard the man clothed in linen, which was upon the waters of the river, when he held up his right hand and his left hand unto heaven, and sware by him that liveth for ever that it shall be for a time, times, and an half; and when he shall have accomplished to scatter the power of the holy people, all these things shall be finished.

There are now three angels before Daniel: one on the west bank of the Tigris (see our comments on 10:4), one on the east bank of the Tigris, and the Angel of the Lord ["upon the waters"]{.class_1922} just as He would be 566 years later on the Sea of Galilee (see Mark 6:48 and our comments on Luke 12:38 in that Commentary). That's also what He does in Revelation 10:2--5. Both passages are connected with the Second Advent.

One of the angels asks the Angel of the Lord, ["How long shall it be to the end of these wonders?"]{.class_1922} (vs. 6). Which wonders? It's the ["time of trouble"]{.class_1922} that ends with a resurrection of the just taking place back up in verses 1--2. And the answer given is the time period of the Great Tribulation (see our remarks under 7:25 and 9:27). Notice, again, that the Tribulation is a ["time of trouble"]{.class_1922} for [Israel,]{.class_1921} not the Church (["when he shall have accomplished to scatter the power of the holy people"]{.class_1922}; see our remarks on []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_308}8:24).

8 And I heard, but I understood not: then said I, O my Lord, what shall be the end of these things?

9 And he said, Go thy way, Daniel: for the words are closed up and sealed till the time of the end.

10 Many shall be purified, and made white, and tried; but the wicked shall do wickedly: and none of the wicked shall understand; but the wise shall understand.

After all the revelation Daniel has been given, there are still things about the vision he doesn't understand. I don't blame him; I don't either. Now some things are clear to us because we have more revelation, laid out more clearly, than Daniel did.

Daniel asks, ["what shall be the end of these things?"]{.class_1922} (vs. 8). The answer he gets in verse 9 is basically: "Run along; that's all you're going to get." Why? Because ["the words are closed up and sealed till the time of the end"]{.class_1922} (vs. 9). Now when John gets the Revelation, those words aren't sealed anymore because ["the time is at hand"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 22:10). Revelation lays everything out where you can get it, and it goes beyond in detail and added information that were not given to Daniel.

Still, as I said in my comments under verse 4, there are things in Daniel no one is going to get until after the Rapture of the Church. But the Lord showed me some things in Daniel that He didn't show Larkin, Scofield, and Bullinger. The Lord showed them some things He didn't show Moody and Torrey. And the Lord showed Moody and Torrey a lot of things Calvin and Luther never saw. In plainer words, there is more the Lord can show you out of that Book; you don't want to stop with Scofield, Larkin, or "Ruckman." Keep on studying, and the Lord may show you something He never showed me.

["Many shall be purified, and made white, and tried"]{.class_1922} (vs. 10)---a reference to both Jewish and Gentile saints in the Tribulation (Rev. 6:9--11, 7:9--14).[ "But the wicked shall do wickedly."]{.class_1922} As I said back under my comments on 11:36, there are times when it looks like God has reserved a particular generation for damnation, and the reason is, because they ["believed not the truth"]{.class_1922} (2 Thess. []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_309}2:10--12). That is, they rejected the Scriptures (John 17:17), and they rejected Jesus Christ (John 14:6). So some of the brethren teach that if a sinner who hears the Gospel won't get saved this side of the Rapture that he [can't]{.class_1921} be saved in the Tribulation. God sends ["them strong delusion, that they should believe a lie"]{.class_1922} and ["be damned"]{.class_1922} (2 Thess. 2:11--12). I might not be as dogmatic about it as some of the brethren, but I do know that you can cross a line like Ahab did to the point where God lets the Devil deceive you to your own damnation (1 Kings 21:19, 22:19--23, 37--38).

But it's not just rejecting the truth, it's having ["pleasure in unrighteousness"]{.class_1922} (2 Thess. 2:12). The reason they reject Christ and His word is because they love the hog pen (cf. Luke 15:15--16). God turns ["them over to a reprobate mind, to do those things which are not convenient"]{.class_1922} (Rom. 1:28). Those worshipers of the Antichrist in the Tribulation are so blinded that they won't repent no matter what God does to them (Rev. 9:20--21, 16:9, 11). They won't believe any gospel, even when it is reduced to worshiping God as Creator (Rev. 14:6--7, 9--11).

["And none of the wicked shall understand."]{.class_1922} They reject the truth of the Scriptures, so God takes away their ability to understand anything He says. For further comment, see our remarks on Luke 8:18 in that Commentary.

["The wise shall understand"]{.class_1922} because they [believe God and His words]{.class_1921} (John 8:47, 18:37). They understand because they [do God's will]{.class_1921} (John 7:17; Psa. 107:43). They understand because [the Lord opens their understanding through His Holy Spirit]{.class_1921} (Luke 24:45; 1 Cor. 2:10--13; 1 John 5:20).

Note the context of that last reference. Following the fact that ["the Son of God is come, and hath given us an understanding"]{.class_1922} is the admonition to ["keep yourselves from idols"]{.class_1922} (1 John 5:21). That is particularly applicable to the Tribulation saint who will be tempted with sinning ["wilfully"]{.class_1922} in returning to the worship of the Antichrist and his image ["after"]{.class_1922} he has ["received the knowledge of the truth"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 10:26). If he does, ["there remaineth no more sacrifice for sins"]{.class_1922} (Heb. 10:26). The blood of Christ will do him no good at all at that point (Heb. 10:29). Salvation in the Tribulation is NOT THE SAME as your []{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_310}salvation right now (Col. 1:14; 1 John 1:7).

11 And from the time that the daily sacrifice shall be taken away, and the abomination that maketh desolate set up, there shall be a thousand two hundred and ninety days.

12 Blessed is he that waiteth, and cometh to the thousand three hundred and five and thirty days.

13 But go thou thy way till the end be: for thou shalt rest, and stand in thy lot at the end of the days.

We have already commented several times on the taking away of ["the daily sacrifice"]{.class_1922} and the setting up of ["the abomination of desolation"]{.class_1922} (Dan. 8:13, 9:27, 11:31). The desecration of the Temple by Antiochus Epiphanes, and later on by the Romans under Titus, certainly were [types]{.class_1921} of that, but they were NOT the fulfillment (Matt. 24:15; Mark 13:14; Rev. 11:2). It was not Mohammedans setting up the Mosque of Omar and the Dome of the Rock on the Temple Mount as Clarke and several others teach. The whole thing is described in 2 Thessalonians 2:3--4 and Revelation 13:13--15.

We have already discussed the discrepancy of the days of the end of the Tribulation in verses 11 and 12 in our comments on 8:13--14. We refer you to those remarks, along with the accompanying chart. There are things that happen between the Lord's return at the Second Advent and the beginning of His Millennial reign, and the restoration of Temple worship as given in Ezekiel 40--48. For example, there is the Judgment of the Nations in Matthew 25 and the burial of the dead from the Battle of Armageddon and the destruction of their weapons in Ezekiel 39. Where all that fits into Daniel 12:11--12, ["Ich weiss nicht."]{.class_1921}

And finally, the book ends on an enigmatic verse: ["But go thou thy way till the end be"]{.class_1922} (vs. 13). Well, what was Daniel's ["way"]{.class_1922} until ["the end be"]{.class_1922}? It was ["the way of all the earth"]{.class_1922} (Josh. 23:14; 1 Kings 2:2). It was ["the way"]{.class_1922} from which no man returns on his own (Job 16:22). It was [death.]{.class_1921} That has been nearly 2,500 years now, and ["the end"]{.class_1922} is not here yet (2015). So the ["rest"]{.class_1922} of verse 13 is the sleep of [death]{.class_1921} (see vs. 12).

But long after the worms get Daniel (Job 19:26), he has the promise from the Lord Himself that he would ["stand in]{.class_1922} \[his\][]{#i4F9B8-8TQm_cNiaQPK_vw1825.xhtml_page_311}[ lot at the end of days."]{.class_1922} So at the end of the Tribulation, going into the Millennium, there will be a resurrection of Israel both nationally and individually (Ezek. 37). Daniel is not only raised, but he is given his inheritance in the land of Israel.

["The end"]{.class_1922} ends with the Devil chained in the Bottomless Pit, the Antichrist and False Prophet in the Lake of Fire, the Gentiles [out]{.class_1921} of the Promised Land (that includes all "Palestinians," Moslems, and Catholics---Eastern or Roman), the nation of Israel converted to their Messiah, the Jewish saints of bygone ages alive, every Jew under his own vine and fig tree in the Promised Land, and a Judean King on the throne of the world whose foot every Gentile must bow down and kiss or join the Antichrist in burning.

That day can't come too soon for me. I mean, ["Even so, come, Lord Jesus"]{.class_1922} (Rev. 22:20). I don't know why He hasn't come back yet and wound up the whole thing. The only solution to this world's problems is for ["the lord of the vineyard"]{.class_1922} to come back and kick the squatters out (see Mark 12:1--11). If I were you, I would put Revelation 22:20 on your permanent prayer list.
